Luminous

by trappedinamatchbox

Summary

Agatha Harkness had always been a woman of precision. She built her life on neatly constructed foundations: lectures prepared weeks in advance, research that left no room for uncertainty, and a quiet home where she and her eight-year-old son, Nicky, lived in their own steady rhythm.
But all it took was a single second—one lapse in control—for everything to shatter.

OR:

Agatha is a Neurology professor at Northwestern. Rio is a paramedic. Rio saves Agatha’s life. Rio also happens to be starting her second year of med school.

Agatha can’t stop thinking about the paramedic. Agatha is fucked.

Chapter 1

“Mama, we’re going to be late!”

Nicky’s voice sounded through the house as Agatha put the finishing touches on her light makeup. She had promised him they would spend the day at the Lakefront to celebrate his last weekend of summer break. Nicky had woken up at the crack of dawn, his excitement making his little body vibrate with energy.

Agatha still took her time in finishing her makeup, and then took an appraising look at her reflection in the mirror. Her long brown hair was down, and she wondered if it was time for a haircut as it almost reached the small of her back. She wore a light blue button down that brought out her blue eyes even more and tucked it into her denim shorts, just as Nicky showed up at her door.

“Moooom,” he whined, and she rolled her eyes with an amused smile. “Come on!”

“You know, the lake is not going anywhere, mister,” She looked at him through the mirror as he approached her from behind and wrapped his little arms around her waist.

“But the longer we take to get there, the less time we’re going to have to enjoy it,” he countered, and she chuckled.

Pulling him in front of her, she bent down to kiss the top of his head. “Go feed Scratchy and we’ll be on our way.”

Nicky celebrated with a ‘yes!’ and ran out of the room as fast as he could. Agatha shook her head amused at her son’s antics, and took one last look in the mirror, pushing her sunglasses to the top of her head for now.

Not bad for forty-five, she thought to herself with a smile.

After checking that they had everything they needed, Agatha put a basket with snacks and drinks in the trunk, before making sure Nicky was buckled in. They lived in Lakeview and it was a 10-15 minute drive to the Lakefront trail. Despite the fact that Nicky had been rushing her, it was still early, barely 9:30, so they’d have plenty of time to enjoy the sunshine and enjoy Nicky’s last weekend of summer break before going back to school.

Getting in the car, Agatha turned the radio on and was half paying attention to what Nicky was babbling about in the backseat and half paying attention to the song playing softly in the car sound system. Singing quietly to herself, she checked on Nicky through the rearview mirror, smiling when she saw his head bobbing to the song absentmindedly. It was such a beautiful day.

She didn’t hear the screech of tires, and she barely heard Nicky’s scream.

And then darkness.

When Agatha woke, the world was a blur of flashing red and blue, the metallic tang of blood, and the low hum of a voice coaxing her back to reality.
“Hey, stay with me,” someone said, firm but gentle.
She blinked up into dark eyes, strong hands checking for injuries with practiced ease. The woman’s hair was pulled back, curls escaping around her temples.

“Your name, ma’am?”

“Agatha,” she rasped, throat dry. “My—my son—”

“He’s conscious,” the paramedic assured her. “Looks like an arm fracture, but he’s stable. My colleague is working on him out here. We’re taking you both in.”

Relief coursed through Agatha so quickly she nearly collapsed back against her seat. That was when she realized her head was pounding. Lifting her hand to her forehead, she felt something wet.

“Yeah, you got a nasty cut there. How are you feeling?” The paramedic asked, securing the C-collar around her neck.

“I…” Agatha swallowed, trying to assess the extent of the damage. “My head hurts. And my side, I think? My ribs.”

“Okay, are you nauseous at all?” She asked, pointing a flashlight at her eyes, making Agatha squint against the harsh light. At her negative reply, the paramedic offered a small, comforting smile. “Okay, let’s get you out of here. Hey, Alice! A little help here?”

It took a few firefighters, but soon Agatha was free of the confines of her trashed car. She still had no idea what had happened, but she was relieved to be alive with what looked like only minor injuries.

The paramedic—Vidal, according to her name tag—listened to her breath sounds with a stethoscope before smiling.

“We’ll take you and your boy to the hospital to get checked out, but it looks like you guys got lucky.” She gave Agatha’s arm a comforting squeeze and started wheeling her gurney to the ambulance. “Hey, buddy, look who’s here.”

“Mama!” Nicky’s voice was full of tears and Agatha had to take a deep breath to keep it together in front of him. “You wouldn’t wake up, mama. I was so scared! And my arm hurts real bad.”

“I’m right here, my sweet boy. I’m so sorry I scared you,” Agatha reached out and touched Nicky’s good arm when they positioned her next to him. She’d caught a glimpse of his eyes still wide in fear, his body trembling as he cradled his injured arm against his chest. “I’m not leaving you, baby.”

“You’re bleeding! Ms. Rio said she would take care of you. Are you okay, mama?”

Agatha frowned at the name, but then followed her son’s gaze to the paramedic that had just jumped into the back of the ambulance with them before closing the door.

“We should be at Northwestern in five minutes. How are you doing, Nicky?” The paramedic asked with a kind smile and Nicky sniffled. “Does your arm still hurt? Yeah?” She offered a sympathetic look when he nodded, his eyes still so full of tears. Agatha felt gutted.

“We’ll be at the hospital soon, sweetheart. I’m sure the doctors will make the pain go away really fast.” She tried to comfort her son, but felt so incredibly helpless, being strapped to a gurney, unable to move.

“You bet. And I bet you’ll get a cool cast too, buddy. So all your friends will be able to sign it.”

“Really?”

Nicky’s voice now reflected a bit of curiosity and Agatha was so grateful to this paramedic for keeping him as calm and as comfortable as possible. Agatha’s head was throbbing, and she was starting to feel a bit nauseous from the pain.

When they finally made it to the hospital, she heard the paramedic present their case to the doctor as both gurneys were unloaded from the ambulance. They were wheeled into the hospital quickly and before she knew it, someone was taking her to get a CT scan, while pushing a consent form into her hands so she could sign off on Nicky’s X-ray.

It was only a couple of hours later that she saw the paramedic again. Her best friend Wanda had been called in as her emergency contact, and was staying with Nicky while he got a cast on his arm. The paramedic had been right; he did have a fracture. Now she was bored out of her mind in the infirmary as they wanted to keep her for a few hours for observation. They’d given her something for the pain and it was starting to make her feel a little loopy.

“Hey, I was looking for you. Agatha, right?” The paramedic smiled at her from the doorway, and in her doped up state, Agatha was sure she looked like an angel. “How are you feeling?”

Agatha blinked slowly and offered a small smile. “A bit groggy,” she replied, and touched the bandage that now covered her forehead. “It’s a mild concussion.”

The paramedic grimaced sympathetically before approaching the bed. “Just take it easy for a few days and you’ll be fine in no time,” she smiled and Agatha returned. “What was the verdict there?” She pointed at the bandage.

“Twelve stitches,” Agatha sighed, remembering how she had demanded that a more experienced physician did the procedure. She wasn’t about to let a med student practice on her forehead for god’s sake.

The paramedic whistled, impressed. Agatha laughed tiredly.

“How’s Nicky?” She asked and Agatha nodded at the room next door.

“He broke his arm. He’s over there getting his super cool cast,” she chuckled, and the paramedic smiled. “Thanks for keeping him calm and for distracting him, by the way. He got so excited about his cast that he forgot about the pain.”

“Hey, I’m just glad you guys are okay,” she touched Agatha’s arm for a moment before stepping back. “I should get back. Tell Nicky I said hi.”

“Thank you for everything, Ms. Vidal,” Agatha reached out, holding out her hand. The paramedic grinned before shaking her hand. Her palm was warm and so, so soft. Agatha felt like she was touching a part of heaven.

Dear lord, she really was high as fuck.

“It’s Rio,” the paramedic said, squeezing her hand, and that was when Agatha realized she was still holding it.

Feeling slightly embarrassed, she nodded. “It was nice meeting you, Rio.”

~*~

The doctors let her go with strict orders that she should not be alone for the next twenty four hours. She tried to argue that she was a doctor herself and she knew damn well what she should be doing with a concussion, but the young man who treated her was not impressed and reinforced that she needed someone to wake her up every couple of hours tonight.

With a resigned sigh, Agatha abided by the doctor's orders and agreed to let Wanda stay the night. If she was honest with herself, it would be great to have someone to watch Nicky as well because she felt so tired after hours in the hospital — as a patient, which was not her preference.

“Mama, look at my cast! Do you like it? Will you sign it?” Nicky’s excited voice cut through the fog of her medicated mind, and she managed a smile in her son’s direction. Maybe having Wanda stay with her wouldn’t be so bad.

A few days later, Agatha still felt a bit sore. Nicky had started third grade, and every day he came home with his cast even more populated with drawings and names than the day before. Her ribs were still killing her, but she just braved through it. In her experience, it was probably just bruised and there wasn’t much that could be done.

However, something that kept coming back to the forefront of her mind was the nice paramedic that had taken care of them. Agatha just couldn’t get that smile out of her head, and for the life of her, she just couldn’t figure out why.

Sure, it had been a while since she had actively admired someone like that, but still. As far as she knew, she was straight, thank you very much, despite those involuntary thoughts that popped up in her head from time to time that she wouldn’t even allow herself to entertain.

Still, in the days that followed, Agatha found herself wondering about the paramedic and her beautiful smile. As she got ready for her new semester at Feinberg School of Medicine, she tried to distract herself from her wandering thoughts. After all, she had a long semester ahead of her with new M2 students and new mentees, as the med students started to focus on their main project for the program. She just hoped she would be assigned to students that were actually worth her time this year.

“You know, you’ve been awfully quiet these past few days. Are you sure you’re okay?” Wanda asked her on the Sunday before she would return to work at Northwestern.

“Yeah, why?”

“Just… usually around this time of the year you’re dreading the new students and can’t shut up about it for starters,” her friend chuckled, and she shrugged.

“I don’t know. I guess the whole accident thing messed me up a bit,” Agatha looked toward her backyard where Nicky was playing with Wanda’s twins Billy and Tommy. “The whole ‘life is short’ and all that, you know? I don’t know. I don’t know what I’m saying,” she laughed at herself, shaking her head. “How about you? I heard you’re taking over a class at Feinberg this semester.” Agatha raised an eyebrow and Wanda laughed.

“Lilia has a big mouth,” the redhead rolled her eyes and took a sip of her beer. “Yeah, she offered it to me last week. Behavioral Science for your little M2s.”

“Oh god, does that mean I’m going to have to put up with you at work even more?” Agatha gasped mockingly and Wanda threw a pillow at her.
“Shut up, you love it.”

~*~

“Mama, do you really have to go?” Nicky’s voice was quiet as they drove through the streets of Chicago on their way to her son’s school. Her car had nearly been totaled, but her car insurance had thankfully come through in record time.

Agatha frowned at his tone and searched his eyes through the rearview mirror.

“Go where, baby?”

“To work. Can’t you just stay home? Where you’ll be safe?” His voice was still so small, so quiet, that Agatha felt her heart break and understanding washed over her. This was the first time they were going to spend the whole day apart since the accident.

For the past week, Wanda had taken Nicky to school along with her boys and brought him back home as well, because Agatha was still sorting out her car situation. Nicky obviously felt that the fact that she was home and not behind the wheel kept her safe.

“Oh, honey, don’t worry. I’ll be at Northwestern all day today, but Aunt Wanda will come pick you guys up and you can hang out with Billy and Tommy for a little bit. And then I’ll be home tonight and we’ll have a special dinner. How does that sound?”

Nicky shrugged, a worried line still creasing his forehead. “Okay.”

He was quiet for the next five minutes until Agatha parked in front of his school. It was only when she was helping him out of the car because of his cast that Nicky finally spoke up again.

“Mama? Do you promise you’ll be careful today? Like pinky promise?” He sounded so serious as his gaze traveled to the bandage that covered the stitches on her forehead. Agatha felt her chest tighten.

Crouching down in front of him, she touched his cheek. “I pinky promise, baby,” she offered him her pinky finger and smiled when he hooked his own with hers. “Everything will be fine. And I promise I’m okay. Alright?”

He nodded before throwing his arms around her neck in a tight hug. “I love you, mama.”

Agatha felt her eyes burn with tears. “I love you too, my sweet boy. So much,” she kissed his cheek and stood up. “Now off you go. Learn lots of new things.”

He finally smiled and accepted his backpack when she helped him put it on. Agatha waited until he was inside the building before allowing herself to collapse against the side of the car. Taking a deep breath, she brushed away the lone tear that had escaped.

Everything would be fine. It was a beautiful day, she repeated to herself like a mantra.

~*~

Agatha stopped by the café on campus to get an iced coffee, before making her way up to her office in the Department of Neurology. It had been a few weeks since she had last been here, and she admitted that she’d missed it and was more than ready to dive back in.

Although she did have a private practice, teaching at Northwestern took a big chunk of her time. And as much as she liked to complain about how frustrating some students could be sometimes, she really loved teaching.

Her first lecture was at 10, and she stopped by the ladies room before making her way to the lecture hall. Looking at her reflection in the mirror, she touched the bandage on her forehead, glad to realize that it didn’t hurt as much anymore. The look on Nicky’s eyes as his gaze focused on her injury still made her chest tighten with anguish.

They had been so lucky that day. It could have been so much worse.

As she stepped out of the bathroom, she pulled the strap of her bag higher on her shoulder, as she tried to hold onto her coffee cup and a water bottle with her other hand. Grimacing when it pulled on her bruised ribs, she entered the lecture hall and quickly made her way to the desk in front of a half circle of desks and chairs that went up for at least six levels.

A few students were already seated, some looking excited and a few of them looking slightly terrified, especially when she met their eyes. Grinning inwardly, she rolled her eyes amused, as she knew her reputation preceded her.

At ten o’clock sharp, she stepped in front of the desk to face her new students. Second-year medical students — they weren’t as green and bright-eyed as their first-year colleagues, but she couldn’t help but think that they looked younger and younger every year.

“Good morning,” she started, her voice firm and unwavering. “I’m Dr. Agatha Harkness and this is Neurology-”

A low gasp distracted her and her eyes followed the sound. Agatha felt her heart skip a beat.

Standing at the door, wearing a student white lab coat with a laptop bag on her shoulder, was the paramedic whose smile she couldn’t forget.

Chapter 2

Chapter Summary

Agatha was packing up her notes, her back turned for just a moment. Rio hesitated before standing up, and as she made her way to the door, she couldn’t help but smile to herself.

“Didn’t expect to see you here, Professor,” she paused halfway there, before turning to the woman in front of the desk.

Agatha straightens, her breath hitching for barely a moment. “Didn’t expect you to be in my class.”

Rio grins. “Guess fate has a sense of humor,” she stepped closer, hands in her pockets. “So…” she started casually, tilting her head. “Do I at least get a ‘good job’ for not making a complete fool of myself in front of the entire class?”

Chapter Notes

Thank you so much! I hope you enjoy this one. I’m so excited to be writing again.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It was barely 9:30 in the morning, and Rio Vidal was already exhausted.

A double shift was nothing new—she needed the money, and her student loans weren’t going to pay themselves—but today had been particularly grueling. The last call had turned dangerous when a distressed family member became violent, and all she wanted now was to lie down for thirty minutes and pretend the world didn’t exist.

She had just closed her eyes when the alarm blared through the firehouse again.

Ambulance 12 and Engine 47, motor vehicle collision with injuries reported.

Groaning, Rio pushed herself up, dragging her weary body forward. When she reached their rig, her partner, William Kaplan, held out a steaming cup of coffee.

“Figured you could use a pick-me-up after that shitshow,” he said with a smirk. Rio sighed in relief, taking the cup gratefully before ruffling his hair. “Jesus, get off me, woman!” he batted her hand away with a laugh.

“You’re my hero, Kaplan,” she teased, throwing the keys in his direction. “I’ll even let you drive for this.”

William gasped mockingly, grabbing the keys in midair and holding them close to his heart, but Rio knew he was secretly pleased. He was young, only 23 years old, and had only been working as a paramedic for a few months. And Rio had a strict rule that no rookie was going to take the wheel before she felt they were ready.

“If I’d known that plying you with coffee was the way to your heart, I would’ve bribed you sooner.”

Rio laughed, and took a sip of the hot beverage, before hopping up on the rig on the passenger side. “Don't push it, kid. Shut up and drive.”

Their radio crackled with details: a collision involving a child.

Rio’s stomach tightened. She hated cases with kids. They made her think of her nieces and nephews—the light of her life. If she knew one thing about her future medical career, it was that pediatrics was out of the question. She didn’t have the stomach for it.

When they arrived, only one car remained. It had taken a bad hit to the side, the impact crumpling the metal like paper. Police were already on scene, one of the officers informing them that the other driver had fled.

Rio barely heard him.

Her eyes were already on the backseat, where a small, terrified boy clutched his arm against his chest, his whole body shaking with sobs.

Shit.

Steeling herself, she approached.

“Hey, buddy! My name’s Rio. Can you tell me your name, sweetheart?”

The boy’s brown hair fell into his wet eyes as he whimpered, “Nicky.” Then, his voice broke completely. “My mom won’t wake up! Please help her!”

“Okay, Nicky, we’re going to help you both, alright? Where does it hurt, buddy?” She kept her voice gentle, and watched as he took a shuddering breath.

“My arm hurts really bad,” he tried to keep his voice steady, but it shook anyway. “Mom! Mama, please wake up!”

Rio felt her heart break for this little boy, hearing such anguish in his voice. He couldn’t be older than nine at most.

Stepping aside to let the firefighters pry his door open, she waited until they gave her the go ahead to check on Nicky. Once they cleared it, she went into the backseat to check him over.

“Hey, buddy, look at me,” Rio waited for Nicky to meet her eyes. “We’re going to get you out of here, okay? See my friend over there?” She pointed at her partner, who offered a smile and a wave in his direction. “His name is William, and he’s going to take care of you while we help your mama, okay, sweetheart?”

Nicky blinked up at her, desperate. “You promise?”

Something about the way he trusted her, completely and utterly, made her throat feel tight.

“I promise I’ll do everything in my power to help her,” she replied seriously, and sighed relieved when Nicky finally seemed to accept her promise. “Will, I need a kids C-collar here!” She called out over her shoulder. “Are you hurting anywhere else, Nicky?”

“I don’t know, I don't think so.”

“Okay, let’s get this on you,” she said gently, securing the C-collar on him. “We’re going to get you out now, and then I’m going to help your mom, alright?”

“Okay.” He replied quietly, still sniffling. When they moved him onto the stretcher and accidentally jostled his arm, he let out a painful gasp and started crying again in earnest.

“I’m sorry, buddy, I know it hurts,” she tried to soothe him. “Will is going to take care of you, okay? I’m going to go check on your mom.”

Once Nicky was safely in Kaplan’s care, Rio turned her attention to the driver’s seat, where her firefighter friend Alice was prying the door open.

The woman inside was unconscious, a nasty gash on her forehead bleeding freely, soaking into her dark hair.

When Alice gave the all-clear, Rio leaned in. “Ma’am? Can you hear me?”

For a long moment, nothing. Then, a groggy, painful groan. The woman’s eyelids fluttered open, and Rio forgot how to breathe.

Blue.

Her eyes were the most stunning shade of blue Rio had ever seen.

She shook herself, snapping back into medic mode. “Hey, stay with me,” she murmured, steady but gentle, keeping the woman’s head still. “What’s your name, ma’am?”

The woman blinked sluggishly. “Agatha,” she rasped. Then, panic flooded her face. “My son! Where’s my son?”

“He’s conscious. Looks like an arm fracture, but he’s stable. My colleague is working on him out here. We’re taking you both in,” Rio reassured her. “I got you, don’t worry.”

~*~

She and William dropped mother and son at Northwestern, and before they could return to the firehouse, another call came in. It had been a simple wellness check, but she was grateful for taking a small break for the next couple of hours after that.

It wasn’t until after lunch, during a quick coffee break, that she found herself thinking about them. Something about the fierce love in Agatha’s groggy voice, the way her hand had lingered on Rio’s, the way Nicky had clung to her every word.

She found herself at Northwestern again, after dropping off an elderly gentleman that had suffered an acute MI. Rio had spent the entire drive giving him CPR, and she hoped he made it.

After she handed him off to the doctors, Rio found herself scanning the ER rooms before she even realized what she was doing.

And there she was. Agatha lay in a hospital bed, looking sleepy and just a little adorable. Rio hesitated for half a second before walking into her room.

~*~

Her conversation with Agatha had been entertaining, and she was intrigued when the woman held onto her hand, thumb brushing against her skin absentmindedly, it seemed. Her smile combined with her eyes made her insides turn to goo, and she figured she needed to get the hell out of there. The woman was a friggin’ patient and clearly recovering from a head injury.

But just as she said goodbye, she spotted Nicky in the room next door, and just knew she had to at least go say hi. The boy had struck a chord deep in her heart, and she couldn’t quite figure out why.

A redheaded woman was with him, obviously trying to distract him from the pain and the prospect of moving his arm to get his cast.

“Knock, knock,” Rio said playfully, and smiled when Nicky’s eyes lit up when he saw her.

“Ms. Rio! Aunt Wanda, that’s the paramedic lady I was telling you about. She saved me and Mama!” Nicky told the redhead excitedly, and Rio couldn’t help but chuckle. “She was like a superhero!”

“Well, I don’t know about that. But I’m glad to see you’re doing better, buddy. And you’re going to get a super cool cast, huh? Your mom told me all about it,” she approached his bed and pointed at the orthopedic technician preparing his cast on the other side of the room. “What’s up, Johnny? You gonna take care of my boy Nicky here?”

“Only the best for you and yours, Vidal,” the older man grinned at her.

Rio shook her head with a laugh, finally looking at the redhead, who was regarding her with a curious expression. “Hi, I’m Rio Vidal.”

“Oh, I’ve heard all about you from this young man here. It’s nice to meet you. I’m Wanda, Agatha’s friend,” she offered her hand for her to shake, and Rio couldn’t help but think about the way Agatha’s touch had lingered just a few minutes ago. “Thanks for taking care of them.”

“Oh, just doing my job. I’m glad they’re okay,” Rio shook her hand, and stepped away for Johnny to start working on Nicky’s cast.

She watched as Nicky grimaced at the tiniest movement in his arm, tears rolling down his cheeks silently, and figured the least she could do was try to distract him by helping him select the color of his cast.

She crouched down beside his gurney, a warm smile on her face. “Alright, buddy, this is a big decision. We have blue, red, green, and even glow-in-the-dark. But be warned, the glow-in-the-dark one? It makes you an official nighttime superhero. You might start fighting crime in your sleep,” she whispered conspiratorially.

Nicky, still sniffling but intrigued, wiped at his eyes. “Superheroes don’t cry, right?” he asked, his voice wavering, and she felt her chest tighten.

“Oh, buddy, even superheroes cry. But you know what they do after? They get back up, just like you’re doing,” she offered him a gentle smile. “So what’s it going to be?

“Glow-in-the-dark! So I can be a nighttime superhero,” Nicky replied immediately, his tears all but forgotten.

“Excellent choice, sir. I hope you use your powers wisely,” she said, making a show of picking up his selected color. “As you well know, with great power…”

“Comes great responsibility, I know,” Nicky completed with a solemn tone to his voice, making Rio chuckle.

When she left the room a few minutes later, her heart felt so much lighter, and she found the strength to keep going about her never ending shift.

~*~

A week later, Rio had a shift straight out of the seventh circle of hell. It had been a long night. Rio barely remembered her last meal, only that it had been too rushed to be satisfying. She hadn’t even had a proper break during her overnight shift—just one call after another, a steady stream of chaos.

By the time she finally got some sleep, she could only manage two hours, her body too tired to stay still for long. But there she was, Making her way to the lecture hall for her very first neurology class of the semester. Her coffee was already half-gone, and she wasn’t sure if it was helping or just adding to the jitteriness settling under her skin. Either way, she was late.

She pushed the door open quietly, hoping she wouldn’t interrupt, but the second it creaked on its hinges, the entire class turned to look at her.

“Ah, perfect timing,” came the voice at the front of the room, sending an unexpected wave of recognition crashing through her. It was Agatha Harkness, standing tall and composed in front of the class, her sharp eyes narrowing slightly as they met Rio’s gaze. The professor—legendary in the department, a neurosurgeon and expert in the field of neurology. Rio’s heart stuttered for a second before she reminded herself to breathe. Agatha, the woman she had saved a week ago, was her professor now. How in the world did that even happen?

The professor’s lips curled up in what seemed like a controlled, polite smile as she adjusted the papers in front of her. “Well, since we have a latecomer, I’ll start again with a quick introduction. My name is Dr. Harkness, and this course is an introduction to neurology, focusing on neuroanatomy, the principles of neurological assessment, and how we approach cases from both a clinical and research perspective.”

Rio slipped into a seat near the back, trying to make herself as small as possible. The last thing she wanted was to draw attention in front of a room full of future doctors, especially after walking in late. But as Agatha began to speak again, outlining the expectations for the class, Rio couldn’t help but notice the bandage on her forehead. Agatha had been hurt in the accident… She’d remembered the woman’s soft smile and the grip of her hand from when Rio had helped her out of that wreck, but seeing her now, poised and commanding in front of the class, was surreal.

After a few moments of Agatha running through the course structure, she stopped abruptly and turned toward the board, writing something down. It wasn’t long before Agatha’s eyes flicked over to her.

“Since we’re speaking about brainstem function today, let’s test some of your knowledge. Who can explain the importance of assessing the brainstem in trauma cases, and why it’s critical for intervention?” She paused, her gaze landing on Rio. “You—yes, you in the back. What do you think?”

Rio froze. She hadn’t expected to be called on, especially not after the way they’d left things between them. She had barely processed the class’s attention settling on her, let alone the weight of being tested in front of Agatha again, with the full weight of her now professor’s gaze upon her.

“Well…” Rio cleared her throat, trying to shake the lingering fuzziness from her head. “I mean, the brainstem is the control center for basic life functions, right? If there’s trauma to the brainstem, it could affect breathing, heart rate, even consciousness. If you don’t assess it right away, it could lead to brain death, or you know, irreversible damage.” She rubbed a hand over her face, trying to focus through the tiredness. “So yeah, it’s basically a life-or-death situation if you don’t handle it properly. And you really want to make sure you’re getting the right information early on. You don’t want to miss anything. Especially in trauma cases.”

Agatha’s lips quirked, but she held her professionalism tight. “Well, that’s a solid answer. If we can start to recognize the signs of brain stem injury in trauma, we can make a plan that’s more effective and tailored to the patient’s condition.” She paused for a moment, as if weighing her next words, before giving Rio a nod.

Rio felt a flicker of warmth rush through her, but she quickly turned her attention back to her notebook, trying not to feel too much of a connection to those eyes that were still on her.

The rest of the lecture continued, Agatha diving into more specifics about brainstem functions and how they related to various kinds of trauma. Rio did her best to stay awake, the exhaustion from her overnight shift making it a challenge to keep up. She jotted down notes, but it was hard to focus, especially with Agatha at the front of the room, making the subject seem so effortless. Rio couldn’t help but admire how she commanded the room despite the faint, lingering vulnerability that was still visible around her bandaged forehead.

By the end of class, Rio found herself lingering, uncertain of what to do next. She hadn’t expected to feel this… drawn to Agatha. She hadn’t expected the rush of adrenaline that came with being in the same space as her, or the unexpected longing that had surfaced in her chest.

Agatha was packing up her notes, her back turned for just a moment. Rio hesitated before standing up, and as she made her way to the door, she couldn’t help but smile to herself.

“Didn’t expect to see you here, Professor,” she paused halfway there, before turning to the woman in front of the desk.

Agatha straightens, her breath hitching for barely a moment. “Didn’t expect you to be in my class.”
Rio grins. “Guess fate has a sense of humor,” she stepped closer, hands in her pockets. “So…” she started casually, tilting her head. “Do I at least get a ‘good job’ for not making a complete fool of myself in front of the entire class?”

Agatha didn’t even look up. “I expect my students to be competent, Ms. Vidal. I don’t hand out praise for meeting the bare minimum.”

Rio huffed a quiet laugh. “Damn. Tough crowd.”

Finally, finally, Agatha looked at her.

And there it was again. That flicker of something unreadable behind her carefully constructed walls.

“In this room,” Agatha said, voice steady but not quite as cold as before, “you’re just another student.”

A warning, not a statement.

Rio caught the slight tension in Agatha’s jaw, the way her fingers curled a little tighter around her notebook.

There was another long pause, and Rio felt the awkwardness settle in. She shifted her weight from one foot to the other before speaking again. “So, how’s Nicky doing?” she asked, her voice gentler now, as if she wasn’t sure how to phrase the question.

The mention of Nicky caught Agatha off-guard. She hadn’t expected Rio to ask. It took a second for her to compose herself before responding, her voice tinged with affection. “He’s… adjusting. It was hard for him, you know. But he’s strong. He’s getting better each day.”

A flicker of emotion crossed Agatha’s face before she caught herself, her professional demeanor quickly returning. “Thank you for asking, though. He means the world to me.”

Rio nodded thoughtfully. “I get it,” she said quietly. “I mean, I know what it’s like to want to protect someone. It’s tough.”

Agatha gave her a small, appreciative smile, though her eyes seemed distant for a moment. “Yes, it is. But that’s why we do what we do, isn’t it?” she said, her voice firm again. “To make sure others don’t have to experience what we’ve gone through.”

Rio’s lips curved into a soft smile, the connection between them lingering a little longer than either of them expected. “Yeah,” she said quietly. “That’s the goal.”

With that, she gave Agatha one last look, unsure whether she’d said too much or not enough. Agatha’s gaze lingered on her for just a beat longer before she cleared her throat, her professional demeanor settling back in.

“See you next week, Ms. Vidal,” Agatha said briskly, turning to gather her papers. “Preferably on time.”

Rio gave her a nod, walking toward the door.“Wouldn’t miss it for the world. See you, Professor.”

As she left the lecture hall, Rio couldn’t shake the feeling that there was more to the professor than she’d expected. Agatha had the reputation to be so composed, so serious and inflexible, but today—just for a moment—there had been something else there. It was a blink and you miss it moment. But it was definitely there.

Something soft.

Chapter End Notes

Thoughts? Comments are good for the soul.

Chapter 3

“Ms. Rio!” Nicky practically jumped out of his seat, waving excitedly. “I’m so happy to see you!”

Chapter Notes

You guys are the best! Thank you so much for taking the time to read, comment and/or leave kudos. It means the world to me.

Agatha sat at her desk, the faint rustle of papers the only sound in the stillness of her office. Her bandage, now more of a quiet reminder than anything else, itched against her forehead, but she barely noticed it. Her thoughts were consumed by the strange pull she felt toward Rio Vidal.

The encounter had been unexpected, to say the least. Agatha hadn’t been prepared to see Rio again, and certainly not like this—standing in front of her as her med student. The woman who had comforted her in the aftermath of the accident, who had held her hand with that effortless care, someone whose smile she hadn’t been able to forget for the past week, was now someone she was supposed to teach. Someone she had to maintain a professional distance from.

Agatha shook her head at herself. This was ridiculous. She had always prided herself on her professionalism, on being able to separate her personal life from her work. She had never allowed herself to get tangled up in anything that would jeopardize her career, her reputation, or the stability she’d worked so hard to create.

And yet, here she was, feeling things she couldn’t explain. At first, she chalked it up to the stress of the accident and the vulnerability she’d felt in the hospital. But now, seeing Rio again, she felt it again. The way her easy grin made her heart flutter. She didn’t quite understand what was happening, but one thing's for certain: it definitely rattled her.

Whatever this strange pull towards the paramedic was, it made her uncomfortable. She wasn’t used to feeling like this. It was uncharted territory. Growing up, she had been taught to repress anything that didn’t align with the strict expectations placed on her. She’d spent her entire life suppressing any inklings that weren’t part of her professional identity, or part of the expectations her mother had placed upon her. She wasn’t supposed to be attracted to women. At least, that’s what her Evanora Harkness had drilled into her head from a very early age.

But there was something about Rio—her confidence, her compassion, and from what she’d seen today, a hint of cheeky humor—that made Agatha question everything she’d told herself. It was confusing, disorienting, and, in a weird way, kind of exhilarating. But it was also terrifying.

Agatha had always been a woman of precision. She’d built her life on neatly constructed foundations: lectures prepared weeks in advance, research that left no room for uncertainty. She could not let a student affect her like that, regardless of what had happened a week before.

Shaking herself out of it, she told herself to get her shit together. She had a job to do. She had to keep things professional. She had to stay focused on her class, on her work.

This thing — whatever it was with Rio Vidal — was nothing.

~*~

A few days after Agatha’s first lecture, she found herself walking across the university campus with Nicky in tow. It was Friday, and the weight of the week had already started to settle on her shoulders, but she couldn’t afford to slow down. Nicky was bouncing beside her, his excitement from school not quite worn off yet. Agatha had picked him up and had to bring him back to campus so she could finish her office hours.

Before they made it to her office on the third floor, Agatha thought she’d buy Nicky a hot chocolate and a pastry to tide him over until they got home. They walked into the campus café, and there was Wanda, already sitting at a table near the window, her bright red hair standing out against the backdrop of students moving around. Wanda smiled at them both and gestured to the empty seats across from her.

“Got the little troublemaker in tow, I see,” Wanda teased, as Nicky immediately slid into the seat beside her.

Nicky grinned, his energy practically radiating off him. “I’m no troublemaker. I’m a superhero, remember? Ms. Rio said so! With my glow-in-the-dark cast!” He showed her his fully signed and drawn on cast proudly.

Agatha gave Wanda a slight, tight smile as she sat down beside her, still processing Nicky’s words. The mention of Rio, so casually and full of admiration, had Agatha feeling something unfamiliar stir inside her.

Wanda laughed and ruffled his hair. “Oh, I apologize, Mr. Superhero. My mistake,” she winked at him before turning to Agatha. “The paramedic seems to have made quite the impression, huh?”

Before Agatha could respond, the door to the café opened, and in walked none other than Rio Vidal.

She didn’t immediately notice Agatha, her focus on the phone in her hands, but when Nicky caught sight of her, his excitement burst through the door.

“Ms. Rio!” Nicky practically jumped out of his seat, waving excitedly. “I’m so happy to see you!”

Rio’s gaze immediately snapped up, and her face broke into a grin when she saw the boy, already half out of his seat. 

“Hey, Nicky! Look at you—glow-in-the-dark cast and all!” She winked at him, moving over to their table with her usual confident but easygoing air. “Love the artwork there, buddy.”

Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, something stirring within her at the sight of Rio smiling at Nicky. 

Wanda’s eyes darted between Agatha and Rio, a curious look in her eyes. Agatha tried her best to keep a professional distance, but the tension was palpable. Rio’s presence in the room shifted the air somehow, and Agatha wasn’t quite sure what to do with it.

Rio finally turned her attention to Agatha, her grin faltering slightly as their eyes met. It was brief, but Agatha saw the flicker of recognition—of something unspoken passing between them.

“Dr. Harkness,” Rio said, her voice casual, but there was an undertone of something more. “Didn’t expect to run into you here.”

Agatha cleared her throat, trying to find her composure again. “I brought Nicky for a little coffee break. Trying to make up for all the hours he’ll be stuck in the office with me.” She couldn’t help but glance at Rio, trying to gauge the energy between them.

“Sounds like a busy day,” Rio said with a small, almost teasing smile. 

“You have no idea,” Agatha replied, a little too quickly. She felt a rush of heat in her chest, but masked it with a light laugh.

“What are you doing here, Ms. Rio? Did you come to save someone?” Nicky jumped into the conversation, his eyes looking up at Rio adoringly.

Rio smiled at him, ruffling his hair. Agatha felt her heart warm. “Nah, today I’m just a student here. Did you know that your mom here is my professor?” She added conspiratorially and Nicky’s eyes widened, turning to his mom for confirmation. Agatha nodded, an amused smile pulling the corner of her lips up.

“Whoa, for real? You’re going to be a doctor too? Mama says she helps people become doctors,” his voice was so full of wonder and pride that Agatha couldn’t help but feel that tug of love for her child in her chest.

“Yup, I’m in my second year. Still got two more years to go.”

“That’s awesome, Ms. Rio. So you’ll get to be a superhero twice over! Saving lives in two different ways. Mama, that’s what I wanna do when I grow up!”

“Yeah? You’re gonna be a double hero, buddy?” Rio teased, and Nicky nodded eagerly. 

Wanda watched the exchange with an amused glint in her eye. Nicky, oblivious to the subtle undercurrent of tension, was clearly delighted to see Rio.

“Wanna sit with us, Rio?” Nicky asked excited, the invitation simple and innocent, yet making the room feel somehow smaller. Agatha couldn’t help but notice how comfortable Rio seemed in Nicky’s presence. It made her heart ache, a warmth spreading through her chest that she wasn’t sure how to process.

Rio locked eyes with Agatha, a questioning look in her eyes. When Agatha gave her a subtle nod, Rio turned to Nicky and nodded with a grin. “Sure. Let me just go get my coffee and I’ll be right back.”

As soon as Rio left, Wanda leaned in just slightly, catching Agatha’s eye. “So,” she said, her voice a low hum, “This is an interesting development.”

Agatha’s lips parted, but she swallowed hard, unsure of how to respond. Instead, she turned her focus back on Rio, trying to find her bearings, even as her mind spun with all the possibilities she didn’t want to consider.

 

~*~

As Rio slid into the seat next to her, Agatha couldn’t help but notice the warmth in the air between them. Her pulse quickened, though she masked it with a polite smile. Rio’s presence felt different now— familiar, yet a reminder of their first meeting, when Agatha had been a patient. But now, seeing her as a fellow academic and with Nicky so excited to see her again, Agatha felt a slight crack in her usual composure.

Nicky, who hadn’t stopped smiling since Rio arrived, leaned forward eagerly. “Ms. Rio, can you come to my school for a show-and-tell?” he asked, practically bouncing in his seat. “You can tell everyone how you save people, and then you can teach us how to be paramedics too.”

Rio laughed softly, her eyes twinkling. “I’d love to, kiddo. But I don’t think they’ll let me make everyone pretend they’re paramedics. You guys might be too busy saving lives.”

Nicky grinned, utterly undeterred. “We could do it! You could teach us, and we’d be like superheroes too! Just like you!”

Rio gave him a playful side-eye. “Maybe we’ll work on our superhero training at a later date,” she said, ruffling his hair before looking over at Wanda. “So, you must be Wanda, right? I think I remember you from the hospital…?”

Wanda’s smile was wide and warm, clearly enjoying the moment. “Yeah, I’m Wanda Maximoff. Nice to finally meet you properly.” She chuckled lightly. “I’m a professor here too. How’s your first week at school been?”

“I think I’ve survived,” Rio replied with a grin. “It’s been a bit of an adjustment being back, but I’m getting the hang of it. I think I have you for Behavioral Science tomorrow, right?”

Wanda nodded. “That’s right. I hope you’ll find it interesting.”

Rio’s eyes softened for a second as she processed the information. “I’m looking forward to it. The program here is so good. I heard fantastic things about it before I started last year, but it really surpassed my expectations,” Rio took a sip of her coffee, before continuing. “Dr. Harkness’ class, for example, was just so incredible, honestly. I was really looking forward to neurology, but I admit I was a little intimidated by her reputation and all that. But she definitely knows how to captivate a room.”

Agatha looked up at the unexpected praise, and for a moment, there was a brief, shy connection between them—Rio’s gaze holding just a little longer than normal. She knew how much her reputation had preceded her, but hearing Rio speak so genuinely made her feel a flush of pride she didn’t always allow herself.

“I think that’s the goal,” Agatha said, trying to keep her voice even, but her smile softened at Rio’s sincerity. “I want to make the material accessible while still keeping it challenging. But it’s good to hear you liked the class.”

“Liked it?” Rio chuckled. “I think I could’ve stayed all afternoon, even though I was tired as hell. It’s rare to find a lecture that can keep me hooked like that, especially with everything else I have going on.”

“Sounds like you’re pretty busy,” Wanda remarked. “The life of a med student and paramedic must be exhausting.”

Rio smiled faintly, though her eyes betrayed a trace of fatigue. “It’s a balancing act, for sure. But I’ve always liked a good challenge.”

Before the conversation could continue, Rio stood up, gathering her things. “I'm so sorry to cut this short, but I’ve got to get to class. It was really nice to meet you properly, Professor Maximoff. And it was so great seeing you again, Nicky. Glad to hear your superhero powers are doing great,” she winked at him, eliciting a giggle. “Dr. Harkness, I’ll see you on Monday.”

“Bye, Rio,” Nicky called out, still grinning from ear to ear. Agatha gave her a nod, polite and professional, though she couldn’t quite hide the trace of softness in her gaze as Rio walked away.

Not even five minutes passed before Nicky asked to go choose one of the pastries. Once he was out of earshot, Wanda turned to Agatha, an amused glint in her eye. “What the hell was that?”

Agatha froze, her hand pausing in mid-air as she reached for her coffee cup. “What do you mean?” she asked, trying to keep her voice casual.

Wanda raised an eyebrow. “Come on, Agatha. I’m not blind. You looked at her a little differently just now. And when she was talking about you? That wasn’t just about your lecture. There’s something there.”

Agatha set her coffee down a little too firmly, her heart racing as she tried to process what Wanda was implying. “No,” she said quickly. “There’s nothing there. She’s a student and… she happened to be the paramedic that took care of me and Nicky. And now I’m just her professor. That’s it.”

Wanda’s smile widened. “Sure, I’m sure you’re just her professor. But you can’t deny there’s a bit of… I don’t know… spark between you two. And don’t think I didn’t notice the way you looked at her.”

Agatha felt the heat rising to her cheeks. “It’s not like that,” she muttered, even though she wasn’t entirely sure that was true.

Wanda leaned back in her chair, studying Agatha with a soft, knowing smile. “Whatever you say, Agatha. But if there is something there, I just want you to know that I’m here if you need to talk. No pressure. Just… don’t bottle it all up.”

“I’m fine,” Agatha said a little too quickly, pushing her coffee cup aside. “We should finish our coffee and head back to work.”

Wanda just shrugged, giving Agatha a knowing glance before taking another sip of her drink. “I’m here if you need me. That’s all I’m saying.”

As they left the café and walked back toward campus, Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that Wanda had seen something she wasn’t ready to confront. But every time her thoughts returned to Rio, her chest tightened with something that felt both foreign and familiar—something she wasn’t prepared to explore just yet.

~*~

Agatha rarely got nervous before a lecture. She had been doing this for years—long enough to know exactly how to command a room, how to keep her students engaged, how to challenge them without discouraging them.

But as she stood at the front of the lecture hall today, marker in hand, she was acutely aware of Rio Vidal sitting in the crowd. It had been a few weeks since classes started, and September was morphing into October fast. One would think that this weird hyper fixation with Rio Vidal would’ve passed by now.

She wished she was that lucky.

It was frustrating, really, how much Agatha noticed her now.

She scanned the room as she spoke, careful not to linger too long on any one student, but her gaze still caught on Rio more than once. The younger woman looked more awake today, more put together, though there was still a hint of exhaustion in the way she rubbed her thumb absently along the side of her notebook.

Agatha forced herself to refocus.

She moved through the first half of the lecture efficiently, walking the class through the hippocampus and its role in memory formation. When she reached a natural pause, she set her marker down and turned fully to the room.

“For those of you considering specializing in neurology,” she said, “or for those who want a deeper understanding of the field, I’ll be taking on a small number of mentees for your main research project.”

That got their attention.

She continued, keeping her tone measured, professional. “Those accepted will work closely with me to refine their focus, develop their methods, and—should their work be of a high enough caliber—submit for potential publication.”

A low murmur spread through the hall. Some students perked up, whispering to each other, already considering their options.

Agatha knew what she would see before she even glanced in Rio’s direction.

The moment she did, though, it nearly knocked the breath from her chest.

Rio had straightened in her seat, eyes bright with something sharp and eager. There was no hesitation in her expression—just pure, unfiltered determination.

It was the most awake Agatha had ever seen her look, with laser focus determination.

She swallowed.

“Those interested,” she continued, keeping her voice even, “should submit a brief proposal outlining their intended focus by the end of the week.”

She forced herself to look away, to shift her attention back to the broader class.

But that moment stuck with her.

She had expected some interest. She had expected students to recognize the value of the opportunity.

She had not expected Rio Vidal to look at her like that—with something bordering on reverence. Like she had just handed her a precious gift.

And that was dangerous.

Because if she let herself think about it too much, she might have to admit how much she liked it.

As soon as class ended, the usual buzz of conversation filled the lecture hall. Agatha stayed by the desk, pretending to organize her notes as students filtered out, some lingering to chat with classmates, others already deep in discussion about potential research topics.

She knew she should leave—head back to her office, put some distance between herself and Rio as fast as humanly possible..

But then, as she reached for her bag, a voice stopped her.

“Professor Harkness.”

She didn’t have to look up to know who it was.

She took a breath before meeting Rio’s gaze.

Up close, the younger woman’s enthusiasm was even more apparent. She had that same sharp focus from earlier, but now, with everyone else leaving, it felt… more direct.

“I wanted to ask about the mentorship,” Rio said, shifting her bag onto her shoulder. “You mentioned proposals—I assume you’re looking for something structured? Literature review, methodology, that kind of thing?”

Agatha nodded. “Yes. It doesn’t have to be exhaustive, but I want to see that you’ve given real thought to your research question and how you intend to approach it.”

Rio nodded, then hesitated for a beat before saying, “I want to focus on Alzheimer’s.”

That made Agatha pause.

It wasn’t an unusual choice. Neurodegenerative diseases were a major area of study, and plenty of students were drawn to them. But something in the way Rio said it—quiet, deliberate—told Agatha there was something personal behind it.

She studied her for a moment. “That’s a broad topic. You’ll need to narrow your focus.”

“I know.” Rio exhaled, shifting her weight slightly. “I was thinking about early-onset cases. Genetic predisposition, potential interventions. My grandmother had it. She was diagnosed when I was a teenager, and it progressed fast.” Her voice didn’t waver, but there was something underneath it—something steady, but undeniably raw. “It’s why I wanted to go into medicine in the first place.”

Agatha hadn’t expected that.

She wasn’t sure what she had expected, but this—Rio speaking with such quiet conviction—unnerved her.

Not in a bad way.

Just in a way she didn’t quite know what to do with.

She kept her expression neutral. “That’s a compelling reason to pursue it.”

Rio gave a small, self-conscious smile. “I figured it’d be a good way to stay motivated.”

Agatha considered her for a moment.

The responsible thing to do would be to treat this as she would with any student. To offer encouragement, set expectations, and send her on her way.

But she was still thinking about the way Rio had looked at her earlier.

And that was a problem.

She cleared her throat. “If you’re serious about this, I’ll expect a strong proposal.”

Rio’s smile widened. “Wouldn’t dream of turning in anything less.”

Agatha should have dismissed her then. Let the conversation end, keep things professional.

But she saw the way Rio’s gaze flickered—just for a second—to her forehead, where the faint line of a scar remained, where the stitches had been a few weeks before.

Rio hesitated. “How’s your head?”

Agatha stiffened, surprised by the question. “It’s fine.”

Rio didn’t look convinced. “I mean, I did pull you out of a car wreck. I feel like I get to ask.”

Agatha exhaled through her nose. “I appreciate the concern, but I assure you, I’m quite recovered.”

Rio studied her for a beat longer, then gave a small, knowing smile.

“If you say so, Professor. I’m glad to hear that.”

There was something in her tone—something that made Agatha’s pulse tick up, just slightly. But before she could figure out what to do with it, Rio was already turning toward the door.

“Oh—and say hi to Nicky for me.”

And then she was gone.

Agatha stood there for a long moment, staring at the empty doorway.

This was going to be a problem.

 

 

Chapter 4

Chapter Summary

Alice grinned, unbothered by Rio’s sudden discomfort. “You’re nervous because it’s not just about the research. You like her, don’t you?”
Rio’s stomach flipped at the question, and she quickly deflected with a forced chuckle. “I just want to get the research done, okay? Can we talk about something else?”

Chapter Notes

Thank you so much for the support!

Fair warning, the scientific stuff is courtesy of Google and I hope it makes sense.

A few days had passed since that conversation after Agatha’s class, and Rio had been busier than ever. Between her shifts, classes, and trying to get a head start on her research proposal, she barely had time to breathe. But if she was being honest with herself, the moments she did have to breathe? She spent them thinking about a certain professor with piercing blue eyes and an unreadable expression.

Which was ridiculous.

She blamed it on the exhaustion.

Or the fact that she’d seen Agatha—Dr. Harkness—at her most vulnerable, something most people probably never had. That had to be it. The memory of holding her hand in the hospital, reassuring her that Nicky was okay, wasn’t something she could just forget.

And yet, despite all her rationalizing, there was something about Agatha that just kept pulling her in, kept her intrigued, and it was something she couldn’t quite define.

But Rio didn’t have time to dwell on that right now.

She walked into the lecture hall a few minutes early, sipping on what was probably her third coffee of the day, and scanned the empty room for a decent seat. She preferred sitting toward the middle—not too close to the front where professors could single you out, but not too far in the back where she might be tempted to zone out.

As soon as she put her things down on her desk, her gaze traveled toward the front of the room, where Agatha was setting up her laptop and notes, apparently having just walked in. She looked as put-together as ever, clad in another navy blue blazer, but Rio wasn’t fooled. She could see the subtle signs of exhaustion as Agatha busied herself turning on her laptop. The faint lines around her eyes, the way she rolled her shoulder slightly as if trying to shake off tension.

She wondered if she’d been getting enough sleep.

Before she could stop herself, Rio found her feet moving.

“What, no dramatic entrance today?” She said casually as soon as she approached the front of the lecture hall.

Agatha’s head snapped up at the sound of her voice, and for just a second, something flickered in her expression before she schooled it back into neutrality.

“Ms. Vidal,” she greeted smoothly, straightening. “You’re early. That’s surprising.”

Rio smirked, settling in one of the chairs at the front row. “Guess I’m just full of surprises.”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “How fortunate for us all.”

Rio chuckled, taking another sip of coffee before nodding toward Agatha’s laptop. “You ready to convince us all to go into neurology today?”

Agatha hummed, crossing her arms, but when she spoke, her tone carried a hint of teasing. “If you still require convincing, perhaps you’re in the wrong place.”

“Touché.” Rio tilted her head. “For the record, I don’t need convincing. Neurology’s my main interest. Always has been.”

That, at least, seemed to catch Agatha’s attention. “Is that so?”

“Yeah,” Rio nodded, stretching her legs out a bit. “Like I said last week, you know? Been wanting to focus my research on Alzheimer’s. My grandmother had early-onset. It was really bad. So it’s, uh… it’s a personal thing. You know?”

Agatha studied her for a moment, something shifting in her expression—something Rio couldn’t quite place. Then, with a hint of a smile, she said, “A noble pursuit.”

It was such a simple response, but something about the way she said it made Rio feel seen. Like finally someone was willing to listen to her about this.

Before she could think too hard about that, Agatha’s gaze flicked back to the podium, and her professional demeanor took over once more.

“I actually had a chance to read your proposal,” Agatha said casually after a beat, her tone betraying a slight edge of approval. “Impressive work. You’ve clearly put a lot of thought into it.”

Rio blinked, surprised, a flush creeping up her neck. “Oh, uh—thanks. Yeah, I submitted it early last week.” She paused, hoping her voice didn’t sound as nervous as it felt. “I figured I should get ahead of it, you know, since it’s a topic I’m passionate about.”

Agatha gave her a small nod. “Well, it shows. Alzheimer’s research is vital, especially with the rising prevalence of early-onset cases. It’s always good to see more students interested in investigating it further.”

Rio smiled, but she didn’t trust herself to say much more. Something about Agatha’s approval—soft as it was—sent a strange warmth through her. But she pushed it down. She didn’t need to read too much into it.

Agatha’s eyes momentarily flicked to the side, and Rio noticed her rubbing the back of her neck before letting out a sigh. Now that she was sitting in front of her, Rio could see her tiredness even more pronounced.

Without thinking, she asked, “Are you okay?”

Agatha looked at her, eyebrows slightly raised. For a moment, there was a flicker of hesitation before Agatha let out a soft sigh, a subtle sign of vulnerability slipping through her professional façade.

“Yeah,” Agatha said, but her voice held an edge of weariness that hadn’t been there before. “Nicky came down with a fever last night. Nothing serious, just a cold, but I stayed up with him most of the night,” She rubbed her temple, as if trying to stave off a headache. “Being a single parent sometimes means not getting the luxury of sleep.”

Rio nodded, feeling a rush of empathy. She remembered how worried Agatha had been the day of the accident. She’d seen the protective way she looked at Nicky, how much she cared for him.

“I hope he feels better soon,” Rio said, her voice gentle. “You’re doing an incredible job with him.”

Agatha’s lips curved into a faint, appreciative smile. “Thank you. I try.”

Before the moment could linger, the rest of the students started filling in, and Agatha quickly transitioned back into her professor mode. The professional wall went up again, but Rio couldn’t help but notice the slight fatigue in her posture.

As the class went on, Rio found it harder to focus. Her thoughts kept wandering to the conversation they’d just had, the rare glimpse of vulnerability she’d seen in Agatha. It was hard to ignore the pull she felt toward her, even harder to ignore the fact that Agatha had impressed her not just with her work but with the little things—like the way she cared for her son, or the way she handled herself in the face of exhaustion.

But for now, she pushed it all aside. They both had a lot of work to do.

~*~

Rio was exhausted, but the adrenaline from the day’s calls kept her moving. It had been a busy shift — emergency calls back to back, with barely any time to eat. The moment she got a break, she plopped down onto the worn leather couch in the firehouse’s break room, kicking off her boots and letting out a long sigh.

Alice Wu, her best friend and a firefighter, grabbed the spot beside her, not missing the chance to snatch the bag of chips Rio had left half-open on the coffee table.

“You look like you’re about to collapse,” Alice said, giving Rio a sideways glance.

“Gee, thanks, friend.” Rio shot her a tired smirk. “I’ve got two hours of sleep in me. I’m fine.”

“Riiiight. You’ve been working this hard for how many days in a row now?” Alice asked, tossing a chip into her mouth.

“Too many,” Rio mumbled, closing her eyes for a moment. “But I don’t mind. Keeps me busy. Gives me less time to think.”

Alice raised an eyebrow, clearly picking up on the subtext. “Ah, so it’s not just the calls that have your brain running in overdrive?”

Rio groaned, rolling her eyes. “I don’t even want to talk about it.”

“Oh, we’re definitely talking about it,” Alice teased. “Something’s got you distracted. You’ve been acting weird ever since you met your hot professor, Dr. Harkness. What’s going on there?”

Rio sighed heavily, dropping her head back against the couch. “I don’t know. I’ve been trying to focus on my project and get things together, but… there’s this weird feeling. I can’t shake it. I just want to know if she’ll even take me on as a mentee.”

Alice leaned forward, eyes narrowing in on Rio. “Wait. You’re still hung up on whether she’s going to mentor you?”

“Yeah, I mean, the list hasn’t come out yet,” Rio said, running a hand through her hair. “And you know, it’s been a couple of weeks already. I don’t know if she’ll even choose me. What if I’m not what she’s looking for?”

Alice frowned slightly, though her voice stayed teasing. “You’re overthinking this. You’ve already shown her your research proposal, right? And I’m pretty sure she’s impressed. She’d be lucky to have you as a mentee.”

Rio gave her a skeptical look. “You think so?”

“Definitely,” Alice said, giving her a firm nod. “I’ve heard things about this Dr. Harkness from Jen, you know. She was in your professor’s class a couple of years ago, and she says Dr. Harkness usually goes for students that show real drive and passion about their research. And I’m pretty sure you’ve shown her how much you want this.”

“I hope so,” Rio muttered, a little self-conscious. “I mean, she’s Agatha fucking Harkness. Everyone knows how legendary she is. I’m just… me.”

“You’re you for a reason,” Alice said with a grin. “And if you get chosen, it’ll be because she sees something in you. Trust me. You’re gonna crush it.”

Rio shrugged, still not entirely convinced, but Alice’s words did make her feel a little better.

“Yeah, I don’t know,” she let out a breath, shaking her arms as if she could shake these feelings out of her. “I’m nervous. I just want to know if she’ll take me on. But I also don’t want to push it and make things weird.”

Alice raised an eyebrow. “Weird how?”

Rio groaned, sinking lower into the couch. “I don’t know, okay? I’m nervous. I can’t just casually ask her about it. It’ll make it way too obvious.”

Alice leaned back with a knowing look. “And there it is. You’re not just worried about the mentee thing, are you?”

Rio froze. “What?”

Alice grinned, unbothered by Rio’s sudden discomfort. “You’re nervous because it’s not just about the research. You like her, don’t you?”

Rio’s stomach flipped at the question, and she quickly deflected with a forced chuckle. “I just want to get the research done, okay? Can we talk about something else?”

But Alice wasn’t backing down. “Come on, Rio. I’ve known you forever. You can’t hide shit from me. You’re into her. You’ve got that look on your face, and every time you mention Dr. Harkness, your voice does this weird thing.”

Rio’s face flushed, and she buried her face in her hands. “It’s not like that. I just… I don’t know what I’m feeling. And I’m definitely not about to go around asking my professor if she’s into women.”

“Well, you’re not going to know unless you do,” Alice said, leaning in with a playful grin. “Maybe she’s into you too, you know?”

Rio scoffed, still feeling uncomfortable with where the conversation was heading. “Please, you’re just making assumptions. I don’t even know if she’s into women. I can’t just ask her about that.”

“Okay, okay. I won’t push you. But just don’t keep avoiding it forever,” Alice said, raising her hands in mock surrender. “You’ll figure it out. I’m sure of it.”

Rio leaned back on the couch, staring up at the ceiling. “I don’t even know if I can handle it if she doesn’t take me on. I’ll have to find someone else.”

Alice smirked, tossing another chip into her mouth. “It’ll all work out. But you might want to start figuring out the ‘feelings’ part, too.”

”Ugh, shut up.” Rio glared at her playfully. “I swear, you’re just here for the drama.”

“You know it.” Alice grinned.

~*~

It felt like the universe was holding its breath when the official list of approved mentees was finally posted. Rio had been checking her email obsessively for the past few days, as if somehow refreshing her inbox would make the results magically appear. But now, with the list in front of her on the university’s portal, her heart was hammering in her chest.

She leaned in close, trying to steady her breath as she scanned the names. Only five people had been approved.

And there it was. Her name, near the top of the list.

Rio Vidal.

She blinked twice, just to make sure she wasn’t imagining things. But it was there—right under the heading for Agatha Harkness’s mentees.

Rio felt a mixture of excitement, disbelief, and a tiny pinch of anxiety. She was in. She was going to be working with Agatha Harkness.

Her mind raced. What now? What do I do? Holy shit.

Her hands shook as she quickly closed the page and shoved her phone back into her bag. She needed coffee. Desperately. Maybe a few laps around the campus to walk it off, clear her head, and pretend like she wasn’t about to melt into a puddle of excitement.

When she got there, the café smelled like roasted coffee beans and fresh pastries, the warmth of the space a welcome contrast to the crisp air outside. Rio stepped up to the counter, her fingers tapping against the strap of her bag as she ordered her usual—black coffee, extra strong.

Her body was still thrumming with energy, a mix of excitement and nerves. She couldn’t believe it. She was officially one of Agatha Harkness’s mentees. 

Agatha Harkness. 

The thought alone made her heart race, and she had no idea if it was from pure professional admiration or the inconvenient crush she was doing her best to ignore. She was 36 years old. Way past the schoolgirl crush phase. 

Her phone buzzed in her pocket, and she yanked it out, already knowing who it was.

Alice 

So? Any news yet???

Rio smirked, thumbs flying over the keyboard.

Rio 

I AM IN!!!! I think I might die from excitement!!!

 

Alice 

Knew it. You’re a nerd. A very lucky nerd.

Rio

I was so sure I wasn’t gonna get in.

Alice 

Please. You’re literally incapable of half-assing anything. 

Of course you got in.

Rio

Still. This is huge.

Alice 

So when’s the wedding?

Rio

I swear I’m gonna block you

Alice

LMAO, just saying, you’ve been obsessed 

with her for weeks. 

Now you get to be up close and personal ;)

Rio

I hate you.

Alice

You love me. Now go be a star student 

and try not to combust in front 

of your hot professor.

 

Rio rolled her eyes but couldn’t stop the laugh that escaped. 

The barista called her name, and she grabbed her coffee, her grip a little tighter than necessary. She needed to walk this off, maybe sit somewhere and let herself process the fact that this was real.

But then her eyes landed on a familiar figure near the corner of the café.

Agatha.

Seated with a cup of tea in front of her, effortlessly composed as always. The dark blue of her blouse complemented her sharp features, and there was a certain elegance to the way she held her cup, fingers poised just so. It was ridiculous how effortlessly stunning she was.

For a split second, Rio considered walking the other way. Not because she didn’t want to talk to her—because she did. A little too much, in fact. But she was still buzzing with excitement, and the last thing she wanted was to make a fool of herself.

But then Agatha looked up, her sharp blue eyes meeting Rio’s with precise timing, as if she’d sensed her presence before even turning her head.

Rio froze for half a second.

Then Agatha’s lips curved into the smallest, knowing smile.

Shit.

Rio cleared her throat, forcing her feet to move. She could do this. She was a professional, damn it.

“Mind if I join you?” she asked, doing her best to sound casual.

Agatha gestured to the empty chair across from her. “Please.”

Rio slid into the seat, wrapping her hands around her coffee cup like it was an anchor.

“I—uh,” she started, then exhaled sharply and gave herself a mental shake. “I wanted to say thank you. For approving me as a mentee.”

Agatha tilted her head slightly, watching her. “You don’t have to thank me. Your proposal was strong.”

Rio huffed a small laugh. “Still, I won’t pretend I wasn’t refreshing my email every ten minutes waiting for that list to drop.”

That earned her a slight, amused arch of Agatha’s brow. “I can imagine. It’s a competitive selection.” She tapped the edge of her cup thoughtfully. “But you stood out.”

The words sent a spark of warmth through Rio’s chest. She cleared her throat. “Well, I promise to make it worth your time.”

“I don’t doubt that,” Agatha said, then took a sip of her tea.

Silence stretched for a beat, not uncomfortable, just charged. Rio tried to keep her thoughts in check, but the longer she sat across from Agatha, the harder it was to ignore how striking she was up close.

She needed to redirect her brain. Fast.

“So,” Rio said, shifting slightly in her seat, “how’s Nicky? He feeling better?”

Agatha’s expression softened in a way that was almost imperceptible, but Rio caught it. “Yes. Much better, thankfully. He’s back to his usual self—running around, asking far too many questions, and insisting he’s going to be a superhero when he grows up.”

Rio grinned. “Good kid. He’s got the right idea.”

Agatha arched a brow. “You approve?”

“Of course,” Rio said easily. “Superheroes save people. Not too different from what I do now.”

Agatha made a quiet sound—almost like a laugh—but her gaze turned slightly more curious. “Did you always want to be a paramedic?”

Rio shook her head. “Not exactly. I mean, I knew I wanted to do something that made a difference. I just took a… longer route to get here.”

Agatha regarded her for a moment before nodding, as if filing that answer away for later.

Rio took another sip of coffee, then tilted her head. “And you? Always wanted to be a neurosurgeon?”

Something flickered across Agatha’s expression—an almost imperceptible hesitation before she answered. “I suppose,” she said. “Though wanting and being expected to are two very different things.”

Rio caught that, but before she could ask more, Agatha smoothly redirected. “Medicine is demanding, no matter the field. Balancing it with personal life isn’t always easy.”

There it was. A natural opening.

Rio leaned back slightly. “Yeah, I bet. Especially for you, with Nicky. Must be tough juggling everything as a single parent.”

She said it casually, like an observation, but she was watching for a reaction.

Agatha nodded. “It can be.” She paused, lifting her cup. “But it’s just the two of us. So we manage.”

Just the two of us.

Rio filed that information away before smirking. “Well, for what it’s worth, I think you’re doing a hell of a job. Nicky’s a great kid.”

Agatha glanced at her over the rim of her cup, something unreadable in her gaze. But then she nodded, as if conceding. “Thank you.”

Rio felt the air shift slightly between them. It was subtle, but it was there. And if Agatha noticed it too, she didn’t show it.

Instead, she set her cup down and said smoothly, “I hope you’re ready for the workload, Rio.”

Rio blinked at the use of her first name, then grinned. “That’s funny—I was just about to say you can drop the formality and call me Rio.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “Then I suppose it’s only fair you call me Agatha.”

Rio’s grin widened. “Deal.”

The conversation moved forward, but Rio felt it now—the shift. A slow, careful unraveling of whatever this was.

And she had no idea what she was supposed to do about it.

~*~

Rio stopped in front of Agatha’s office, still feeling the buzz from her cardiology lecture. It had been a long day—class, a rushed lunch, and now this—but despite the exhaustion settling in her bones, anticipation kept her alert. Their first official mentorship meeting. She knocked lightly before stepping inside.

Agatha was seated at her desk, reading glasses perched on her nose as she flipped through some notes. She looked up at Rio’s entrance, eyes sharp as ever.

“Rio,” she greeted. “Right on time.”

“Wouldn’t miss it,” Rio said, lowering herself into the chair across from Agatha’s desk. She was trying not to fidget, but there was something about sitting across from her professor—not just in class, but here, in a setting that felt more intimate—that made her hyper aware of herself.

Agatha set her notes aside, folding her hands over them. “I had a chance to go through your proposal in more detail. Your approach to studying early-onset Alzheimer’s is ambitious. Targeting mitochondrial dysfunction as an early biomarker—have you looked into the studies from UCSF and the Mayo Clinic?”

Rio nodded, her excitement kicking in. “Yeah. Especially the ones examining how impaired mitophagy—basically, the brain’s ability to clear out damaged mitochondria—correlates with disease progression. UCSF’s recent work with cerebrospinal fluid markers looks promising. If we can reliably track mitochondrial damage in the early stages, we might be able to identify patients at risk before they even show symptoms.”

Agatha’s expression remained measured, but there was a flicker of something in her eyes—interest, maybe something deeper. “Early intervention is key. If mitochondrial dysfunction is one of the earliest detectable signs, that could open new doors for treatment.”

“Exactly.” Rio leaned forward slightly. “If we can confirm that mitochondrial stress appears before significant amyloid or tau buildup, it could shift how we diagnose the disease. Right now, PET scans and cerebrospinal fluid tests mostly detect damage that’s already well underway. But if we catch it earlier, we might be able to intervene before neurodegeneration becomes irreversible.”

Agatha tapped a thoughtful rhythm against her notes. “Your methodology needs refining, though. Tracking mitochondrial health in living patients is complex—how do you plan to approach that?”

Rio grinned. “That’s where I was hoping for your insight.”

Agatha huffed a quiet breath, something like amusement in her eyes. “Clever,” she teased, but instead of immediately moving on to logistics, she tilted her head slightly. “What drew you to this research? Beyond your personal connection.”

It wasn’t an unexpected question, but the way Agatha asked it—genuine, searching—made Rio pause for a beat before answering.

“I think…” Rio exhaled, choosing her words carefully. “I’ve always liked puzzles. Neurology is full of them, and Alzheimer’s is one we haven’t solved yet. It’s frustrating, but in a way that makes me want to push harder.”

Agatha’s lips tilted up, just slightly. “A good answer.”

Rio felt warmth settle in her chest at the quiet approval. She was about to ask another question when Agatha, almost casually, set her pen down and shifted in her chair.

“You had a shift last night, didn’t you?”

The sudden shift in topic caught Rio off guard. “Uh, yeah,” she said, rubbing the back of her neck. “Not too bad, though. A few falls, a dislocated elbow, and one guy who was convinced he was dying of a heart attack but really just overdid it at a buffet.”

Agatha huffed softly. “That’s quite the range.”

“You get used to it,” Rio said with a grin. “What about you? Any fires to put out today?”

Agatha exhaled, shaking her head. “Nothing as dramatic. Just students trying to negotiate their grades and an endless stream of emails.”
