Rio chuckled. “Yeah, I can see how that might be just as exhausting.”

Agatha gave her a wry look but didn’t disagree.

Rio hesitated for a moment before leaning back slightly in her chair. “I was actually wondering—how do you balance all of this? Teaching, research, surgery, Nicky… seems like a lot.”

There was a slight pause, just enough for Rio to catch it.

Agatha’s expression remained composed, but there was something quieter in her voice when she answered, “I manage.”

Rio nodded, choosing her next words carefully. “Must be nice to have people to lean on when things get overwhelming.” She kept her tone light, but she was watching Agatha closely now.

Agatha hummed, tilting her head. “I have my friends, of course.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, waiting just a beat.

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, then pressed together again, as if choosing her words. “But beyond that, it’s mostly just me and Nicky.”

That pause again.

Rio didn’t let the small, ridiculous flicker of satisfaction show on her face. Instead, she just nodded. “Sounds like a full plate.”

Agatha exhaled, a hint of dry amusement in her voice. “That’s one way to put it.”

For a brief moment, there was a comfortable silence between them. Then Agatha tapped her fingers against the desk once. “Alright, Ms. Vidal. Back to work.”

Rio smirked. “Right. Research first, personal life later.”

Agatha gave her a knowing look, but there was a ghost of a smile on her lips before she picked up her pen again.

Maybe this mentorship was going to be even more interesting than she thought.

 

 

 

Chapter 5

Chapter Notes

Thank you so, so much for the support. I’m having a blast writing this and am already four chapters ahead. So while I can’t commit to a set posting schedule because I’m an overworked student like Rio, I can promise that I’ll try to post every day or every other day at least.

Agatha had barely poured her coffee when she heard the thunder of small feet barreling down the hall.

“Mom! Are you ready? We have to go!”

Nicky skidded to a stop in the kitchen, half-dressed, socks mismatched, and his hair an absolute disaster. His eyes were bright with excitement, practically vibrating where he stood.

Agatha arched an eyebrow over the rim of her mug. “You’re the one who isn’t ready.”

Nicky looked down at himself, then back up at her with a sheepish grin. “I got distracted.”

“By what?”

“Dinosaurs.”

Agatha sighed but couldn’t fight the amused huff that escaped her. “Of course.”

She took another sip of coffee as Nicky darted back to his room, presumably to finish getting dressed, and let herself enjoy the rare quiet of a weekend morning.

A weekend off. An entire day with just her and Nicky. No lectures, no mentorship meetings, no endless emails, no surgeries.

And yet—

She exhaled slowly, rubbing her thumb against the ceramic of her mug. Almost two months. That was how long Rio Vidal had been occupying far too much space in her thoughts.

At first, she’d told herself it was just because Rio had caught her at a vulnerable moment, and had quite literally saved her that day with the accident. So, you know, it was just gratitude and a healthy dose of drugs when she was basically thirsting over her in the hospital. Plus, she was really good with Nicky too, and had been so caring with him on the day of the accident. She’d become his personal hero.

Then, as the days went by and she discovered Rio was her student, she took her incessant thoughts about her to be just about professional interest. Rio was sharp, ambitious, and capable—Agatha had mentored enough students to recognize potential when she saw it.

But this wasn’t that.

It wasn’t just admiration. It wasn’t just interest in Rio’s work.

It was something else. Something less defined, something she hadn’t had the patience – or courage – to untangle.

Because if she did—if she acknowledged what exactly this fixation meant—then she’d have to face the fact that it wasn’t going away.

And that was not something she was prepared to do.

“Okay, I’m ready!”

Nicky appeared again, this time properly dressed, his coat only half-buttoned in his rush. Agatha set down her coffee, shaking off her thoughts, and grabbed her own coat.

“Then let’s go,” she said, and Nicky whooped as he ran ahead, already out the door before she could lock up.

~*~

A few hours later, Agatha found herself at the Museum of Science and Industry with Nicky. It was one of her son’s favorite spots in the city and she loved that he was so fascinated with science. In fact, he was so much like her when she was at that age — bright eyed, curious and eager to learn — with the exception that Nicky didn’t have the weight of her mother’s expectations on his shoulders, like she did as a child. And that was a blessing.

It was the sound of laughter—loud, bright, familiar—that made Agatha pause.

She and Nicky had been wandering through the exhibits for over an hour, stopping whenever something caught his interest. Right now, they were near the giant heart display, where Nicky had insisted on going through the maze-like structure twice, narrating every step like he was on some grand expedition.

But now, Agatha turned her head, drawn toward the sound.

And there they were.

Rio and another woman—shorter than her student, Asian, with red streaks in her hair, a sharp grin on her face as she said something that had Rio laughing, head tipped back slightly, body leaning into the motion.

It was strange, seeing Rio like this—off-duty, at ease. Not exhausted from an overnight shift, not focused on research or classwork. Just… being.

Nicky spotted them before Agatha could even process what to do with this encounter.

“Ms. Rio!”

And then he was off, sprinting toward her before Agatha could stop him.

Rio turned just in time to catch the incoming blur of energy in the form of her 8-year-old son. She let out a surprised laugh as Nicky launched himself at her, wrapping his arms around her waist.

“Hey, buddy!” she said, crouching down to ruffle his hair. “Didn’t expect to see you here.”

Agatha followed at a more measured pace, schooling her expression into neutrality.

Rio straightened, her lips twitching into a smirk. “Professor,” she greeted, something teasing in her tone. “We keep running into each other. Starting to think it’s fate.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Or just probability.”

The woman beside Rio raised an eyebrow, glancing between them before sticking her hands in her jacket pockets. Rio looked at her friend, and Agatha caught her rolling her eyes for a brief moment, as if there was some kind of inner joke she wasn’t in on. “Alice, this is Dr. Harkness. She’s my Neurology professor.”

Alice’s eyebrows shot up. “Oh. The mentor.”

Agatha caught the emphasis and the way Rio shot Alice a warning look, but she decided—for now—not to address it. Instead, she turned her attention to Alice and inclined her head slightly. “And you are?”

“Alice Wu,” Alice said, offering her hand. “I work with Rio at the firehouse.”

Agatha shook it briefly, nodding. “Pleasure.”

Alice smirked. “Likewise.”

Meanwhile, Nicky was still bouncing on his feet. “Ms. Rio, we’re looking at the heart exhibit! Have you seen it?”

“Dude, you can definitely call me Rio. And yeah,” Rio said, crouching again so they were at eye level. “It’s one of my favorites. The circulation maze is fun, right?”

“Uh-huh! I did it twice. I bet I could do it faster than you.”

Rio gasped dramatically. “Big words, little dude.”

Alice hummed. “Oh, now you have to prove yourself.”

Agatha crossed her arms, watching them. She had always known Nicky was fond of Rio, but seeing them like this—how easily he gravitated toward her, how naturally Rio responded—was different.

And the worst part was, Agatha didn’t mind it.

She should suggest they go their separate ways. This was a chance encounter, nothing more.

But when Nicky tugged on Rio’s hand, already talking a mile a minute about the next exhibit, Agatha found herself saying nothing at all.

Eventually – after an hour of Nicky dragging Rio around the museum and her student just following him around, looking amused – they ended up at the museum café, settling at a small table with coffee and snacks. Nicky, still buzzing with excitement, had claimed Alice’s attention, proudly telling her about his collection of pressed pennies from various museum machines. Alice, to her credit, played along, listening attentively

Which left Agatha and Rio, for the first time, with a moment alone.

Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, watching Rio over the rim of her cup. “You’re good with him,” she noted.

Rio glanced toward Nicky, who was now excitedly explaining the mechanics of a penny press. “Yeah, well. I’ve had practice.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Oh?”

Rio smirked, shifting in her chair. “I’m the youngest of four. Between my brothers and my sister, I’ve got six nieces and nephews.”

Agatha blinked. “Six?”

“Mm-hmm.” Rio popped a grape from her snack pack into her mouth. “Two of them are still toddlers. One just started kindergarten. The rest are already convinced they know more than me.”

Agatha huffed a small laugh. “That does explain a lot.”

Rio tilted her head. “What’s that supposed to mean?”

Agatha gave her a pointed look. “You talk to Nicky like you actually enjoy it. Most adults tolerate children at best.”

Rio scoffed. “First of all, kids are hilarious. Second, they’re way less exhausting than most adults. They tell you exactly what they’re thinking. No bullshit.”

Agatha hummed, glancing toward Nicky, who was now gesturing wildly as Alice pretended to be deeply impressed. “I suppose you have a point.”

Rio took another sip of her coffee, then grinned. “What about you? Were you always the responsible one, or were you a menace as a kid?”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “I was a delight, thank you very much.”

Rio snorted. “Yeah, sure.”

Agatha shook her head, though there was a flicker of something more complicated behind her expression. “I didn’t have much room to be anything else.”

There was something in her tone that made Rio pause. She studied Agatha, the sharp edges of her usual demeanor softened just slightly.

“Guess that explains why you’re so good at keeping everyone else in check,” Rio said, her voice light but thoughtful.

Agatha exhaled, tilting her head. “And here I thought that was just my natural charm.”

Rio smirked, but before she could fire back, Nicky’s voice cut in.

“Mom! Can we get more pennies?”

Agatha turned toward him, already reaching for her purse. “One more. That’s it.”

Nicky cheered and dragged Alice back toward the machine.

Rio watched them go, then leaned back in her chair, glancing at Agatha again. “You know, for someone who claims not to spoil him…”

Agatha huffed, unable to hide a smile. “Don’t even.”

Rio just grinned. After a beat, she asked. “So what was little Agatha like as a kid?”

Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, choosing her words carefully. “There’s not much to tell.”

Rio didn’t push, but she was watching Agatha closely, something patient and steady in her gaze.

Agatha exhaled quietly, glancing toward Nicky, who was still grinning as Alice helped him feed another penny into the press. “I suppose… most people know my mother’s name.”

Rio’s brows lifted slightly, but she didn’t interrupt.

“Evanora Harkness,” Agatha said, rolling the name over her tongue like something foreign, but saw the flicker of recognition in Rio’s eyes. “World-renowned neurosurgeon. Pioneer in pediatric neurosurgery. Brilliant. Respected.” She let out a quiet breath. “And impossible.”

Rio tilted her head. “Impossible how?”

Agatha turned her coffee cup in her hands, watching the way the light caught the ceramic. “She demanded perfection. In everything. Orders were given, and they were to be followed. No exceptions.”

Rio stayed quiet, listening.

“For a long time, I did exactly what she expected. Got the best grades, went to the best schools, built the career she had mapped out for me.” Agatha’s lips curved slightly, but there was no real amusement in it. “But then I did something that wasn’t in her plan.”

Rio’s expression softened. “You had Nicky.”

Agatha nodded. “When I was suddenly pregnant, she told me I was throwing everything away. That I couldn’t be a single mother and still be excellent.” A sharp exhale. “I told her I’d rather be a mother than be excellent by her definition.”

A beat of silence.

Rio’s voice was quiet when she finally spoke. “And that was it?”

Agatha’s fingers tensed slightly around her cup. “We haven’t spoken since. She doesn’t even know him. Said she had no interest in meeting the one thing that would ruin everything she’d worked so hard for me to accomplish. Like my life was her accomplishment, not my own.”

It wasn’t something she talked about often. Not even with Wanda, who had been there for the fallout. And yet, here she was, telling Rio Vidal of all people.

What was it about this woman that made Agatha want to let her guard down?

Before she could dwell on it, she felt something warm cover her hand.

She looked down, startled, as Rio’s fingers rested lightly over hers.

It wasn’t much. Barely even a touch. But the warmth of it settled deep, catching her off guard.

Rio didn’t say anything at first. She just let it sit there, a quiet offering of understanding.

And Agatha—who was so used to standing alone, to holding everything together with sheer force of will—found herself not pulling away.

For a moment, neither of them moved. Agatha wasn’t sure why she did it—maybe it was curiosity, maybe it was something deeper, something she wasn’t ready to name—but before she could think better of it, she turned her palm up beneath Rio’s.

The shift was small, but it changed everything.

Rio’s fingers hesitated for only a second before settling against Agatha’s, their palms meeting properly for the first time since the hospital. Back then, Agatha had been too dazed, too exhausted to think much of it. But now… now she was acutely aware of the warmth of Rio’s skin, the roughness of her fingertips, the steady pressure of a hand that was used to saving lives.

The contact lingered—not deliberate, not hesitant, just there, as if neither of them saw a reason to move away.

Agatha forced herself to clear her throat, needing something to ground herself. “So, six nieces and nephews,” she said, a touch wry, though her voice was softer than she intended. “That explains why you’re good with kids.”

Rio huffed a quiet laugh, the corner of her mouth twitching up. “Yeah. Being the youngest of four means I was basically raised in chaos. Lots of babysitting, lots of scraped knees, and a deeply ingrained ability to negotiate with a five-year-old over bedtime.”

Agatha arched a brow. “And yet, you still chose to go into emergency medicine. Glutton for punishment much?”

“Oh, absolutely,” Rio said with a grin. “But hey, at least my patients don’t throw tantrums over not getting the blue cup at dinner.”

Agatha hummed, her thumb brushing absentmindedly over the side of Rio’s hand. “You’d be surprised.”

Rio chuckled, shaking her head, but she didn’t pull away. If anything, her fingers curled slightly, almost instinctively, as if holding Agatha’s hand was the most natural thing in the world.

And the strangest part?

Agatha let her.

~*~

Their conversation flowed easily. But at some point, the casual touch changed. For a moment, Agatha wasn’t sure when their hands had shifted.

Rio’s fingers had begun a slow, absentminded movement, tracing the lines of Agatha’s palm, gliding up along her wrist before curling lightly around her own fingers. It wasn’t intentional—not really. It felt like a thoughtless habit, the way someone might fidget with a pen or toy with the hem of a sleeve. But it was Rio’s fingertips dancing against her skin, and Agatha could feel every deliberate, unhurried stroke.

She wasn’t even sure if Rio realized she was doing it.

Agatha didn’t stop her.

She should have.

Instead, she found herself caught in something weightless, something fragile—like they had slipped into a space that existed outside of reality. The distant hum of the café, the occasional bursts of laughter from other patrons, the sound of her own child’s voice somewhere across the room—it all felt muffled. Like a dream she wasn’t fully awake from.

She forced herself to focus on Rio’s words, anchoring herself.

“So why now?” Agatha asked, her voice softer than she’d meant. “Med school, I mean. Why wait?”

Rio exhaled, her fingers still lazily skimming over Agatha’s palm. “A lot of reasons,” she admitted. “Didn’t have the money, for one. And I guess I just didn’t have the drive.”

Agatha frowned slightly, watching Rio’s expression shift—not guarded, but thoughtful.

Rio let out a small, humorless laugh. “I always wanted to do it, but when my grandmother died… it just felt like too much. Like, what was the point? I was exhausted, grieving, and the idea of spending another decade in school felt impossible.”

Agatha didn’t say anything, just let Rio talk.

“She died seven years ago.” Rio’s voice was steady, but her fingers tightened briefly around Agatha’s own before resuming their slow movement. “And for a while, I just convinced myself that being a paramedic was enough. That I was still helping people. That I didn’t need more than that.”

Agatha’s thumb moved, just slightly, brushing against the inside of Rio’s wrist.

Rio inhaled. “But then I started thinking about… genetics. About what happens if my mom…” She trailed off, shaking her head. “That’s what finally pushed me. The idea that maybe, just maybe, I could help figure this thing out before it’s too late.”

Agatha didn’t respond immediately. She just let the words settle between them, the weight of them heavy in the space they’d created.

She understood it—more than Rio probably realized.

For the first time since this had started, Agatha let herself move. Her fingers flexed slightly beneath Rio’s, then turned, shifting just enough to let her fingertips skim against the inside of Rio’s palm. It was barely anything, a whisper of contact, but she felt Rio react—just the smallest hitch in her breath, just the way her fingers stilled for half a second before continuing their slow, languid tracing.

Agatha didn’t know what they were doing.

Didn’t know why she wasn’t pulling away.

But she wasn’t.

And neither was Rio.

The moment stretched, a strange, delicate thing neither of them seemed willing to break.

Then—

“Mama! Look, I got a dinosaur!”

The bubble shattered.

Agatha and Rio jerked apart so fast it was almost comical, hands retreating as if burned.

Nicky came barreling toward them, clutching a small stuffed dinosaur in his hands, his face alight with excitement. Right behind him, Alice strolled at a much more casual pace, one brow quirked as she took them in.

Agatha wasn’t sure what she and Rio looked like just then, but whatever it was had Alice’s lips twitching in an attempt to hold in a laugh.

“Hey, Professor,” Alice greeted easily. “Hope we’re not interrupting anything.”

Agatha smoothed her hands against her lap, schooling her expression. “Not at all.”

Beside her, Rio cleared her throat, reaching for her coffee like it might ground her.

Alice’s smirk deepened just a fraction.

Agatha didn’t look at Rio.

And she definitely didn’t think about the way her palm still tingled.

~*~

Agatha had spent the entire weekend trying to rationalize what had happened in that café.

She was a woman of logic, of carefully constructed barriers, of rules she did not break. And yet, the moment Rio Vidal had started tracing lazy, absentminded circles over her palm, she had not stopped her. Had not even wanted to.

That was the problem.

She could have chalked it up to the setting—to the quiet space they’d carved for themselves, to the way Rio had been so open, so achingly honest about why she’d finally taken the leap into medical school. It would have been easy to convince herself that it was just the weight of that conversation, just a brief lapse in her usual control.

Except she couldn’t stop thinking about it.

About how it had felt—those feather-light touches, the warmth of Rio’s skin against hers, the way neither of them had pulled away.

About how much she had liked it.

And now, as she stepped into her lecture hall early Monday morning, she was still trying to decide what the hell she was supposed to do about it.

She had expected to have a few quiet moments to collect herself before class. To center her thoughts, to shake off whatever lingering haze had followed her through the weekend.

Instead, she stepped inside and found Rio already there.

Sitting at one of the desks near the front, elbows propped on the surface, scrolling idly through her phone.

For once, she did not look exhausted.

Her uniform of exhaustion—dark circles, weary eyes, the telltale signs of someone who lived in a constant state of overwork—was absent. Instead, she was well-rested, fully alert, and wearing a loose, easy expression that Agatha didn’t think she’d ever seen on her before.

For a brief moment, Agatha was frozen in the doorway.

As if Rio’s presence had thrown her off completely.

She wasn’t sure why she was surprised. Rio was an excellent student. Of course she would be early. Of course she would take this mentorship seriously.

Except—

There was something about the way Rio looked up and met her eyes. The way her mouth curled just slightly, like she had been waiting for her.

Something had shifted.

They both knew it.

“Professor,” Rio greeted, voice light. She pocketed her phone and stretched her arms over her head before settling in her chair. “Fancy meeting you here.”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, shaking off whatever ridiculous awareness had settled in her bones. She strode toward her desk, setting her materials down with deliberate ease. “Ms. Vidal. You’re early.”

Rio shrugged. “Figured I’d get here before the chaos.”

There was something almost too casual in the way she said it.

Agatha gave her a measured look. “Did you need something?”

Rio tilted her head, considering. Then, with the same easy confidence that had undone Agatha in that café, she said, “Just wanted to say good morning.”

Agatha’s fingers curled slightly against her desk.

It was so simple. So casual. And yet, it carried the weight of something more.

She should have said something dismissive. Should have moved the conversation away from whatever charged undercurrent had begun to take root between them.

Instead, her mouth betrayed her.

“Good morning,” she murmured, softer than she’d meant.

Rio’s smirk lingered as she leaned back in her chair, stretching her long legs out in front of her. “You know, I think that’s the first time you’ve ever greeted me back,” she said, amusement threading through her voice. “You know, with actual words.”

Agatha arched a brow, ignoring the way something in her chest tightened at the statement. “I wasn’t aware you were keeping track.”

Rio shrugged, all easy confidence. “I notice things.”

That much was obvious.

Agatha busied herself with organizing her lecture notes, but her gaze flickered to Rio again, noting—now that it had been pointed out—just how different she looked.

“Your weekend off must have been good,” she said, keeping her tone neutral. “You actually look well-rested for once.”

Rio let out a short laugh. “It’s been so long since I got a full eight hours, I almost didn’t know what to do with myself.”

Agatha hummed. “I imagine it was a nice change.”

“It was,” Rio admitted. “Didn’t have to deal with anyone bleeding, panicking, or throwing up on me. Pretty rare.”

Agatha smirked, flipping open her notebook. “I assume you’re talking about your patients and not your coworkers.”

Rio grinned. “I plead the fifth.”

The corner of Agatha’s mouth twitched despite herself. There was an ease between them, an effortless rhythm that she wasn’t sure how to navigate. She knew she should put some distance between them—re-establish boundaries, remind herself that this was a student-teacher relationship, nothing more.

And yet.

Her gaze flickered to Rio again, to the relaxed way she sat, to the way she was watching Agatha with that same quiet amusement, like she knew something Agatha didn’t.

Before she could think of a way to redirect the conversation, the sound of the lecture hall door opening broke the moment.

Students started trickling in, the spell between them dissipating as the room filled with noise.

Agatha exhaled, straightening her posture. “Looks like your moment of peace is over, Ms. Vidal.”

Rio pushed herself up, rolling her shoulders. “Guess so.” But just before she moved to her usual seat, she shot Agatha a look, something teasing but thoughtful. “Good talk, Professor.”

And then, just like that, she was gone, slipping back into the sea of students as if nothing had happened.

Agatha let out a breath, forcing her focus back onto her notes.

Yes. This was going to be a very, very long semester.

~*~

The library was quieter than usual for this time of day, a rare pocket of peace amid the usual academic chaos. Agatha hadn’t planned on stopping—she was only passing through after a meeting—but the sight of a familiar figure slumped over a study table made her pause.

Rio Vidal sat with her elbows braced on the desk, fingers buried in her dark hair, a deep frown creasing her brow as she stared at her laptop screen like it had personally offended her. A thick nephrology textbook lay open beside her, pages marked with a mess of sticky notes, and a mostly empty coffee cup perched precariously near the edge of the table.

Agatha hesitated. She should keep walking. She should pretend she hadn’t seen Rio and go on with her evening.

But then Rio let out a deep, frustrated groan and dropped her head onto the desk with a soft thud.

Agatha sighed, already regretting her decision as she crossed the distance between them.

“I doubt that’s helping your paper write itself,” she said dryly.

Rio’s head shot up, eyes widening slightly before she exhaled, a slow, tired grin pulling at her lips. “Professor.” She leaned back in her chair, stretching her arms overhead with a low groan. “Didn’t expect to see you here.”

“I was on my way out,” Agatha said, glancing down at the mess of notes and the barely blinking cursor on Rio’s laptop screen. “But judging by the look of things, you’re not having a productive evening.”

Rio scoffed. “That’s an understatement.” She rubbed her hands over her face, slumping in her chair. “I swear, I’ve rewritten this thing a dozen times, and it still sounds like garbage. The pathophysiology section is killing me.”

Agatha pulled out the chair across from her and sat, crossing one leg over the other. “Nephrology?”

Rio nodded. “Yeah. Paper’s due tomorrow, and my brain is refusing to cooperate.”

Agatha studied her for a moment, the tension in her shoulders, the way she kept absently rubbing at her temples. “When was the last time you ate something?”

Rio blinked. “Uh.”

“That’s what I thought.” Agatha shook her head. “No wonder your brain isn’t cooperating.”

Rio smirked. “Didn’t realize you were adding mother hen to your list of titles, Professor.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I’d simply prefer not to deal with one of my mentees passing out from sheer stubbornness.”

Rio huffed a laugh but didn’t argue. Instead, she leaned forward, resting her arms on the table. “You ever had this problem? The whole staring at a paper until your soul leaves your body thing?”

Agatha tilted her head. “More times than I can count.”

Rio grinned, like she’d won something. “So even the great Agatha Harkness struggled with deadlines.”

“I was a student once, Rio.”

Rio hummed, a teasing lilt in her voice. “Hard to imagine.”

Agatha shook her head, but there was a small, begrudging smile tugging at her lips. Before she could redirect the conversation, Rio ran a hand through her curls, exhaling slowly.

“I just want to get this right,” she admitted. “I keep thinking about how I wasted so much time before med school, and now that I’m here, I can’t afford to screw it up.”

Agatha’s gaze softened. “You didn’t waste time,” she said.

Rio let out a breathy chuckle. “Tell that to all the years I spent not doing this.”

“You had your reasons.” Agatha hesitated, then leaned forward slightly. “And you’re here now. That’s what matters.”

Rio met her gaze, something shifting in her expression, something unreadable. And then, almost absentmindedly, she reached across the table, fingertips brushing lightly over the back of Agatha’s hand.

Agatha stilled.

It wasn’t a deliberate touch, nothing calculated. Just a soft, fleeting press of warmth.

“Thanks,” Rio murmured, letting her touch linger.

Neither of them moved.

Agatha wasn’t sure who shifted first—who turned their hands just slightly, so their fingers met properly—but suddenly, they were there, touching in a way that felt neither accidental nor entirely intentional. Just… natural.

Rio’s thumb traced the edge of Agatha’s knuckles, barely there.

Agatha inhaled, slow and steady, and curled her fingers just slightly in response.

For a moment, the library, the paper, the looming deadlines—all of it faded into the background.

Rio was watching her, that easy confidence tempered by something quieter.

“I should let you work,” Agatha murmured, though she didn’t move.

Rio exhaled a small laugh, fingers lingering a second longer before finally, gently, pulling away. “Yeah. Probably.”

The moment passed, slipping between them like something delicate, but not lost.

Agatha stood, smoothing out her coat, before reaching into her purse and fishing out a granola bar. “Eat, Ms. Vidal. Your paper will be better for it.”

“Yes, Professor,” Rio accepted the snack, grinning as she saluted lazily.

Agatha rolled her eyes but didn’t bother fighting the smile as she turned and walked away.

She was in so much trouble.

~*~

The next day, Agatha wasn’t expecting to run into Rio again so soon. She had just finished reviewing some notes in her office when she decided to step outside for some air, letting the crisp afternoon cool her mind before her next lecture.

She had barely made it a few steps down the hallway when she heard a familiar voice behind her.

“Professor.”

Agatha turned just as Rio fell into step beside her, a fresh wave of energy in her stride that was a stark contrast to the exhausted student she’d seen last night.

“Ms. Vidal.” Agatha gave her a once-over, noting the clear eyes, the relaxed posture. “I take it you survived your nephrology paper?”

“Barely,” Rio said, slinging her bag over her shoulder. “But it’s done. And now I’m officially free for the rest of the day.”

Agatha lifted a brow. “No shift?”

“No shift,” Rio confirmed, almost savoring the words. “For once, I actually get to do the whole normal student thing. You know—go to class, complain about class, eat something other than gas station snacks…”

Agatha huffed, amused. “Sounds revolutionary.”

Rio grinned. “Right? And speaking of food—” She shot Agatha a casual glance, like this was nothing, like this was normal. “I was thinking of grabbing something to eat. You want to join?”

Agatha blinked.

It was so… easy.

Not a request, not a deliberate invitation. Just a simple, almost offhanded suggestion, like it was the most natural thing in the world.

And maybe it shouldn’t have felt so natural. But it did.

Agatha hesitated for a beat too long, and Rio, catching it, smirked. “I promise it’s not a trap. Just food. I wouldn’t dream of making you socialize against your will.”

Agatha sighed, shaking her head. “That’s reassuring.”

Rio didn’t push. She just walked beside her, easy and comfortable, waiting.

And Agatha—who had spent far too long ignoring whatever was happening between them—found herself saying, “Fine. But if the food is terrible, I’m blaming you.”

Rio beamed. “I can live with that.”

Agatha wasn’t sure when exactly she had stopped fighting this.

Maybe she hadn’t. Maybe she was still pretending she had a choice.

But for now, she let herself walk with Rio, step for step, down the hall.

Once they were outside, Agatha checked her phone as they walked, quickly typing out a message to Wanda.

Agatha

Can you pick up Nicky from school 

and keep him for a bit? I’ll owe you.

The response was almost immediate.

Wanda

Wow. Dr. Harkness is letting loose? 

This I have to see.

Agatha rolled her eyes but smirked, typing back.

Agatha

Don’t be dramatic. It’s just food.

Wanda

Suuure. Just food. Tell your “just food” I said hi.

 

Agatha locked her phone before Rio could catch her smiling.

“So,” Rio said, glancing over. “You trust Wanda with Nicky?”

“With my life,” Agatha said simply. “And his.”

Rio hummed. “You two go way back, huh?”

Agatha nodded. “Since college. We met in our first year, and somehow, she managed to tolerate me long enough that we’re still friends.”

“Tolerate you?” Rio echoed, teasing. “That sounds dramatic.”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “Wanda would agree with you. She claims I was insufferable.”

Rio chuckled. “I refuse to believe that.”

Agatha shook her head. “You’d be surprised.” She exhaled, softening. “She’s Nicky’s godmother. I’m her twins’ godmother as well.”

Rio’s expression warmed. “That’s nice. You’ve got family that isn’t, you know…” She hesitated, clearly remembering their conversation at the café.

Agatha nodded once, grateful she didn’t have to elaborate.

They reached a small deli near campus, the kind of place packed with students during the day but quieter in the late afternoon. They settled into a booth, and Agatha found herself surprised—again—at how easy this was.

Their food arrived quickly, and their conversation drifted. Rio asked about the twins, and Agatha told her about their chaotic energy, how Wanda claimed they were little geniuses but somehow still managed to get peanut butter on the ceiling. Rio, in turn, told her stories about her own nieces and nephews—about her teenage nephew who thought he knew everything, about her niece who had recently discovered sarcasm and was now unbearable.

“Sounds like they take after their aunt,” Agatha noted dryly.

Rio placed a dramatic hand over her heart. “I take offense to that.” 

Agatha merely lifted a brow, and Rio grinned. “Okay, maybe a little.”

It was easy. That was the problem.

They tried to keep their distance, but now that the touching had begun, it was impossible to ignore. Agatha’s knee brushed against Rio’s under the table. Rio’s fingers drummed absently on the table, close enough that Agatha could feel the warmth of them. At one point, when Agatha reached for her drink, Rio did the same, their hands colliding for the briefest second.

And neither of them pulled away quickly.

Agatha swallowed.

She should be careful. She should.

But then Rio smirked, tilting her head. “You know, it’s Friday.”

Agatha blinked. “So it is.”

Rio leaned back, stretching slightly. “And since, for once, I don’t have to work right after class and you don’t have to rush home…” She shot Agatha a look, deceptively casual. “We could take advantage of happy hour.”

Agatha hesitated, just for a second too long.

Rio caught it, grinning. “It’s just a drink, Professor.”

Agatha exhaled, then—before she could overthink it—sighed. “Fine. But if the drinks are terrible, I’m blaming you.”

Rio laughed, pushing back from the table. “You’re really big on assigning blame, huh?”

Agatha smirked, standing as well. “It’s a specialty of mine.”

They walked out together, too close, their arms brushing. And Agatha, for all her logic and restraint, didn’t move away.

 

 

Chapter 6

Chapter Summary

Again, thank you so much for the support!

The bar was dimly lit, the kind of place that felt removed from time—warm, but not too loud, with a steady hum of conversation and clinking glasses. It wasn’t packed yet, just a few people scattered at tables, some at the bar nursing drinks.

Rio let Agatha pick where to sit, and maybe that was a mistake because Agatha chose a corner booth. An L-shaped one. Which meant they weren’t side by side, but they weren’t across from each other either, more like in a perpendicular angle. Rio was going to die.

She kept her expression neutral as she slid in after Agatha, the leather seat cool under her hands. The distance between them wasn’t much. If she shifted even slightly, she could—

No. She needed to relax.

A server appeared, and Agatha ordered an Old Fashioned, because of course she did. Rio went for a whiskey sour, and then they were alone again.

The air felt charged. Or maybe that was just her.

“So,” Agatha said, turning slightly toward her. “How long have you been a paramedic anyway?”

“About ten years,” Rio said, glad for the familiar subject. “Didn’t exactly have the grades or the money for med school right away, but I still wanted to do something in the field.”

Agatha hummed, considering. “And now?”

Rio shrugged. “Now I know I made the right call. I don’t think I’d be as good at this if I hadn’t done that first.”

Their drinks arrived, and Rio took a sip before continuing. “It changes you, being out there. You see things firsthand that you don’t get in a classroom.”

Agatha studied her. “And Alice? How did that happen?”

Rio smirked. “She bullied me into friendship.”

Agatha lifted a brow, amused.

Rio huffed a laugh. “I met her on my first day at the firehouse. She used to be an EMT before she switched to firefighting, and she was relentless. Kept correcting me, saying I was too careful.”

Agatha tilted her head. “Too careful?”

Rio grinned. “Yeah. I was trying to be super by the book, and Alice was like, ‘You’ll never keep up in the field if you hesitate.’ So she spent the those first few weeks making sure I didn’t.”

Agatha’s lips twitched. “Sounds like her.”

Rio eyed her. “You like her already?”

Agatha exhaled, looking down at her drink. “She seems… reliable.”

“She is,” Rio said. “She’s my person. And my roommate. We’ve been sharing an apartment for the past couple of years, and thankfully we haven’t killed each other yet.”

Agatha was quiet for a moment, running her finger along the rim of her glass. “It’s good to have someone like that.”

Rio nodded. “Yeah.”

It wasn’t much—just a small shift, a tiny movement—but Agatha’s knee brushed against hers. Rio froze, but Agatha didn’t move away.

Her heart did something stupid.

She swallowed, forcing herself to stay cool. “What about you?” she asked, voice only slightly strained. “Did you always know you wanted to be a neurosurgeon?”

Agatha took a measured sip of her drink. “God, no.”

Rio waited, watching the way Agatha’s fingers traced idle circles on the tabletop.

There was something there, something weighty in the way Agatha said it. But Rio didn’t push.

Instead, she let her hand drift—not far, not quite touching, but close enough that if Agatha wanted to close the gap, she could.

And after a beat, she did.

Just the lightest press of her fingers against Rio’s. Shy. Hesitant.

Rio’s brain short-circuited.

She was freaking out on the inside.

But she followed Agatha’s lead, just barely hooking her pinky over Agatha’s, grounding herself in that small, impossible point of contact.

It wasn’t much. It wasn’t anything, really.

But God, it felt like everything.

Agatha, meanwhile, seemed unaware of how the air between them had shifted. She took a slow sip of her drink, her eyes on Rio, but her thoughts appeared to be elsewhere, distant for a moment.

“I was never supposed to be a neurologist,” Agatha said after a beat, her voice carrying an odd weight to it. It wasn’t quite the tone Rio was used to from Agatha—the steady, confident demeanor now giving way to something more reflective. “I mean, neurology was always there, but my mother… she’s a legend in the field. Evanora Harkness. The neurosurgeon. It was always about living up to that, and I was never going to do it, not in her eyes.”

Rio blinked, her pulse quickening for a moment, but she didn’t interrupt. She already knew about Evanora—Agatha had mentioned her in passing during their previous conversations—but hearing her talk about her, hearing the slight bitterness in her voice, made Rio want to listen more closely.

“I wanted to be anything but what she was,” Agatha continued, her gaze distant, fingers tracing the lip of her glass again. “I figured I’d go into something else. Anything else. But in the end, neurology… it found me. I realized it wasn’t because of her. It was because it was the only thing that ever really felt like it made sense to me.”

Rio could hear the conflict in Agatha’s voice, the way she had wrestled with her career, her calling, while trying to escape from her mother’s towering legacy. The complexity of it was like a puzzle to her, one she hadn’t quite figured out, and Rio could relate to that in her own way—though she wasn’t quite sure how yet.

“I didn’t want to be my mother’s daughter, you know?” Agatha chuckled softly, shaking her head, but there was something vulnerable in the laugh, something Rio wasn’t used to seeing from her. “But in the end, it was her field that felt right. It wasn’t about living up to her, it was about finding something I loved. And it’s been the hardest thing to come to terms with.”

Rio could feel the honesty in Agatha’s words, the rawness that had surfaced just now. She leaned in slightly, an impulse she couldn’t quite ignore. “I get that,” she said quietly. “Not wanting to follow in their footsteps, only to end up realizing that you do. In your own way, of course.”

Agatha met her gaze then, eyes soft and searching. “How did you know? That neurology was it for you?”

“I didn’t really know,” Rio admitted, her voice low. “I kind of… stumbled into it. When I lost my grandmother, I knew I couldn’t keep ignoring the signs. It felt like a wake-up call. But I wasn’t sure if I had the strength for it. I just knew I couldn’t live with wondering what could have been. And even then, it still took me years to actually take the leap and start med school.”

She exhaled, relieved in some odd way to have said it aloud. She hadn’t talked about her grandmother, not like this, with anyone outside of Alice.

Agatha didn’t respond right away, but Rio could feel her eyes on her, like Agatha was taking her in, trying to understand her a little better. The quiet stretch of time between them was charged, both of them aware of the closeness now—of the shared honesty, and of the way their knees remained casually pressed together under the table.

After a moment, Agatha smiled, but it was more wistful than Rio was used to. “It sounds like you’ve been through a lot to get here,” she said softly, almost like she was talking to herself as much as she was talking to Rio.

“Yeah,” Rio said, a smile tugging at the corner of her lips. “It’s been a ride.” She leaned back in her seat a little, allowing herself the smallest bit of space between them. It was still too much. The tension between them had built up too much to ignore, but she didn’t know how to ease it. It felt like the slightest movement would tip them into something they hadn’t quite defined yet.

But when Agatha leaned in, her knee brushing lightly against Rio’s again, the proximity was undeniable. Rio felt herself getting lost in it, the steady rhythm of her heartbeat pulsing louder in her ears as she tried to keep it cool, tried to stay calm.

“You know,” Agatha said after a beat, her voice a little quieter than before, “there are worse ways to spend a Friday night.”

But her words weren’t dismissive. It wasn’t like she was trying to change the subject or push the conversation away. If anything, it felt like an invitation—one Rio wasn’t sure how to accept.

Rio smiled softly, the smallest of chuckles escaping her lips as she adjusted her posture, leaning toward Agatha again. “Maybe,” she said, her tone teasing but thoughtful. “But I definitely  don’t mind this.”

Agatha’s lips quirked slightly in return, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, she tilted her head, her fingers brushing against Rio’s again, more purposeful this time.

“Good,” Agatha said, her voice low, but there was something else beneath it, something she didn’t dare put into words. It felt like something was shifting between them, and she wasn’t quite ready to label it. Not yet.

Rio noticed the subtle hesitation in Agatha’s voice. She didn’t push it, but she didn’t pull back either. She let her hand stay where it was, her fingers brushing gently against Agatha’s wrist. She couldn’t help but notice how natural it felt—how the warmth of Agatha’s skin seemed to match the warmth of the moment.

The space between them was small now, but not small enough to dismiss the pull that had been there since they first met. Rio’s heart was in her throat, her mind racing as she tried to keep her cool. But with every brush of Agatha’s fingers, it became harder to breathe evenly.

Agatha’s hand lingered there, barely making contact but undeniably present. Her gaze flickered between Rio’s eyes and her lips, a familiar tension beginning to build in the space around them, like something was on the verge of happening but hadn’t quite yet.

“So, you really think you’re ready for med school this time?” Agatha asked, her voice a little sharper than she intended. Rio wondered if it was a question she genuinely wanted to know the answer to, or if it was just a way to distract herself from the way her pulse had picked up from the simple, casual touch.

Rio leaned in a little closer, her breath hitching as she tried to think of anything else besides the fact that Agatha’s fingers were still gently grazing against hers. “I’m… I think so,” she answered, voice almost too soft. “It’s still scary sometimes. Especially with my completely insane hours as an EMT. But it’s like I’ve made my peace with it, you know?”

Agatha nodded, her thumb lightly running over the back of Rio’s hand without thinking. She couldn’t help it. The way their fingers were so naturally aligned—it felt like they had always belonged that way. Her eyes darted to Rio’s, searching for something she couldn’t quite name.

“Peace with the fact that you’re going to be saving lives?” Agatha’s words were slow, deliberately teasing, but there was a vulnerability in them that only Rio could see.

Rio smiled softly. “Peace with the fact that I’m doing something that actually matters.”

Agatha was quiet for a moment, taking in the way Rio spoke, the conviction in her words. Rio always had that energy about her—strong, grounded, despite everything she’d been through. It was almost magnetic.

The conversation lulled for a moment as they shared a quiet moment together, their hands now fully intertwined on the table. Agatha’s fingers began to gently play with Rio’s, tracing the lines of her palm with barely-there movements, testing the waters.

Rio bit her lip, trying to steady her breath as she allowed Agatha’s touch to linger. She wasn’t sure if it was the whiskey or the proximity or the undeniable connection that had been building for weeks, but there was something about this moment—about being here with Agatha—that felt different. It felt like the edges of something were about to be crossed, but neither of them was willing to be the one to rush it.

But even as their fingers danced together, neither of them could deny the magnetism that was starting to pull them closer.

Rio’s heart was pounding, the sensation of Agatha’s fingertips brushing against hers sending a rush through her. She didn’t know how to label this, how to define what was happening. All she knew was that it felt like they were both standing on the edge of something—something big, something scary—but something neither of them was willing to walk away from.

“Agatha,” Rio murmured softly, her voice almost uncertain, as though she needed the reassurance of hearing her name.

Agatha’s gaze softened as she met Rio’s eyes, her fingers pausing for a moment as she tried to figure out the words. But all she could manage was a quiet, “Yeah?”

Rio swallowed, her fingers tightening slightly around Agatha’s, as though the connection between them needed something to hold onto. “I—” She stopped herself, unsure how to continue, unsure if she even wanted to put words to what was happening.

Agatha’s fingers brushed lightly over Rio’s once more, her thoughts tangled in the sensation of the moment. She pulled her hand back, her voice quieter, more vulnerable than usual.

“I don’t know what this is,” she admitted, looking down at their hands. “I’ve never… been with a woman before. I don’t really know what I’m doing, Rio.”

Rio’s heart skipped a beat at the rawness in Agatha’s voice. She didn’t respond immediately, just letting the words hang in the air between them. There was a quiet understanding there—an acknowledgment of how complex this was.

“I get that,” Rio said softly, her thumb grazing over Agatha’s wrist absentmindedly. “It’s just… I can’t seem to stop myself from wanting to be close to you. I don’t know why. I just—”

Agatha sighed, leaning back against the booth, running a hand through her hair in frustration. “You’re my student, my mentee. This is a complete mess, Rio. I know I’m supposed to be professional, but I can’t help this pull toward you. And that… scares me. I don’t even know how to process any of it.”

Rio’s heart twisted. She understood, she did. The boundaries, the roles, the complexities—they were all real. But there was something undeniable between them, something that couldn’t be ignored forever.

“I’m not asking for anything, Agatha. I just—” Rio paused, her own breath catching. “I don’t want you to pull away because of this. I’m just… I just want to be close to you. That’s all.”

Agatha’s eyes softened, conflicted. She knew Rio wasn’t trying to push her into anything. It was just… complicated.

“You should be focused on your work. This is… I don’t know how this works. I’m your professor, your mentor. I should be setting an example, not feeling… this.”

Rio nodded slowly, understanding the gravity of what Agatha was saying. “I know. But maybe we don’t have to figure it all out right now. Maybe… we just acknowledge that something’s there, and we let it be for now.”

Agatha hesitated, her eyes locking with Rio’s. There was something in her gaze, something both cautious and hopeful. She didn’t pull her hand away this time, but instead, she let it stay, fingers resting lightly against Rio’s.

“Yeah,” Agatha said, her voice barely above a whisper. “Something’s definitely there.”

They both sat in that quiet understanding, the tension between them thick and palpable. Neither of them knew what would come next, but for that moment, they didn’t need to. There was time to figure it out. For now, the truth of what was between them was enough.

~*~

After a couple of hours in that quiet booth, the conversation between Agatha and Rio had shifted from personal stories to more lighthearted, casual banter. The drinks had come and gone, and neither of them had noticed the time slipping by. There was a natural flow to their interaction now, an ease that had settled between them.

Agatha leaned back, taking a deep breath, her smile soft but genuine. “I don’t even remember the last time I had a conversation that felt like this,” she admitted, her tone light but sincere.

Rio smiled back, the warmth of the moment sinking in. “I’m glad we could have it. It’s nice… to talk to someone who gets it.”

The air around them felt easy, almost familiar, as though the world outside had faded into the background. They hadn’t been in a rush, no pressure to move or go anywhere. It was simply two people, in a booth, sharing stories and letting the night unfold naturally.

But eventually, the evening did draw to a close. Rio glanced down at her phone and realized the time. “I should probably get going,” she said, feeling a reluctance to end the night. “I told Alice I’d be home early and even make dinner. She’ll probably wonder if I’ve disappeared into the abyss.”

Agatha chuckled, standing up with her. “I think you’ve earned the right to disappear into the abyss for a little while. But yeah, I guess we both should. I still need to pick up Nicky.”

As they made their way toward the door, Agatha hesitated for a moment, then turned to Rio, her expression shifting slightly. “Hey, by the way… next Friday? It’s my birthday.”

Rio’s brow furrowed slightly, intrigued. “Your birthday?”

“Yeah,” Agatha replied, her voice a little lighter, almost bashful. “It’s on Halloween. So, every year, I throw a small get-together the Saturday after, because, you know, Nicky’s all about his sacred trick-or-treating time.” She chuckled, her tone fond as she thought about her son. “Anyway, I was wondering… if you’d like to come by? I mean, it’s nothing big, just a few friends and some food and drinks, but… I’d really like to have you there.”

Rio felt a rush of warmth flood through her at the invitation, mixed with something deeper, something unfamiliar but undeniably welcome. She hadn’t expected this, but it felt natural. Like Agatha was offering her something important, a chance to step closer into her world.

“I’d love to,” Rio said without hesitation, a smile tugging at her lips. “I’ll bring something too, if you want. You can’t have a birthday party without something homemade, right?”

Agatha grinned, her heart lightening in her chest. “That sounds perfect.”

As they stood at the entrance of the bar, the night still humming in the air around them, Rio felt a small spark of excitement at the thought of Agatha’s invitation. It was a simple thing, but it felt significant—a gesture that wasn’t just about the birthday party, but about something deeper that was beginning to form between them.

“I’ll make it work with my schedule,” Rio said with a soft smile, her eyes meeting Agatha’s. “Wouldn’t miss it.”

Agatha’s face softened, her lips curving into a smile. “I’m glad.” She hesitated for a moment, pulling her phone out of her pocket. “Here,” she said, handing it to Rio. “Why don’t you add your number there, and I’ll send you the details later in the week.”

Rio took the phone with a small, amused smile. “Sure thing.”

She quickly saved her contact information, and before she handed it back to Agatha, their fingers brushed for a brief, electric moment. Both of them froze for a second, their eyes meeting again. The contact was innocent enough, but it was still… something. Rio’s pulse quickened, her mind swirling with thoughts that she couldn’t quite organize.

As Agatha took her phone back, the space between them felt suddenly charged, even though they were just standing there, both waiting for the next step.

Without thinking too much about it, Rio stepped forward, her movements deliberate but hesitant, until she was standing close enough that she could feel the heat radiating from Agatha’s body. For a second, the world seemed to hold its breath, and then, with a gentle confidence, Rio placed a soft, lingering kiss to Agatha’s cheek.

She pulled back slightly, searching Agatha’s face for any sign of hesitation or discomfort, and asked, her voice low and a little tentative, “Is that okay?”

Agatha blinked, seemingly stunned at the unexpected intimacy of the gesture. For a moment, she couldn’t quite respond, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, she just nodded, the corner of her lips curling up.

“Yeah,” Agatha said quietly, her voice steady but with a soft edge to it. “It’s more than okay.”

Rio smiled, the expression lingering with something both content and uncertain. She gave Agatha one last lingering glance before she turned to leave, her steps slow but purposeful as she made her way to her Uber. 

~*~

On the following Monday, Rio went straight from her chaotic shift to Northwestern, feeling like she had been hit by a bus emotionally. When she got to the lecture hall, thirty minutes before the class was supposed to start, she felt like she was just about to collapse from sheer exhaustion and grief.

The room was still empty when Agatha walked in, and for a moment, it felt like the world outside had paused. Rio wasn’t sure if it was just the exhaustion weighing on her or if it was the undercurrent of something else—something that had been growing since their night out on Friday—but the minute Agatha stepped through the door, her presence was magnetic. It made Rio’s heart beat a little faster, even though she wasn’t sure what she was feeling. She’d never been one to lose control over someone’s proximity before, but with Agatha, everything felt different.

She had come early to class, despite the overnight shift, because she couldn’t shake the feeling that she needed to see Agatha again. But today, she was distracted, her thoughts swirling around the little girl she had lost during one of her calls. A child the same age as her niece, Sophia. She couldn’t help but think of her sister, how she would’ve felt if it were her daughter lying cold on that stretcher.

When Agatha looked over at her, there was a quiet intensity in her gaze. Rio didn’t expect Agatha to notice, but she did.

The professor hesitated, then walked down the aisle, her boots clicking softly against the floor. Instead of standing at the podium like usual, Agatha came straight to Rio, sitting down beside her in the first row, her presence filling the space between them. The softness of Agatha’s eyes, her concern—it was almost too much to take in all at once.

Agatha’s hand brushed against Rio’s wrist, a gentle, almost unconscious move. The touch made Rio’s chest tighten. Her fingers tingled with the memory of Friday night—the lingering way their hands had brushed, how close they had been, the electric charge that had passed between them even when words weren’t spoken.

“You okay?” Agatha’s voice was soft, careful, but still with that underlying strength that Rio had come to appreciate so much. There was no pretense, just a genuine question.

Rio looked at her for a moment, the weight of her emotions threatening to spill out. She took a slow breath, the words coming unbidden before she could stop them.

“I lost a kid last night,” Rio said, her voice quieter than usual, as if saying it out loud might make it more real. “She was the same age as my niece.” She exhaled, her chest tight. “It… it gets to you sometimes, you know?”

Agatha didn’t flinch, didn’t back away. Instead, her hand moved, settling lightly over Rio’s wrist, her thumb brushing softly against the skin. Rio couldn’t help but lean into the touch, the contact grounding her in a way she didn’t expect.

“I’m sorry, Rio,” Agatha said quietly, her voice soft but firm, like she truly understood. She didn’t try to say anything else; she just stayed close, her touch a subtle offering of comfort.

Rio nodded, swallowing against the lump in her throat. She hadn’t expected to feel this… supported. But there it was, the way her fingers lingered on Rio’s skin, the way she didn’t pull away. It felt like more than just empathy—it felt like Agatha caring, and Rio didn’t quite know how to process that yet.

Agatha’s hand didn’t move away. Instead, it seemed to settle more naturally, like it belonged there. Rio’s heart skipped a beat, her pulse racing under Agatha’s gentle touch. She wasn’t sure if Agatha realized the effect she was having on her, but she couldn’t pull away either. It felt right, even if it was just for this brief moment, just the two of them.

“Do you want to talk about it?” Agatha asked softly, her eyes never leaving Rio’s face. “I know it’s not easy, but I’m here.”

Rio felt her throat tighten again, but this time she didn’t hold back the tears. “I’m fine,” she said, but the words didn’t come out as convincingly as she’d hoped. Agatha didn’t seem to mind.

“I know it’s not easy,” Agatha said again, her hand still gently resting over Rio’s. “But you don’t have to carry it alone,” she reached out with her other hand to gently brush the lone tear that had escaped.

For a brief moment, Rio let herself relax into the touch, her heart lightening just a little, as if Agatha’s quiet presence could ease the weight of it all. There was something in Agatha’s demeanor that made Rio feel like she wasn’t just a student, but a person—someone worth caring about.

“I’m okay,” Rio said finally, her voice quieter. “I just—sometimes it feels like I’m carrying too much, you know?”

Agatha nodded, her thumb still brushing lightly over Rio’s wrist. “I get it. And you don’t have to talk if you don’t want to. But just… know I’m here.”

The words were simple, but they made Rio’s heart swell with an emotion she wasn’t ready to name.

The room began to fill slowly with students, and Agatha pulled away. The first few students entered, noticing the two of them sitting close together, but Rio was glad that Agatha didn’t immediately withdraw despite ending their physical connection.

But as the students filed in, Agatha gave Rio’s shoulder a gentle squeeze before standing up, moving back to the front of the room. Rio let out a breath she hadn’t realized she was holding, her hand still tingling from the contact, the warmth of Agatha’s fingers still lingering on her skin.

Agatha stood at the front of the room, beginning to prepare for the lecture, but there was something different in the way she looked at Rio. It wasn’t just professionalism; there was a quiet understanding between them now, an unspoken connection that neither of them had to put into words.

Rio was still reeling from their brief exchange, the sensation of Agatha’s touch still burning on her wrist. She wasn’t sure what to make of it all, but she knew one thing for certain—she couldn’t shake the feeling that things had definitely changed between them. 

 

 

Chapter 7

Chapter Notes

You guys are amazing! I'm so so glad you're enjoying this. Thank you so much for your thoughtful comments.

The week had passed quickly, each day blending into the next with little more than texts exchanged between Agatha and Rio. They’d started it on Monday evening, when Agatha, still thinking about what Rio had shared in class, decided to reach out.

Agatha

Hey, Rio. How are you holding up? 

Rio had responded promptly, but Agatha couldn’t stop thinking about it. The next day, she’d checked in again, asking how her day had been. And it continued like that—back-and-forth messages about life, about the challenges Rio faced in the field, about the moments that kept them both grounded. Agatha had found herself looking forward to Rio’s messages, especially when they came late at night, her mind winding down from the day’s tasks.

On Friday morning, Agatha woke up to the soft buzz of her phone on the nightstand. Groggy, she reached for it and smiled when she saw Rio’s message.

Rio Vidal

Happy birthday, Agatha! 

I hope you have an amazing day. 

I’ll try to swing by your office sometime after Wanda’s class.

Agatha’s heart fluttered a little at the message. It had only been a week since their first night out together, yet it felt like so much had shifted between them. She hadn’t expected it, not really, but now she couldn’t help but feel a soft anticipation as she typed her reply.

Agatha

Thank you! I’ll be around all day. 

I’ll give you the details for tomorrow’s get-together 

when you swing by my office. 

I’ve got Nicky’s sacred trick or treating tonight, 

but tomorrow will be fun.

She hit send and set her phone down, just as Nicky burst into the room, his face lit with excitement.

“Mama!” he burst into the room, already grinning from ear to ear. “Happy birthday!”

Agatha laughed, her heart instantly lighter as he jumped onto her bed, bouncing with energy. She pulled him close, squeezing him tightly.

“Thanks, kiddo. Are you excited for today?” she asked, her fingers gently ruffling his hair.

Nicky nodded vigorously, his face lighting up. “Yes! Halloween! And we’re gonna get so much candy!”

She smiled, feeling a warmth she only ever felt when he was around. “You bet. But first, how about we tackle some special birthday breakfast? You ready for some pancakes?”

He didn’t need any further encouragement, already bouncing off the bed and heading toward the door. 

Agatha chuckled softly and followed him downstairs. As she got dressed and ready for the day, she checked her phone one last time. Rio hadn’t replied yet, but Agatha couldn’t help the little flutter in her chest as she thought about her—about their growing connection, and the unspoken things that hovered between them.

Maybe this year, everything would be different. And maybe, just maybe, Rio could be part of that change.

With a sigh, Agatha tucked her phone into her pocket and joined Nicky in the living room, already excited for the day ahead.

~*~

Agatha’s office door creaked open just a little while later, and she looked up from her papers to see Rio standing in the doorway, holding a tray with two cups of coffee in one hand and a single flower in the other.

“Happy Birthday,” Rio said softly, her voice almost like a melody that wrapped around Agatha. Her smile was warm, her eyes a little too knowing, like she had already seen too much of Agatha and liked what she saw.

Agatha’s heart skipped, and she blinked, trying to keep herself composed, but it wasn’t easy. “Rio, you didn’t have to do this. Thank you.” Her voice came out quieter than she intended, and she stood to take the tray from her, putting it on her desk. The soft light pink carnation caught her eye first, delicate and beautiful in Rio’s hand.

Rio shrugged slightly, her cheeks tinged with a faint pink when she offered her the flower. Agatha's smile widened as she accepted it, their fingers brushing.

“It’s nothing. I just thought you might like something special for your birthday.” She stepped forward, closing the space between them. Her eyes met Agatha’s for just a moment longer than usual. Then, with a soft exhale, Rio leaned forward and pulled Agatha into a quick but sincere hug.

Agatha froze, caught off guard by the warmth of it, and the closeness. Rio’s scent—faintly of coffee and something citrus—was all around her. The hug was brief, but it lingered in the air, sparking something between them. Agatha felt a tightness in her chest, unsure if it was the unexpected tenderness or the tension that had been simmering beneath the surface for days now.

“Happy birthday,” Rio whispered against her ear, pulling back just slightly, but keeping her hands lightly on Agatha’s shoulders. Her touch was steady but left something unexplained in the space between them.

Agatha didn’t know what to say. The words felt trapped in her throat, and her pulse had picked up. Rio had that effect on her—she always had.

“Thank you,” Agatha finally breathed out, her voice rougher than she expected. Her gaze locked with Rio’s again, the weight of their shared moments over the past week hanging between them like an unspoken understanding.

Neither of them moved, both caught in the bubble of unacknowledged want and something else, something more, that was starting to get harder to ignore.

Agatha cleared her throat, forcing her attention away for a moment. “This is really sweet, Rio. I—” Her words faltered, her hand curling slightly around the flower stem she was holding. She almost didn’t know what to say, unsure of the boundaries they were now tiptoeing around.

Rio’s gaze softened, a silent question in her eyes. “You okay?”

Agatha swallowed, feeling the heat of Rio’s hands still on her, her presence too much to ignore, too much to just brush aside. She wanted to say something that made sense, something that wouldn’t make this weird, but her brain wasn’t cooperating. Instead, she just nodded. “Yeah. Yeah, I’m good.”

But even as the words left her lips, she wasn’t so sure.

The tension simmered between them, palpable, as if they were both holding their breath, afraid to exhale.

Rio’s fingers moved before she could think better of it, brushing a strand of Agatha’s hair behind her ear, the touch lingering just a second longer than necessary. She watched as Agatha’s breath hitched, her eyes fluttering shut for the briefest moment. And then, almost without thinking, Rio let her hand drift, her palm cupping Agatha’s cheek gently, the warmth of her skin searing against her own.

Agatha didn’t pull away. If anything, she leaned into Rio’s touch, her eyes dark and unreadable, lips parted slightly. The air between them was heavy, charged, thick with everything they hadn’t said.

And then she moved—just barely, just enough. It was the smallest tilt forward, but Rio caught it.

It felt inevitable.

Agatha’s pulse pounded as Rio leaned in, closing the space between them. She hesitated for a fraction of a second, her lips hovering just above Agatha’s, afraid of spooking her, afraid of what this would mean, but unable to stop herself. And then, finally, she let her lips brush against Agatha’s—light, tentative, just the barest whisper of a kiss.

Agatha exhaled sharply, her hands twitching like she wasn’t sure whether to pull Rio closer or push her away. But she didn’t move away. If anything, she melted just slightly, like something inside her had finally cracked open.

And then—

A knock.

Loud. Sharp.

Agatha jerked back so fast she nearly hit the edge of her desk. Her breath caught in her throat, her fingers flexing at her sides as if she could somehow will away the electric charge still running through her.

Rio’s hand dropped immediately, her expression shifting from unguarded softness to something more controlled, but Agatha still caught the flicker of frustration in her eyes, the way her breath came uneven.

The knock came again, more insistent this time.

Agatha forced herself to move, to step away, to shove this—whatever this was—into the farthest corner of her mind. She smoothed a hand over her hair, exhaling sharply as she turned toward the door.

“Come in,” she called, and winced at the way her voice was just slightly off.

The door swung open, and a tall, broad-shouldered student stepped inside, looking determined. Agatha immediately recognized him—Thomas Jordan. One of the students who had applied for her mentorship program but hadn’t made the cut.

“Professor Harkness,” he said, his voice polite but firm. “Do you have a moment?”

Agatha inhaled slowly, steadying herself. “I’m in the middle of something,” she said, her voice back under control. “If this is about the mentorship, Jordan, I’ve already made my decisions.”

Behind her, Rio had taken a step back, her expression unreadable. She didn’t seem flustered, not exactly, but there was still something lingering in the way she was watching Agatha.

“I just wanted to speak with you about it,” Jordan continued, undeterred. “I really think you should reconsider.”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, already feeling a headache forming. This wasn’t the first time a rejected student had tried to challenge her choices.

“This isn’t the time or place for this conversation,” she said, keeping her voice even. “If you’d like to discuss it during office hours, you’re welcome to make an appointment.”

Jordan’s jaw tightened, but he nodded. “Understood.” His gaze flicked to Rio briefly, something unreadable passing over his expression, before he turned and left the office, the door clicking shut behind him.

Agatha sighed, pressing her fingers to her temples.

“Well,” Rio said after a moment, her voice just slightly amused. “That was a buzzkill.”

Agatha let out a breath of laughter, shaking her head. But when she looked at Rio again, the amusement faded slightly. Because Rio was still watching her, still standing just close enough that Agatha could feel the ghost of where her touch had been.

They had been seconds away.

The weight of it settled between them, thick and undeniable.

And for the first time, Agatha didn’t know what to do.

Agatha barely had a chance to collect herself before Rio moved closer again.

It was subtle—just a slight shift forward—but it sent a fresh wave of heat up Agatha’s spine.

She should step back. Should reclaim the space between them. Should do something to pull herself together.

But she didn’t.

Rio’s hand found her arm, the touch grounding yet unbearably gentle. Then, before Agatha could say anything, Rio leaned in and pressed a slow, lingering kiss to her cheek.

Agatha barely contained the sharp inhale that wanted to escape.

Rio’s lips were warm, her breath fanning over Agatha’s skin as she lingered for just a second too long before pulling away. When she did, she was smiling—soft and knowing, like she could see straight through Agatha’s unraveling composure.

“I rearranged my schedule,” Rio murmured, her voice just above a whisper. “Picked up a shift tonight instead, so I’ll be able to make it to your party tomorrow.”

Agatha swallowed, forcing herself to focus. “You didn’t have to do that.”

“I wanted to.” Rio’s eyes flickered with something unreadable. “I’ll see you tomorrow, then?”

Agatha hesitated.

Every part of her was screaming that this was a terrible idea. That inviting Rio into her space, into her life in this way, was only going to complicate things further.

And yet—

“Yeah,” she said, her voice quieter than she intended. “I’ll send you the details.”

Rio’s smile deepened, and for a brief, reckless moment, Agatha thought she might kiss her again.

But she didn’t.

Instead, she squeezed Agatha’s arm lightly before stepping back, grabbing her coffee cup making her way to the door.

The office felt unbearably still after she was gone.

Agatha let out a slow, unsteady breath, pressing a hand to her cheek where Rio’s lips had been.

 

~*~

Agatha had been tense all day, and she hated that.

It wasn’t like she hadn’t hosted these get-togethers before—she had. Every year, the Saturday after her birthday, a small group of friends gathered at her place for drinks, food, and easy conversation. It was comfortable. Predictable.

And yet, tonight, Agatha had been adjusting the glassware on her bar cart for the third time, barely listening as Wanda talked about something or other in the kitchen.

She was waiting.

And then, finally, the doorbell rang.

Nicky, who had been bouncing off the walls since he got home from trick-or-treating the night before, gasped as if Santa himself had arrived. “I’ll get it!” he shouted, already sprinting for the door.

Agatha barely had time to tell him to slow down before the door swung open, and there she was.

Rio Vidal stood on her doorstep, looking entirely too good in jeans and a deep red V-neck shirt that did unspeakable things to Agatha’s brain, and holding a casserole that smelled absolutely delicious.

She had expected Rio to look good—she always did, even in scrubs—but this was something else. Agatha’s stomach flipped, and her mouth went dry, and she hated that Wanda was still in the kitchen because she would absolutely notice.

Before she could say anything, Nicky let out a thrilled, “Rio! You’re here!” and practically launched himself at her.

Rio laughed as she caught him. “Hey, kid,” she greeted, pulling him into a hug as she balanced the casserole in the other. “I see the sugar rush is in full effect.”

“Mom lets me have as much candy as I want on Halloween!” Nicky declared proudly. “Wanna see how much I got?”

Rio grinned. “Obviously.”

Agatha, who had managed to recover somewhat from her momentary brain malfunction, cleared her throat. “Let her inside first, Nicky.”

Rio’s gaze lifted, and when their eyes met, there was something warm, something knowing in the way she looked at her.

“Hey,” she said, soft.

Agatha exhaled. “Hey.”

Behind her, Wanda emerged from the kitchen, glass of wine in hand, and arched a brow at the scene in front of her.

“Well, look who finally made it,” she said, smirking at Rio.

Rio chuckled, stepping fully inside. “Didn’t want to miss the birthday festivities.”

Wanda’s smirk widened as she took a slow sip of her wine, her gaze flicking pointedly between Rio and Agatha. “Oh, I’m sure.”

Agatha shot her a look. “Not a word.”

“I didn’t say anything,” Wanda said, entirely too innocent, before holding out her hands to take the casserole from her.

Rio, amused, just glanced between them like she knew exactly what was happening and was deciding to let it happen.

As soon as she handed the casserole to Wanda, Nicky tugged on her hand. “Come on! I wanna show you my candy!”

Rio laughed, letting herself be dragged toward the living room, and Agatha let out a slow breath.

Wanda leaned in, voice low. “You’re so screwed.”

Agatha closed her eyes briefly before fixing Wanda with a sharp look. “Shut up.”

Wanda just let out a knowing laugh and strolled back toward the kitchen.

Yes. It was going to be a long night.

~*~

 

The party had barely begun, and Agatha already felt like she was teetering on the edge of something dangerous.

The moment Rio stepped inside, it was like the entire atmosphere shifted. Not that anyone else seemed to notice—Nicky was too busy showing off his candy stash, and Wanda was too busy being smug—but Agatha felt it.

Maybe it was because she had spent the entire week texting Rio. Maybe it was because Rio had brought her coffee and a flower and touched her like she was something fragile and precious. Maybe it was because Agatha hadn’t stopped thinking about the almost-kiss in her office, about how she had been the one leaning in.

Either way, she was on edge in a way she hadn’t been in years.

She took a steadying sip of her wine as she moved toward the living room. Most of the usual guests had arrived—Wanda, of course, plus the twins, Lilia, and a few other close colleagues. The atmosphere was relaxed, filled with low chatter and laughter. It was normal.

Except for the fact that Rio was here.

And she looked so damn good.

Agatha tried not to stare as Rio knelt on the floor next to Nicky, listening intently as he sorted through his candy, dramatically explaining the hierarchy of his favorites.

“Okay, but peanut butter cups are obviously the best,” Rio said, shaking her head at Nicky’s ranking.

Nicky gasped, scandalized. “No way! Sour gummies are way better.”

“Wrong,” Rio said, popping a peanut butter cup into her mouth. “But I’ll forgive you because you’re still young.”

Nicky squinted at her, as if trying to figure out whether or not she was worthy of forgiveness. Then, with a dramatic sigh, he tossed a pack of sour gummies into her lap. “Fine. But only because you’re cool.”

Agatha felt something in her chest tighten.

It was one thing to know that Nicky had taken a liking to Rio. It was another to witness it.

She wasn’t sure why it made her feel so—so—

No. She wasn’t going to think about that right now.

Instead, she turned toward the kitchen, only to be intercepted by Lilia.

“You look stressed,” Lilia commented, sipping her drink.

Agatha exhaled. “I’m fine.”

Lilia hummed, unconvinced, then glanced toward the living room, where Rio was now very animatedly pretending to be offended by something Nicky had said. “Ah.”

Agatha frowned. “What?”

Lilia smirked. “Just making an observation.”

Agatha groaned. “Not you too.”

“I mean, it’s not every day you invite one of your students to your birthday party,” Lilia mused.

“She’s also a paramedic,” Agatha said, as if that helped. "And a friend."

Lilia just looked at her, entirely unimpressed.

Agatha sighed. “It’s not—”

“Not a thing?” Lilia supplied. “Because it kind of looks like a thing.”

Agatha didn’t answer, mostly because she had no answer to give. And also because she'd just realized that while Lilia was one of her closest friends, she was also the Chair of Medicine at Norwestern, and this was probably something that would be very much frowned upon.

Lilia grinned, clearly enjoying this far too much, and obviously not caring about whatever was going on between her and Rio. “Don’t worry, I won’t say anything.”
