Agatha shot her a look.  Lilia just clinked her glass against Agatha’s and wandered off, looking far too pleased with herself.

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose.

This was going to be a long night.

And yet, when she glanced back toward the living room, where Rio was now sitting comfortably on the floor, laughing at something Wanda said, Agatha couldn’t bring herself to regret inviting her.

Not even a little.

~*~

As the evening carried on, Agatha found herself acutely aware of Rio’s presence.

Not in an obvious way—Rio blended in easily, laughing with Wanda, listening patiently to Nicky’s never-ending candy monologue, and even humoring the twins when they tried to rope her into their argument about which one of them was the superior soccer player. But still, Agatha felt it.

It was impossible not to.

And maybe that was why she found herself moving toward Rio when she caught her still sitting on the floor, surrounded by children, looking both amused and vaguely trapped.

“Come on,” Agatha said, standing over her with a pointed look. “I think you’ve endured enough.”

Rio looked up at her, lips twitching into something wry. “You saving me?”

“Something like that,” Agatha murmured, offering a hand.

Rio took it without hesitation, and Agatha pretended not to feel the warmth that shot through her as she helped her up.

“Drinks are in the kitchen,” she said, leading the way. “I assume you’re having something stronger than juice boxes?”

“Desperately,” Rio said, rubbing her temple. “I love kids, but they can be exhausting sometimes.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “Try living with one.”

Rio grinned. “I have nieces and nephews. I get the appeal of returning them.”

Agatha smirked, shaking her head as she reached the kitchen. She picked up a bottle of whiskey and raised a brow. “This work?”

Rio leaned against the counter, watching her. “You have great taste.”

Agatha poured her a drink, handing Rio her glass before taking a slow sip of her wine. The party was still lively in the other room, but here, in the kitchen, things felt quieter.

More intimate.

Rio leaned a hip against the counter, swirling her drink idly. “So, do you always do something like this for your birthday?”

Agatha nodded. “Ever since Nicky was born. Halloween is his. I never want to take that from him.”

Rio smiled slightly, as if she liked that answer. “And before that?”

Agatha exhaled. “I didn’t really celebrate.”

Rio’s expression shifted—curious, maybe even a little sad—but she didn’t pry. Instead, she took a sip of her drink and murmured, “Well, I’m glad I’m here.”

Agatha’s fingers tightened around her glass.

She was too. And that, more than anything, was the problem.

The warmth in Agatha’s chest was entirely too much.

It wasn’t the wine. It wasn’t the party. It wasn’t even the way Rio was watching her over the rim of her glass, something thoughtful and unreadable in her gaze.

It was just her.

And Agatha was in trouble.

She set her drink down, clearing her throat. “You didn’t have to rearrange your schedule for this, you know?”

Rio tilted her head. “Didn’t I?”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, but Rio just smirked, reaching into her purse that still hung across her body.

“Actually,” she said, pulling out a small box, “I also got you something.”

Agatha blinked, taken aback.

Rio handed it to her, almost sheepishly. “It’s not a big deal.”

Agatha swallowed, her fingers brushing against Rio’s as she took the box. “You didn’t have to get me anything.”

“I wanted to,” Rio admitted simply.

That was somehow worse.

Agatha exhaled and opened the box.

Inside, nestled in black velvet, was a sleek, silver fountain pen.

She ran a thumb over it, and as she did, she caught the small engraving on the side. AH.

Her initials.

She looked up, heart in her throat. “Rio—”

“You’re always grading or writing something,” Rio said, shrugging, like she hadn’t just given Agatha a gift that made her feel completely undone. “Figured you might like something nice to use.”

Agatha stared at her, unable to formulate words.

It was small. It was simple. But it was thoughtful.

Too thoughtful.

She gripped the pen tighter. “I—”

And then, of course, the moment was ruined.

“Oh, there you are.”

Agatha and Rio both turned to see Wanda leaning against the kitchen doorway, arms crossed, watching them like a cat that had caught something particularly interesting.

Agatha barely resisted the urge to sigh. “Wanda.”

“Hey, don’t stop on my account,” Wanda said breezily, stepping into the room. “I was just wondering where the guest of honor had gone. And now I see she’s been occupied.”

Agatha shot her a look. “Do you need something?”

Wanda smirked. “No. Just enjoying the view.”

Rio, unbothered as ever, took another sip of her drink. “You’re enjoying something.”

“Oh, I definitely am,” Wanda said, then gestured toward the pen in Agatha’s hand. “What’s that?”

“A gift,” Agatha said, a little too quickly.

Rio just smirked.

Wanda’s brows lifted. “Oh? How nice.”

Agatha set the box down, ignoring the way Wanda was very clearly storing this information for later.

“Well,” Wanda said, clapping her hands together, “much as I love crashing a moment, I actually do need to steal the birthday girl for a bit. People are asking for you.”

Agatha exhaled, then glanced at Rio.

Rio tipped her head toward the door. “Go. I’ll be here.”

There was something in the way she said it, something steady, something warm.

Agatha swallowed.

Then, before she could overthink it, she touched Rio’s hand, just for a second. Just enough to feel her warmth before she pulled away. Rio’s lips parted slightly, surprised, but she didn’t pull away.

Agatha forced herself to step back. “I’ll be back.”

Rio nodded. “I’ll be here.”

And then, before Wanda could say anything else, Agatha walked away.

Her hand still tingled.

Her heart was still too fast.

And she had no idea what to do about it.

~*~

Agatha returned to the kitchen, exhaling slowly as she set her empty wine glass down on the counter. The buzz of conversation still carried from the other room, but she allowed herself a brief moment of solitude. She hadn’t expected to feel this… settled tonight. Not with everything that had been brewing between her and Rio. And yet—

“You disappeared on me,” Rio murmured, her voice warm with amusement.

Agatha lifted a brow. “Wanda said people were asking for me.”

Rio hummed. “I noticed. You make a very good host.”

Agatha smirked. “I try.”

Rio stepped closer, her eyes flickering toward the fountain pen resting beside the wine bottle. “So… did you like your gift?”

Agatha picked it up, running her fingers over the smooth surface. “It’s thoughtful,” she admitted. “And personal.”

Rio grinned, leaning casually against the counter. “So, you liked it.”

Agatha let out a soft breath, glancing at her from beneath her lashes. “I loved it.”

Something passed between them then—something quiet, but heavy. Agatha was aware of how close Rio was, of how easily she could reach out and touch her if she wanted to.

Rio must have felt it too, because after a beat, she reached for Agatha’s hand, gently brushing her thumb along the inside of her wrist. The touch was light, but deliberate.

Agatha swallowed. “You’re being bold again.”

Rio smirked. “You bring it out in me.”

Agatha didn’t pull away. Instead, she let herself feel it—the warmth of Rio’s skin, the unspoken thing that had been simmering between them for weeks.

Rio’s voice softened. “I wasn’t sure if I should come tonight.”

Agatha tilted her head slightly. “Why?”

Rio exhaled, the pad of her thumb still moving in slow circles against Agatha’s wrist. “Because I knew I’d spend the whole night looking at you.” Her mouth quirked into a wry smile. “And I didn’t know if I could be subtle about it.”

Agatha’s heart did something entirely inconvenient. She should say something to draw the line back where it belonged, but the words didn’t come.

Rio, as if sensing the shift, slowly released her hand. “Happy birthday, Agatha,” she murmured, leaning in to place a lingering kiss on her cheek. And then, before Agatha could think of a single response that didn’t betray everything she was feeling, Rio was already gone.

Agatha stood there for a moment longer, staring at the place where Rio had just been.

It was ridiculous, really, how much she already missed the warmth of her touch.

~*~

The room was filled with laughter and chatter as the children played in the other room. Agatha and Rio were sitting side by side on the couch, a slight electric hum between them. Rio’s arm was casually draped over the back of the couch, fingers lightly grazing Agatha’s shoulder every so often, as if it were nothing more than an absentminded touch. Yet every time, Agatha could feel it, that quiet and deliberate contact that made her heart beat a little faster. Their thighs brushed occasionally, a touch that seemed innocent enough, but in the midst of their conversation, it felt anything but.

Viz, Wanda’s husband, leaned forward, his interest piqued as he looked at Rio. “So, Rio,” he said, taking a slow sip of his drink. “I’ve always wondered—what’s the adventure aspect of your job like? I mean, you’ve had to see some crazy stuff, right? Has there ever been a moment where you thought, ‘This is insane, and I can’t believe I’m doing this’?”

Rio chuckled, clearly accustomed to such questions. “Oh, definitely. One of the more interesting calls I had was at this… bizarre local festival. Think carnival meets a street fair, but with way more fireworks than should’ve been allowed in a public space.” She leaned back slightly, looking toward Agatha, her voice taking on a playful tone. “So, there was this woman who, at some point, in the midst of all the chaos, got hit by a rogue bottle rocket.”

Wanda raised an eyebrow. “A bottle rocket? How?”

Rio shook her head, laughing softly. “You’d think it’s one of those things that only happens in movies, but no. This woman, bless her, was so caught up in the excitement that she turned her head just in time for a bottle rocket to fly straight at her face. She ended up with a singed eyebrow and a slight burn on her cheek.”

Lilia let out a small laugh, shaking her head. “How did she react?”

“She was in shock at first,” Rio continued, “but she insisted she was fine—just a little embarrassed. It wasn’t until we got her checked out that we realized she’d actually had a mild concussion from getting knocked back by the impact of the rocket.” Rio’s eyes twinkled as she added, “We had to convince her that maybe she should go to the hospital and skip the rest of the fireworks. She was adamant, though, that she was going back to celebrate. She didn’t want to miss the finale. We ended up giving her a ride home myself after she stubbornly refused going to the hospital.”

“See, that’s what I love about you paramedics,” Viz said, leaning back with a grin. “You guys can handle just about anything, even fireworks to the face. I wouldn’t last five minutes in your shoes.”

Rio shrugged with a small smile. “It’s the job, and you get used to the weirdness. The job’s full of unexpected moments.”

“Speaking of unexpected,” Lilia chimed in, clearly curious. “What’s the weirdest case you’ve ever seen? I’m sure there are plenty of strange ones.”

Rio thought for a moment, her gaze drifting as she considered the question. “Oh, I’ve seen plenty of strange things. But the weirdest one that really stands out recently happened about six months ago.” She let out a slow breath, the memory still vivid in her mind. “It was a call to this downtown apartment building—old, not well-maintained. We get there, and there’s a guy, about in his mid-thirties, completely calm, just sitting on the steps of his apartment building, holding a frozen chicken.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her lips curling into a smile. “A frozen chicken?”

Rio nodded. “Yeah, he was holding a whole frozen chicken like it was a teddy bear. I asked him what had happened, and he told me—very seriously—that it was a family heirloom and that it had been handed down for generations. Apparently, this chicken had once been part of some absurd ritual in his family where it was meant to ‘bring peace’ to their home.”

Wanda snorted. “You’re kidding.”

Rio shook her head. “Not at all. He kept saying that he had to take it out and ‘air it out,’ like it was some sort of sacred object. That's why someone called 911, because he was just sitting there holding out this frozen chicken on the front steps of his building. The man was convinced it had spiritual powers—he swore the chicken was the reason his bad luck had started and that he had to reverse it.”

“Was he okay?” Lilia asked, her voice laced with concern.

“He was fine physically,” Rio continued, a small laugh escaping her lips. “But let’s just say I had to gently tell him that there’s no scientific evidence that frozen chickens can reverse bad luck.” She paused for a beat, eyes dancing with mischief. “He took it better than I expected—though, he did insist that I take a picture with the chicken before I left. I think he wanted to prove to his friends that it wasn’t just some delusion.”

The entire group erupted in laughter, with Viz almost spilling his drink.

“Good thing you didn’t end up taking that chicken as a souvenir,” Agatha teased, leaning forward just slightly, her shoulder brushing against Rio’s in the process. Rio, still grinning, let her fingers lightly caress Agatha’s arm, the touch so gentle it could almost have been accidental, yet both of them felt the quiet charge.

“I think my real souvenir was the memory of that guy telling me to ‘respect the chicken’,” Rio replied with a wry smile.

Wanda leaned back in her chair and asked, "Any others that stick out?”

Rio gave her a thoughtful look, leaning back slightly, still aware of the subtle warmth between her and Agatha. “Well, there was this one time that I was called to a golf course at three in the morning. The guy who called in had a random panic attack on a golf cart.”

“What?!” Viz laughed incredulously.

Rio nodded, her smile turning mischievous. “Yep. He was driving around on the golf cart at three a.m., in the pitch black, by himself—doing laps for no reason—when suddenly, he just froze up. Thought he was going to die. My partner and I got there to find him literally sitting on the ground, sobbing with a golf club clutched in his hands like it was his only lifeline. And when we asked him what happened, he said, ‘I thought I saw the ghost of a golfer that died years ago.’”

The group was laughing now, and even Agatha found herself unable to hold back her amused smile.

“Well, I guess some people are just more spiritually sensitive than others,” she teased.

Rio gave her a sly look, a twinkle in her eyes as she leaned in slightly. “Maybe so… But I’ll tell you one thing—there’s something about dealing with chaos that makes you feel more alive. Even if it’s as absurd as a man having a panic attack because of a ghostly golfer.”

Agatha couldn’t help but smile softly, her gaze lingering on Rio. “I think I’m starting to understand chaos a little better these days.”

Rio gave her a soft, knowing smile, fingers absently tracing the curve of Agatha’s arm again. “Good,” she whispered. “It suits you.”

For a brief moment, the world around them faded into the background, and it was just the two of them, caught in an undeniable connection.

Then, as if snapped out of a trance by the sounds of Nicky running around with the twins, Lilia grinned at the obvious tension between them. “Alright, who’s ready for another round of drinks?”

Agatha and Rio both laughed quietly, the tension still crackling between them, but for the moment, they were content to let the chaos of the evening carry on around them.





Chapter 8

Chapter Notes

I am little overwhelmed by the support and I just wanted to take the time to say how much I appreciate it. I'm trying to reply to comments, but time is not really on my side, as I'm juggling work and a second go at a university degree, focusing on a career change.

This has been so fun to write and I can't wait for you guys to get to later chapters. I hope you enjoy this one! Please let me know your thoughts in the comments!

The party had slowed down, the air in the house settling into a comfortable lull as the children played quietly in the corner, occasionally shrieking with laughter. Rio leaned back into the couch, eyes drifting to the doorway and then back to Wanda and Viz who were chatting animatedly with her, their voices light and easy.

“You’ve seen some wild stuff,” Viz was saying with a grin, clearly impressed by Rio’s stories. “I can’t imagine what it’s like dealing with all that chaos every day.”

Rio laughed, the sound warm and easy. “It’s part of the job,” she said, her tone light but filled with a deep appreciation for the unpredictability of her work. “You learn to go with the flow—or not at all.” She let her gaze flicker back to Agatha, who had just walked Lilia to the door. Even from across the room, Rio could see the way Agatha’s shoulders had loosened, the tiredness of the night evident in the way she moved, but there was something else—something different about the way she held herself.

Wanda caught her gaze and followed it, her smile growing. “You two seem to be getting along well,” she said, her voice soft but knowing.

Rio glanced back at her with a small grin. “Yeah, Agatha’s great,” she said, the warmth of her words genuine. She wasn’t sure why, but even with just that short exchange, it felt like the walls between them had been crumbling slowly, like she could finally breathe in a space where things felt just a little bit more real.

The moment stretched between them until the sound of Agatha’s footsteps returning to the room broke the silence. She came back into the living room, her movements easy, unhurried, as if the night had unfolded just as it should. Her eyes met Rio’s almost immediately, a soft, unspoken understanding between them as she dropped onto the couch beside Rio.

Rio smiled, her heart doing a little flip at the ease with which Agatha settled in. Without thinking, her arm moved to rest once again on the back of the couch, this time letting it fall gently over Agatha’s shoulders, a subtle, comforting gesture. Agatha didn’t stiffen, didn’t pull away—she just melted into the touch, resting her head slightly against Rio’s arm with a quiet sigh of relief.

Wanda, who had been watching the entire exchange with a keen eye, raised an eyebrow. The look on her face was impossible to miss, a knowing smirk playing at the corners of her lips. She exchanged a glance with Viz before turning back to Rio and Agatha.

“Well, I think it’s time to call it a night,” Wanda announced, her voice light but full of the unspoken truth that lingered in the air between them. “I can see you two have things to… figure out.”

Rio blinked, her eyes flicking briefly to Agatha, whose gaze had softened as she looked up at her, still resting against her side. The way Agatha was leaning into her felt so natural, so easy, as if it were the most normal thing in the world. There was no tension, no hesitance. Just the two of them, together, in this moment.

“Yeah, I think that’s probably a good idea,” Viz added, chuckling quietly as he stood up to stretch. 

Wanda’s gaze lingered on them for a moment longer, a soft smile tugging at her lips. “You two have a good night,” she said, the words light but with a knowing look as she moved to grab her coat. “No need to get up, Agatha. We’ll see ourselves out. Enjoy the rest of your night,” she finished with a playful wink, making Agatha roll her eyes.

Wanda and Viz said their goodbyes, taking the twins with them as they left for the night. The door clicked shut, and suddenly, it was just the three of them—Nicky, who was fading fast as he played with toy figures on one of the armchairs, and Agatha and Rio, still sitting close together on the couch.

Agatha glanced up at Rio, her eyes holding a quiet warmth as she let out a soft exhale. “Thanks for being here tonight,” she said quietly, her voice holding a thread of something Rio couldn’t quite place.

“Of course,” Rio replied, leaning slightly toward her, the quiet intimacy of the moment wrapping around them like a blanket. “I wouldn’t have missed it.”

Agatha shifted a little, her body relaxing fully into Rio’s side now, the gentle pressure of Rio’s arm around her shoulders feeling so comforting, so right. Rio’s fingers brushed lightly through Agatha’s hair, just a fleeting touch, but it felt so intimate, so familiar, as if they had been doing this for years.

They were quiet for a few minutes, just enjoying each other’s presence and touch. For once, Rio felt like they were finally heading in the right direction, but she didn’t want to rush Agatha into anything, so she just let things happen. Agatha had fully rested her weight on Rio’s side, and it felt like a slice of heaven, and she wasn’t even exaggerating. Rio placed an affectionate kiss to Agatha’s hair and felt as she sighed contentedly.

After a few minutes, Agatha realized Nicky had fallen asleep on the armchair, and let out a sigh, seemingly moving to get up against her will.

“Hey, I can carry him upstairs if you want?” Rio offered, making Agatha meet her eyes for a moment.

“Are you sure? He’s heavy,” Agatha warned and Rio nodded with a smile. “Alright, then. I appreciate it, really. It feels like I’m getting closer and closer to the point where I won’t be able to carry him anymore.”

Rio carefully picked Nicky up, cradling him in her arms with surprising ease, his small, familiar weight resting against her chest. She glanced back at Agatha, a quiet smile tugging at the corner of her lips.

“I’ll take him upstairs to bed,” Rio murmured, her voice soft in the quiet of the living room. Agatha nodded, her eyes following Rio as she moved toward the staircase.

As Rio climbed the stairs with Nicky nestled securely in her arms, she felt a surge of warmth—both from the closeness with the boy and the unspoken connection she felt with Agatha downstairs. It was as if something had shifted, both between her and Agatha and within herself, something she hadn’t expected but couldn’t deny.

When Rio came back downstairs, she found Agatha standing by the counter, her back turned as she fiddled with something, no doubt checking on the last remnants of the party. The flickering light from the kitchen cast a soft glow over her, making her look both grounded and delicate at the same time.

Agatha glanced up as Rio approached, her eyes instantly locking onto hers. There was an unreadable expression there, but Rio saw the warmth beneath it. Agatha gestured to the whiskey bottle on the counter. “Care for a nightcap?” she asked, her voice low, just for Rio.

Rio hesitated for a moment, but then her own desire for something more—more connection, more time with Agatha—pushed her forward. “Yeah, I’d like that,” Rio replied, her voice steady but the flutter in her chest undeniable.

They both moved toward the counter, Agatha pouring some whiskey for Rio and another glass of wine for herself. Rio’s heart beating a little faster, the air between them thick with an unspoken tension, the weight of what had been building ever since Agatha had walked back into the room after seeing Lilia off.

They sat down together on the couch again, facing each other, a little closer than before, the space between them shrinking with every passing second. The way their bodies aligned, their legs brushing against each other with every slight movement, made Rio’s pulse race.

Agatha took a sip of her wine, her gaze flicking over to Rio before she settled in next to her, their thighs brushing again. Rio could feel the heat of Agatha’s body seeping into her own. The need to touch was unbearable now.

Slowly, cautiously, Rio reached out, letting her fingers trail lightly along the extension of Agatha’s arm as it rested on the back of the couch. She was testing the boundaries, but she couldn’t help herself—couldn’t fight the urge to feel Agatha’s warmth under her touch. 

Agatha’s breath caught slightly, the subtle tension in her body radiating through her, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, she tilted her head slightly, looking at Rio, a mixture of uncertainty and something else in her eyes.

Rio’s heart raced, and she asked, almost breathlessly, “Did you like your birthday?”

Agatha’s eyes flickered down to Rio’s lips, her gaze lingering there, as if she couldn’t help herself. She bit her bottom lip, and Rio felt a shiver go down her spine at the sight. It was as if Agatha was caught between wanting to pull back and wanting to lean in, the same conflict that had been brewing between them all night.

Rio’s chest tightened with anticipation, the air so thick now that it was almost suffocating. She could feel every inch of Agatha’s proximity, the soft warmth of her body next to hers, the quiet energy that seemed to crackle between them, pushing them closer, even without words.

For a moment, neither of them spoke. The silence was charged with so much unspoken feeling that it felt as if the room itself was holding its breath. Then, finally, Agatha looked up at her, her lips still caught between her teeth.

“I did,” Agatha whispered, her voice just above a breath. “More than I expected.”

The vulnerability in her voice, the honesty, sent a thrill through Rio. She took a deep breath, her fingers still tracing the edge of Agatha’s arm, her heart hammering in her chest.

“Good,” Rio murmured, her voice barely audible, her eyes searching Agatha’s. She could see the flicker of something deeper in Agatha’s eyes, a yearning that matched her own.

In that moment, the pull between them was too much to ignore. The way Agatha’s gaze lingered on her lips, the way Rio felt the electricity in the air, it was impossible to pretend it wasn’t there anymore.

With a soft sigh, Rio leaned in just slightly, close enough that she could feel the heat of Agatha’s breath against her skin, but not yet close enough to close the distance entirely. The tension was unbearable, and yet they both seemed to hesitate, each waiting for the other to make the first move.

Finally, Rio whispered, her voice soft, “I’m glad it was a good birthday.”

Agatha’s response was a quiet hum of agreement, her hand moving to brush against Rio’s where it rested on her arm, the touch light but electric. There was a shared understanding now, something unspoken that was far too strong to ignore, but they both knew there was more to figure out, more to navigate, before they could fully give in to whatever this was..

She swallowed hard, heart racing in her chest, but she couldn’t seem to stop herself. She leaned in just a fraction, watching Agatha’s eyes flicker from hers to her lips and back, that hesitation finally giving way to something else. It was a pull, an undeniable pull, like a magnetic force that neither of them could resist any longer.

Rio closed the gap, their lips brushing together tentatively at first. A soft, sweet kiss that felt almost like an apology, like they were both saying, Is this okay? But it wasn’t long before it deepened, as if their bodies had been waiting for this moment—waiting for the connection to finally click into place.

Rio’s hand slid up Agatha’s arm, fingers finding her wrist and pulling her a little closer. Agatha responded in kind, one hand reaching to rest gently on Rio’s cheek, the touch soft but grounding, anchoring them both in this moment. Rio’s heart was pounding now, every nerve alive with the feel of Agatha’s body now pressed against hers, the taste of her lips, the warmth of her breath.

The kiss lingered, intense and deep, both of them caught in the moment, but Rio could feel the weight of the situation pressing down on her. Agatha had been so hesitant, so unsure, and though the chemistry between them was undeniable, Rio couldn’t bring herself to push for more—not tonight, not when it was clear Agatha was still navigating this new territory.

Pulling away slowly, she took a breath and placed a soft kiss on Agatha’s forehead. “I think I should go,” Rio said softly, her voice tinged with regret but also a knowing calm. “We should talk about this… properly, you know? But not tonight. Not like this.”

Agatha nodded, her eyes dark with desire, but there was understanding there. 

They stood up, and Agatha followed her to the door, as she called for an Uber. Rio paused as she reached for the handle, turning to face Agatha once more.

Agatha stepped closer, and without a word, she cupped Rio’s face, pulling her into a gentle, lingering kiss goodbye. Rio felt a thrill shoot through her chest at the softness of Agatha’s lips, the way Agatha’s hand rested against her cheek like a silent promise.

When they pulled apart, Rio offered a small smile, the kind that only deepened as she looked at Agatha. “I’ll text you.”

“I’ll be waiting,” Agatha murmured, her voice almost like a promise in itself, before she pulled Rio in for one last lingering kiss.

Rio stepped out of the door, her breath catching as she made her way down the steps, a giddy feeling in her chest. As soon as she was inside the Uber, she leaned back with a contented sigh, a smile tugging at her lips. Everything felt surreal—like she was in a dream, and she didn’t want to wake up.

The ride home felt like it took forever, the excitement of the night swirling inside her, making her head spin in the best way possible. When she finally stepped inside her apartment, she was met with the sounds of laughter, the faint hum of music, and the warm presence of her friends.

Alice was in the living room, practically jumping out of her seat when she saw Rio. “Look who decided to show up!” Alice teased, grinning ear to ear. “How was the party? Or should I say, how was your date with the professor?”

Jen, sitting next to her, raised an eyebrow, clearly amused. “You know, I’m really starting to think our girl has been holding out on us,” she teased, nudging Alice.

Rio rolled her eyes, grinning at her friends. “What? Just because I had a nice time doesn’t mean—”

“—You had a very nice time,” Alice interrupted with a playful smirk. “Did you? Huh? Did you kiss her? What happened? Did you—”

“You guys are terrible,” Rio said with a laugh, but there was no hiding the grin that spread across her face. “Yes, we kissed. Happy now?”

“Oh, so there was a kiss!” William, Rio’s partner from the firehouse, chimed in, making the whole group burst into laughter. “Pay up, losers!” He put his hand out waiting for the dollar bills to be deposited there.

“You’re killing me,” Rio muttered, but the joy in her heart was clear. She could feel the warmth of her friends around her, the teasing laughter, but none of it could wipe the smile off her face. Her heart was light, and for the first time in what felt like forever, she was genuinely happy.

As the night went on, they all shared stories and laughed, but Rio couldn’t stop thinking about the kiss, about Agatha’s warmth, about the quiet understanding that had passed between them. It was complicated, yes. But for tonight, that kiss, that feeling of connection, was more than enough.

And when she finally went to bed, it was with a happy sigh, a sense of peace settling over her as she drifted off to sleep, the thought of Agatha still lingering in her mind like the sweetest kind of dream.

 

~*~

 

Rio had never considered herself the type to get butterflies, but as she stepped into the lecture hall, coffee tray in hand, her stomach was a swarm of them. It had been a little over twenty-four hours since she’d last seen Agatha, but she’d been counting the seconds, replaying every stolen touch, every lingering glance, every quiet moment between them at the party.

She wasn’t sure what this was—what they were stepping into—but the thought of seeing Agatha again made her pulse race in a way she couldn’t deny.

The room was still empty, just the way she wanted it.

The overhead lights cast a soft glow over the rows of seats, the hush of early morning making everything feel more intimate, like the world had paused just for them. She moved towards the first row, setting the coffee and bag of pastries down on one of the desks.

She hadn’t even thought twice about bringing Agatha coffee. It had been automatic, the same way she had gone out of her way to pick up those pastries—the ones she’d seen Agatha get the first time they had coffee together.

She pulled out her phone and sent a quick text.

Rio

I’m already here. Brought coffee and something sweet for you. You have about 30 minutes before your minions start piling in.

 

She set the phone down, heart hammering against her ribs, a small grin playing at her lips.

The moment the message was delivered, she felt the weight of anticipation settle over her. It was ridiculous, really, how much she was looking forward to this, but she didn’t care.

She leaned back in her seat, eyes flickering to the door every few seconds, waiting for the moment Agatha would walk in.

It didn’t take long.

Barely five minutes after Rio sent the text, she heard the click of heels echoing down the hall. Her pulse jumped.

And then Agatha was there.

She walked in like she always did—composed, sharp, carrying herself with that quiet authority that made even the most arrogant students sit up and pay attention. But the moment she spotted Rio, something shifted. The tension in her shoulders eased, her lips parting just slightly, as if she hadn’t expected Rio to actually be there waiting for her.

Or maybe she had.

Maybe she had been looking forward to this just as much.

“Morning,” Rio said, grinning as she leaned forward, resting her elbows on the desk.

Agatha’s eyes flicked to the tray beside her, taking in the two cups of coffee and the small bag. “You brought me breakfast?”

Rio shrugged, feigning nonchalance. “Figured you might need it. Thought about getting you something healthier, but then I remembered you having these the last time we got coffee. So.”

Agatha let out a soft huff, the corner of her mouth twitching up as she walked closer. She set her bag down on her desk before making her way to Rio, reaching for one of the cups. Their fingers brushed as she picked it up, and neither of them moved away immediately.

Heat curled in Rio’s stomach at the brief contact.

“You didn’t have to,” Agatha murmured, studying her with an unreadable expression.

“I know,” Rio said, holding her gaze. “Wanted to.”

Agatha exhaled, something flickering in her eyes before she took a careful sip of her coffee. Whatever she found in the taste must have pleased her, because she hummed, the sound barely audible but enough to make Rio’s skin prickle.

“You look more rested than usual,” Agatha noted after a beat, eyes sweeping over Rio’s face. “Tell me you actually got some sleep.”

Rio smirked. “Five whole hours. Practically a luxury.”

Agatha arched a brow, unimpressed. “That’s still not enough.”

“Maybe,” Rio admitted, unwrapping one of the pastries and breaking off a piece. “But I’m used to it. Besides, it was a quiet shift. No chaos this time.”

“Miraculous,” Agatha said dryly, but there was warmth beneath the teasing.

Rio popped the piece of pastry into her mouth, watching as Agatha took the seat beside her, the space between them practically nonexistent.

Neither of them acknowledged it.

Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, watching Rio over the rim of her cup. Rio could feel her eyes, that sharp, assessing gaze that always made her pulse quicken just a little. She was starting to get used to it, though. Used to Agatha looking at her like she was something worth studying.

This morning, at least, she wasn’t being scrutinized for exhaustion. For once, she’d gotten a decent night’s sleep—though she suspected that had more to do with the warmth still lingering from her weekend with Agatha than anything else.

She drummed her fingers lightly against the side of her cup, letting the silence stretch just enough before offering Agatha a lopsided grin. “So, how was the rest of your weekend?”

Agatha hummed, setting down her cup. “Pleasantly quiet. And yours?”

Rio huffed a laugh, stretching her legs under the desk. “Oh, you mean after I left your place floating on a cloud?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though Rio didn’t miss the way her lips twitched. “Yes, after that.”

Rio chuckled, shifting her weight slightly so that her knee just barely brushed against Agatha’s. She took a slow sip of her coffee before resting her arm on the desk, fingers ghosting near Agatha’s wrist. “Well, I got home to what can only be described as a full-blown intervention.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her gaze flicking briefly to their almost-touch before returning to Rio’s face. “Intervention?”

“Mhm.” Rio let her fingers drift a little closer, her touch featherlight as she traced the edge of Agatha’s wrist. “Alice, her girlfriend Jen, my partner William, and a couple of other firefighters were hanging out. The second I walked through the door, it was like a pack of wolves descending.”

Agatha smirked. “And what exactly were they intervening about?”

Rio sighed dramatically. “My love life, apparently. Or lack thereof, until now.” She flicked her gaze up to Agatha’s, something playful but sincere in her eyes. “I was immediately interrogated. Where had I been? Why did I look like I had just won the lottery? Did I—” She coughed, lips twitching. “Did I just get laid?”

Agatha inhaled sharply, her fingers curling slightly against the desk as she turned her gaze toward her coffee. “Good Lord.”

Rio laughed, tilting her head slightly. “I set the record straight, don’t worry.”

“I should hope so,” Agatha muttered, though the way she shifted, the subtle tightness in her jaw—it wasn’t lost on Rio.

“Although…” Rio trailed off, shifting just slightly so that her knee pressed more firmly against Agatha’s. She let her fingers skim lightly up the inside of Agatha’s wrist, lingering. “Alice was convinced I at least made out with someone. And well…”

She didn’t finish the sentence. She didn’t need to.

Agatha exhaled, finally meeting Rio’s eyes, and there it was again—that charge between them, humming just beneath the surface. Rio’s heart picked up speed, but she didn’t look away.

“Is that so?” Agatha murmured, tilting her head ever so slightly.

Rio’s lips curled into a slow smile. “Mhm.”

They sat there, caught in something that neither of them had quite figured out how to name yet. Small touches, careful movements, the warmth of their knees pressed together under the desk.

Then, footsteps echoed in the hallway.

They pulled apart instantly.

Agatha straightened, and stood up, smoothing the front of her skirt as she took a sip of coffee, while Rio leaned back in her chair, clearing her throat.

A second later, the first students walked in.

And of course, Jordan was among them.

His gaze landed on them almost immediately, his expression unreadable.

“Morning, Dr. Harkness,” he said, his tone carefully neutral as he moved toward the second row. Then, after a brief pause, his eyes flicked to Rio. “Vidal.”

Rio met his gaze evenly, giving him a slow nod. “Jordan.”

Agatha, ever composed, barely acknowledged him, already shifting her attention to her notes.

But Rio could feel it. The shift. The weight of Jordan’s stare. The subtle tension in the air.

She took another sip of her coffee, stealing one last glance at Agatha.

It would be fine.

They would be fine.

Even if Jordan was already watching a little too closely.

Chapter 9

Chapter Notes

I cannot thank you enough for the overwhelming support! I'm just so so glad that you're all as excited about this as I am.
I know I've been spoiling you all with daily updates, but that can only happen because I'm already about five chapters ahead, writing wise. Also, Rio's assignment topic is my absolute favorite topic in neuro and I loved it so much last semester. Neuroanatomy is amazing and I'm absolutely in love.

Thanks again and enjoy!

As the lecture began, Agatha slipped into professor mode, her voice measured and confident as she walked the class through today’s topic. She had been teaching for years, but today, she was hyper aware of Rio’s presence in the front row. Hyper aware of the way Rio leaned forward, actively engaged, her fingers tapping absently against the edge of her notebook.

If Agatha hadn’t been looking for it, she might have missed the way Rio’s shoulders tensed whenever Jordan spoke up in class, his tone a little too clipped, a little too calculated.

Agatha, however, missed nothing.

By the time the lecture was almost finished, she was already thinking ahead, and had prepared an assignment that would push her students to dig deeper. She tapped the board lightly with the end of her marker.

“For your next assignment,” she said, scanning the room, “I want each of you to talk about a key neurological structure and explore its role in cognition and behavior. You’ll examine how it impacts emotions, memory, and even disorders related to its dysfunction.”

There were murmurs throughout the classroom as students jotted down notes.

“To make it more interesting,” Agatha continued, her eyes flicking briefly to Rio before looking back at the class, “Through a lottery app, I’ve selected topics for each of you, which you’ll find in your inbox by the end of the day.”

Rio smirked slightly at that, and Agatha could tell she was intrigued. 

The rest of the class proceeded as usual, but as the students packed up their things and began filing out, Agatha noticed something.

Rio didn’t linger.

There was no teasing remark. No playful smile thrown her way before she left. Instead, she simply glanced at Agatha, offering a small but knowing smile before slipping out the door.

Agatha frowned slightly, watching her go.

Then, her phone buzzed in her pocket.

She pulled it out, and when she saw the name on the screen, her lips twitched.

Rio  

Waiting for you in your office.

Agatha exhaled, shaking her head slightly before tucking her phone away.

 

~*~

 

Agatha closed the door behind her, exhaling softly as she took in the sight of Rio already sitting in her office. She was lounging in the chair across from Agatha’s desk, one leg crossed over the other, looking far too comfortable for someone who had just come off a night shift.

“Professor,” Rio greeted, her voice carrying that teasing lilt Agatha was coming to expect from her.

Agatha arched a brow, setting her bag down. “You don’t usually wait for me in my office. Especially after leaving without even a word.”

Rio hummed, stepping closer. “Noticed that, did you?”

“Oh, I noticed.”

Something thick settled between them — something warm, charged – the tension was undeniable. Agatha felt it wrap around her, pulling her in like a tide she wasn’t sure she wanted to resist.

“So.” She folded her arms, trying to ground herself. “Limbic system and emotional processing for you. Satisfied with your assignment?”

Rio scoffed, shaking her head. “I don’t know how you did it, but you somehow managed to give me the best topic in neuro.”

Agatha smirked. “I didn’t do anything, the lottery thing app did all the work.”

“Yeah? Maybe you’re more in tune with me than you think, then.”

The words shouldn’t have sent a thrill through her, but they did. Agatha glanced away for a moment, pushing her hair behind her ear. When she looked back, Rio was watching her intently.

Agatha swallowed. “How was the rest of your weekend?”

Rio exhaled a soft laugh, rubbing the back of her neck. “Oh, you mean after my friends spent the entire night roasting me alive?”

Agatha’s lips twitched. “That bad, huh?”

Rio chuckled, looking a little self conscious. “Yeah. It’s fine, though. I mean they were teasing me for a reason and they weren’t wrong,” she teased, her eyes sparkling with mischief. “I probably walked in looking like I’d just won the lottery.”

Their laughter settled into something softer, something closer. Agatha felt the warmth of it linger in her chest, felt the way it shifted something inside her, like a door she hadn’t realized was locked had just been nudged open.

Then Rio’s voice dropped, quieter now.

“But for real,” she murmured, “I think they were just happy to see me happy.”

Agatha’s breath caught.

She didn’t know what to say to that. Didn’t know how to acknowledge the way it made something tighten in her chest.

So instead, she reached out, fingers brushing lightly over Rio’s wrist, just a tentative touch—one that Rio responded to immediately. She turned her hand over, fingers skimming Agatha’s palm before linking loosely with hers.

Agatha’s breath hitched. It was too much and not enough.

She barely realized she was leaning forward until Rio’s free hand reached up, fingertips grazing her jaw. Agatha exhaled sharply, her lips parting just slightly.

Rio’s gaze flickered down, and the tension between them crackled.

Then, as if drawn by a force neither of them could resist, Rio leaned in, brushing her lips over hers. Agatha’s fingers curled around Rio’s, holding her there for just a second longer, just enough to let the moment settle between them, before—

A knock on the door shattered the quiet.

They pulled apart, Rio exhaling a sharp breath just as Agatha turned, schooling her features into something far more neutral before walking to the door.

Agatha barely cracked the door open, just enough to see Thomas Jordan standing there with his usual stiff posture and overly serious expression.

“Professor,” he said, glancing briefly past her shoulder as if trying to see inside. “I had a question about the assignment.”

Agatha resisted the urge to sigh. Of course he did. “Go ahead.”

Jordan adjusted his backpack strap. “Are we supposed to just hand in the report, or will there be a presentation component as well?”

Agatha kept her voice even. “All the information you need will be in the email I’m sending to the class later today. If you have any further questions, you can schedule a meeting during my office hours.”

Jordan frowned slightly, clearly wanting a more immediate answer, but nodded. “Understood. Thank you, Professor.”

Agatha nodded back, offering a polite smile before closing the door.

She turned to find Rio already rolling her eyes, arms crossed. “He’s so insufferable.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “You don’t even know what he wanted.”

Rio scoffed. “I could hear him, you know. You forget that he’s been in my class for over a year now. He’s the guy who corrects people just for fun and thinks he’s so much better than everyone.”

Agatha gave her a knowing look.

Rio pointed at her. “See? Even you think so.”

Agatha shook her head, but before she could respond, Rio was already stepping closer, hands settling lightly on her waist, pulling her in with an ease that made Agatha’s breath hitch.

“Now,” Rio murmured, tilting her head, “where were we?”

Agatha barely had time to exhale before Rio kissed her again—this time deeper, lingering. Agatha let herself sink into it, unable to stop herself, stop this undeniable chemistry between them, as her fingers tightened on the fabric of Rio’s lab coat, pulling her closer.

Rio hummed against her lips, one hand sliding up to cup her jaw, her thumb brushing lightly against Agatha’s cheek. It was slow, unhurried, like they had all the time in the world.

When Rio finally pulled back, Agatha couldn’t suppress a sound of protest.

Rio grinned. “I’d love to stay here and keep making out with you, but I have a couple of errands to run before I head to the library.”

Agatha arched a brow. “You mean you’re going to ply yourself with even more caffeine?”

Rio snorted. “Tempting, but no. I have a cardiology assignment to work on.”

Agatha smirked, reaching up to fix the collar of Rio’s lab coat. “Good to know you’re prioritizing your studies.”

Rio’s fingers squeezed lightly at her waist. “Don’t worry, Professor. I always make time for the important things.”

Agatha felt her stomach flip at the way Rio was looking at her.

Then, with one last lingering touch to her arm, Rio stepped back, grabbing her bag. “I’ll see you later.”

Agatha watched her go, exhaling slowly, pulse still racing.

She was in so much trouble.

 

~*~

 

Later that week, Agatha found herself in Wanda’s living room, nursing a drink after work. She had stopped by to pick up Nicky, and Wanda had insisted they stayed for dinner. Now, as Viz took the boys out to the backyard to throw some ball around, she finally found herself with a moment alone with her best friend.

Agatha traced the rim of her glass with her finger, her thoughts swirling just as much as the whiskey inside. Wanda was watching her intently, that look of patient expectation that only came from years of friendship.

Agatha sighed. “It’s not that simple.”

Wanda arched an eyebrow. “It never is. But let’s hear it, anyway.”

Agatha exhaled sharply through her nose. “I am grading her. I’m also her mentor, not just her professor. That makes it more complicated.”

Wanda nodded slowly, considering. “Okay, that’s fair. But be honest with yourself—would you ever let your feelings affect how you grade her?”

Agatha frowned. “Of course not.”

“Would you hold her to a different standard than any of your other students?”

Agatha shook her head. “No.”

“Would she expect that from you?”

“No,” Agatha admitted, running a hand through her hair. “She’d probably be offended if I did treat her differently. She’s too damn stubborn.”

Wanda smirked. “Sounds like someone else I know.”

Agatha shot her a dry look before sighing again. “I just don’t want to cross a line I can’t come back from.”

Wanda tapped her nails against her glass thoughtfully. “Is this really about ethics? Or is it about you being afraid to want this?”

Agatha’s throat felt tight, and she stared into her drink like it might hold the answer. When she finally spoke, her voice was quieter.

“I think I’ve always been afraid to want this.”

Wanda’s expression softened.

Agatha swallowed. “I spent my whole life trying to be exactly what my mother expected me to be. And that didn’t include—” She hesitated, then forced herself to say it. “Women.”

She felt Wanda’s gaze sharpen, but her voice was gentle. “Did you ever let yourself think about it?”

Agatha let out a bitter huff. “I didn’t let myself do much of anything. I shoved it down, focused on my career, and then on Nicky. I built my life the way I was supposed to.”

Wanda was quiet for a moment, then tilted her head. “And now?”

Agatha exhaled slowly. “Now I feel freer than I ever have, like a weight has been lifted, you know?”

Wanda’s lips quirked. “So something has happened between you two.”

Agatha hesitated, then sighed, a reluctant smile tugging at her lips. “At my party.”

Wanda’s eyes lit up. “ I knew it .”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “It wasn’t—” She hesitated, warmth creeping up her neck. “It wasn’t much. We kissed.”

Wanda grinned like the cat that got the cream. “And?”

Agatha bit her lip, thinking about the way Rio had touched her—gently, carefully, like she was something precious. About how her heart had raced in a way she hadn’t felt in years.

“And it was…” She shook her head, fighting back a stupidly giddy smile. “It was good.”

Wanda laughed, delighted. “Oh, look at you.”

Agatha groaned. “Don’t start.”

“I have never seen you like this.” Wanda’s grin widened. “You’re glowing.”

“ I am not glowing .”

“You absolutely are!” Wanda leaned in. “So, what happened after?”

Agatha took a sip of her drink to buy herself a second. “She brought me breakfast on Monday.”

Wanda gasped dramatically. “Stop. Breakfast? The romance of it all.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t fight the grin that tugged at her lips. “She showed up before class with coffee and pastries. She even got the ones she saw me having when we ran into each other in the café.”

Wanda clutched her chest. “Agatha Harkness, you sap.”

Agatha groaned and rolled her eyes. “This was a mistake.”

“Oh, no, this is the best thing that’s ever happened to me,” Wanda said gleefully. “You, giddy over a woman? I never thought I’d see the day.”

Agatha shook her head, laughing despite herself.

Wanda nudged her foot with her own. “Listen, Ags. I get the concern, I do. But from what I’m seeing? This isn’t just some passing thing for you. This means something. And from what I saw at your party, the way she looked at you, treated you? This isn’t just some fling for her either. Rio is a smart cookie and she wouldn’t just jump into this, with how complex this thing is, just for the hell of it, you know?”

Agatha exhaled, staring at her drink again.

Wanda reached over, squeezing her hand. “So, be careful. Be smart. But don’t be afraid to be happy.”

Agatha met her gaze, something settling in her chest.

For the first time in a long time, she thought maybe—just maybe—she could be.

~*~

On Saturday, Agatha hadn’t planned to be out for long. She and Nicky had spent the morning at the museum, then wandered into a street fair they’d stumbled upon on their way home. The air smelled like roasted nuts, cider, and freshly baked bread, the crisp air of the fall season making it all the more inviting.

As Nicky happily munched on kettle corn, Agatha found herself texting Rio. It had become a habit — small check-ins, jokes, things that made her think of her. They hadn’t seen each other since Monday as both had been incredibly busy this week, and though it had only been a few days, it was ridiculous how much Agatha had felt the absence.

 

Rio

How’s your Saturday so far?

Agatha  

Eventful. Nicky dragged me to the museum, and now we’re at a street fair. My arms are full of things I didn’t plan on buying.

Rio  

Classic. What’d he con you into this time?

Agatha

A dinosaur book, and a bag of kettle corn the size of his torso.

Rio

He’s got taste. Where’s this street fair?

Agatha

Why? You planning on stalking me?

Rio

Always .

 

Agatha rolled her eyes but felt warmth bloom in her chest. She was about to type a reply when Nicky suddenly tugged at her sleeve.

“Mom! Look, it’s Rio! Over there!”

Agatha’s head snapped up, her stomach flipping before she even registered where he was pointing.

And there she was.

Rio stood by a food truck, her head thrown back in laughter at something Alice had said. She looked absolutely gorgeous — jeans, boots, and a fitted deep green sweater under her leather jacket. The sight of her, casual and relaxed, made something tighten in Agatha’s ribs.

Before she could react, Nicky took off running.

“Rio!”

Rio turned at the sound of his voice, her face lighting up just in time for him to crash into her. She let out a surprised laugh, crouching down. “Whoa! Hey, kid! Didn’t know I’d be running into my favorite Harkness today.”

Agatha followed at a more measured pace, schooling her features even as her pulse hammered in her throat.

“Well, well,” Rio grinned as she stood, sliding her hands into her jacket pockets. “Fancy meeting you here.”

Alice, standing beside her, glanced between them with a smirk. “Wow, what are the odds, huh?”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Chicago’s a big city.”

Rio’s smile was all mischief. “And yet, here you are. Stalking me.”

Agatha huffed, rolling her eyes. “You wish.”

Nicky looked up at Rio excitedly. “Can you come with us?”

Rio hesitated for the first time, glancing at Agatha, as if waiting for permission.

Agatha sighed, shaking her head fondly. “Rio probably has plans already, sweetheart.”

Rio grinned. “Actually, I don’t. Me and Alice were just hanging out. We were about to go home, to be honest,” her grin was teasing but hopeful.

“Great, so now you can come with us, right? Please, it’ll be fun!” Nicky insisted, and Rio looked at her again. Agatha nodded, an amused grin on her lips.

“Sure, why not?” Rio replied casually, but even she could hear the slight giddiness in her voice.

Alice snorted. “You two are ridiculous.” Agatha shot her an exasperated look, but Alice only winked before stepping back. “I’ll leave you lovebirds to it. See you at home, Rio.”

“Subtle,” Rio muttered under her breath.

Agatha ignored the heat creeping up her neck. “What were you even doing here?”

“Day off,” Rio said, falling into step beside her. “Alice and I were just grabbing food. Thought I’d have a rare, relaxing Saturday. And then—” she nudged Agatha’s shoulder playfully “—you appeared to torment me.”

Agatha fought back a smile. “Oh, how tragic.”

They wove through the street fair together, stopping to browse little stalls. Nicky dragged them toward a booth selling handcrafted wooden puzzles, and Rio crouched beside him, listening intently as he explained which one he wanted. Agatha found herself watching them, a strange, unfamiliar warmth settling in her chest.

It felt easy.

It felt dangerous.

And yet, when Rio straightened and shot her a look—soft, searching—Agatha didn’t fight it.

~*~

Agatha hadn’t expected to spend her afternoon like this—walking side by side with Rio through the street fair, Nicky happily bouncing between them. It felt domestic in a way that made her heart trip over itself if she thought about it too much.

And yet, she couldn’t bring herself to put distance between them.

It wasn’t anything obvious. Not really. But Rio’s presence had a way of filling up the space around her, drawing her in without even trying. She walked close enough that their arms brushed occasionally, and every time it happened, Agatha had to force herself not to react.

Meanwhile, Nicky had taken full advantage of Rio’s enthusiasm. He had her crouching at almost every stall, helping him inspect everything from polished stones to tiny model airplanes. He talked nonstop, and Rio, for her part, seemed to be enjoying every second of it.

At one point, she even threw Agatha a grin over her shoulder. “Is he always like this?”

Agatha snorted. “Only when he likes someone.”

Rio’s smile softened at that as she looked back down at Nicky, who was currently debating whether to get a tiny wooden fox or a dolphin. “Good to know I made the cut.”

Agatha tried not to let that mean something.

Eventually, they found themselves in front of a coffee stall. The scent of freshly brewed espresso filled the air, and without thinking, Agatha glanced up at the menu. Before she could even open her mouth, Rio turned to the barista and said, “A black coffee, another one with a splash of vanilla and a hot chocolate, please.”

Agatha blinked at her.

Rio just smirked. “I pay attention.”

That did something to Agatha’s chest that she absolutely refused to acknowledge.

When they had their drinks, they found a small bench under a tree, where Nicky happily dug into his hot chocolate, his legs swinging back and forth. Rio settled beside Agatha, leaning back with an easy sort of confidence that made her look like she belonged there.

“So,” Rio said, sipping her coffee. “Aside from being dragged to a museum and bribed into this fair, how’s your day been?”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “Bribed? Please.” Rio gave her a knowing look. Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, as if considering. “It’s not that terrible, you know.”

Rio smiled. “Neither is the company.”

Agatha exhaled, letting the moment settle. It had been a while since she felt this… light. Not just because of Rio, but because she wasn’t wearing the weight of work, of responsibilities, of expectations so heavily today.

She glanced at Rio. “What about you? Doing anything else today besides running into me?”

Rio hummed, tilting her head slightly. “Nah. Just planned to relax. Maybe catch up on some reading.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Reading? For fun?”

Rio grinned. “Shocking, right?”

“Very. I didn’t think you even had time for stuff like that.”

Rio chuckled, then nudged her playfully. “What about you? Any wild Saturday night plans?”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I’m a mother to an eight-year-old and a professor. Wild doesn’t exactly apply to me.”

Rio scoffed. “Please. I’ve seen you at work, Dr. Harkness. You terrify grown ass humans on a daily basis.”

Agatha smirked. “And yet, here you are, voluntarily spending time with me.”

Rio’s gaze flickered, something unreadable passing through her expression. Then, before Agatha could dissect it, she grinned. “Guess I like living on the edge.”

Before Agatha could formulate a response, Nicky perked up beside them. “Rio, can we go look at the toy swords again?”

Rio shot Agatha a look. “Toy swords?”

Agatha sighed. “It’s a phase.”

Nicky tugged at Rio’s sleeve insistently. “Please?”

Rio laughed, already standing. “Alright, kid, let’s go find your future weapon of choice.”

Agatha just shook her head, watching as they wandered off toward one of the stalls again.

This was dangerous. This feeling.

But for now, she allowed herself to enjoy it.

Yeah. She could definitely get used to this.

Agatha moved around the kitchen in a steady, almost meditative rhythm as she cooked. Nicky sat on a stool beside her, watching intently as she flipped pancakes and scrambled eggs. He had been in charge of mixing the batter, his small hands careful as he stirred, but Agatha took over when it came time for the hot pan.

The morning was slow and easy, warmth filling the space between them. But Agatha’s mind kept drifting — kept replaying last night. The quiet intimacy, the way Rio had been so attuned to her, so patient, so undeniably present. It had been… more than she ever expected, more than she even thought she could have.

She caught herself smiling as she plated the eggs. It wasn’t just the physical closeness that had taken her breath away — it was the way Rio made her feel seen, the way she made space for Agatha in a way no one ever had before.

The sound of footsteps descending the stairs pulled her out of her thoughts. She turned to see Rio walking into the kitchen, looking effortlessly beautiful despite the slightly rumpled edges of her clothes. Her hair was still tousled from sleep, and she met Agatha’s gaze with a small, warm smile.

“Morning,” Rio greeted, her voice still carrying the rasp of sleep.

Nicky turned to look at her, blinking in surprise. His eyes flicked to Agatha in clear confusion, as if trying to piece together why Rio was here at breakfast time.

“Hey, buddy,” Rio said with an easy grin, slipping into one of the chairs at the table.

Nicky glanced back at Agatha, who kept her voice casual as she said, “Rio stayed over because it got late last night. We were talking a lot, and it made more sense than her driving home in the middle of the night.”

Nicky processed that for a moment, then shrugged. “Oh. Okay.”

Rio chuckled, leaning her arms on the table. “You okay with me sticking around for pancakes?”

Nicky nodded, grinning. “Yeah! Mom makes the best pancakes.”

Rio winked. “Good to know.”

Breakfast was easy, full of light conversation and laughter. Rio teased Nicky about his favorite soccer players, stole a bite of his pancake just to hear him protest, and shared stories about the firehouse. Agatha watched it all unfold, sipping her coffee, feeling something settle in her chest—something content. Something she wasn’t sure she was ready to name.

After breakfast, they lingered in the living room for a while. Nicky built something elaborate with his Legos while Rio and Agatha just hung out, their knees bumping occasionally, their conversation flowing easily. But eventually, Rio checked the time and let out a small sigh.

“I should get going,” she said, stretching. “I’ve got a shift tonight, and I still have a few things to do at home before then.”

Agatha nodded, pushing down the small pang of disappointment. “Of course.”

Rio grabbed her jacket, but before she could slip it on, Agatha stepped closer. Her hand brushed over Rio’s wrist, just enough to make her pause. “Last night was…” She hesitated, searching for the right words. “Amazing,” she finally settled on, a quiet certainty in her voice.

Rio’s expression softened, her eyes holding something deep, something knowing. She reached out, tucking a stray curl behind Agatha’s ear. “Yeah,” she murmured, a slow, lazy smile tugging at her lips. “It really was.”

Agatha exhaled, and before she could overthink it, she leaned in, pressing a lingering, unhurried kiss to Rio’s lips. When she pulled back, Rio just looked at her for a moment, her thumb brushing lightly against Agatha’s hand.

“I’ll see you tomorrow,” Rio promised.

Agatha nodded, watching as Rio turned to Nicky, who was now setting up a game to play on his Xbox.

“See you later, Rio!” Nicky called, with a bright smile on his face.

Rio grinned and walked over to him. “Later, kiddo.” She held up her hand for a high-five, which Nicky returned with enthusiasm. Then, with one last glance at Agatha, she squeezed her hand as she passed by her, and then she was out the door.

Agatha lingered for a second before turning back to the kitchen, wiping down the counters and putting away the last few dishes. Nicky reappeared a few minutes later, kicking his soccer ball lightly against the floor.

“That was nice,” he said casually. “Having breakfast with Rio.”

Agatha turned to look at him, considering his words for a moment before asking, “Do you like Rio?”

Nicky nodded immediately. “Yeah, she’s cool. And funny. And nice.”

Agatha smiled, leaning back against the counter. “Yeah, she is.”

And as she stood there, letting the quiet settle around them, she realized how much those words meant.

Monday morning arrived, and Agatha’s mind buzzed with a mix of excitement and anxiety. She had sent Rio a quick text while sipping her coffee.

Agatha

How was your shift? If you’re able to get to Northwestern earlier today, I’ll have breakfast ready for us.

I’ll be there in 30 minutes. And don’t worry about breakfast, I can grab us something on the way.

Agatha

No, I’ve got it this time. You don’t need to worry. See you soon.

Rio hesitated, the weight of her words clearly pressing down on her. “We had a patient last night, a GSW,” she began, her voice shaking slightly. “And one of his buddies pulled a gun on me and Will.”

Rio nodded but looked away, her jaw tight. “Yeah, but… it was scary. Especially for Will. He’s only 23, and he’s never had to deal with anything like this before. “I keep thinking about Will,” Rio said quietly. “How fragile life is, you know? I don’t want anything bad to happen to him. But what if I can’t always protect him?”

Agatha’s heart ached for her, knowing how deeply she cared for her colleagues, for the people she worked with. “You don’t have to protect everyone all the time,” Agatha said gently. “You’re human, too. And no one expects you to carry everything.”

Rio met her gaze, her eyes soft and full of vulnerability. “I’m just scared sometimes, you know? I’m not sure how much longer I can keep doing this. It gets exhausting.”

“I know,” Agatha said, feeling the weight of Rio’s words, knowing she didn’t have an easy job. “But you don’t have to shoulder it alone. You’ve got people who care about you. You’ve got me.”

Rio’s eyes softened even more, her hand reaching across the desk to rest on Agatha’s. She gave it a gentle squeeze, a silent acknowledgment of the support Agatha was offering.

Then, as the silence stretched between them, Rio’s phone buzzed. It was a reminder about class. They both looked at the time and realized it was almost time for students to start trickling in.

“We should probably get ready,” Agatha said reluctantly, standing up. “Class is almost here.”

“I know,” Rio said with a small smile, standing up with her. She took a deep breath, still looking a little shaken but steadier now, thanks to Agatha’s presence. “Thanks for breakfast. I really needed this.”

“Anytime,” Agatha said, squeezing Rio’s shoulder. “Don’t forget, you don’t have to carry it all by yourself.”

Rio smiled softly as they both prepared to face the flood of students. “I won’t forget. I promise.”

Rio placed a gentle kiss to Agatha’s lips, before making her way to her usual spot. The first students began trickling into the lecture hall, but for a brief moment, the world around them seemed a little less overwhelming.

Agatha was sitting at her desk in her office a couple of days later, going over a few papers when she heard the knock. Nicky was completely engrossed in his book by the window, and barely looked up. She’d had to pick him and bring him back to Northwestern so she could finish her office hours, but at this point, he was already used to it.

She called out, “Come in,” expecting it to be one of the students with a simple question about the assignment.

But when the door swung open, it wasn’t the usual polite knock-and-enter from a student. It was Thomas Jordan, his gaze immediately locking with hers as he stepped inside with a look of quiet determination. His demeanor immediately put Agatha on edge.

“Professor Harkness,” Jordan said, his voice smooth but laced with an undertone that immediately set her instincts on alert. “I just wanted to clarify the presentation requirements for the assignment.”

Agatha straightened in her chair, offering him a tight smile. “Everything you need to know is in the email I sent last week,” she replied coolly, her mind already anticipating where this conversation might be headed.

Jordan didn’t move, his posture stiff and his eyes not leaving her. “Right, of course. But actually, there’s something more important I wanted to discuss — something more pressing.” He took another step into the room, and Agatha’s gut tightened. “I was hoping we could revisit the mentorship decision.”

She felt the shift in the air, the slight pressure in his voice. It was more than a student simply asking for clarification; this was an attempt at leverage, a challenge.

“I’ve already made my decision, Jordan, as I’ve already told you several times,” Agatha said firmly, her tone unwavering. “I approved five students for the mentorship. My decision is final.”

Jordan’s eyes narrowed, the tension in his body rising as his tone shifted. “With all due respect, Professor, I think you made a mistake,” he said, his voice dropping a notch. “Rio Vidal? She’s not even that good and she’s exhausted 90% of the time, can barely keep up in classes. I’m the one with the qualifications and availability. Do you know who my father is? I’m a legacy here. I deserve that mentorship, and I know you know it.”

Agatha’s breath caught. She could feel his frustration rolling off him in waves, the way he was slowly closing the space between them, trying to intimidate her with his presence. His gaze was unrelenting, and for a brief moment, she wondered if he had ever actually cared about the mentorship or if this was just about proving himself to her.

“I’ve already made my decision,” she repeated, her voice steady despite the rising tension. “You’re a bright student, but I’ve made the choice to mentor Ms. Vidal and the other students as their research proposals were excellent and in line with my area of research. I’m not reconsidering. I suggest you look for another mentor next semester.”

Jordan stepped closer to her desk, and Agatha instinctively stood straighter, the air between them thick with unspoken threats. “You don’t understand, Professor,” he said, his voice low and menacing now. “If you just give me a chance, I could do so much more than her, than any of them. You might want to think about that, before you lose out on the opportunity to work with someone who can truly make a difference. Someone who actually deserves that spot.”

The words were sharp, cutting through the air like a threat, and Agatha’s heart rate spiked. There was something in his demeanor now—something darker, more insistent—that made her stomach churn. He wasn’t just disappointed; he was angry, and his anger was directed at her.

Her hand tightened around the edge of her desk, and for the first time, she felt the weight of his intimidation. This wasn’t just a student disagreeing with a decision; this was someone trying to manipulate her, to push her into backing down.

“I have made my choice, Mr. Jordan,” she said one last time, her voice cold but firm. “And I won’t be swayed. I don’t care who your father is, as you’re the one enrolled in this program, not him.”

Jordan seemed to consider her for a moment, then nodded stiffly. “Fine,” he muttered. “But don’t say I didn’t warn you.” With that, he turned sharply and walked out, his footsteps heavy, the door closing behind him with a definitive snap.

Agatha stood still for a moment, her heart pounding in her chest. She hadn’t realized how shaken she was until the door clicked shut. She had dealt with challenging students before, but there was something about the way Jordan had entered her space, his body language so aggressive, that made her skin crawl. And that last part — “Don’t say I didn’t warn you” — echoed in her mind.

Nicky glanced up from his book, sensing the change in the atmosphere. “Is everything okay, Mom?”

Agatha forced a smile, her voice a little too tight. “Everything’s fine, sweetie. I just need a quick break, okay?”

She took Nicky’s hand and guided him out of the office. They walked to the nearby café, and Agatha ordered them both hot chocolate, trying to shake off the unease that had settled in her chest. She needed to clear her head, needed to reset.

As they sipped their drinks in silence, Agatha’s phone buzzed in her pocket. She pulled it out, finding a message from Rio:

Rio

Hey beautiful! How’s your day going? Hope everything’s good.

Agatha

I’m okay. Just had a run-in with Jordan. He’s been pushing me on the mentorship thing. I’m feeling a little shaken, honestly.

 

Rio

Are you okay? Did he do anything to you? 

Want to talk later?

Agatha

I’ll be fine. I just need to process this. But yes, maybe later. Let’s catch up.

After a few more minutes, Agatha felt a little more composed, but the knot in her stomach remained. Once Nicky had finished his drink, they headed back to the building. Agatha’s mind was still reeling from her encounter with Jordan. She knew she needed to talk about it, but she wasn’t sure who to turn to.

As she walked through the hallways, she ran into Wanda, who noticed immediately that something was off.

“Agatha,” Wanda said, raising an eyebrow. “What happened? You look like you’ve just seen a ghost.”

Agatha sighed, glancing around to make sure Nicky wasn’t paying attention. “It’s a student, Thomas Jordan. He came into my office hours, tried to pressure me again about the mentorship. I’ve told him several times that my decision was final, but he… he hasn’t taken it well. The way he was acting — it felt more like a threat than a request.”

Wanda’s expression darkened. “A threat? Are you serious?”

“Yeah,” Agatha replied quietly, her voice shaken. “He got way too close to me, started speaking in that way — like he was warning me, you know? I don’t know. It really rattled me. I don’t know if I’m overreacting, but it didn’t sit right with me.”

Wanda placed a hand on her shoulder, her eyes serious. “You’re not overreacting, Agatha. That doesn’t sound like just disappointment. That sounds like intimidation. You need to keep an eye on him. And report him if necessary.”

Agatha nodded, grateful for Wanda’s support. “I will. I just need to clear my head, but I’ll be okay.”

They exchanged a few more words before Agatha headed back to her office. Despite her efforts to push it out of her mind, Jordan’s words lingered, like a shadow she couldn’t quite shake.

Agatha was still on edge by the time she got home. Even as she went through the familiar motions of her evening—making dinner, helping Nicky with his homework—her thoughts kept circling back to Jordan. The way he had walked into her office like he owned the place, the tone of his voice, the way he hadn’t even tried to mask his frustration. She didn’t like it.

Rio let their hands rest together for a moment, tracing her thumb over Agatha’s knuckles absentmindedly. The room felt warm, settled in a way that made her want to stay right here, with Agatha curled up beside her, for as long as possible.
