Wanda nodded, picking up a section of the model. “Excellent. This will give us a hands-on look at the limbic system, which, as we were just discussing, plays a key role in emotional processing.”

Rio caught the way Agatha’s mouth twitched ever so slightly before she took a step back, clearly ready to make her exit.

“Well, I’ll leave you to it,” Agatha said, nodding to Wanda before sparing Rio one last look.

Rio exhaled slowly, only now realizing she’d been gripping the edge of her desk.

Wanda, who never missed anything, gave her a knowing look before addressing the class again.

“Now,” she said, gesturing to the brain model. “Let’s take a closer look.”

Rio did her best to focus.

But damn if it wasn’t hard.

 

~*~

Rio was waiting outside Agatha’s office, arms crossed as she tried to calm the fluttering nerves in her stomach. Jordan was standing beside her, pretending to look at his phone but clearly waiting for an opening to say something.

“Guess the teacher’s pet’s here early, huh?” Jordan said, his voice casual but with a clear edge of sarcasm.

Rio rolled her eyes but kept her gaze ahead, not giving him the satisfaction of a reaction. “Do you need something, Jordan?” she raised an eyebrow, her tone cool and formal.

Jordan merely shrugged. “So you and Dr. Harkness are getting pretty close, huh?”

Rio glanced at him sharply, but before she could respond, the door to Agatha’s office opened. Agatha stepped out, her attention shifting immediately to Jordan.

“Mr. Jordan, you’re early for your meeting. Come on in,” she said, her voice polite but firm.

Rio gave a small nod as Agatha motioned for Jordan to enter. She remained outside, stewing over Jordan’s comments. What does he think? That he can just say whatever he wants?

Her eyes narrowed as the door clicked shut. She had been ready to talk to Agatha about Nicky’s question, but now she just felt irritated, unsure if she should bring it up right away or let things settle.

After a few minutes, the door opened again, and Jordan stepped out, clearly irritated. It didn’t take long for  Agatha to pop her head outside, catching Rio’s eye immediately. She gave Rio a small, apologetic smile.

“Sorry about that,” Agatha said. “Jordan can be a bit relentless.”

Rio smiled back, though she still felt a little on edge. “It’s fine. I just—”

“You okay?” Agatha asked, her voice warm and understanding. Rio took a breath, finally letting go of the irritation as she walked into Agatha’s office.

“Yeah, I just need to tell you something,” Rio said, her tone softer now that they were alone. “It’s about Nicky.”

Agatha’s brow furrowed, a sudden wave of concern crossing her face. “What happened?”

Rio exhaled and sat down in one of the chairs, trying to push aside the discomfort she still felt. “This morning, he asked me if I liked you… as a girlfriend.”

Agatha froze for a moment, blinking at her in surprise. “What?”

Rio chuckled nervously. “Yeah. I wasn’t sure how to answer, so I thought I should just tell you before he says anything to you.”

Agatha blinked again, then burst out laughing. The sound was rich and warm, completely unexpected but easing the tension in the room. “He asked you that?” she repeated, shaking her head in disbelief.

Rio smiled sheepishly. “Yeah. He’s very direct.”

Agatha shook her head again, amusement still flickering in her eyes. Then, her expression softened, and she leaned in slightly. “But listen, Rio…” Her voice lowered a bit, her eyes locking with Rio’s. “I don’t care about labels. I just care about us.”

Rio felt a knot in her stomach loosen, but she rushed to speak before Agatha could continue. “I mean, I didn’t know how you felt about labels or whatever, so I didn’t want to—”

“Rio, hey,” Agatha interrupted softly, her hand gently reaching for Rio’s. “That’s a label I could get behind. If that’s what you want too.”

Rio felt her heart race, her breath catching as she looked into Agatha’s eyes. She smiled slowly, the relief overwhelming. “Okay,” she whispered, the weight of the conversation settling between them but in a way that felt right.

~*~

After her nephrology class, Rio felt the weight of the week finally lifting a little. She pulled out her phone and texted Agatha.

Rio

Hey, how about joining us for a drink tonight? Alice, Jen, and Will are coming too, and I think it could be fun for all of us to hang out. Let me know if you’re free.

She pressed send, leaning back in her seat. A few minutes later, her phone buzzed with Agatha’s reply.

Agatha

Sounds good! Let me check with Viz if he can keep Nicky for a bit after soccer practice. I’ll let you know soon.

Rio smiled, excitement bubbling up at the thought of spending more time with Agatha outside of their usual setting. Just as she was about to put her phone down, another message came through from Agatha.

Agatha

By the way, would it be alright if I brought Wanda too? She’s been asking about you.

Rio felt her stomach flutter at the thought of Wanda joining them. She and Wanda had shared a couple of casual conversations, and the idea of Agatha wanting her friend to join them only seemed to signal how comfortable Agatha was getting with the idea of them spending more time together.

Rio

Of course! The more the merrier. I’ll text you the address. Let me know when you’re on your way.

Rio set her phone down and let out a small sigh of contentment. It felt good to have plans, to know there would be space for laughter and lightheartedness that evening. It had been a stressful week for both of them, and the thought of just enjoying the evening together was a welcome reprieve.

 

~*~

Rio arrived at the bar feeling lighter than she had in a long time. Maybe it was the easy way things had settled between her and Agatha after their conversation earlier that day — when she’d told Agatha that Nicky had asked if she liked his mom as a girlfriend, and Agatha hadn’t objected. She’d expected hesitation, maybe even a deflection, but Agatha had only let the words settle between them without resistance.

That meant something.

She spotted Agatha and Wanda easily, already seated at a booth near the back. Agatha looked stunning, as she always did, but there was something softer about her in this moment—her shoulders a little more relaxed, the dim bar lighting catching on the edges of her smile. Rio didn’t think she’d ever get used to the way Agatha looked at her now, not with distance or guarded politeness, but with familiarity. With affection.

As soon as Agatha met her gaze, Rio felt her own smile forming, something instinctive. She walked toward them, heart picking up speed, and slid into the booth beside Agatha, their bodies naturally gravitating toward each other.

“Hey,” Rio murmured, leaning in to press a slow, warm kiss to Agatha’s cheek. Her hand found Agatha’s thigh under the table, fingers resting there like it was the most natural thing in the world.

Agatha exhaled, barely audible, but Rio felt it against her skin. “Hey,” she answered, turning just slightly so their faces were closer. “You look—” Agatha paused, eyes scanning her, taking her in. “Beautiful.”

Rio’s lips curled. “I was about to say the same thing.”

Wanda, sipping her drink, raised an eyebrow. “You two are adorable. Sickening, but adorable.”

Rio let out a soft laugh, but it didn’t deter her from staying close to Agatha, from letting her thumb trace absentmindedly along the inside of Agatha’s knee.

“They’ll be here soon,” she said, glancing toward the entrance.

As if on cue, the door swung open, and Alice walked in with her girlfriend, Jennifer, and Will. Alice immediately spotted them and waved in that exaggerated, look at me way she always did.

“There they are,” Alice called as she strode over, clapping a hand on Rio’s shoulder. “Hey, stranger.”

Rio grinned and nudged her with her elbow. “Took you long enough.”

Alice ignored her and turned to Agatha. “Good to see you again.”

Agatha gave a small nod. “Likewise.”

Rio cleared her throat, turning to Jennifer and Will. “Alright, let’s make this official. Agatha, Wanda — this is Jen, Alice’s girlfriend, and Will, my partner from the firehouse.”

Jen smiled warmly, extending a hand. “It’s great to meet you both.”

Will shook Agatha’s hand, offering a friendly grin. “Nice to finally meet you. Rio talks a lot about you.”

Rio groaned, already knowing where this was going. “Okay, not in a weird way.”

Agatha’s lips curved, interest flickering across her face. “Oh?”

Alice leaned in, all too eager. “Oh yeah. She’s been talking about you nonstop since—”

Rio shot her a sharp look, and Alice smirked but let it go. For now.

They ordered drinks, the conversation slipping into an easy rhythm, but the teasing wasn’t over yet.

“So,” Wanda mused about an hour into their evening, giving Alice a curious look. “You mentioned something about the museum?”

Alice grinned, clearly delighted to have an audience. “Oh, you don’t know the half of it. Nicky was so into the exhibits that I had to keep him occupied for, what, forty minutes? Just so these two could have some alone time.”

Rio blinked. “Wait — you did that on purpose?”

Alice scoffed. “Uh, yeah. You think I didn’t notice the whole vibe you two had going on? Please, I knew exactly what was happening. And Nicky? That kid was so locked in on that heart exhibit, I could’ve left him there for hours.”

Wanda snorted, shaking her head. Even Agatha smirked, clearly amused.

“I did notice you were keeping him busy for a while,” Agatha admitted, sipping her drink. There was a teasing glint in her eyes, subtle but unmistakable.

Alice shrugged, looking very pleased with herself. “I mean, you two needed some alone time to sort out your shit, right?”

Rio exhaled, shaking her head, but she couldn’t fight the warmth spreading through her chest. She leaned back against the booth, her knee brushing against Agatha’s under the table.

Alice, for once, seemed to shift into something more genuine. She watched them for a moment, expression thoughtful. “I’ll admit,” she said, voice quieter now, “I was a little worried you two were in over your heads.”

Rio felt Agatha still slightly beside her, though her expression remained neutral.

Alice continued, her gaze flicking between them. “But… I see it now. You two make sense.”

Rio glanced at Agatha, and for the first time tonight, there was something solid there — something unspoken, but understood.

“We’re figuring it out,” Rio said softly, her fingers grazing Agatha’s under the table.

Alice studied them for a beat longer, then nodded. “Good.”

The conversation shifted, flowing into stories from work, casual banter, and shared laughter. But through it all, Rio felt something different tonight.

She felt settled.

Because Alice was right. They were in deep. But for once, that didn’t feel like a bad thing.

 

~*~

 

The night stretched on in easy conversation and laughter, drinks dwindling as the stories got better — especially when Alice started digging into Rio’s early days as a paramedic.

“—and this rookie right here,” Alice gestured at Rio, who groaned dramatically, “once tried to outmuscle a very intoxicated patient into sitting still for an IV. Guess how that went?”

Will, Rio’s current partner, grinned. “Oh, this is gonna be good.”

Alice smirked. “He threw up directly on her. Head to toe. I’ve never seen a person look so personally betrayed in my life.”

Will burst into laughter, practically doubling over. “No way.”

“It was disgusting,” Rio muttered, shaking her head. “And Alice here did not help. She just stood there, laughing.”

“I was supervising,” Alice said, deadpan. “And now you have a great ‘humble beginnings’ story. You’re welcome.”

Agatha, sitting beside Rio, smirked over the rim of her wine glass. “I do appreciate a well-crafted narrative.”

Rio shot her a look. “Et tu, Agatha?”

Agatha gave a slow, deliberate shrug.

Will was still grinning. “I’m just glad I know all this now. I will be using it against you.”

“Great,” Rio muttered. “This is the worst night of my life.”

“Oh, please,” Alice nudged her. “You love the attention.”

At the other end of the table, Wanda checked her phone and sighed. “Alright, some of us actually need sleep.”

“Already?” Jen asked.

“Yes, already.” Wanda directed her gaze at Agatha. “Nicky’s all set for the night, so don’t rush. Take your time, enjoy yourself. Just text me when you’re on your way to get him.”

Agatha smiled, grateful. “Thank you, Wanda.”

“Of course,” Wanda said, sliding out of the booth. “Enjoy yourselves.”

The group lingered for a while longer, but eventually, the night started winding down. Will left first, then Alice and Jen, Alice shooting Rio one last smirk before disappearing into the night.

That left just the two of them.

Stepping outside the bar, the night air cool against her skin, Agatha exhaled softly. Rio was beside her in an instant, hands tucked in her jacket pockets.

“So,” Rio murmured, glancing around. “Uber?”

Agatha nodded. “Uber.”

Rio watched as Agatha fiddled with her phone, a comfortable silence stretching between them. 

She turned slightly, studying Agatha in the dim glow of the streetlights. “You know,” she murmured, voice dipping lower, “I really like seeing you like this.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Like what?”

“Relaxed,” Rio said, letting her fingers graze Agatha’s wrist. “Happy.”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, something flickering across her expression — surprise, maybe. Understanding. Her gaze dropped briefly to Rio’s mouth before she met her eyes again.

And then, before either of them could overthink it, Rio took a step forward and pressed Agatha against the cool brick of the bar.

Agatha barely had time to react before Rio’s lips were on hers — firm, certain, stealing the breath from her lungs. She gasped softly against her mouth, her hands finding Rio’s waist, pulling her closer as she melted into the kiss.

It was different from their first. No hesitation. No questions. Just a slow, deep certainty, the weight of the night pressing in around them.

When they pulled apart, Agatha exhaled, her forehead resting lightly against Rio’s.

Rio smirked. “You make me want to do reckless things.”

Agatha let out a quiet laugh. “That was reckless.”

“Mm,” Rio hummed. “Not sorry.”

Agatha shook her head, arms still around Rio’s waist. She let out a contented sigh.

Rio pushed a strand of her hair behind her ear, “You know… when I told you what Nicky said about the girlfriend thing?”

Agatha's expression softened. “Yeah?”

“You didn’t object.”

A slow smile tugged at Agatha’s lips. “Neither did you.”

Rio studied her for a beat, then, almost shyly, she admitted, “No. I didn’t.”

Agatha’s  grip on her tightened, just slightly. “Do you want to object?”

Rio’s breath hitched, something settling in her chest as she shook her head. “No,” she said, quiet but sure. “I don’t.”

Agatha’s  smile widened, a warmth flickering behind her eyes. “Good,” she inhaled deeply before glancing down at her phone. “Come home with me?”

Rio’s brows lifted slightly, but then a slow, easy grin spread across her lips. “Yeah,” she said. “I’d like that.”

Agatha exhaled, relieved, before pulling up the Uber app.

“You keep looking at me like that, Vidal,” she murmured without looking up, “and I might have to reconsider inviting you over.”

Rio smirked. “No, you won’t.”

Agatha huffed, but she didn’t argue.

A few minutes later, the Uber arrived, and they slid into the backseat together. The drive to Wanda’s was quiet, filled with an easy anticipation. Agatha sent a quick text letting Wanda know they were on their way, and Rio watched the way her fingers moved over the screen, something oddly domestic about it.

When they reached Wanda’s, Agatha barely had to knock before the door swung open.

Wanda stood there, arms crossed, eyes flicking between them with an amused smirk. “Well, well,” she drawled. “Look who finally decided to call it a night.”

“Don’t start,” Agatha warned, stepping inside.

Rio just grinned. “Hey, Wanda.”

“Hey, Rio.” Wanda smirked. “Have fun?”

Agatha shot her a look. “Nicky?”

Wanda chuckled. “He’s on the couch, passed out. Viz got them all settled after soccer practice.”

Agatha sighed, running a hand through her hair. “I appreciate it.”

Wanda’s eyes flicked to Rio, her smirk deepening. “You ready for an early morning? That kid’s got more energy than should be legally allowed.”

Rio chuckled. “I can handle it.”

“Uh-huh.” Wanda clearly didn’t believe her, but she stepped aside.

Agatha moved to the couch, kneeling beside Nicky. “Nicky, sweetheart,” she murmured, brushing his hair back.

He stirred, blinking up at her. “Mom?”

“Time to go home, baby.”

Nicky yawned, rubbing his eyes before noticing Rio. “Rio.”

“Hey, bud,” Rio said softly. “You ready?”

He nodded, still groggy, as Agatha helped him up. She grabbed his backpack, giving Wanda a grateful look. “Thanks again.”

Wanda smiled. “Don’t mention it. Have a good night, you guys.”

As they stepped outside, Nicky curled up against Agatha’s side, half-asleep before they even reached the waiting Uber.

Rio caught Agatha’s eye, and in the quiet hum of the ride home, she reached over, lacing their fingers together.

Agatha squeezed back.

Tonight, everything felt exactly as it should be.

 

 

Chapter 13

Chapter Notes

As always, I appreciate you guys more than you know. I hope you enjoy this one.

Wednesday evening came too quickly.

Rio leaned against the lockers at the firehouse, scrolling through her phone while the rest of her shift wound down. The station was still buzzing with activity—someone was messing with the coffee machine in the kitchen, a couple of the guys were finishing reports, and Alice was loudly debating something with William near the engine bay.

Rio tuned it all out, her focus entirely on her phone as she typed out a message.

Agatha

Just confirming—your plan is still to leave after your shift?

Rio

Yep. Gonna power through and drive straight there. Should get to my parents’ place around 9ish.

Agatha

That’s a long day.

Rio

I’ve had longer .

She grinned, knowing exactly how Agatha would react to that—probably shaking her head, maybe even rolling her eyes a little. And sure enough, a moment later—

Agatha

Still. Be careful on the road.

Rio

Always.

The conversation stretched into easy back-and-forth messages. They made tentative plans to see each other over the weekend once Rio was back in town. She’d be working Friday, but maybe they could grab dinner on Saturday. And if not, definitely Sunday.

By the time she threw her duffel bag over her shoulder and headed out to her car, she was still smiling.

A few hours later, Rio stepped into her parents’ house and was immediately wrapped in the familiar warmth of home. Her mom pulled her into a hug, her dad clapped her on the back, and before she even made it to the kitchen, one of her brothers was already trying to wrestle her into a headlock.

It was chaos. Loud, overwhelming, wonderful chaos.

She spent the rest of the evening catching up with her family — helping her mom sneak extra seasoning into a dish, listening to her dad talk about his latest garage project, and bickering with her brothers over who was washing the dishes. Her sister Gabriela, of course, was the ringmaster of it all, stirring up trouble and dodging responsibility at every turn.

By the time Rio finally got a moment to herself, it was late, and she was sprawled out on her childhood bed, scrolling through her phone. She was about to text Agatha when her phone buzzed first.

Incoming video call: Agatha.

A grin tugged at her lips as she swiped to accept, and then Agatha’s face filled the screen, slightly grainy but still just as stunning as ever.

“Hey,” Rio greeted, her voice already softening.

“Hey yourself,” Agatha murmured, a small smile on her lips.

Rio shifted, getting more comfortable against her pillows. “Just got exiled to my room for a bit. Too much chaos in the kitchen.”

Agatha smirked. “You? Running from chaos? I don’t believe it.”

Rio rolled her eyes, about to retort, when suddenly there was a blur of movement behind her — a mess of dark hair and a wicked grin as her sister Gabriela all but launched herself onto the bed.

“Ohhh,” Gabriela sing-songed, peering at the screen, “is this the girlfriend?”

Rio groaned, trying to shove her away. “Gabi, seriously—”

But Gabriela was already grinning wide. “Hi! You must be Agatha. I’m Gabriela, everyone’s favorite sibling.”

Agatha raised an amused brow. “Oh? I was under the impression that was Rio.”

Gabriela gasped dramatically. “She told you that? Lies. Slander .”

Rio groaned again. “Please ignore her.”

“No, no, don’t ignore me,” Gabriela insisted. “I have questions.”

Rio made a strangled noise. “You do not have questions—”

“Oh, but I do,” Gabriela countered, eyes dancing. Then she leaned in closer to the camera and whispered, “Blink twice if you’re in this under duress.”

Agatha actually laughed, and Rio buried her face in her hands.

“I hate you,” she muttered.

“No, you love me,” Gabriela corrected smugly before turning back to Agatha. “It’s nice to meet you. And don’t worry, I won’t actually interrogate you. Yet.”

“I appreciate that,” Agatha said, thoroughly entertained.

Gabriela, still lounging on Rio’s bed, leaned in toward the screen with a conspiratorial grin. “Sooo, how did you two meet?”

Agatha glanced at Rio, whose expression was already screaming oh no.

“At Northwestern,” Agatha said smoothly. “I’m her professor.”

Gabriela’s eyes widened. “Wait, what ?” She whirled on Rio, smacking her arm. “You didn’t tell me that part!”

Rio groaned, rubbing her temples. “Because I knew you’d be like this.”

Gabriela cackled. “Oh, this is so much better than I imagined.”

“She’s not just my professor,” Rio muttered.

Agatha, enjoying this far too much, took pity on her. “Technically, we met before that,” she said, tilting her head. “Rio pulled me out of a wrecked car.”

Gabriela’s mouth dropped open. “Wait. Wait. You—” She turned to Rio. “You saved her life, and she’s your professor? This is straight-up a soap opera. Tell me there was dramatic eye contact. Tell me .”

Rio groaned. “I was literally just doing my job.”

“And yet,” Gabriela mused, looking back at Agatha, “here you are.”

Agatha’s lips twitched. “Here I am.”

Gabriela shook her head in awe. “Unbelievable. You’re living in a romance novel, baby girl,” she ruffled Rio’s hair, much to her utter embarrassment. “I’m a little jealous, to be honest.”

Rio gave Agatha a long-suffering look. “You see what I deal with?”

Agatha chuckled. “I think it’s charming.”

Gabriela grinned. “Oh, I like her. She’s smart and hot!”

Rio groaned again as Gabriela dramatically flopped off the bed and walked out, still laughing to herself. “Bye, Agatha! It was nice to meet you,” she called out over her shoulder before closing the door.

Agatha smirked. “I have to say, I like her too.”

“Sure you do,” Rio huffed, but there was warmth in her eyes as she let her head tip back against the pillow. “I miss you.”

Agatha’s teasing faded into something softer, something real. “I miss you too.”

 

~*~

The house was quiet that morning, the kind of stillness that only came after a long night of family and food. Most of the household was still sleeping off the previous night’s Thanksgiving feast, but Rio had never been the type to sleep in, even when she wanted to. Not when her mind was tangled in thoughts of her.

She found her mother in the kitchen, already making coffee, the rich aroma filling the air.

“You’re up early,” her mom said, glancing over her shoulder.

Rio gave a half-hearted shrug as she pulled out a chair at the kitchen table. “So are you.”

Her mother hummed, setting down two mugs before sitting across from her. She didn’t say anything else, just took a slow sip of her coffee and gave Rio that look — one that had always made her feel like a kid caught sneaking cookies before dinner. Like her mom could see straight through her.

Rio exhaled, rubbing the back of her neck. “I, uh… there’s something I wanna tell you.”

Her mother just nodded, waiting.

Rio hesitated, fingers drumming against the ceramic of her mug. “I’m seeing someone.”

The slow, knowing smile that spread across her mom’s face was both comforting and terrifying. “Oh?”

“Yeah,” Rio huffed, shaking her head. “Her name’s Agatha.”

Her mom tilted her head slightly. “Agatha.” She let the name settle before taking another sip of coffee. “Tell me about her.”

Rio ran a hand through her hair. “She’s… incredible. She’s brilliant . The kind of person who walks into a room and everyone just knows she’s the smartest person there. Sharp as hell, but also—” She sighed. “She’s got this softness under all of it, you know? Even if she tries to hide it.”

Her mom’s smile grew. “You’re already completely gone for her, aren’t you?”

Rio let out a dry laugh. “I think I was from the start.”

Her mom’s gaze softened. “How did you meet?”

Rio hesitated for a second, then decided there was no point in holding back now. “I was the one who got the call about her accident,” she admitted. “She and her son — his name is Nicky — were in a car crash. Nothing too serious, but I was the paramedic on scene. I pulled her out of the wreck. That’s how we met.”

Her mother blinked, surprised. “ Dios mío . That’s a hell of a way to meet someone.”

“Yeah,” Rio breathed out a small laugh. “And then a week later, I walked into class and there she was—my professor.”

That made her mother’s eyebrows rise. “Your professor?”

“Not just my professor,” Rio murmured, voice quieter now. “My mentor, too. She’s overseeing my research project.”

Her mom sat back slightly, absorbing that. “That’s complicated, mija .”

“Yeah.” Rio dragged a hand down her face. “That’s what I keep telling myself. That it’s too complicated, too risky. But I can’t—” She exhaled shakily. “I can’t help it. I tried to fight it, I really did. But then she’d look at me, or say my name a certain way, and it was over.”

Her mother watched her carefully. “And how does she feel about you?”

Rio swallowed. “She’s scared, too. I know she is. She tries to keep a distance sometimes, keep things professional, but then she’ll just…break. Like the way she kisses me when she thinks too hard about it. Or the way she’s letting me in, little by little. And then there’s Nicky — her kid is amazing, Mom, and I—” She let out a shaky breath, pressing her fingertips to her temple. “I’m already in too deep. I don’t know how to not feel this way anymore.”

Her mother reached across the table, taking Rio’s hand in hers. Her grip was warm, steady. “ Mija ,” she said gently. “Loving someone is always a risk. But if she makes you happy, if you trust her, then let yourself have this.”

Rio looked down at their joined hands, swallowing past the tightness in her throat. “But what if I get hurt?” she whispered.

Her mother gave her hand a small squeeze. “Then you get back up. But you don’t run from something good just because you’re scared.”

Rio let out a shaky exhale.

After a moment, her mom gave her a teasing smirk. “I’m gonna need to meet this woman properly, you know.”

Rio let out a watery laugh. “Yeah. I figured.”

Her mother sat back, nodding as if she’d made up her mind. “I like her already.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “You don’t even know her.”

Her mother smiled knowingly. “I know you . And I see the way you talk about her.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t fight the small smile that tugged at her lips.

Her mother took another sip of coffee before leveling her with a look. “She’d better be worth all this stress.”

Rio let out a breath of laughter, shaking her head. “She is.”

Her mom’s eyes twinkled. “Good.” Then she grinned. “And if she’s as brilliant as you say, I’m sure she already knows she’s got a very protective Puerto Rican mother to win over.”

Rio groaned, burying her face in her hands. “I’m never telling her that.”

Her mom just laughed, patting her hand. “Too late. I am meeting her. And when I do, I’ll tell her myself.”

Rio sighed, shaking her head, but she was smiling. “Great.”

~*~

By the time Rio crossed into Chicago city limits, exhaustion was beginning to creep in. The long drive, the emotional weight of the past few days, and the knowledge that she had a shift coming up soon all pressed against her, making her shoulders ache.

She pulled into the firehouse parking lot just as her phone buzzed in the cupholder.

Agatha

Back in one piece?

Rio smiled, grabbing her phone as she killed the engine.

Rio

Just parked at the station .

Agatha

Already on shift?

Rio

Yeah. Should be an easy one .

Agatha

You always say that .

Rio

  And it’s always true .

Agatha

Somehow I doubt that.

Rio huffed out a quiet laugh, running a hand through her hair.

Agatha

Get some coffee. Be safe .

Rio

Always. 

Rio stared at that last message for a second, then tucked her phone away and stepped into the station, the familiar hum of the place washing over her.

~*~

As Rio sat on the bench in the locker room, rolling out the tension in her shoulders, she pulled out her phone and sent a quick message.

Rio

Shift’s over. Finally.

She leaned back against the cool metal of the lockers, letting out a slow breath as she waited. It had been a long night, but not the worst she’d ever had. Still, exhaustion clung to her limbs, making her crave a hot shower and something decent to eat. A few hours of decent sleep.

Her phone buzzed.

Agatha  

How was it?

Rio

Not bad. A few calls. Nothing too crazy.

Agatha  

Good .

There was a brief pause, and then another message came through.

Agatha

Have you eaten?

Rio smirked, already suspecting where this was going.

Rio

Haven’t had the chance yet .

Agatha

I’m making breakfast. You should stop by .

Rio raised an eyebrow, biting back a grin. Casual. Like it wasn’t a big deal. But the fact that Agatha was inviting her over first thing in the morning, after everything that had happened between them before Rio left for Thanksgiving? Yeah. It felt like something.

Rio

You’re cooking for me now?

Agatha

Don’t get used to it .

Rio

Too late. Be there soon.

She grabbed her bag and slung it over her shoulder, already feeling lighter as she headed for the door.

~*~

Rio parked in front of Agatha’s house, shutting off the engine and taking a second to just sit there. The sky was still tinged with the last traces of dawn, the crisp morning air visible in the breath she exhaled.

She was exhausted, sore from a long shift, but the anticipation buzzing under her skin was enough to keep her moving. It had only been a few days, but it felt longer. Too long.

Shaking her head at herself, she grabbed her bag and stepped out of the car, making her way up the steps. Before she could knock, the door swung open.

Agatha stood there, wrapped in a soft-looking sweater, her hair a little messy like she’d only run her fingers through it. Her lips parted slightly, like she’d been expecting Rio, but still wasn’t prepared for the sight of her standing there.

Rio grinned, leaning against the doorframe. “Hey, Professor.”

Agatha huffed, but her lips twitched. “You’re impossible.”

“Mm, you missed me.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but Rio caught the way her gaze lingered, the warmth in her expression. She stepped back, opening the door wider. “Come inside before you freeze.”

Rio stepped in, the warmth of the house immediately sinking into her skin. It smelled like coffee and something fresh, something good. She glanced toward the kitchen. “You actually cooking or just putting together something fancy from a box?”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “I’ll have you know, I am perfectly capable of making a decent breakfast.”

Rio smirked, toeing off her boots. “Guess I’ll be the judge of that.”

Agatha shook her head, but there was something softer in her expression now, something unguarded as she watched Rio settle in like she belonged there.

Rio didn’t think — she just acted. With Agatha this close, her warmth sinking into Rio’s skin, her voice quiet and unguarded, there was only one thing left to do.

She closed the distance, pressing her lips to Agatha’s in a kiss that was soft, lingering, the kind that said I missed you without needing any words.

Agatha melted into it almost instantly, her fingers curling around Rio’s sweater, pulling her just a fraction closer. It wasn’t rushed or desperate—just a slow, aching relief, like drinking water after a long shift, like coming home.

When they finally broke apart, neither of them stepped back. Agatha’s forehead rested against Rio’s, their breaths mingling in the small space between them.

Rio smiled, hands still resting on Agatha’s waist. “That a good enough hello?”

Agatha huffed out a small laugh, shaking her head. “You’re impossible.”

“Yeah, yeah,” Rio murmured, brushing her thumb over Agatha’s hip. “But you like me anyway.”

Agatha didn’t deny it. She just let out a small sigh, a quiet hum of contentment, and Rio was about to kiss her again—

“Rio!”

Rio barely had time to turn before Nicky came bounding toward her, full of excitement. She stepped back just in time, just enough to make it look like nothing had happened—though Agatha’s slightly flushed cheeks were a dead giveaway.

Nicky crashed into Rio, hugging her tight. She laughed, lifting him slightly before setting him back down.

“Hey, buddy!”

“You were gone for forever ,” Nicky said dramatically, looking up at her with wide eyes.

“I know,” Rio said, ruffling his hair. “But I’m back now. And I hear there’s breakfast?”

Nicky’s face lit up. “Yeah! Mom made eggs, bacon and French toast!”

Rio glanced at Agatha, raising an impressed eyebrow.

Agatha crossed her arms, unimpressed. “Yes, Rio. I know how to cook. You’re well aware of that by now.”

Rio smirked, like she wasn’t entirely convinced. “Guess we’ll see.”

Nicky didn’t give her a chance to tease further, grabbing her hand and tugging her toward the kitchen. “Come on! Before it gets cold!”

Rio followed, catching Agatha’s gaze over Nicky’s head. Agatha just shook her head, exhaling a laugh, but there was no hiding the warmth in her expression.

Yeah. Rio had missed this.

~*~

It was a few days later, and the early morning was freezing, a flurry of snowflakes falling as Rio walked from her car to the cozy cafe near the firehouse. The bell above the café door jingled as she stepped inside, rubbing at her tired eyes. It was early, just past six, and she’d barely managed to drag herself here after her shift. She just wanted caffeine — something hot and strong to keep her upright until she could crash for a few hours.

She was just waiting for her order when she heard it.

“Rio?”

Her heart stumbled.

That voice.

She turned slowly, almost unwillingly, and there she was — Sam.

For a moment, Rio just stared. It had been nearly seven years, but the sight of Sam still hit like a gut punch. She looked almost exactly the same — sharp hazel eyes, a familiar dimple in her cheek, the same confident stance. Except now, there was something softer in her expression, something hesitant.

Now, Rio thought bitterly. Now you hesitate?

“Wow,” Sam breathed, looking her over. “I—I wasn’t sure it was you.”

Rio forced a shrug, keeping her face blank. “Well. It is.”

Sam let out a breath, shifting on her feet. “You look good.”

Rio scoffed, shaking her head. “Don’t.”

Sam flinched, and for a brief second, Rio saw something like regret flicker across her face. But it didn’t matter. Nothing Sam felt now could erase what she’d done.

Seven years ago, Rio needed her. She’d been drowning in grief, barely holding herself together as her grandmother — one of the most important people in her life — slipped away to Alzheimer’s. And Sam had left. She’d walked away when Rio had needed her the most, had chosen distance instead of staying, had told Rio she couldn’t handle it.

She had abandoned her.

And now? Now she wanted small talk? Fuck, no. Fuck her.

“Rio, I—”

“ Don’t ,” Rio said again, sharper this time. “Whatever you’re about to say? I don’t want to hear it.”

Sam exhaled, rubbing the back of her neck. “Look, I know I messed up—”

“Messed up?” Rio let out a humorless laugh. “You left me, Sam. You walked away while I was watching my grandmother die.”

Sam’s face tightened. “I wasn’t in a good place either, Rio. You weren’t the only one hurting.”

Rio’s jaw clenched. “No, but I was the one left behind.”

Silence stretched between them, thick and heavy.

Sam swallowed, looking down for a moment before meeting Rio’s gaze again. “I am sorry,” she said quietly. “I know it doesn’t change anything, but I need you to know that.”

Rio inhaled slowly, forcing herself to keep steady. She believed Sam was sorry. But that didn’t mean it mattered.

“Thanks,” Rio said, voice flat. “But I don’t need that from you anymore.”

Sam’s expression flickered, but she nodded. “I get it.”

And with that, Rio turned back to the counter, grabbing her coffee as soon as it was ready. She didn’t look back as she walked out the door.

She sat in her car, her exhaustion had been replaced by something else — an old ache she thought she’d buried. Her muscles felt tight, her throat raw from holding back everything she hadn’t said.

She wanted to shake it off, to push it aside, but instead, she found herself pulling out her phone and opening her messages. She knew it was too early, but she couldn’t help herself. She needed this. Needed her.

Rio  

You up?

Agatha responded almost instantly.

Agatha 

I am now. What’s wrong?

Rio hesitated. She almost brushed it off, almost told her it was nothing. But then she remembered what her mother had told her — don’t run from something good just because you’re scared.

Rio  

Can I come over?

A brief pause. Then—

Agatha

Of course. Come.

Rio exhaled, already grabbing her keys. She didn’t know what she needed right now, but she knew where she wanted to be.

 

~*~

The city was still waking up as Rio pulled onto Agatha’s street. The early morning haze clung to the pavement, the air crisp with the lingering bite of autumn. She drummed her fingers against the steering wheel, trying to shake the lingering weight of her conversation with Sam.

She had thought she was over it. Thought she had made peace with the way things had ended. But seeing Sam again had ripped something open, and now, all she could think about was how easily someone who claimed to love her had left.

And how different it felt with Agatha.

Rio didn’t know what she was doing, not really. She and Agatha were still figuring it out. But she trusted Agatha in a way she hadn’t trusted anyone in a long time.

She parked, climbed out of the car, her body already moving on instinct. Agatha had barely gotten the door open before Rio was there, stepping inside, the warmth of the house wrapping around her.

Agatha took one look at her face and softened. “Come here.”

Rio let herself be pulled in, Agatha’s arms wrapping around her without hesitation. The warmth of her, the steadiness—it was like exhaling after holding her breath for too long.

For a while, neither of them said anything. Agatha just held her, hands smoothing over Rio’s back in slow, grounding strokes. It wasn’t rushed or demanding. Just there.

Finally, Agatha murmured, “Talk to me.”

Rio exhaled against her shoulder, then pulled back just enough to meet Agatha’s gaze. “Ran into my ex this morning.”

Agatha’s brows pulled together. “The one who—”

“Yeah.”

A flicker of something passed through Agatha’s eyes — understanding, maybe even anger on her behalf — but she didn’t push. She just traced her fingers along Rio’s jaw, a quiet invitation to keep going.

“She said she was sorry,” Rio continued, voice rough. “And maybe she meant it, I don’t know. But it doesn’t change anything. It doesn’t fix it.”

“No,” Agatha agreed softly. “It doesn’t.”

Rio swallowed, shaking her head. “I thought I was over it. But seeing her just—” She exhaled sharply. “It messed me up.”

Agatha studied her, then reached up, brushing a loose strand of hair from Rio’s face. “You don’t have to be over it,” she said. “Someone you trusted hurt you. That doesn’t just disappear.”

Rio’s throat tightened. “But I am over her. I don’t want her back. Ever.”

Agatha’s lips curved slightly. “I know that.”

And somehow, that simple acknowledgment made something inside Rio unwind. She let out a breath, some of the tension easing from her shoulders.

They stood there for a long moment, just looking at each other. And then, without thinking, Rio reached out, cupping Agatha’s face in her hands.

Agatha didn’t move, didn’t pull away. She just let her.

“I hate that she made me afraid,” Rio admitted, voice barely above a whisper.

Agatha’s hands came up to rest over Rio’s, her thumbs sweeping gently across her knuckles. “What are you afraid of?”

Rio let out a quiet, almost broken laugh. “That I’m gonna lose something good again.”

Agatha’s expression softened, something deep and warm settling in her gaze. She leaned in, pressing the faintest of kisses to Rio’s forehead, lingering there.

“You’re not going to lose me,” she murmured.

Rio’s breath hitched. She closed her eyes, letting herself sink into the moment, into the feeling of Agatha’s lips against her skin, of her steady presence grounding her.

She pulled back just enough to look at her again, searching Agatha’s face for any sign of hesitation. But there was none. Just quiet certainty.

Rio didn’t overthink it. She just kissed her.

It wasn’t desperate or rushed. It was slow, lingering — an unspoken promise between them.

And for the first time since running into Sam, Rio felt like she could breathe again.

Agatha’s lips were soft against hers, the kiss slow and steady, like neither of them were in any hurry to let go. Rio tilted her head, deepening it just a little, her fingers curling at Agatha’s waist. There was something grounding about this — about the way Agatha gave herself over to the moment, to Rio. No second-guessing, no hesitation. Just them.

When they finally parted, their foreheads touched, breaths mingling in the quiet space between them. Agatha’s hands settled on Rio’s arms, a gentle weight.

“You okay?” Agatha murmured.

Rio let out a breath, nodding. “Yeah.” She huffed a small laugh, pressing her thumb against the corner of Agatha’s mouth. “You always ask me that.”

Agatha arched a brow, her lips twitching. “And?”

Rio shrugged. “I like it.”

Agatha’s expression softened. She shifted, fingers trailing lightly along the inside of Rio’s wrist. “You don’t have to be okay all the time, you know,” she said. “You don’t always have to power through.”

Something tightened in Rio’s chest. “I know.”

Agatha searched her face for a moment, then nodded, accepting that for now. “Come on,” she said, voice gentle. “Let’s get some coffee in you.”

Rio let Agatha tug her toward the kitchen, watching as she moved around the space, making the process look effortless. She filled the silence with the small things — asking how Rio’s shift had gone, whether she’d managed to eat, little details that, somehow, made Rio feel more seen than anything else had in a long time.

When Agatha slid a mug toward her, Rio wrapped her hands around it, savoring the warmth. “Thanks,” she murmured.

Agatha just hummed, watching her over the rim of her own mug.

For a while, they just sat in comfortable silence, the early morning light slipping through the windows, painting soft gold across Agatha’s face. It was easy — the kind of quiet that didn’t demand anything, that just was.

And Rio realized she needed this. Needed her.

After a while, she set her mug down and exhaled. “I meant what I said before,” she admitted. “I don’t want to lose this. I don’t want to lose you.”

Agatha met her gaze, something unreadable passing through her expression. Then she reached across the table, her fingers brushing lightly over Rio’s hand. “Then don’t.”

Rio swallowed, her heart beating a little too fast. “Is it that simple?”

Agatha gave a small, wry smile. “Nothing about this is simple, Rio. We know it’s not. But it’s ours.”

Something in Rio settled at that.

She turned her hand over, lacing her fingers through Agatha’s, and let herself hold on.




Chapter 14

Chapter Notes

Thank you so much for your thoughtful and kind comments. They really do warm my heart.

This chapter is LONG because Agatha is really in her feelings, so she just needs to vent and process them.

I hope you guys enjoy it.

Agatha watched as Rio sat at the kitchen table, fingers idly tracing patterns against her mug. She had barely taken more than a few sips of her coffee, her shoulders heavier than usual, the weight of the morning — and everything that had come before it — settling deep into her bones.

It wasn’t just exhaustion from her shift. Agatha could see it in the way Rio blinked a little too slowly, in the tension at the corners of her mouth. The run-in with her ex was still clinging to her.

Agatha exhaled, setting her own mug down. “Why don’t you just stay?” she murmured.

Rio blinked, looking up at her. “Stay?”

“You’re exhausted,” Agatha said, leaning against the counter. “Just go upstairs, get some sleep. I’ll wake you when I get back.”

Rio hesitated, her jaw tensing for a moment like she was gearing up to protest. Always so stubborn. But then she sighed, running a hand down her face. “I don’t want to—”

“Be a bother?” Agatha finished for her, arching a brow.

Rio gave her a sheepish look, rubbing the back of her neck. “I just—”

Agatha reached for her hand, squeezing gently. “Just stay,” she repeated, softer now.

Rio hesitated a beat longer, but her body betrayed her. The sheer exhaustion in her muscles, the way her eyes drooped slightly, the way her fingers curled instinctively around Agatha’s — it all gave her away.

“…Okay,” she finally murmured, barely more than a breath.

Agatha tugged on her hand, guiding her up the stairs and into her bedroom. The room was dim in the early morning light, the bed neatly made, untouched since she’d woken up with Rio’s text. Agatha let go of Rio’s hand and moved to the dresser, pulling out a pair of sweatpants and an oversized shirt—one Rio had worn before, soft with age.

She set them on the bed before turning back to find Rio already peeling off her hoodie, her movements sluggish but practiced.

Something about the way she moved—the way exhaustion weighed her down but didn’t break her — made something in Agatha’s chest ache.

She stepped forward before she could think twice about it, wrapping her arms around Rio’s waist from behind, pressing her forehead between her shoulder blades. She felt Rio sigh, her whole body sinking into the embrace like it was second nature.

Agatha tightened her arms, pressing a kiss between Rio’s shoulder blades, then another against the side of her neck. Just holding her there, wanting nothing more than to take away the weight pressing down on her.

Rio sighed again, this time almost contentedly, before turning in Agatha’s arms. Her hands found Agatha’s waist as she leaned in, pressing a soft, grateful kiss against her lips. It wasn’t rushed or deep, just there — a quiet thank you, a moment of surrender.

Then, without another word, Rio climbed into bed, burrowing under the duvet with a muffled groan.

Agatha chuckled, shaking her head as she gathered her own outfit for the day before heading into the bathroom.

By the time she emerged, hair damp from her shower, Rio was already fast asleep.

And that’s when it hit her.

Oh.

The realization was quiet at first, settling in the back of her mind.

Then it bloomed.

Something warm and terrifying all at once.

She loved her.

It wasn’t a question, wasn’t a maybe. It was a truth, sitting heavy in her chest like it had been there for longer than she’d realized.

She had a momentary jolt of panic — a brief, instinctual what the hell am I supposed to do with this? But then she looked at Rio again, at the peaceful rise and fall of her breathing, at the way she had curled into herself like she was finally safe enough to let go.

And suddenly, it didn’t feel so terrifying after all.

She exhaled, shaking her head at herself before turning toward the door.

Nicky would be up soon.

And for now, that was enough.

~*~

Before leaving for work, Agatha made her way back to the bedroom. The room was still quiet, the curtains drawn just enough to let in a sliver of  the soft morning light.

Rio was curled up under the duvet, her breathing steady, her face finally relaxed in sleep. She looked soft like this — no weight of exhaustion dragging down her features, no lingering tension in her shoulders.

Agatha lingered in the doorway for a moment, just watching her.

Then, without thinking, she stepped closer, sitting lightly on the edge of the bed. She reached out, brushing a strand of dark hair away from Rio’s face, fingers barely grazing her cheek, before pressing a gentle kiss to her hair.

Warmth spread through her chest, full and steady.

It had been a long time since she had felt something like this — if she ever truly had before.

She let herself sit there for a beat longer, taking in the sight of Rio safe in her bed, before finally standing and making her way downstairs.

~*~

A few hours later, just as she was finishing up a consultation, her phone buzzed on her desk.

Rio 

Hey, I’m making lunch. If you have time, stop by.

Agatha felt a small smile tug at her lips before she even realized it.

Her fingers hovered over the keyboard for a second before she typed back.

Agatha 

I’ll be there soon.

Rio 

Good. I’ll make extra.

Agatha 

You better.

Tucking her phone away, Agatha gathered her things and headed out.

When she arrived, the scent of something savory filled the air. She stepped into the kitchen to find Rio standing at the stove, stirring a pan, looking far more awake than she had that morning. She was still in the oversized shirt and sweatpants Agatha had given her, her hair slightly mussed from sleep.

Rio looked up at the sound of footsteps, offering a sheepish smile. “Hey.”

Agatha arched a brow, arms crossing over her chest. “You’re supposed to be resting.”

“I did rest,” Rio countered, nudging at the food with a spatula. “For hours, actually. Woke up starving, so I figured I’d make something before heading to the library.”

Agatha’s gaze flickered over Rio, taking in the way she was still in the oversized shirt and sweatpants she had left for her. The sight sent something warm curling low in her stomach.

Rio glanced around as if suddenly realizing what she’d done, then let out a small laugh, rubbing the back of her neck. “Hope you don’t mind that I just — y’know — made myself at home.”

Agatha shook her head, lips twitching. “No, I don’t mind.” Her voice was quieter now, softer. “I like coming home to you.”

Rio’s eyes flicked up to hers at that, something shifting in them before she turned back to the stove, focusing intently on the food. “Yeah, well. Figured I owed you breakfast after letting me crash here like a total mess.”

Agatha stepped closer, leaning against the counter beside her. “You weren’t a mess,” she murmured.

Rio let out a small, disbelieving huff but didn’t argue. Instead, she plated the food, nudging Agatha’s hip with hers. “Sit down, professor. I’ll make you a plate.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but did as she was told, settling at the table as Rio brought over two plates of steaming stir-fry.

They ate together, conversation easy, the morning’s weight feeling more distant now.

At some point, Rio glanced up between bites. “How’s your day been?”

Agatha wiped the corner of her mouth with her napkin. “Busy. I had a consultation this morning.”

Rio’s brows lifted slightly. “Oh, yeah? At the hospital?”

“No, my practice.”

Rio blinked, surprised. “Your practice?”

Agatha tilted her head slightly. “I see private patients twice a week. Mostly consults, post-op care, and a few long-term cases.”

Rio let out a low whistle. “Damn. And here I thought your schedule couldn’t possibly get busier.”

Agatha smirked. “Surprised?”

“Not really,” Rio admitted. “You’re kind of a machine.”

Agatha hummed, reaching for her water. “I prefer ‘highly disciplined.’”

Rio grinned. “Of course you do.”

They finished eating, the easy rhythm between them settling into something comfortable.

As Rio stretched, checking the time, she sighed. “I should head out soon.”

Agatha gathered the dishes, glancing at her. “I’ll go with you. I have a meeting at Northwestern.”

~*~

As they stepped out into the crisp Chicago afternoon, Rio twirled her keys around her finger, glancing over at Agatha. “You good with me driving?”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Should I be concerned?”

Rio smirked, unlocking the car. “I’m an excellent driver, professor.” She shot Agatha a teasing glance before slipping into the driver’s seat.

Agatha rolled her eyes but climbed in, settling into the passenger seat as Rio started the car. The engine rumbled to life, and soon they were weaving through the streets of Chicago, the city buzzing around them.

The drive was smooth, the kind of comfortable silence that neither of them felt the need to fill. Agatha found herself watching Rio in the quiet moments — the way she kept one hand on the wheel, the other tapping absently against the gearshift, the faint concentration in her brow as she navigated the traffic.

When they pulled onto Northwestern’s campus, the place was already teeming with students. Rio eased the car into a parking spot, shifting into park before letting out a small breath. “Alright. Made it in one piece.”

Agatha smirked, unbuckling her seatbelt. “You’re very proud of yourself, aren’t you?”

Rio shot her a grin. “A little.”

They stepped out of the car, and as they started towards the main building, Agatha felt it — a shift in the air, the distinct sensation of being watched.

She followed the prickling at the back of her neck, her gaze sweeping the campus before landing on a familiar figure in the distance.

Jordan.

He stood near the entrance, his expression thunderous, his gaze locked onto them.

A shiver ran through Agatha’s spine.

Rio, beside her, was still oblivious, focused on adjusting her bag strap as they walked. Agatha hesitated for only a second before schooling her expression, forcing herself to look away.

She wasn’t sure what unsettled her more — the way Jordan was staring at them, or the quiet, inevitable sense that this wasn’t the last time she’d feel his eyes on her.

~*~

Agatha spent the afternoon buried in work, which was exactly what she needed to shake the lingering unease that had settled over her after earlier this afternoon. She had three back-to-back meetings with her mentees, each one at different stages of their research projects, and she gave them her full attention, pushing them to refine their ideas and plan their next steps.

By the time she wrapped up the last meeting, she let herself lean back in her chair, exhaling slowly. Three down, two to go. Rio and her other mentee were scheduled for the next afternoon.

The thought of Rio tugged at something in her chest. She had been carrying herself differently since this morning — quieter, a little withdrawn, the weight of that run-in with her ex still pressing against her shoulders.

Agatha pulled out her phone before she could overthink it.

Agatha

How’s the library treating you?

A few minutes passed before Rio’s response came through.

Rio 

Still here. My laptop and I are in a deeply toxic relationship at this point.

Agatha smirked, shaking her head.

Agatha 

Have you eaten?

This time, Rio’s response was quicker.

Rio  

…Do a granola bar and a questionable cup of coffee count?

Agatha rolled her eyes. She didn’t even bother with a response before grabbing her coat.

The café was only a short walk from campus, and by now, she knew exactly what to order. She got herself a latte and grabbed a black coffee for Rio, along with a croissant and one of those chocolate chip muffins Rio always gravitated toward when they were together.

Fifteen minutes later, Agatha stepped into the library, scanning the rows of tables until she spotted her.

Rio was hunched over her laptop, one hand in her hair, her brows furrowed as she stared at whatever was on the screen. A half-empty cup of coffee sat forgotten at the edge of the table, and Agatha didn’t even have to get closer to know it was cold.

Shaking her head, she approached, setting the coffee and the bag of pastries on the table without a word.

Rio blinked in surprise, glancing up. When she saw Agatha, her face lit up, a slow smile spreading across her lips.

“Oh,” she said, eyes dropping to the coffee. “Well, hello there.”

Agatha crossed her arms, raising an eyebrow. “A granola bar and whatever that was—” she nodded at the abandoned cup “—is unacceptable.”

Rio hummed, already reaching for the latte. “You’re starting to sound a lot like my mother.”

Agatha snorted, shaking her head. “I’ll take that as an insult.”

Rio just grinned, pulling the pastry bag closer. “You check on all your mentees like this, professor?”

Agatha scoffed. “Don’t flatter yourself.”

Rio let out a soft laugh, taking a sip of her coffee. “Mm. You know, I was going to share my groundbreaking insights for our next meeting tomorrow. But now? I’m not sure.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I think I’ll survive.”

Rio hummed again, clearly amused. “We’ll see.”

Agatha sat down across from her, watching as Rio tore off a piece of croissant and popped it into her mouth. She was still tired — Agatha could see it in the way she moved, the slight slump in her shoulders — but some of the tension from earlier had faded.

That was enough.

Agatha took a sip of her own coffee, glancing at the open laptop screen. “What are you working on?”

Rio immediately angled it away from her, shooting her a look. “Oh, no. No, no, no, no. You, of all people, should know I can’t show you that.”

Agatha arched her brow. “You do realize I’m going to grade it eventually?”

“Yes,” Rio said, breaking off another piece of croissant. “But I need to maintain an air of mystery.”

Agatha smirked. “And here I thought you were an open book.”

Rio grinned. “Not when it comes to your assignments.”

Agatha just shook her head, watching as Rio took another bite of food.

After a moment, she spoke again. “Are you free tonight?”

Rio quirked an eyebrow. “Why? You trying to get me into bed again?”

Agatha let out a breath of laughter, shaking her head. “Subtle.”

Rio smirked. “I try.”

Agatha exhaled, leveling her with a look. “I was thinking dinner. And just…spending time together.”

Something shifted in Rio’s face at that, something softer, but she didn’t look away this time.

After a beat, she nodded. “Yeah,” she said quietly. “I’d like that.”

The drive to pick up Nicky was quiet, but comfortable. Agatha still felt the lingering warmth of Rio’s soft thank you from earlier, echoing in her chest like a steady hum. She glanced at Rio from the corner of her eye, watching as she absentmindedly drummed her fingers against her thigh, lost in thought.

When they pulled up to the soccer field, Agatha spotted Nicky immediately — his curls bouncing as he slung his bag over his shoulder, his face lighting up the second he saw them. He ran toward the car at full speed, skidding to a dramatic stop right in front of her.

“Can we get burgers?” he asked, breathless with excitement.

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “We’ll see.”

Before she could say anything else, Rio crouched slightly, resting her hands on her thighs as she grinned at Nicky. “How about this — I’m starving, you’re definitely starving, and your mom worked all day. I say we go out, eat too much food, and call it a win.”

Nicky gasped, spinning back to Agatha with hopeful eyes.

Agatha sighed, shaking her head. “Fine. But you are eating vegetables.”

Nicky groaned, dramatically throwing his head back, and Rio draped an arm over his shoulder as they walked toward the car. “We’ll suffer together, kid.”

Agatha felt something loosen in her chest at the easy way Rio handled Nicky. It was seamless, effortless in a way Agatha hadn’t even realized she wanted until now.

The restaurant was warm and busy, filled with the sounds of clinking dishes and quiet conversation. Nicky had devoured his burger and run off to the kids’ area, leaving Agatha and Rio alone at the table.

Agatha was just about to finish the last of her drink when a familiar voice called her name.

“Dr. Harkness?”

She looked up to find a broad-shouldered man approaching the table, his expression bright with recognition.

“Mr. Gallagher,” she said, straightening slightly.

Gallagher grinned. “I wasn’t expecting to run into you here. It’s been, what — almost a year?”

“Something like that,” Agatha agreed. “How have you been?”

Gallagher beamed. “Better than I ever expected. My wife and I just got back from a trip to Italy, which — if you’d told me two years ago I’d be able to do that, I wouldn’t have believed you.”

Agatha nodded, a genuine smile tugging at her lips. “It’s good to hear you’re back to doing the things you love.”

She gestured to the slides behind her as the images of the brain and its various sections lit up the screen. Her voice grew steadier as she talked about the amygdala, its role in processing emotions and fear responses.

“The amygdala is particularly significant when it comes to the processing of emotional memories. It’s often linked to anxiety disorders and PTSD, where hyperactivity in this area of the brain can lead to exaggerated emotional responses.”

Rio moved smoothly into the next slide. “The hippocampus, on the other hand, is primarily involved in memory formation. Damage to this area, especially in conditions like Alzheimer’s disease, can lead to serious memory impairments and cognitive decline.”

As she spoke, she kept her focus on her slides and the material in front of her, but every now and then, she’d glance over at Agatha, who was watching her with an encouraging expression. It was just enough to keep her grounded.

“And while we’ve discussed some of the common pathologies associated with the limbic system,” she concluded, her voice stronger now, “there is still so much we don’t fully understand. The relationship between the limbic system and our emotional states is complex, and understanding how its dysfunction can lead to both mental health disorders and neurodegenerative diseases remains one of the most exciting challenges in neurology today.”

She paused for a moment, looking out at the professors and her peers, before giving her closing statement. “As we continue to explore the limbic system’s full range of influence, we open up more potential for treatment and intervention. By understanding these processes more thoroughly, we can move closer to more effective therapies for everything from anxiety to Alzheimer’s, and even beyond.”

“Yeah, it is,” Rio replied with a grin. “It’s not much, but it’s home.”

Rio chuckled softly. “Of course, buddy. Go ahead.”

As Nicky busied himself with the table, Agatha and Rio exchanged a look. Agatha’s gaze softened as she watched Nicky, her love for him shining through in the way she looked at him. Rio’s heart did a little flip, and she couldn’t help but smile to herself.

“You two make a great team,” Rio said quietly, just loud enough for Agatha to hear.

Agatha turned to meet her gaze, and Rio could see the affection in her eyes. “We do,” Agatha agreed, her voice full of warmth.

Rio’s heart skipped a beat, but she didn’t have time to dwell on it before Nicky called out, “I’m done! All set!”

Agatha grinned. “You’re quick, I see.”

“You gotta be when you’re this good,” Nicky replied with a mischievous grin, making Rio chuckle.

With everything ready, they all sat down to eat, and the conversation flowed easily. Nicky talked about school, Agatha talked about work, and Rio shared little anecdotes about her day. The tension Rio had felt earlier began to fade as they settled into the easy rhythm of conversation.

Midway through dinner, Agatha glanced around, then asked, “So where’s Alice tonight? She not home?”

Rio paused before answering, feeling her cheeks warm slightly. “She’s making herself scarce tonight. She’s got her own plans. She was happy to let us have the place to ourselves. And…she’s happy for me too.

Agatha nodded with a soft smile, clearly understanding. The three of them continued eating, and Rio felt an overwhelming sense of contentment. They’d had dinners together before — several times — but this felt different. This was her home. It felt like a milestone, a small but meaningful one. Agatha and Nicky, in her space, sharing this quiet evening together.

After dinner, they lingered at the table for a while, sipping on drinks and talking. Rio felt more at ease than she had expected, the weight of any earlier nerves long gone. She had to admit, having Agatha and Nicky in her world like this was exactly what she had always imagined — yet so much better.

As the evening wound down, Agatha and Nicky offered to help clean up, but Rio insisted she had it covered. She was happy to do it herself, to keep the rhythm of the night moving. 

“Thanks again for coming over,” Rio said with a smile, feeling her heart swell. “I know it’s a little different from usual, but I’m glad you’re here.”

Agatha smiled warmly at her, her hand gently brushing Rio’s. “I’m glad we’re here, too.”

 

~*~

As the night wore on, the three of them continued to chat and enjoy their time together. Nicky, ever the energetic kid, was now sprawled out on the couch, watching a cartoon while munching on a cookie Rio had left for him.

After a while, the sound of his soft breathing filled the room, and Rio noticed that Nicky had finally dozed off, his small body curled up comfortably in the cushions.

Agatha caught Rio’s gaze and gave her a soft smile. “Looks like we have a moment to ourselves,” she murmured, her voice warm and quiet, careful not to wake Nicky.

Rio smiled back, feeling a gentle rush of affection for Agatha as she leaned against the counter. “I guess we do,” she said, her voice low.

They stood in the comfortable silence for a few beats, both savoring the peacefulness of the moment. Rio felt the space between them draw tighter, the air filled with an unspoken understanding. Then, as if drawn by a magnetic pull, they moved toward each other.

Agatha’s hand reached up to gently brush Rio’s cheek, and without thinking, Rio leaned into the touch. Their lips met softly at first, a lingering kiss that held the weight of all the moments they had shared. It wasn’t rushed. It was everything they had quietly been waiting for — just a moment to breathe each other in.

When they finally pulled apart, Rio smiled up at Agatha, a soft blush tinting her cheeks. Agatha’s expression was tender, though there was something deeper in her eyes, a quiet resolve that Rio couldn’t quite place.

Agatha paused, her thumb gently grazing Rio’s lips. “I’ve been thinking,” she started, her voice soft but steady. “I want to tell Nicky about us.”

Rio blinked, her heart skipping a beat. She hadn’t been expecting that. “Are you sure?” she asked, her voice quiet but earnest. “I mean, I’m okay with it, but… it’s a big step, don’t you think?”

Agatha nodded slowly, her gaze never leaving Rio’s. “I know. But I think it’s time. He’s already noticed something is different between us. I don’t want to hide it from him. I want to be honest with him, you know?”

Rio’s heart swelled at the thought of Nicky knowing. “I want that, too,” she whispered, feeling a rush of affection for Agatha. “I think it’ll be good for him to know.”

Agatha leaned in once more, pressing a soft kiss to Rio’s forehead. “Thank you for being okay with it,” she said quietly. “I just wanted to make sure you’re comfortable with it, too.”

Rio nodded, smiling up at her. “I’m ready when you are.”

They stood there for a moment, letting the quiet settle around them. Rio felt a sense of peace she hadn’t known she needed — this was the next step, and it felt right. She was ready. And it looked like Agatha was, too.






Chapter 16

Chapter Notes

You’re all amazing and your comments never fail to make me smile.

It was a quiet Saturday morning, the house filled with the comforting scent of coffee and the soft clinking of Nicky’s spoon against his cereal bowl. Agatha sat across from him, her hands wrapped around her coffee mug as she watched him eat, working up the nerve to say what had been on her mind for days.

They had plans to meet Rio for lunch and then go Christmas shopping, and the thought of spending the day together, all three of them, made her chest warm. But if they were going to do this — really do this — then it was time to be honest with Nicky.

She took a slow, steady breath. “Hey, sweetheart,” she started, setting her mug down. “There’s something I want to talk to you about.”

Nicky looked up from his cereal, blinking at her with curious blue eyes. “Yeah?”

Agatha hesitated only for a second before she smiled. “You know Rio and I have been spending a lot of time together, right?”

“Uh-huh.” He took another bite, chewing thoughtfully. “I like her. She’s fun.”

Agatha’s smile softened. “Me too.” She cleared her throat. “I like her a lot, actually. More than just a friend. She’s my girlfriend.”

Nicky froze mid-bite, then set his spoon down with a soft clink. He looked at her with wide eyes, then suddenly grinned. “Ooooh! So that’s why I saw you kissing on the lips the other day.”

Agatha choked on her coffee. “You—when—” She shook her head, eyes widening. “How did you—?”

Nicky shrugged, completely unfazed. “You thought I was sleeping, but I saw it in the reflection on the TV.” He smirked like he had just solved a great mystery. “I knew it!”

Agatha exhaled a laugh, running a hand down her face. “Right. Of course.”

Nicky picked up his spoon again. “So does that mean she’s gonna be around a lot more?”

Agatha let out a relieved breath. “If that’s okay with you, yes.”

He considered that for a moment, then shrugged. “I mean, I already like her. She’s cool. And she’s really nice to me.” He scooped up another bite of cereal. “As long as she still plays video games with me sometimes.”

Agatha laughed, warmth blooming in her chest. “I think that can be arranged.”

Nicky grinned and went back to eating like nothing had changed, and Agatha just sat there, watching him, a weight lifting from her shoulders.

She reached across the table, ruffling his hair affectionately. “Thanks, sweetheart.”

“For what?” he asked through a mouthful of cereal.

She shook her head, smiling. “For being you.”

~*~

 

As soon as they arrived at the café where they were meeting Rio, Nicky spotted her first. She was standing near the entrance, scrolling through her phone, bundled up in a dark blue coat that made her look effortlessly gorgeous, even in the freezing weather.

Without hesitation, Nicky sprinted ahead of Agatha, nearly slipping on the icy sidewalk in his excitement. “Rio! Guess what!” he called out, his voice bright with excitement.

Rio looked up just in time to catch him as he barreled into her, wrapping her arms around him with an amused laugh. “Whoa there, buddy! What’s up?”

Nicky pulled back just enough to look up at her with a wide grin. “I know you’re my mom’s girlfriend!”

Agatha, who had just caught up to them, groaned, covering her face with one hand. “Oh my God, Nicky.”

Rio blinked, clearly caught off guard, before breaking into a grin. “Oh yeah? Who told you that?” she teased, her gaze flicking to Agatha with obvious delight.

Nicky puffed out his chest like he had just cracked the case of the century. “She did. At breakfast. But I already knew because I saw you guys kissing.”

Rio’s eyebrows shot up as she turned to Agatha, who looked like she was mentally weighing the pros and cons of disappearing into the snow.

“You saw us?” Rio asked, trying not to laugh.

“In the reflection on the TV,” Nicky confirmed proudly. “You guys thought I was sleeping, but I wasn’t.”

Agatha let out a slow breath, leveling a look at Rio. “Say nothing,” she warned, though there was a hint of amusement in her voice.

Rio, of course, grinned like she had just won the lottery. “Oh, I wouldn’t dream of it.” She leaned in slightly, voice dropping into something warm and teasing. “Girlfriend.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but couldn’t fight the small, helpless smile that tugged at her lips.

“Are we eating or what?” Nicky asked, already tugging Rio toward the entrance. “I’m starving.”

Rio laughed, reaching back to take Agatha’s hand in hers, giving it a gentle squeeze before letting go. “Yeah, let’s get inside before we all freeze.”

Agatha exhaled, shaking her head fondly as she followed them in. This day was already off to a chaotic start, but she wouldn’t have it any other way.

As they stepped inside the café, the warmth was a welcome contrast to the biting cold outside. Nicky marched ahead, already scanning the place for an empty booth, while Rio hung back just enough to fall into step beside Agatha.

“So,” Rio whispered, leaning in slightly, her breath warm against Agatha’s ear. “The kid caught us, huh?”

Agatha shot her a look, though it lacked any real bite. “Apparently,” she muttered.

Rio grinned, nudging her playfully with her elbow. “And here I thought we were being so discreet.”

“We were discreet,” Agatha whispered back, eyes flicking toward Nicky, who was now climbing into a booth near the window. “It’s not my fault my son has the observational skills of a detective.”

Rio laughed softly, her fingers grazing the back of Agatha’s hand before pulling away. “Well, I think it’s kind of cute. He was so proud of himself back there, you should’ve seen his face.”

Agatha sighed, shaking her head as they approached the booth. “I did see it. It’s the same face he makes when he’s smug about winning at Mario Kart.”

“Ah,” Rio said knowingly, sliding into the booth across from Nicky. “So I should be worried about what he’s gonna do with this information.”

Agatha only hummed as she settled in next to Nicky, who was already busy inspecting the menu.

Rio smirked, keeping her voice low. “You know, if he’s this sharp now, we’re never gonna get away with anything.”

Agatha leveled her with a look. “Stop acting like you’re planning crimes.”

Rio raised her hands in mock innocence. “Hey, I’m just saying. The kid’s got skills.”

Nicky, oblivious to their exchange, looked up from his menu. “Are you guys whispering about me?”

Agatha and Rio exchanged a quick glance before Rio grinned. “Nope.”

“Yes,” Agatha said at the same time.

Nicky narrowed his eyes at them suspiciously before shrugging and turning his attention back to his menu. “Well, okay. I’m getting burgers.”

Agatha exhaled as she leaned back against the seat, her foot nudging lightly against Rio’s under the table. She knew she’d have to deal with the teasing looks Rio was undoubtedly going to give her for the rest of the day, but she also knew — despite her embarrassment — that she wouldn’t change a thing.

As much as she had worried about how Nicky would take the news, he was fine. Happy, even. And that made all the difference.

~*~

 

As they strolled through the mall, the scent of cinnamon and pine lingering in the air, Nicky practically buzzed with excitement. His small hand swung in Agatha’s as he kept pace between her and Rio, his eyes darting between the twinkling lights and festive storefront displays.

“So we’re really spending Christmas with Rio’s family?” he asked, looking up at Agatha with wide, eager eyes.

Agatha glanced at Rio, who smiled warmly before answering. “Yeah, buddy. You and your mom are gonna get the full Vidal family experience.”

Nicky grinned. “Are there any kids?”

“Oh, so many,” Rio said dramatically, stuffing her hands into the pockets of her coat. “Let’s see… there’s Sofia, she’s five, then there’s Mateo—he’s eight. And then there’s Josephine, who’s nine, and then her brother James and her sister Julia are teenagers already.. Oh! And little Oliver, he’s three.. But don’t be fooled, he may be the youngest, but he’s the boss of everyone.”

Nicky’s eyes widened. “That’s so cool! Do they like video games?”

“Mateo loves them,” Rio confirmed. “And Julia is really good at chess if you’re into that.”

“I beat Mom at chess all the time,” Nicky boasted, grinning up at Agatha.

Agatha scoffed. “Twice. In the last six months.”

“Still counts,” he said smugly.

Agatha chuckled before glancing at the nearby shops. “Alright, we should probably focus. What do you think your parents would like?”

Rio considered for a moment before guiding them toward a cozy little boutique filled with handcrafted goods. After some browsing, they settled on a set of beautifully painted ceramic mugs, perfect for Rio’s parents, who were avid coffee drinkers. Along with it, they picked out a bag of high-quality coffee beans from a local roastery. Thoughtful, simple, and useful.

“Okay,” Rio said, adjusting the bags in her arms. “Now I have some top-secret shopping to do, so I’ll meet you guys back at the food court in, say, twenty minutes?”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Top-secret, huh?”

Rio winked. “Very classified. You could come with me, but then you’d ruin the surprise.”

Agatha smirked. “Fine, go do your classified shopping.”

Nicky waved enthusiastically. “Get something cool!”

Rio ruffled his hair before slipping away into the crowd, leaving Agatha and Nicky to wander on their own.

As they walked through the mall, Nicky looked up at Agatha, his expression thoughtful. “It’s really cool that Rio is your girlfriend now.”

Agatha felt warmth spread through her chest, her grip on his hand tightening slightly. “Yeah?”

“Yeah,” he said easily. “I mean, you guys were really obvious with the kissing and stuff, you know?” he teased, his eyes sparkling with mischief.

Agatha rolled her eyes but chuckled, ruffling his hair as they turned a corner—only to nearly collide with someone.

“Excuse me—” Agatha started, but the words died in her throat as she took in the person standing in front of her.

Evanora Harkness.

Her mother.

Agatha hadn’t seen her mother in years, but it didn’t matter. The moment their eyes met, it was like she was ten years old again, standing in a hospital hallway under the too-bright fluorescents, waiting for another reprimand, to hear just how she had failed this time, how disappointed her mother was..

Evanora stood in front of her now, poised as ever, dressed in a perfectly tailored winter coat, her sharp gaze raking over Agatha like she was looking for flaws.

“Agatha,” Evanora said smoothly, as if they were nothing more than polite acquaintances who had simply drifted apart. “I didn’t expect to see you here.”

Agatha schooled her expression, instinctively straightening, as if she were about to be graded on her posture, her presence. “Mother,” she said, her voice even, careful.

She felt Nicky shift beside her and tightened her grip on his shoulder, pulling him protectively behind her..

Evanora’s gaze flicked to him, the corner of her mouth curling — not quite a sneer, but something dangerously close. “And the boy,” she said, as if he were nothing more than an afterthought.

Agatha felt her stomach turn. She still remembered the way Evanora had spat out the word mistake when she’d told her she was pregnant. You’ve ruined everything I’ve built for you, Agatha.

“Nicky,” Agatha said, voice firmer now, protective. “My son.”

Evanora hummed, studying him, as if she were assessing something she didn’t particularly care for. “Yes. I recall.”

Nicky, oblivious to the weight pressing down on Agatha’s chest, gave a small, polite wave. “Hi.”

Evanora didn’t return the greeting. Instead, she turned her gaze back to Agatha, her expression unreadable. “And where is his father?”

It was a calculated jab, one Agatha had seen coming from a mile away.

“Not relevant,” she said, jaw tight.
