Evanora exhaled sharply through her nose, the closest thing to a laugh she would ever allow herself. “Of course.”

Agatha knew that tone, knew the layers underneath it, the things unsaid. Of course, because you wouldn’t know how to make the right choice if I handed it to you on a silver platter.

“Mama,” Nicky said, tugging at her sleeve. “We should go. We’re meeting Rio soon.”

Evanora’s brow arched at the name, a flicker of something in her gaze — disapproval, interest, the calculation of how this new piece fit into the puzzle she thought she knew.

“Rio?”

Agatha lifted her chin. “Yes. My girlfriend.”

She didn’t shrink under her mother’s gaze. Not this time. Not ever again.

Evanora’s expression barely shifted, but Agatha knew her well enough to know that whatever was coming would be something that would be cutting.

“Interesting,” was all she said. Not I’m happy for you. Not I hope she treats you well. Just interesting.

Agatha felt her nails dig into her palm, anger stirring in her ribs. But before she could respond, before she could decide whether it was worth it to even fight this—

“Hey,” a familiar voice called out, light, teasing. “Didn’t I say my shopping was top secret? Are you guys stalking me? You’ll ruin the surprise!”

Agatha turned, and there was Rio, rounding the corner with a playful smirk — until she saw Agatha’s face.

The shift was immediate. The teasing glint in Rio’s eyes faded, her posture straightening.

“Hey,” she said again, softer this time, cautious.

Agatha’s throat was tight, but she forced herself to breathe. She wasn’t a child anymore. She wasn’t standing in that hospital hallway. She was here, in the present, with her son, with the woman she loved.

And Evanora Harkness had no power over her anymore.

If Agatha repeated it as a mantra she might even believe it.

Rio’s eyes flicked between Agatha and the older woman, tension crackling like a live wire between them. Her playful demeanor was gone, replaced by something sharper, more alert.

“Hey,” she said again, voice low as she stepped closer, her fingers brushing against Agatha’s wrist. “Everything okay?”

Evanora turned her gaze on Rio, eyes cool and assessing, like she was looking at an insect she was considering crushing under her shoe.

“I don’t believe we’ve been introduced,” she said, her tone smooth but utterly devoid of warmth. “Dr. Evanora Harkness.”

Rio straightened, still feeling the tension rolling off Agatha in waves. “Rio Vidal,” she said, keeping her voice steady. “Nice to meet you.”

Evanora’s lips curved into something that was almost a smile, but not quite. “I hear you’re my daughter’s girlfriend,” she said, voice dripping with condescension. Then she let out a quiet, mocking laugh. “Like she couldn’t stoop any lower. You just had to prove me wrong, didn’t you, Agatha?”

Agatha didn’t respond. She just stood there, silent and stiff, her expression blank in that way that meant she was barely holding herself together.

And that was enough for Rio to see red.

“I don’t give a shit who you are,” Rio said, stepping forward, placing herself firmly between Agatha and Evanora. “But I do know that you have no business saying a damn thing about Agatha.” Her voice was low, controlled, but filled with unmistakable anger. “Your daughter is the most incredible person I’ve ever met. She’s brilliant, she’s kind, and she’s worked her ass off for everything she has, without your help.” She scoffed. “You should be ashamed of yourself for what you’ve done to her.”

Evanora’s lips parted, as if she were about to respond, but Rio wasn’t interested in hearing another word.

“We’re done here,” she said sharply, turning to Agatha and grabbing her hand. “Come on, love.”

Agatha still hadn’t said a word, her expression unsettlingly blank. Nicky looked up at her uncertainly, then at Rio, before taking her other hand.

And just like that, Rio pulled them both away.

Agatha moved numbly beside her, her body obeying the motion without truly registering it. Her brain was oddly detached, floating somewhere outside of herself, analyzing the way her emotions had shut down completely — a textbook limbic system response. Her amygdala was quiet, no fear or anger making it fire. Her hypothalamus had kicked in, sending out a full-body response, shutting down everything that wasn’t necessary for immediate survival.

Survival.

That’s what this felt like.

She barely registered it when Rio led them into a more secluded corner of the mall, away from the holiday crowds. She barely felt it when Nicky let go of her hand, murmuring something about needing the bathroom.

But she did feel it when Rio wrapped her arms around her, holding her tight.

It was like a floodgate breaking.

Agatha sucked in a sharp breath, and suddenly everything crashed back in — rage, hurt, humiliation, love, everything all at once. Her hands clutched at Rio’s jacket, her forehead pressing against Rio’s shoulder as a shudder ran through her body.

Rio’s arms tightened around her. “I got you,” she murmured. “I got you, baby.”

And for the first time in years, Agatha let someone else hold the weight for her.

~*~

 

Rio felt Agatha’s sharp inhale against her shoulder, felt the way her hands clenched into the fabric of her jacket. She pressed a steady kiss to Agatha’s temple, keeping her close, keeping her grounded.

“It’s okay,” Rio murmured. “You can let go, my love.”

Agatha shook her head almost immediately, swallowing hard before taking a deep, shaky breath. “Not in front of Nicky,” she whispered, voice raw.

Rio nodded, understanding.

A little to the side, Nicky stood watching them, brows furrowed with concern. “Are you okay, mama?” he asked, voice small.

Rio turned to him, schooling her expression into something reassuring. “Yeah, kiddo,” she replied before Agatha could say anything, forcing a smile. “Everything’s fine.”

But he didn’t look convinced. He glanced at Agatha again, then back at Rio. “I still gotta go to the bathroom,” he said, hesitating.

Agatha straightened slightly, visibly trying to pull herself together. “Rio, can you take him?” she asked, her voice quieter now.

“Of course,” Rio said without hesitation. She squeezed Agatha’s arm gently before turning to Nicky. “Come on, bud.”

Nicky lingered for another second, his big eyes flicking back to his mom like he wanted to say something, but then he just nodded and followed Rio.

Agatha exhaled shakily as soon as they were out of sight. She hated this. Hated that, even after all these years, Evanora still had this power over her. Hated that a single encounter could reduce her to this.

She pressed her fingers to her temple, trying to push back the migraine that was already creeping in.

A few minutes later, Rio and Nicky returned. Rio’s expression was carefully neutral, but there was something in her eyes — concern, protectiveness, barely concealed anger — that made Agatha’s throat tighten all over again.

“We good to go?” Rio asked, her voice softer now.

Agatha nodded. “Yeah. Let’s go.”

The drive back was quieter than usual, Nicky occasionally sneaking glances at his mom, clearly still worried. Agatha did her best to act normal, but she could tell he wasn’t buying it.

By the time they got home, her phone buzzed with a message from Wanda.

Wanda

Twins want a playdate. Nicky up for it?

Relief washed through her. She needed time. Just an hour or two to sit with everything, to recover from the emotional whiplash of the day.

She turned to Nicky. “Hey, sweetheart. Wanda just invited you over. Want to go play with Billy and Tommy for a bit?”

Nicky’s face lit up. “Yeah! Can I?”

“Of course,” Agatha said.

Rio met her eyes, understanding instantly. “I’ll take him,” she said quietly.

Agatha gave her a small, grateful nod.

As Rio and Nicky left, Agatha finally let herself sink onto the couch, pressing the heels of her hands into her eyes.

Finally, she could breathe.

~*~

 

Agatha sat on the couch for a few minutes, her hands pressed against her temples as she tried to push the suffocating weight of everything that had happened out of her mind. Her mother’s words still rang in her ears, a constant buzz that made it hard to think clearly. There was a sharp ache in her chest, a familiar tightness that had been there for years, but this time it felt different. This time, it wasn’t just about her mother’s rejection; it was about the fear of it affecting everything she had with Rio.

Her phone buzzed again, and Agatha glanced down at the message from Wanda. It was short, but the words hit her harder than she expected.

Wanda

Rio is on her way back. She told me what happened. You’re amazing, Agatha. I’ve got Nicky for as long as you need. Whatever you need, okay?

Agatha stared at the message for a moment, her eyes stinging. Wanda had always been there for her, but this… this felt different. Wanda didn’t just see the doctor, the professor, the mother. Wanda saw her. And right now, that made all the difference.

With a shaky breath, Agatha replied.

Agatha

Thanks, Wanda. I’ll be okay. Just need some time to breathe. You’re a good friend.

She set the phone down and leaned back against the cushions, allowing herself a few moments to just sit in the quiet. The only sound in the room was the soft hum of the living room heater, but it felt far away. She thought about how she’d gotten here — how much had changed in such a short time. From the loneliness of the last few years to finding someone like Rio… It felt like she was on the verge of something huge, but it was so damn hard to shake the shadow of her mother’s rejection.

She knew she had to work through it, for herself, for Rio, for Nicky.

Minutes later, she heard the door open softly, followed by the familiar sound of Rio’s footsteps. She straightened up a little, willing herself to get it together. Rio stepped inside, and for a moment, everything else faded. Rio’s presence was like a balm for Agatha’s racing thoughts.

“How’s he doing?” Agatha asked, trying to sound casual, though she could feel the tightness in her chest again.

“He’s good,” Rio replied with a soft smile. “He’s excited to play with the twins, so I think we’re in the clear.”

Agatha smiled faintly, though it didn’t quite reach her eyes. She didn’t know how long she’d be able to keep pretending everything was fine. Rio’s gaze softened when she saw the look on her face, and without saying a word, she crossed the room to sit beside her.

“You okay?” Rio asked gently, her voice full of concern.

Agatha hesitated, unsure of what to say. She didn’t want to unload everything onto Rio, but she could feel herself breaking down again, the raw emotion threatening to spill out.

“I don’t know,” Agatha whispered, her voice tight. “I just… I hate how she still has so much power over me.”

Rio’s hand found hers, squeezing it tightly. “You don’t need her approval, Agatha. You’re already amazing just the way you are. And I’m here. I’ve got you.”

Agatha swallowed hard, trying to push down the tears. “I know. I just… I don’t want to be afraid of her anymore.”

Rio pulled her into a gentle hug, and Agatha let herself melt into it for a moment, allowing the comfort of Rio’s touch to calm the storm inside her.

“Take all the time you need,” Rio murmured. “We’re in this together, okay?”

Agatha nodded, taking a shaky breath. “Yeah… together.”

She felt a little better just saying it out loud. The weight wasn’t entirely gone, but it was lighter with Rio there.

It wasn’t long before Agatha’s phone buzzed again, this time from Wanda.

Wanda

You’ve got this, Agatha. Take care of yourself, and remember, I’ve got Nicky for as long as you need. And you’re amazing. Don’t let anyone, not even her, make you forget that.

The sincerity in Wanda’s message made the knot in her throat almost unbearable.

Agatha’s body felt heavy with exhaustion, both physical and emotional, but it was the weight of the emotional turmoil that made her feel like she couldn’t breathe. She sat there for a moment, eyes closed, trying to gather the strength to pull herself together. She knew Rio was still next to her, but the words felt stuck in her throat. The ache from her mother’s cruel words was so deep that it felt like it would never go away.

But the pressure inside her chest was too much to bear, and before she could stop herself, the dam inside her cracked. A sob broke free, shaky and ragged, and Agatha buried her face in her hands. She hadn’t allowed herself to break down like this in years, especially not in front of anyone. Her mother had taught her from a young age that vulnerability was a weakness, that she had to be strong and composed at all times, especially as a woman in her field. She had learned how to hide everything — her pain, her fear, her hurt. But now, with Rio sitting beside her, with Rio holding her, the walls came down.

“Hey,” Rio’s voice was soft but firm as she wrapped her arms around Agatha. She pulled Agatha close, not hesitating, not trying to fix anything, just holding her, steady and unwavering.

It was everything Agatha had never allowed herself to have. A safe space. A person who didn’t expect her to be anything but who she was.

“I… I hate it, Rio,” Agatha choked out between tears. “I hate that she still has this power over me. She always made me feel like I wasn’t enough. Like I had to prove myself all the time. All the time. I could never relax, I always had to be ready.” Her voice trembled as she spoke, a rawness to it that she hadn’t shown in years.

Rio held her tighter, her hand gently brushing Agatha’s back in soothing circles. “You don’t have to prove anything, babe. Not to her, not to anyone. You’re more than enough. You’re the most amazing person I know.”

“But she—” Agatha’s voice cracked again, and she swallowed hard, fighting to hold herself together. She was scared of what would happen if she didn’t. But Rio was patient, just holding her, letting her cry it out.

“You don’t have to push it down anymore,” Rio whispered. “Not with me. Not ever again. I’ve got you, my love. I’ve got you. You’re safe.”

Agatha’s shoulders shook, but the weight in her chest began to lift ever so slightly with Rio’s words. She let herself lean into Rio’s embrace, allowing herself to break down completely. She had never allowed herself this freedom, never let herself feel the raw pain in its entirety, because her mother had drilled into her that vulnerability was weakness, and weakness led to failure.

And failure was unacceptable.

But Rio wasn’t pushing her away. Rio wasn’t telling her to pull herself together. She was simply there. Agatha had never experienced anything like it—never let herself be this real with someone. It was terrifying and beautiful all at once.

“I’ve got you, Agatha,” Rio repeated, her voice full of love and strength. “You’re safe with me. You’re not alone, baby. You’re not alone anymore, I promise.”

And for the first time in her life, Agatha allowed herself to believe it. She wasn’t alone. Rio was there, her rock, her anchor. Agatha’s tears were softer now, more like the quiet aftermath of a storm, as Rio held her, letting her cry until there was nothing left to say.

When the sobs had finally subsided, Agatha took a deep, shaky breath and pulled back a little, wiping her eyes. She could feel the tears still wet on her face, but there was a sense of relief she hadn’t expected.

“Thank you,” Agatha said hoarsely, her voice raw, but she felt lighter now. Rio had seen her at her weakest, but all she saw was strength.

Rio smiled, brushing a stray hair from Agatha’s face. “You don’t need to thank me. You don’t have to carry this alone anymore, love.”

Agatha looked at Rio, really looked at her, and for the first time, the future didn’t feel like a daunting mountain to climb. With Rio by her side, maybe she could finally start to face the scars her mother had left behind and heal.

“I love you,” Agatha whispered, the words slipping out before she could even stop them. It was as if, in this moment of rawness, it felt natural, as if it was the only truth that mattered.

Rio’s eyes softened, and she cupped Agatha’s cheek gently. “I love you too. So much.”

They shared a quiet moment, both of them letting the silence between them speak louder than anything else. Agatha had always had to face her demons alone, but now, she wasn’t alone anymore. Rio was with her, and somehow, that made everything seem just a little more bearable.

The pain wasn’t gone, and maybe it never would be, but with Rio, Agatha knew she could face it—and maybe, just maybe, she could finally let go of the past.

~*~

 

 

Chapter 17

Chapter Notes

Christmas with the Vidal family is finally here! This turned out to be so long that I had to split into two chapters. So we're getting Rio's POV first, and then Agatha's.

As always, thank you so much for taking the time to tell me your thoughts. I appreciate you more than you know.

The soft morning light filtered through the curtains, casting a golden glow over the room. Rio lay awake, staring at the ceiling, her arm draped over Agatha’s waist as she listened to the steady rhythm of her breathing. Agatha was still asleep, curled toward her, her body warm beneath the sheets.

Rio shifted just slightly, careful not to wake her, and let her fingers trace lazy, absent patterns along the bare skin of Agatha’s back. She moved slowly, reverently, feeling every dip and curve, the way the muscles beneath her fingertips rose and fell with each steady breath.

But her mind wasn’t nearly as peaceful.

She couldn’t stop thinking about yesterday. About her.

Evanora Harkness. That horrible, cold woman who had looked at Agatha with such disdain, like she was nothing. Like she was still some foolish child waiting to be scolded and corrected.

Rio clenched her jaw, her fingers stilling against Agatha’s skin for a moment before she forced herself to relax. The anger she felt now was just as sharp as it had been in the moment—a seething, protective rage. But she didn’t want to hold onto that right now. Not while she had Agatha here, safe and warm in her arms.

Instead, she focused on her, on the woman beside her.

Her fingers resumed their slow, soothing path, moving down along the curve of Agatha’s spine.

She thought about last night. About the way Agatha had looked at her, voice low and rough when she’d whispered, “Make me forget. Just for a little while.”

And Rio had.

She had touched her with devotion, had kissed away the tension, replaced it with pleasure, with love. Had taken her time, whispering soft reassurances against her skin, letting her feel nothing but warmth and need and safety.

Because she loved Agatha. Fiercely, deeply. And she would never let that woman—or anyone else—make her feel like she was anything less than extraordinary.

Rio shifted closer now, pressing a lingering kiss to Agatha’s hair. Agatha stirred, letting out a soft sigh as she stretched slightly, her body pressing instinctively toward Rio’s warmth.

A moment later, her lashes fluttered open, and she blinked sleepily at Rio, a faint crease of confusion between her brows before she fully registered where she was.

“Hey,” Agatha murmured, voice raspy from sleep.

“Hey,” Rio said softly, her fingers still tracing slow circles against Agatha’s back.

Agatha exhaled deeply, her eyes searching Rio’s face, and Rio knew she was remembering too.

“You okay?” Rio asked, her voice careful, gentle.

Agatha took a moment before answering, shifting onto her back and staring at the ceiling. “I don’t know,” she admitted quietly. “It still feels… heavy.”

Rio nodded, reaching up to brush a few strands of silver-streaked hair from Agatha’s face. “That’s okay,” she murmured. “You don’t have to be okay yet.”

Agatha turned her head then, meeting Rio’s gaze. There was something vulnerable there, something unguarded that Rio rarely saw.

“I meant what I said,” Rio continued softly. “She doesn’t get to touch you anymore. Not her words, not her presence, not anything. Not if I have anything to say about it.”

A ghost of a smile flickered at the corners of Agatha’s lips, and Rio leaned in, pressing a slow, reassuring kiss there.

When she pulled back, Agatha exhaled again, closing her eyes for a moment before opening them.

“Thank you,” she whispered.

Rio just tucked her in closer, holding her like she was something precious. Because she was.

~*~

For the first time in what felt like forever, Rio had four whole days off.

Four whole days with no firehouse calls, no lectures or study sessions. Just Christmas, family, and—most nerve-wracking of all—introducing Agatha to the people who had shaped her.

Her hands gripped the steering wheel as she pulled up in front of Agatha’s house, her stomach doing an odd little flip. She knew Agatha was willing to do this, that she wanted to be there for Rio, but she also knew what a big step this was for her. Agatha didn’t do family gatherings, didn’t do warmth and chaos and open affection—at least not the way Rio’s family did. And yet, she was doing this anyway. For her.

The thought made something tighten in Rio’s chest—an overwhelming mix of gratitude and love.

She parked, took a breath, and stepped out into the biting cold, pulling her coat tighter around her. She had barely made it up the steps when the front door swung open.

“Rio!”

Nicky’s grin was wide as he threw himself into her arms, nearly making her lose her balance. She laughed, ruffling his hair.

“Hey, kiddo! You excited?”

“Yeah! We’re finally going!” He bounced on his feet. “And Mom made me pack and repack my bag like three times already.”

Rio snorted. “Sounds about right.”

As she straightened, her gaze drifted past Nicky, landing on Agatha in the kitchen. Even from a distance, she could see the tension in her shoulders, the way her fingers fidgeted with something on the counter.

She knew that tension. Felt it in her own bones.

For a moment, she just watched. God, she loved her so much.

Then she nudged Nicky toward the hallway. “Go grab your coat, buddy. I’ll be right there.”

As he scurried off, Rio walked toward the kitchen, her boots barely making a sound against the hardwood floor. She didn’t say anything at first, just leaned against the counter beside Agatha, close enough that their arms brushed.

“Hey,” she said softly.

Agatha exhaled slowly, her fingers still fidgeting with the straps of a tote bag. “Hey,” she murmured back.

Rio tilted her head, searching Agatha’s face, taking in the faint crease between her brows, the way she kept adjusting things that didn’t need adjusting.

“You okay?”

Agatha hesitated for half a second before offering a small, tight smile. “Of course.”

Rio hummed, unconvinced. “Liar.”

That earned her a look, but Rio just smirked, bumping their shoulders.

“You know, it’s not too late to turn around. We could stay here, order takeout, watch Christmas movies.”

Agatha exhaled a soft laugh, shaking her head. “No, you want to do this. And I said I’d come with you.”

“Yeah, but only if you’re comfortable with it,” Rio reminded her.

Agatha finally met her gaze then, and something in her expression softened. There was still hesitation there, but beneath it, there was something else too. Something warm, something sure.

“I’m nervous,” she admitted, voice quiet. “But I want to go.”

Rio smiled, reaching out to tuck a strand of hair behind Agatha’s ear. “Then we’ll go.” She paused, letting her fingers trail lightly along Agatha’s jaw. “And for the record, my family is going to love you. Just like I do.”

Agatha huffed a breath, but there was a faint pink to her cheeks, and Rio counted that as a win.

Before either of them could say anything else, Nicky’s voice echoed down the hall. “I’m ready!”

Agatha shook her head, amusement flickering in her eyes as she picked up the tote bag. “Let’s do this, then.”

And with that, they stepped out into the cold, into something new, something theirs.

~*~

 

The drive was peaceful, the highway stretching ahead of them as soft holiday music played in the background. Nicky sat in the backseat, flipping through a book, while Agatha sat beside Rio, one hand resting on her thigh.

They had settled into a comfortable silence when Rio, keeping her eyes on the road, asked casually, “So… any news on the surgery we’re supposed to watch in January?”

She could feel Agatha’s eyes flick toward her.

“Still scheduled as planned,” Agatha replied.

Rio hummed. “And… do we have results yet on who’s getting to scrub in?”

Out of the corner of her eye, she saw Agatha narrow her eyes at her, a knowing smirk tugging at her lips. “You know I can’t say anything yet.”

Rio sighed dramatically. “Yeah, but if you could—”

“I can’t.” Agatha cut her off smoothly, but there was amusement in her tone.

Rio glanced at her with a lopsided grin. “Not even a hint?”

Agatha shook her head, but there was a playful gleam in her eyes. “Nice try.”

Rio huffed, turning her attention back to the road. “Fine. Be all professional about it.”

Agatha let out a soft chuckle. “It’s still up in the air, if it makes you feel better. My colleagues haven’t sent in their evaluations yet.”

Rio clicked her tongue. “Slackers.”

Agatha hummed in agreement, then smirked. “Besides, wouldn’t want to get your hopes up too much.”

Rio gasped, placing a hand over her heart. “Wow. That’s cold, Professor Harkness.”

Agatha just leaned back, looking thoroughly pleased with herself.

Nicky, not looking up from his book, muttered, “You guys are so weird.”

Rio nearly choked on a laugh, and Agatha reached back to tickle his legs, a small chuckle escaping her lips.

And just like that, the nerves from earlier faded, replaced by something light, something easy. Something that felt a lot like home.

Rio waited a beat, then glanced at Agatha again, turning on the full force of her best wide-eyed, innocent look. “Okay, okay. But can you at least say your top five picks?”

Agatha huffed out a laugh, shaking her head. “You’re relentless.”

Rio shrugged, keeping her face as angelic as possible. “I’m just a humble student, eager for knowledge.”

Agatha lifted a skeptical brow. “You’re incorrigible.”

“Determined,” Rio corrected, flashing a grin. “So… top five?”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, as if considering it, before tilting her head. “Well, if I had a list—which I’m not saying I do—it wouldn’t necessarily be ranked.”

Rio hummed. “But you do have a list?”

Agatha smirked. “I didn’t say that.”

Rio gasped, feigning offense. “Oh my God. I’m not even on it, am I?”

Nicky piped up from the backseat without looking up, “She never said that either.”

Rio threw a hand in the air. “Thank you, Nicky! At least someone has my back.”

Agatha just smirked, looking entirely too entertained.

Rio narrowed her eyes at her before sighing dramatically. “Fine. I’ll just suffer in suspense.”

Agatha leaned in slightly, lowering her voice. “I will say… you might be a strong contender.”

Rio whipped her head toward her so fast she nearly swerved. “What?!”

“Eyes on the road, Vidal,” Agatha said smoothly, though she was clearly amused.

Rio groaned. “You’re killing me, Harkness.”

Agatha smirked, sitting back in her seat, looking entirely too smug. “Good to know.”

 

~*~

 

As they pulled up in front of her parents’ house, Rio felt that familiar warmth settle deep in her chest. No matter how long she’d been away, no matter how much time passed, coming home always felt the same. Safe. Comforting. Like she could breathe a little easier just by being here.

And, as always, her mother was already at the door before Rio had even cut the engine, a bright, welcoming smile on her face.

Rio felt her entire body relax at the sight.

Gloria Vidal was, in many ways, Rio’s mirror image—same dark eyes, same expressive face, same way of holding herself like she was always ready to pull someone into a hug. She waved enthusiastically, practically vibrating with excitement, and Rio could already hear the warmth in her voice, even from this distance.

But beside her, Agatha had gone tense.

Rio glanced over, seeing the tightness in her jaw, the way her fingers curled slightly against her thigh like she was steeling herself. Without thinking, Rio reached over, squeezing her thigh gently before taking her hand in hers. She brought it to her lips in a soft kiss, lingering just a second longer than necessary, hoping to ground her.

Agatha let out a slow, steady breath, then nodded once, just barely.

That was enough.

Rio turned back to the front of the house, catching the way Nicky was watching Gloria with wide, curious eyes. He stepped out to the car, but stayed close to Rio’s side, unusually quiet, and she could tell he was feeling just a little shy.

She ruffled his hair, grinning when he swatted at her hand, and wrapped an arm around his shoulders. “Come on, buddy,” she murmured, leading him toward the house.

Agatha met her at the passenger side, and Rio watched as she took one last deep breath, squaring her shoulders like she was stepping into an OR instead of into a warm, welcoming home.

Rio gave her fingers one final squeeze before letting go.

“It’s gonna be fine,” she murmured.

Agatha nodded, but Rio didn’t miss the flicker of nerves in her eyes.

Then Gloria stepped onto the porch, hands already reaching out for Rio, and there was no more time to worry.

The moment Rio set foot on the porch, Gloria pulled her into a tight, warm embrace, her familiar perfume wrapping around Rio like a second layer of comfort.

“ Mi amor , you’re finally here!” Gloria exclaimed, squeezing her tight before pulling back just enough to hold her face between her hands. She studied her like she always did, as if making sure she was eating enough, sleeping enough, taking care of herself. Then she kissed her cheek and finally let her go, only to immediately turn her attention to Nicky.

“And you must be Nicky!” she said, eyes twinkling with warmth.

Nicky hesitated for just a second, glancing at Rio as if for reassurance, and Rio gave him a little nod. That was all it took for him to step forward, offering a small but polite, “Hi.”

“Oh, you’re even cuter than Rio said you were,” Gloria said, crouching slightly so she wasn’t towering over him. “I hope you brought your energy, because there are a lot of kids inside, and I have a feeling they’re going to want to play with you.”

At that, Nicky perked up. “Really?”

Gloria nodded. “I’ve got four grandbabies running around in there, and they’ve been dying to meet you ever since Rio told us you were coming. And we’re still missing two kids, but they’re going to be here soon.”

That was enough to make Nicky visibly brighten, and he cast a quick, excited look at Agatha before turning back to Gloria. “Okay,” he said, with a little more confidence this time.

Gloria grinned, clearly already smitten, but when she straightened, her gaze finally landed on Agatha.

Rio didn’t miss the way Agatha subtly tensed beside her again.

For a brief second, Gloria simply took her in, the way mothers do when they already know something is different, something is important. Then her smile softened, and she reached out, resting a gentle hand on Agatha’s arm.

“And you,” she said warmly. “You must be Agatha.”

Agatha swallowed, nodding once. “I am.”

Gloria’s smile grew. “It’s so good to finally meet you. Rio talks about you all the time.”

Agatha’s eyes flicked to Rio, something amused yet slightly overwhelmed in them, but Rio looked a bit sheepish.

“ Mamá ,” she groaned, a blush creeping up her cheeks.

Gloria laughed, then squeezed Agatha’s arm before finally stepping aside, gesturing for them all to come in. “Come, come! It’s freezing out here, and we’ve got food, drinks, and enough noise to keep you on your toes all night.”

As they stepped inside, the warmth of the house immediately enveloped them, along with the distant sound of laughter, children playing, and the unmistakable hum of a house filled with love.

And as Rio helped Agatha out of her coat, she leaned in, whispering softly in her ear, “See? You’re already a hit.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh, rolling her eyes, but when she turned to glance at Rio, there was something softer in her gaze. Something grateful.

And Rio knew, right then and there, that this Christmas was going to be perfect.

~*~

Rio barely had time to brace herself as she stepped into the living room before two small bodies crashed into her legs, nearly knocking her off balance. She let out a surprised laugh as she looked down, finding Sofia and Mateo clinging to her, their little faces beaming up at her.

“Aunt Rio!” Sofia shrieked, squeezing her tight. “We missed you!”

“We missed you so much!” Mateo echoed, his arms wrapped around her waist like he was trying to fuse himself to her.

Rio grinned, crouching down so she could hug them properly, kissing the tops of their heads. “Missed you guys too, cariños . What’ve you been up to? Wreaking havoc, I bet.”

Sofia giggled, nodding proudly. “We made Christmas cookies, and we only burned a few!”

“That’s an improvement from last year,” Rio teased, ruffling her hair. “I bet they taste great.”

“They really don’t,” Mateo whispered conspiratorially, and Rio had to bite her lip to keep from laughing.

Before she could say anything else, a shadow loomed over her, and then she was being yanked up into a crushing hug, her feet briefly lifting off the ground.

“Finally decided to visit, huh?” came Victor’s deep voice, warm with affection.

Rio barely had time to hug him back before he released her just enough to ruffle her hair, like she was still a damn five-year-old. She groaned, shoving at his chest as she tried to fix the mess he’d made.

“Jesus, Vic, I’m not a kid,” she grumbled, even as she fought back a smile.

Victor just smirked. “You’re still the baby sister. That’s never changing.”

“Yeah, well, I could still outrun you.”

Victor chuckled, clearly unbothered. “Keep dreaming, kid.”

Before Rio could fire back, movement in the corner of her eye caught her attention, and she turned just in time to see Gabriela approaching, already rolling her eyes at their sibling antics.

“You two done?” she asked dryly, hands on her hips. “Or should we wait for you to start wrestling in the middle of the living room again?”

Rio snorted, rolling her eyes. Gabriela’s gaze, however, immediately flicked to Agatha, and a slow smile spread across her face.

“Well, well, well” she said, stepping forward, her eyes gleaming with mischief. “So this is the famous Agatha.”

Agatha, to her credit, didn’t look as panicked as Rio thought she might. She stood tall, composed as ever, though Rio could see the slight tension in her shoulders.

Rio exhaled quietly, reaching out to gently take Agatha’s hand in hers, lacing their fingers together before giving it a reassuring squeeze.

“Gabi,” she said, tilting her head. “Be nice.”

Gabriela just grinned. “Oh, I am always nice. But you know how much I love getting to know your special someones.”

Rio groaned, already regretting all of her life choices. “God, someone get me a drink,” she sighed dramatically but didn’t let go of Agatha’s hand as she turned back to her family. “Alright, alright, before my sister scares you off, let’s do this properly.”

She squeezed Agatha’s fingers gently, then gestured toward her siblings. “Agatha, this is my oldest brother, Victor—he’s the one who thinks messing up my hair is an acceptable greeting.”

Victor grinned, reaching out to shake Agatha’s hand. “Gotta keep her humble,” he said, then gave Agatha an appraising look. “Good to meet you. You must be pretty special if you got this one to bring you home for Christmas.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow, a small, polite smile on her lips. “I’d like to think so.”

Victor chuckled. “I like her.”

Rio rolled her eyes before turning to Gabriela. “And this troublemaker here is my sister, Gabriela. You guys met a few weeks ago when she rudely interrupted our call. She’ll pretend she’s all put together, but she’s actually the worst.”

Gabriela gasped in mock offense, placing a hand over her chest. “I am a wonderful older sister.”

Rio snorted. “Yeah, yeah. Anyway, these two”—she gestured toward the two kids still hanging off her—“are her little monsters, Mateo and Sofia.”

Sofia beamed, but Mateo’s attention had already shifted, his eyes lighting up when he spotted Nicky standing close to Agatha, watching the chaos unfold with wide eyes.

“Hey,” Mateo said, pointing at Nicky. “How old are you?”

Nicky blinked, a little taken aback by the sudden attention. “Um… eight.”

Mateo’s entire face brightened. “Cool, me too! You wanna play Mario Kart? We got the new one, and I bet I can beat you.”

Nicky looked up at Agatha, silently asking for permission, and when she gave him an encouraging nod, he turned back to Mateo with a competitive little smirk. “I don’t know… I’m pretty good.”

Mateo gasped. “No way! Come on, we’ll see.” He grabbed Nicky’s wrist and started pulling him toward the den where the gaming setup was. “I’ll let you be Yoshi.”

Rio watched as Nicky hesitated only for a second before following Mateo eagerly, already chatting excitedly. Sofia ran after them, giggling, and within moments, it was like Nicky had always been there, like he was just another one of the kids in the family.

Rio turned back to Agatha, catching the way her lips parted slightly, like she was almost startled by how easily Nicky had been swept up into the madness. Her eyes were soft, unreadable, and Rio had to fight the urge to kiss her right then and there.

Instead, she gave Agatha’s hand another squeeze, voice low and warm as she said, “Told you they’d love him.”

Rio glanced around the room, then turned back to Victor with a smirk. “So, where are your monsters? Hiding?”

Victor let out a long-suffering sigh. “Teenagers,” he rolled his eyes, as if that explained everything. “James is on his way—he’s bringing his girlfriend to meet Mom. Julia and Josephine are upstairs doing… whatever it is preteens do these days.”

Gabriela snorted. “Jo is nine.”

Victor rolled his eyes. “Try telling her that. She wants to do everything Julia does. If Julia so much as breathes a certain way, Jo has to do it, too. It’s exhausting.”

Rio laughed, shaking her head. “Sounds about right.”

Victor narrowed his eyes at her. “You say that like you weren’t the same way with me.”

“ I was not .”

Gabriela and Victor both gave her identical unimpressed looks.

“Okay, maybe a little,” Rio admitted, shrugging. “But come on, I turned out great.”

Victor sighed. “Yeah, yeah. Anyway, I’ll go check on them in a bit. James should be here soon.”

Rio nodded before glancing at Agatha, who was watching the exchange with an amused little smile, still holding onto Rio’s hand. There was something warm in her gaze, like she was taking it all in, letting herself relax into it.

Rio bumped her shoulder against Agatha’s. “Welcome to the madness.”

~*~

 

Rio grinned as she stepped into the kitchen, the warmth and delicious aroma of simmering spices wrapping around her like a familiar embrace. The scent of roasting pork and fresh cilantro filled the air, and she could already spot trays of empanadas and tamales waiting on the counter. It wasn’t even evening yet, but Gloria Vidal was always ahead of the game when it came to feeding an army—which was what Christmas Eve in the Vidal household usually felt like.

She walked up to her mother and pressed a quick kiss to her hair before turning to Agatha with a teasing smile. “If you want to survive the madness, alcohol is the way forward, my love.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh, shaking her head, but before she could say anything, Gloria turned from the stove, wooden spoon in hand, and raised an eyebrow at Rio.

“Are you actively trying to scare her?”

Rio snorted. “Nah, just preparing her.”

Gloria gave Agatha a warm, knowing smile. “She’s being dramatic.” Then, with a slight tilt of her head, she added, “But also not wrong. The house is only going to get louder from here.”

Agatha, to her credit, didn’t look deterred. If anything, she seemed almost… intrigued. Like she was watching something rare unfold in front of her, something she had never quite experienced herself.

Rio squeezed her hand. “So, wine? Beer? Something stronger?”

Agatha considered for a moment before arching an eyebrow at her. “What are you having?”

Rio smirked. “Oh, I’ll be hitting the tequila once the cousins start showing up, but for now? Wine sounds good.”

Gloria chuckled as she turned back to her cooking. “You always start out saying that, but we all know how this ends.”

Rio gasped in mock offense. “I am a picture of moderation, Mamá .”

“Uh-huh.” Gloria didn’t even turn around as she said it.

Agatha bit back a smile. “Wine sounds perfect,” she said, and Rio immediately went to grab a bottle and two glasses.

As she poured, she glanced at Agatha, who was taking everything in—the bustling kitchen, the warmth, the easy teasing between Rio and her mother. There was something soft in Agatha’s expression, something almost hesitant, like she wasn’t sure how to let herself settle into this.

Rio handed her a glass and gently bumped their knuckles together. “Welcome to the family chaos, babe.”

Gloria wiped her hands on her apron and turned to face Agatha, her eyes sparkling with curiosity. “So, tell me about your life, sweetheart,” she said casually, leaning against the counter. “What’s it like being a professor, a surgeon, and… well, whatever else you’ve got going on?”

Agatha smiled, shifting a bit awkwardly but warming to Gloria’s relaxed demeanor. “It’s a lot, that’s for sure,” she began, shrugging lightly. “Being a professor is great—challenging, but rewarding. Watching students go from knowing nothing to actually grasping complex stuff is kind of amazing.” She glanced at Rio, who was leaning against the doorframe, watching her with a soft smile. “I mean, I don’t know if I’m changing the world, but I like to think I’m helping them think in a way that could.”

Gloria chuckled and waved a hand dismissively. “Oh, don’t be modest. I bet you’ve got a few world-changers in there, just waiting to happen.” She reached for a bottle of wine and popped the cork. “And what about the surgeon part? I assume you’ve got stories?”

Agatha rolled her eyes playfully, her voice becoming more animated. “Oh, I’ve got stories. Some good, some… terrifying. It’s definitely not the kind of job where you just walk in and have a normal day. There’s always something unexpected, something urgent. But, I’ll admit, I love the adrenaline of it. There’s just nothing like it.”

Gloria poured herself a glass of wine and leaned in, her eyes gleaming. “Sounds like you live for the thrill, huh?”

Agatha laughed, the tension from earlier slowly melting away. “I guess you could say that. There’s something about the pressure that pushes me to do my best. It’s intense, but… it feels right.” She hesitated, glancing over at Rio. “I’m good at it, and that’s what matters to me. It’s hard, but I love it.”

Rio gave her a proud smile, her hand slipping into Agatha’s with the quiet support that only she seemed to provide. Agatha gave her a brief, thankful glance before returning her focus to Gloria.

“Well,” Gloria said with a wink, “sounds like you’ve got your hands full. Teaching and surgery both? How do you keep it all together?”

Agatha chuckled softly, her shoulders relaxing a little. “Honestly? I don’t know if I do. But I make it work. And I have a really good support system. My son, Nicky…” She smiled at the thought of him. “He keeps me grounded. He’s my constant. And Rio.” She turned to Rio, a softer smile on her face. “She’s been my rock too.”

Gloria raised an eyebrow, her expression shifting slightly, but still playful. “I can see that. You two seem really good for each other.” She paused, then added with a wink, “You must be, if you can survive all of this chaos and still love each other.”

Agatha laughed, a warm feeling blooming in her chest. “I think we’re doing alright.”

“Well,” Gloria said, pouring another glass of wine, “you’re certainly welcome here. You know you’ve got a place with us.” 

“Thanks, Gloria,” Agatha said quietly, touched by the warmth in the older woman’s voice.

Rio’s smile widened, and she gave Agatha’s hand a quick squeeze. “See? Told you she’d like you.”

Agatha felt herself relax even more, knowing she was finally starting to feel at home here, with Rio, her family, and all the chaos that came with them.

~*~

 

Checking that Nicky was fully entertained with Mateo and Sofia, Rio let him know that she and Agatha were going upstairs and that if he needed anything, to just call her mom in the kitchen. Nicky nodded, almost absentmindedly, his gaze never leaving the TV as he intensely played Mario Kart. Rio chuckled, ruffling his hair before pulling Agatha towards the stairs.

As they ascended, Rio glanced over at Agatha, sensing a subtle tension in her. “You good?” she asked gently. Agatha gave her a small, reassuring smile, but Rio could tell she was still adjusting to the hustle and bustle of her family.

When they reached the top of the stairs, Rio led Agatha to her childhood room. The door creaked open, and Agatha stepped in, taking in the sight of Rio’s past life on full display. Her soccer trophies were lined up proudly on the shelves, old posters adorned the walls, and photos from her childhood captured moments of laughter and memories that felt distant now.

“Wow,” Agatha murmured, taking it all in as she stepped further inside. She looked at Rio, amusement dancing in her eyes. “You were a serious soccer player, huh?”

Rio shrugged, a grin tugging at her lips. “Yeah, I was obsessed with it for a while. Thought I’d go pro for a minute there.” She glanced around the room, her gaze lingering on a photo of her with a medal around her neck from a tournament win. “Funny how things change.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, clearly intrigued. “So, no pro career, but a very decorated high school and college athlete, huh?”

Rio laughed softly. “Yeah, I guess you could say that. It was the one thing I was really passionate about, but you know how life goes… It had to take a backseat to everything else.”

Agatha nodded, her expression thoughtful. “I get that. The things we think are our future sometimes end up… not fitting anymore.”

Rio hesitated for a moment, then sat down on the edge of the bed, looking up at Agatha. “How about you? Any teenage ambitions that you left behind?”

Agatha paused, her fingers lightly grazing the framed photo of Rio with her soccer team. “I guess I always wanted to be a doctor. Ever since I was a kid, that was my thing.” She smiled wistfully. “I don’t remember a time I didn’t want to do it. But I wasn’t thinking about being anything else. Just… what she wanted me to do, you know?”

Rio turned her head toward Agatha, sensing the shift in tone, but not pressing for more. Instead, she reached for Agatha’s hand, pulling her to sit beside her on the bed. “I get that,” she said quietly. “You don’t always get to choose the path you walk, right?”

Agatha squeezed her hand, grateful for the moment of quiet understanding. She leaned into Rio, letting herself be grounded by the comfort of her presence. “No, not always,” she agreed softly. “But I love what I do now, so I guess it all worked out in the end, despite her interference.”

For a moment, they sat there in the stillness, the only sound the faint hum of voices downstairs. Agatha turned her head slightly to meet Rio’s gaze. “You’ve done a lot with your life, Rio. Even if the soccer career didn’t happen, you’re doing something amazing now.”

Rio smiled warmly, the way she always did when Agatha said something so tender. “Thanks. I think… I think this is the life I was supposed to have all along.”

Agatha leaned forward, brushing her lips against Rio’s, letting the quiet affirmation of the moment linger between them. “You’re right. Maybe we don’t always know what’s ahead, but we find our way eventually.”

As they pulled away from the kiss, the moment felt sacred, private, and full of quiet understanding. Rio smiled softly at Agatha, her thumb tracing over the back of Agatha’s hand. For the first time, Agatha’s shoulders seemed to relax completely, as if she had let go of a weight that had been pressing on her chest.

“I’m glad you’re here,” Rio whispered.

Agatha’s eyes softened. “I am, too. But I still feel like I’m trying to catch my breath with all the family chaos.”

Rio chuckled. “That’s just the Vidal way,” she said teasingly. “If you’re not being pulled in a million directions, then you’re not doing it right.”

Agatha laughed quietly, but her eyes flickered with a hint of nerves. “It’s just… a lot. I want to fit in with them, but I don’t know how. And I don’t want to disappoint you, or Nicky, or your parents.” She paused. “I don’t want to mess this up.”

Rio tilted her head, studying Agatha’s expression with care. “Agatha, you’re already doing more than enough. This isn’t about fitting into some mold of what you think they want. It’s about being you—the person I love. And if anyone in this family doesn’t see that, they’re blind.” She squeezed Agatha’s hand, her voice steady and warm. “Trust me, they’re gonna love you just as much as I do.”

Agatha took a deep breath, the weight of Rio’s words settling in her chest like a gentle, steady anchor. She glanced out the window for a moment, watching the faint outlines of snowflakes starting to fall. The peacefulness of the moment made her feel a little more grounded, like maybe she wasn’t as out of place as she’d feared.

“I think I’m just scared,” Agatha admitted softly, her voice almost too quiet to hear. “I’ve been alone for so long, and the idea of this… being a part of something bigger, it’s just hard to wrap my head around.”

Rio reached over, cupping Agatha’s face in her hands. “You don’t have to be perfect, Agatha. You don’t even have to have all the answers. Just… be here with me. That’s all I need.”

Agatha’s lips parted as if to say something, but she stopped herself, her eyes searching Rio’s face for reassurance. And she found it—soft, unyielding, and full of patience. Rio wasn’t expecting anything from her but to be herself.

After a long, breathless beat, Agatha finally nodded. “Okay,” she said, her voice steady. “I’ll try.”

Rio leaned in, brushing her lips against Agatha’s forehead before pulling her into a tight hug. Agatha sank into it, letting herself be wrapped up in Rio’s embrace, feeling the safety of this moment, the certainty that they were in this together.

“You’ve got this,” Rio murmured against her ear. “And no matter what happens, I’ll be right by your side.”

Agatha pulled back slightly, lifting her head to meet Rio’s eyes. “Thank you,” she whispered, her voice thick with emotion.

Rio smiled softly, brushing a strand of hair out of Agatha’s face. “You don’t have to thank me, love. I’m just happy you’re here.”

They stayed like that for a moment, a simple, quiet peace between them, until the sounds of children calling for Rio downstairs echoed up to the room.

“Guess we should go face the madness, huh?” Rio said with a mischievous grin, squeezing Agatha’s hand.

Agatha laughed softly, but it was a more genuine sound now, the nervous edge starting to fade. “I think I’m ready.”

“Good,” Rio said, standing up and offering Agatha a hand to help her up. “Let’s go show them what this madness looks like.”

~*~



Chapter 18

Chapter Notes

I apologize for the delay. It has been a busy week. But now you guys get to enjoy this ridiculously long chapter as we dive into the second part of the Christmas festivities at the Vidal home.

Agatha watched as Rio moved through her family with an ease that was both effortless and deeply affectionate. It was something she had admired about her from the start—that warmth, that ability to make people feel seen, to make them feel like they belonged.

Right then, though, it was the teenage boy near the door who caught her attention. He was tall, lanky, shifting his weight from foot to foot, hands stuffed into his pockets. There was something familiar about the nerves in his posture, the way he kept glancing toward the redheaded girl beside him.

Before Agatha could wonder who he was, Rio stepped forward, immediately picking up on his discomfort.

“Hey, James, you look like you’re about to give a presentation,” she teased, a playful smile tugging at her lips.

James exhaled a quiet laugh, but his hand moved to rub the back of his neck. “Yeah, well… kinda feels like I am,” he muttered. Then, with a steadying breath, he gestured to the girl beside him. “This is my girlfriend Amelia.”

The redheaded girl at his side blushed almost instantly, offering a shy, polite smile. She was sweet-looking, a little timid, and Agatha recognized the way she stayed half a step behind James, as though unsure of how much space she was allowed to take up.

Rio, of course, wasted no time in making her feel at ease. “Hi, Amelia, nice to meet you,” she said warmly, stepping forward. “I’m James’ aunt, Rio, and this is my girlfriend Agatha and her son Nicky.”

Agatha nodded in greeting, watching as Amelia’s eyes flicked to her with a brief moment of curiosity before darting down to Nicky, who gave her a polite little wave.

“It’s nice to meet you,” Amelia said softly.

“You too,” Agatha replied, offering an encouraging smile. She could definitely relate to jittery nervousness the girl was probably feeling.

James, meanwhile, looked like he was both relieved and mortified at once. He glanced at Rio as if bracing himself, but instead of teasing, she just placed a reassuring hand on his shoulder.

“You’re doing great, kid,” she said, her voice softer now. “Just breathe. It’s not a trial.”

James chuckled, his shoulders relaxing slightly. “Feels like it.”

“Welcome to the family,” Rio said to Amelia with a wink. “Don’t worry, we’re mostly harmless.”

Amelia let out a small laugh, her blush still lingering but her posture relaxing ever so slightly.

Before they could go any further, the door swung open again, and this time, the sound that followed was not quiet at all.

A loud, gleeful screech filled the house, followed by the frantic patter of little feet. Agatha turned just in time to see a small blur of energy launch itself toward Rio.

“Auntie Rio!”

Rio reacted instantly, dropping into a crouch and catching the child just in time, lifting him effortlessly into the air. The little boy giggled wildly as she tossed him up and then pulled him close, pressing a loud kiss against his cheek.

“Hey, little monster!” Rio laughed. “Where do you think you’re going, huh?”

The boy—Oliver, Agatha assumed—clung to her, still giggling, his tiny hands fisting in the fabric of her shirt. “I missed you!”

“I missed you too, buddy,” Rio murmured, rocking him slightly before finally setting him back down on his feet.

Agatha glanced up as another man—tall, with a striking resemblance to Rio—stepped into the house, shaking his head at the scene before him. “He’s been talking about seeing you all day,” he said, exasperated but amused.

“Of course he has,” Rio said smugly, reaching out to ruffle Oliver’s dark curls. “I’m his favorite.”

Pedro—Agatha was fairly sure this must be Pedro—snorted. “You bribe him with too many snacks.”

“It’s called bonding,” Rio corrected.

Pedro just rolled his eyes before looking toward Agatha, his expression shifting slightly as his gaze flickered between her and Rio. “And you must be Agatha.”

Agatha straightened slightly, offering a small nod. “That’s me.”

Pedro glanced at Rio, then back at her, a slow smirk tugging at his lips. “Well,” he said, his tone teasing, “it’s nice to finally meet the woman my sister can’t stop talking about.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, tilting her head slightly. “Oh? And what exactly has she been saying?”

Rio groaned immediately. “Pedro, I swear to God—”

Pedro just grinned wider. “Oh, you know. Just that you’re brilliant, terrifyingly smart, and that she’s completely—”

Rio slapped a hand over his mouth before he could finish. “Nope, we’re done here.”

Agatha couldn’t help but laugh, watching the way Rio glared at Pedro, who was still smirking behind her hand.

She could get used to this, she thought.

The chaos, the warmth, the teasing.

The family.

~*~

A couple of hours passed, the house still buzzing with conversation and laughter, the energy never quite dipping. Agatha had settled into a comfortable rhythm—watching Rio move between her siblings with effortless ease, accepting teasing with eye rolls and sharp retorts, indulging in affectionate gestures that made it so clear how deeply she belonged here.

And then the last arrival stepped through the front door.

Agatha didn’t need to be told who he was. She knew instantly.

The moment Rio’s eyes landed on him, her entire expression changed. Something softer flickered across her face, something unguarded and unmistakably warm. And then she was moving, crossing the room in long strides before he even had a chance to take his coat off.

“Papi,” she said, her voice lighter, like a daughter greeting the safest place she knew.

The man—Juan Vidal—lit up at the sight of her. It wasn’t just a smile, not just recognition. His whole face softened, his eyes crinkling at the edges, his arms already opening as if he’d been waiting all night just for this moment.

“Mi niña,” he murmured, his voice rich with affection as he pulled her into a tight embrace.

Agatha watched as Rio all but melted into it. She couldn’t make out what he whispered to her in Spanish, but she saw the way Rio nodded and closed her eyes briefly, the way her shoulders relaxed, the way her fingers curled into the back of his jacket like she was grounding herself.

Then, when he finally pulled back, he cupped her face in both hands, his calloused thumbs brushing over her cheeks. He looked at her like she was still his little girl, like no amount of time would ever change that. Then, with a quiet fondness, he leaned forward and pressed a kiss to her forehead.

From across the room, Gabi huffed dramatically.

“Hey, Papi, we’re here too. You know, your other children?”

The room burst into laughter, but Juan didn’t let go of Rio just yet. He turned his head slightly, smirking at Gabi before shaking his head in mock exasperation.

“Sí, sí, I see you,” he said, finally loosening his hold on Rio, though he kept an arm over her shoulders as he turned toward the rest of the family.

That was when Rio stepped back, shaking her head fondly before glancing at Agatha.

And just like that, the warmth in Juan’s expression didn’t fade—it shifted, turning curious but just as kind as he followed Rio’s gaze.

“Papi,” Rio said, reaching for Agatha’s hand. “This is Agatha.”

For a moment, Juan’s gaze settled on her, steady and assessing—not scrutinizing, but as if he truly wanted to understand who she was before saying anything.

Then he stepped forward and extended a hand.

“Agatha,” he said, his voice warm, his grip strong but gentle when she took it. “It is very nice to meet you.”

“You too, Mr. Vidal,” Agatha replied politely.

Juan chuckled at that, shaking his head. “Juan,” he corrected. Then, with an easy smile, he added, “If my daughter brought you here, it means she loves you. And if she loves you, then this family does as well.”

Agatha blinked, momentarily caught off guard. It was such a simple statement, yet the weight of it—of unconditional acceptance, of belonging—settled deep in her chest in a way she didn’t quite know how to process.

She barely had time to respond before Rio moved again, reaching out just as a small blur rushed past them.

“Whoa, buddy—gotcha,” Rio said, effortlessly catching Nicky mid-run. He let out a surprised little giggle as she swung him around before settling him on her hip.

With a grin, she turned back toward Juan. “And this little tornado is Nicky. Agatha’s son.”

Juan’s expression shifted again, filling with even more warmth. “Ah,” he said, looking at Nicky with the same soft affection he had given Rio. “Hola, campeón.”

Nicky beamed. “Hi!”

Juan reached out, ruffling the boy’s curls. “Mucho gusto, Nicky.”

“Mucho gusto,” Nicky repeated, giggling.

Agatha found herself exhaling, some quiet part of her relaxing in a way she hadn’t even realized she needed to. This family—it was nothing like the one she had grown up with. Nothing like the coldness and emptiness of her childhood home. And yet, standing there, watching Juan interact so naturally with her son, she felt something she hadn’t felt in a long time.

She felt at home.

~*~

The house bustled with movement as everyone finally began settling in for dinner. The dining table was filled with plates of food, bowls passed back and forth, the scent of warm spices and roasted dishes filling the air. Agatha found herself seated between Rio and Nicky, who had climbed into the chair beside her with all the confidence of a child who already felt completely at ease in this house. Across from them sat Juan, Pedro, and Victor, while Gabi, Gloria and Holly, Pedro’s wife, took their spots down the table.

Conversation flowed easily, voices overlapping as everyone reached for food, filled their plates, and stole bites off each other’s dishes with the kind of familiarity that only came from years of shared meals.

“So, Rio,” Juan said as he leaned back slightly, fork in hand. “Are you still working those insane paramedic shifts while studying?”

Rio groaned, reaching for her drink. “Oh, here we go.”

Pedro smirked. “What? It’s a fair question. We gotta check in and make sure you’re not running yourself into the ground.”

“She is,” Agatha murmured before she could stop herself.

That earned her a look from Rio, half amused, half betrayed. “Hey.”

Juan laughed, clearly delighted. “See? Even Agatha knows you overwork yourself.”

“Okay, okay, everyone relax,” Rio said, waving a hand as she tried—and failed—to look innocent. “I’m managing it just fine.”

Gabi raised an eyebrow. “So you’re still getting two hours of sleep and calling it fine?”

“That’s an exaggeration,” Rio muttered, stabbing a piece of food with her fork.

“No, it’s not,” Agatha said, leveling her with a look. “You came into class once on barely that much sleep. I could see the imprint of the firehouse couch on your face.”

That got a full round of laughter from the table, Pedro and Victor both groaning in unison.

“Dios mío, she hasn’t changed at all,” Pedro said, shaking his head.

Victor snorted. “Still running on caffeine and bad decisions.”

Rio rolled her eyes but didn’t argue, mostly because Agatha was giving her a pointed look that very much said they’re not wrong.

“Alright, fine,” Rio conceded. “Yes, I’m still working. But I like it. And before anyone starts yelling, I also love med school, and I know how to balance it.”

“Well, at least tell us you’re not slacking in class,” Juan said, giving her a teasingly stern look.

That was when Holly, who had been listening with a grin, glanced at Agatha and asked, “And how exactly did you two meet, anyway?”

Agatha took a sip of wine, momentarily glancing at Rio before answering. “Well, believe it or not, we met because she was working.”

“I was the paramedic on scene when Agatha and Nicky got into a car crash,” Rio added, her voice gentler now.

The teasing in the air dimmed slightly as everyone took that in, but Agatha saw only curiosity on their faces—concern, yes, but not the heavy, lingering kind.

“Damn,” Victor muttered. “That must’ve been intense.”

Agatha nodded. “It was. But I—” She glanced at Rio, something small and unspoken passing between them as she reached out to squeeze her hand. “I was very lucky to have her there.”

Rio cleared her throat, shifting slightly in her chair as if the compliment made her a little uncomfortable under the weight of so many eyes. “Well. Just doing my job.”

“And then a week later, I walked into my neurology lecture and—surprise,” Agatha said, arching an eyebrow. “Guess who was sitting in my classroom?”

Pedro let out a low whistle. “Damn.”

Victor smirked. “Now that’s a plot twist.”

Rio groaned, already anticipating where this was going. “Don’t—”

Pedro ignored her completely. “So, professora,” he said, turning to Agatha with a grin. “Is our little sister a good student?”

Agatha felt Rio stiffen slightly beside her, but she only hummed, lifting her glass as if contemplating the question. “Oh, she’s an excellent student,” she said, deliberately slow. “Dedicated, hardworking…”

Rio relaxed.

“…and very dramatic.”

Rio’s head snapped toward her. “What?”

Victor laughed. “Oh, please elaborate.”

“She has a flair for the dramatics,” Agatha continued, sipping her wine. “Always making some grand expression of suffering over an assignment that she, more often than not, already has completed.”

Pedro nearly choked on his drink. “That sounds exactly like her.”

“I knew it,” Victor added, nudging Gabi, who was already cackling.

Rio threw her hands in the air. “Oh, come on. I am not dramatic.”

Agatha simply arched a single, knowing eyebrow.

Rio groaned. “You’re supposed to be on my side.”

“I’m merely reporting what I’ve observed,” Agatha said, her voice far too innocent. ”What was it that you said the other day? That you and your laptop were in a very toxic relationship over that nephrology assignment?”

That only earned more laughter from the table, and Rio sighed, muttering something under her breath before shaking her head.

“Alright, since everyone is so interested in my academic life,” Rio said, pointedly ignoring her brothers’ continued smirks, “I’ll have you know that Agatha’s class is fantastic. Genuinely. She’s a wealth of knowledge when it comes to medicine and neurology, and honestly, if I wasn’t already into neuroscience, I would be after sitting through just one of her lectures.”

The teasing momentarily quieted at that, and Agatha found herself blinking at the sincerity in Rio’s tone.

It wasn’t said for the sake of deflecting her family’s jokes. It was just honest.

A warmth spread through Agatha’s chest, though she fought to keep her expression neutral. “Thank you, Rio,” she said softly.

Rio just shrugged, reaching for her drink. “Don’t get used to the compliments,” she teased, though her ears were slightly pink.

Victor leaned toward Pedro, stage-whispering, “She totally has a crush on her professor.”

Rio groaned again, reaching for her napkin and tossing it at him. “Oh, my god, shut up.”

Agatha, for her part, simply sat back and watched the chaos unfold, hiding a small smile behind the rim of her wine glass.

As the laughter and teasing settled into more casual conversation, Agatha took a moment to glance at Rio, who was sipping her drink, still recovering from the relentless hazing of her siblings. Something about the easy way Rio fit into this space, the warmth of her family, the effortless back-and-forth, made Agatha feel—

She wasn’t sure.

Comfortable, maybe. Included, even.

And she wasn’t used to that.

So instead of lingering too long on the feeling, she leaned back slightly and said, “Since we’re already talking about how brilliant your sister is, I should probably mention that she gave a presentation last week that left my colleagues speechless.”

Rio’s head snapped toward her, eyes narrowing. “Oh, so now you want to talk about what they thought? But when I asked—”

Agatha, entirely unbothered, cut her off smoothly. “Oh, I’m not telling you about it. You’re not allowed.”

Rio gaped at her. “What?”

Agatha took a sip of her wine, entirely too composed. “But telling your family about it? That’s an entirely different matter. I’m not breaking any rules there.”

Rio groaned. “That’s not fair.”

Victor perked up immediately. “Wait, wait, wait—so what exactly did they say?”

Agatha smiled, glancing at the expectant faces around the table. “Oh, they were thoroughly impressed,” she said, and then, because it was the truth, she added, “I think some of them were even a little in awe.”

Rio made a strangled noise. “Agatha.”

“She was excellent,” Agatha continued, pretending not to hear her. “Her knowledge was thorough, her delivery was confident, and she handled questions better than most seasoned professionals.”

Pedro let out a low whistle. “Damn, Rio. Look at you, girl.”

Gabi, who had been watching Rio’s slow descent into barely concealed embarrassment at the Agatha’s praise, smirked. “Papi, do you hear this? Your baby girl is out there showing up entire panels of professors.”

Juan, who had been quietly observing the exchange with a look of fond amusement, nodded. “I would expect nothing less from her.”

Rio groaned again, slouching dramatically in her seat. “I hate all of you.”

“You love us,” Pedro corrected.

Agatha turned her attention back to Juan, still smiling. “It’s true, though. You should be very proud of her.”

Juan gave her a knowing look, something warm and understanding in his expression, before he turned to Rio and reached over to squeeze her hand. “I always am.”

Rio sighed but squeezed back. “Thanks, Papi.”

As the laughter continued, Victor leaned forward with a mischievous glint in his eye. “So, professora, was there a specific moment when you knew Rio was your favorite student?”

Agatha tilted her head, considering. “Oh, that’s difficult,” she mused. “Was it the time she walked into my lecture hall running on two hours of sleep, holding a coffee the size of her head?”

Pedro let out a bark of laughter. “Yep. That sounds right.”

Agatha smirked. “Or maybe it was when she started flirting with me even though she knew I was her professor and mentor.”

The reaction was immediate.

Rio’s head snapped toward her, eyes wide. “Agatha.”

Victor slammed a hand on the table. “No way.”

Pedro practically wheezed. “Oh, this is fantastic.”

Holly, who had been quietly enjoying her wine, let out a delighted laugh. “Rio, really?”

Rio groaned, dragging a hand down her face. “It wasn’t—okay, it wasn’t that bad—”

“That bad?” Victor repeated, grinning. “So you were flirting?”

“I was—” Rio started, then stopped, looking completely cornered. “It was lightly flirtatious!”

Pedro cackled. “So, confirmed.”

Gabi shook her head, grinning. “You’re unbelievable.”

Rio turned to Agatha, betrayal all over her face. “You just threw me to the wolves.”

Agatha, entirely unrepentant, sipped her wine and hid a laugh, completely entertained. Victor let out a whoop of laughter, while Rio groaned dramatically, slumping back in her chair.

Agatha just smiled to herself, warmth settling in her chest as she took in the easy, chaotic rhythm of the Vidal family.

She could get used to this.

As the laughter finally started to settle—though Rio was still grumbling under her breath about betrayal—Gabi leaned forward with a grin. “Alright, Agatha, since we’re already embarrassing Rio, let’s hear more about this flirting. Did she come up with some cheesy pickup line in the middle of class?”

Agatha smirked. “Oh no, she was more subtle than that. A lingering look here, a teasing comment there…” She tilted her head at Rio. “Though I do recall a certain moment when she told me she enjoyed my lectures a little too much.”

That was the moment Rio nearly choked on her wine. “Oh my God.”

Agatha just smiled, tilting her wine glass idly in her hand. “Let’s just say… there was an unmistakable tone.”

That sent the table into another uproar of laughter, with Victor pretending to wipe a tear from his eye. “I’m so proud of you, Rio. Truly.”

Rio threw her hands up. “Oh my God.”

Agatha watched, entertained, as the banter continued. She wasn’t in a hurry to explain everything about her and Rio—some things were better left for quieter moments—but this felt like a nice glimpse into Rio’s world. A bit loud, chaotic, and full of love. She could get used to this.

Pedro leaned forward, eyes gleaming. “Wait, wait. Define ‘a little too much.’”

Rio groaned and leaned back in her seat, crossing her arms over her chest. “Oh, you are all so embarrassing,” she muttered, clearly exasperated, but her amusement was still visible in the corners of her eyes.

“You’re lucky I’m not telling your siblings about all the other stuff,” Agatha teased, but when Rio shot her a look, Agatha couldn’t help but wink. “But she did make the first move.”

The table burst into laughter again, Rio slumping even further into her seat, her face reddening.

Pedro pointed at her, practically gasping for air. “So, not only did you flirt with her, but you also kissed her first?”

Rio shot her brother a glare. “I did not kiss her first,” she protested, but her words fell flat.

Agatha, barely suppressing a smile, looked at Rio with a tilt of her head. “Oh, you did.”

And just like that, the teasing picked up again, the room echoing with laughter. Rio was sinking into her seat, all but hiding behind her own hands as she tried to disappear.

Rio, trying to recover from the relentless teasing, finally muttered, “Okay, okay. I kissed her first. Happy now?”

Agatha smiled sweetly, but there was a glint of mischief in her eyes. “Just thought you’d want to get that out there.”

Just as Rio began to prepare her defense for another round of laughter, Nicky, who had been playing somewhere else, wandered back into the room. His little face was drowsy, eyes half-closed with exhaustion, and his legs were heavy from all the running around.

He barely made it a step before spotting Rio. Without hesitation, he rushed toward her and, before anyone could react, climbed right into her lap, snuggling up against her.

Rio blinked in surprise as the little boy settled into her embrace, his small hands clutching at her shirt. “Hey, buddy,” she whispered softly, her fingers smoothing through his hair. Her earlier embarrassment melted away as Nicky nestled in, the weight of his small body feeling like comfort in her arms.

Agatha watched quietly, feeling the warmth between the two of them. There was something effortless about the way Rio wrapped her arms around Nicky, just as if he had always been there. As if this, this chaotic family, was part of her, too.

As Nicky yawned, content to curl up in Rio’s lap, Agatha’s heart did a quiet flip. She glanced at Rio, who was already looking down at Nicky with a soft, loving gaze. Agatha couldn’t help but smile, her heart swelling with something that felt close to belonging.

The moment felt perfect in its simplicity. The teasing, the laughter, the noise of the family—it all felt like part of the same fabric that now connected them.

Rio caught Agatha’s eye, a soft, tender smile forming between them. No words were necessary; the way Rio gently stroked Nicky’s back was all the answer Agatha needed. She felt like she had found her place here, with Rio, with Nicky, in this messy, beautiful family.

~*~

After placing Nicky carefully in the children’s room, Agatha lingered for a moment, watching Rio. The way she moved so naturally, so lovingly, with the kids made Agatha’s chest tighten in the best way. She had already grown so fond of this family. Rio gently kissed Nicky on the forehead, adjusting his blanket with such care before ensuring the hallway light filtered into the room just enough.

Agatha stepped into the room behind her, her heart swelling with affection as she took in the sight. When Rio turned toward the door, Agatha reached for her hand, gently pulling her into a soft kiss. As their lips met, the moment was filled with warmth, with gratitude, with love unspoken. Agatha pulled away just enough to whisper, “You’re so good with him. So good to me. I’m so glad we found you.”

Rio smiled, the expression in her eyes almost unreadable for a moment, before she pulled Agatha in for another kiss. Agatha didn’t mind the interruption—she was content, grounded in this moment with Rio. But just as they deepened the kiss, a voice rang out from behind them.

“Ugh, Aunt Rio, please get a room,” Julia’s laughing voice cut through the quiet, and Agatha couldn’t help but laugh softly, startled at first but then chuckling at how typical it was.

Rio groaned playfully, pulling away from Agatha and turning toward her niece. “Alright, alright,” she said with a laugh, “We’ll start with the presents. I’ll keep it PG, I promise.”

Nicky looked at him, narrowed his eyes in mock seriousness, then nodded. “Aye, but only if ye swear to follow the Pirate Code.”

Mateo grinned. “What’s the Pirate Code?”

“Rule number one—no telling Mom when we sword fight,” Nicky declared.

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose. “Oh god.”

~*~

The kitchen was filled with the scent of cinnamon, coffee, and something savory roasting in the oven. The house was still humming with the energy of Christmas morning—children’s laughter echoing from the living room, the occasional rustle of wrapping paper, the murmur of conversation from the hallway.

Agatha stood near the counter, fingers curled around a warm mug of coffee. Across from her, Gloria moved with effortless ease, checking on a pot simmering on the stove.

For a while, neither of them spoke. It was a comfortable quiet, the kind that didn’t demand to be filled.

“You know,” Gloria finally said, glancing at Agatha with a small smile, “when Rio told me you two would be here for Christmas, I was a little surprised.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Because I don’t seem like the kind of person to celebrate Christmas?”

Gloria huffed a soft laugh. “Because Rio doesn’t bring people home unless they mean something to her.”

Agatha’s fingers tightened slightly around her mug. She looked down, as if the steam curling up from the coffee held the answer she was searching for.

“She didn’t tell me that,” Agatha admitted quietly.

Gloria tilted her head, watching her carefully. “That doesn’t surprise me. Rio can be open about a lot of things, but when something really matters to her? She holds it close.”

Agatha swallowed. “I don’t want to—” She stopped herself, shaking her head. “I don’t want to make things complicated for her.”

Gloria studied her for a moment before setting down the wooden spoon she had been stirring with. “Agatha,” she said gently, “Rio’s life is already complicated. That’s the nature of what she does, who she is. But the thing about my daughter is—she doesn’t shy away from what she wants.”

Agatha let out a quiet breath. “She thinks she wants this,” she murmured, more to herself than anything.

Gloria raised an eyebrow. “And you don’t?”

Agatha didn’t answer right away. It wasn’t that she didn’t know—she did know. She just wasn’t sure what to do with it.

Gloria smiled knowingly. “You remind me a little of her father,” she said, turning back to the stove.

That startled Agatha. “I do?”

Gloria nodded. “Juan was careful. Thoughtful. He never rushed into things—he always had to be sure first. And sometimes, that meant he second-guessed himself, even when everyone else could see the truth clear as day.” She glanced at Agatha again, her expression warm but pointed. “Don’t let that happen to you.”

Agatha exhaled slowly. There was a weight in Gloria’s words, not heavy in a burdensome way, but grounding.

“I don’t know how to be what she deserves,” Agatha admitted after a moment, voice quieter now.

Gloria smiled, soft and sure. “Then it’s a good thing that’s not for you to decide.”

Agatha blinked.

Gloria reached out, gave Agatha’s hand a reassuring squeeze. “You’re here. That means something. Just don’t be so busy doubting yourself that you forget to enjoy it.”

Agatha stared at her for a long moment before letting out a slow breath. A small, almost wry smile tugged at her lips. “You’re a very persuasive woman, Gloria.”

Gloria chuckled, picking up her spoon again. “I raised four kids, querida. Persuasion is a survival skill.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh before taking another sip of her coffee.

Gloria was quiet for a beat before she said, “Rio told me a little about your mother.”

Agatha stilled.
