It wasn’t a surprise, really. Rio had never pushed her to talk about Evanora, but she had seen enough to know. Still, hearing it out loud was different.

She forced a small, almost detached smile. “What did she say?”

Gloria studied her for a moment before answering, “That she was difficult when you were growing up. That she made you believe you had to earn her love.”

Agatha swallowed, her fingers tightening around her mug. She should have expected Rio to say something like that. But hearing it framed so plainly made it sting in a way she hadn’t prepared for.

She let out a soft, humorless breath. “That’s one way to put it.”

Gloria leaned against the counter, her expression unreadable. “She must have been proud of you, though. You’ve done so much. Built so much.”

Agatha huffed out something that was almost a laugh. “Pride would have required her to acknowledge me as more than a disappointment.”

Gloria frowned, her gaze soft but sharp. “That’s not right.”

Agatha shrugged, as if it didn’t matter. “It is what it is.”

Gloria was silent for a long moment, then said, “You know, I used to think love had to be hard. That it had to be earned.” She shook her head. “But that’s not love, Agatha. That’s control.”

Agatha’s breath hitched slightly. She wasn’t sure if it was the words themselves or the way Gloria said them—gentle, matter-of-fact, as if she were simply stating a truth Agatha had never let herself accept.

Gloria continued, her voice even, steady. “My father was like that. Love was something you had to prove yourself worthy of. And for a long time, I believed him.” She looked at Agatha, something soft but firm in her gaze. “Until I met Juan. Until I built my own family.”

Agatha swallowed. “And did that change things?”

Gloria smiled, small and knowing. “It changed everything.”

She reached for Agatha’s hand again, squeezing it gently. “Love doesn’t keep score, Agatha. It doesn’t demand perfection. You don’t have to earn your place here. You already have it.”

Agatha didn’t realize she had been holding her breath until she exhaled, something in her chest loosening.

She didn’t know what to say, not really. But she found herself nodding, her fingers curling slightly around Gloria’s.

For a long time, love had felt like something fragile, something conditional. She didn’t know if she believed—fully believed—what Gloria was saying.

But standing here, in this kitchen, in this home that wasn’t hers but didn’t feel entirely not hers either… she wanted to try.

 

Chapter 19

The highway stretched ahead of them, a long ribbon of asphalt cutting through the winter landscape. Snow still clung to the edges of the road, remnants of the cold front that had passed through while they were at her parents’ house. The car hummed steadily beneath them, a quiet, constant presence as they made their way back to Chicago.

Rio’s hands rested easily on the wheel, her fingers tapping idly against the leather as she stole a quick glance at the rearview mirror. Nicky was fast asleep in the backseat, his new pirate hat slipping down over his face, the toy sword from his costume held loosely in his arms like a prized possession.

Her gaze shifted to the passenger seat, where Agatha sat, looking out the window, her expression thoughtful but relaxed.

Rio exhaled, a slow, contented breath, letting the warmth of the past few days settle over her.

Christmas had been… a lot. A lot in the best possible way.

She had always loved the holidays, the messiness of it, the loudness, the way her family had a habit of talking over one another, laughter filling every room. And this year had been no different. If anything, it had been even better. Because Agatha had been there. Nicky had been there.

And they had been welcomed.

Her parents, her brothers, Gabi, even the kids—everyone had taken them in like they’d always been part of the family. Nicky had spent hours playing with Mateo and Sofia, darting through the house like he belonged there. And Agatha… well, Agatha had just fit. Completely. Even with her usual composed demeanor, Rio had caught the softening in her, the way she had let herself be taken into the warmth of Rio’s family, whether she realized it or not.

She thought about the way her mom had pulled Agatha aside in the kitchen, their quiet conversation stretching longer than Rio had expected. She hadn’t asked about it yet, but she had noticed the way Agatha had looked afterward—less guarded, maybe. A little more at ease.

Rio couldn’t stop the small smile tugging at the corner of her lips.

It was good. All of it. Better than she had let herself hope for.

She had been worried, in the back of her mind, about how Agatha would handle it—the sheer volume of her family, the chaos, the love that sometimes came in overwhelming bursts. But Agatha had taken it in stride, had watched Rio’s dad’s terrible magic tricks with a straight face before finally laughing, had indulged in Gabi’s teasing with a roll of her eyes but a small, fond smile. And when the time had come for presents, she had watched Nicky’s excitement with something in her expression that Rio didn’t quite have words for.

She had seen it, though.

The way Agatha wanted this.

Maybe she wasn’t fully there yet, maybe there were still things she had to work through—but Rio knew Agatha wanted this, wanted them .

And fuck, that felt good.

She reached out, letting her hand find Agatha’s where it rested on her thigh, threading their fingers together without looking away from the road. Agatha glanced over, arching a brow, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, she gave Rio’s hand a small squeeze, her thumb brushing lightly over her knuckles.

Rio smiled.

She didn’t need to say it. Not yet.

But this—this was home.

~*~

By the time they reached Agatha’s house, the familiar skyline of Chicago glittered against the night sky. The warmth of the car made the winter air outside feel sharper as they opened the doors.

Nicky, who had been half-dozing for the last stretch of the drive, perked up as soon as Rio unlocked the car doors. He yawned, stretching his arms above his head, then blinked up at them with a lopsided smile. “We home?”

Agatha turned in her seat, brushing a strand of hair from his face. “We are.”

“Finally,” Rio teased, undoing her seatbelt and stepping out. “I was starting to think you were gonna knock out completely back there.”

“I wasn’t sleeping,” Nicky insisted, though the slight rasp in his voice suggested otherwise.

Rio smirked as she pulled their bags from the trunk. “Sure, bud. Whatever you say.”

The house was just as they’d left it—warm, dimly lit, carrying the faintest trace of Agatha’s perfume in the air. Nicky kicked off his shoes without bothering to line them up properly, already shrugging off his coat as he turned to his mom.

“Can we play my new video games now?”

Agatha chuckled as she hung up her own coat. “You don’t even want a break first?”

Nicky shook his head, clearly determined.

Rio snorted, tossing her own coat over a chair. “You’ve been gone for two days, and the first thing you wanna do is whoop our asses in Mario Kart?”

Nicky grinned. “Uh-huh.”

Agatha sighed in mock defeat, ruffling his curls. “Fine. But I want at least five minutes to settle in.”

“Five minutes,” Nicky agreed, though the way he bounced on his feet made it clear he’d be counting every second.

Rio smirked, following Agatha into the kitchen while Nicky rushed to set up the game console. The moment they were out of earshot, she leaned against the counter, watching as Agatha poured herself a glass of water.

“You think if we let him win, he’ll tire himself out faster?”

Agatha scoffed, sipping her water. “He’ll know. And he’ll never let us live it down.”

Rio chuckled, shaking her head. “Alright, then. No mercy.”

They played for hours, the house filled with the sounds of frantic button-mashing and Nicky’s triumphant cheers every time he managed to pull ahead. Despite her best efforts, Rio couldn’t quite keep up—Nicky had clearly spent too much time honing his skills, and Agatha, despite her protests, was more competitive than she let on.

Eventually, though, exhaustion won out. One minute, Nicky was upright, determined to play just one more round, and the next, he was slumped against Agatha’s side, his head resting against her arm as his breathing slowed.

Rio smirked. “Guess that’s game over.”

Agatha hummed, brushing a hand through his curls. “Looks like it.”

Rio stretched, rolling her shoulders. “Want me to take him?”

Agatha shook her head. “I’ve got him.” She shifted carefully, gathering him in her arms, and Rio couldn’t help but watch as she carried him toward his room.

She followed, lingering in the doorway as Agatha tucked Nicky in. He stirred slightly when she adjusted his blankets, mumbling something under his breath before settling again. Agatha ran her fingers through his hair, a quiet, affectionate gesture that made Rio’s chest feel warm.

By the time they returned to the living room, the adrenaline from the game had faded into something quieter, more comfortable.

Rio flopped onto the couch, stretching her legs out. “So, what’s the plan for New Year’s?”

Agatha arched a brow as she sat beside her. “Are you asking if I have plans or if I want plans?”

Rio smirked. “Both.”

Agatha considered this for a moment, then shook her head. “No plans yet.”

Rio hummed, pretending to think. “Maybe we could do something small. Just us. Some friends. Maybe some good food, good wine, and absolutely no Mario Kart.”

Agatha chuckled. “Afraid of losing again?”

Rio gasped, placing a hand over her chest in mock offense. “I let you win.”

“ Right ,” Agatha said dryly.

Rio grinned, nudging her knee. “Seriously, though. What do you think?”

Agatha leaned back against the couch, considering. “That sounds nice. So what, you’re suggesting… a party?”

Rio snorted. “God, no. I meant something small. Close friends. Alice and Jen, Wanda and Viz and the kids… maybe Lilia, if she doesn’t already have plans.”

Agatha hummed, considering. “That could work.”

Rio tilted her head. “You sure? I don’t want to drag you into something if you’re not feeling up for it.”

Agatha gave her a look—one of those quiet, steady ones that always made Rio feel like she was being read a little too easily. “I’m sure.”

Rio grinned. “Alright, then. Small gathering, good food, good wine, and maybe Mario Kart.”

Agatha laughed. “Maybe.”

Rio leaned in slightly, letting her fingers trail up Agatha’s arm. “You know, for someone who pretends to be above it all, you get really competitive.”

Agatha scoffed, but there was a flicker of amusement in her eyes. “ I do not .”

Rio laughed, shifting closer. “You absolutely do. I saw how you nearly threw your controller earlier.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, she let out a quiet sigh, her body relaxing into the couch. “Fine. Maybe I slightly enjoy winning.”

Rio grinned. “Uh-huh. And who was it that swore revenge when Nicky beat her last week?”

Agatha shot her a pointed look. “You’re very smug right now.”

Rio smirked. “I’m always smug.”

Agatha sighed, shaking her head. “You’re impossible.”

“And yet, here you are, dating me.”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, but Rio could see the small smile forming at the corner of her lips. “Unfortunately.”

~*~

A few days later, the firehouse was winding down from the overnight shift, and Rio was running on fumes. She sat on the worn-out couch in the common area, legs stretched out, her body aching from the past twelve hours. Across from her, Alice scrolled through her phone while Will stood by the counter, sipping coffee.

“So, Agatha’s house, eight o’clock?” Will confirmed, glancing over his mug.

Rio nodded, rubbing a hand over her face. “Yeah, she’s got most of the food covered, but we should probably grab extra drinks.”

“Already on it,” Will said. “Eddie’s picking up wine, and I’ll grab beer and whatever Alice decides she wants to regret tomorrow.”

Alice flipped him off without looking up. “I have refined taste, thank you.”

Rio smirked. “Yeah, real refined. Just wait—Alice will show up an hour late like she always does and then pretend it was intentional.”

Will raised an eyebrow. “She does that?”

“Oh yeah,” Rio said, stretching. “She calls it ‘making an entrance.’”

Alice looked up with a smug grin. “And it works every time.”

Will chuckled. “Guess I’ll see it in action.”

“You’ll see a lot in action tonight,” Rio chuckled, standing up and grabbing her bag. “Anyway, I’m heading straight to Agatha’s. Gotta pretend to be useful before passing out for a few hours.”

Will smirked. “Tell her we’ll be on time.”

Rio snorted. “You mean I’ll be on time, and Alice will—”

“Make an entrance,” Alice cut in. “You’re welcome in advance.”

Shaking her head, Rio gave them a lazy wave and stepped outside. The cold bit through her clothes, but at least it kept her awake on the drive over. By the time she reached Agatha’s house, her limbs felt heavier, and the idea of crashing in Agatha’s bed for a few hours sounded a lot better than any party.

She parked and unlocked the door before pushing it open.

Inside, the house was already half-prepped for the night—decorations stacked on the dining table, a to-do list scribbled out beside them. The smell of fresh coffee and something sweet lingered in the air.

And then there was Agatha, standing in the kitchen in an oversized sweater, her hair slightly mussed from sleep. She glanced up from whatever she was writing, a knowing smile tugging at her lips.

“You look terrible.”

Rio groaned, dropping her bag by the door. “Flatter me some more, why don’t you?”

Agatha smirked, setting her pen down. “Come here.”

Rio didn’t need to be told twice. She crossed the room, and the second Agatha wrapped her arms around her, she melted into the warmth. Exhaustion pressed heavier against her, but she didn’t care.

Agatha pressed a kiss to her temple. “Coffee’s fresh. I made cinnamon rolls.”

Rio hummed against her shoulder. “You’re spoiling me.”

Agatha chuckled. “Go eat, then sleep. I need you functional for tonight.”

Rio smirked, pulling back just enough to look at her. “Define functional.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but kissed her anyway. “Go.”

With a dramatic sigh, Rio pulled away, heading toward the kitchen. “You’re so bossy.”

“You love it,” Agatha called after her.

And, well—yeah. She really did.

~*~

A few hours of sleep made all the difference. When Rio finally surfaced, it was mid-afternoon, and Agatha’s house had shifted into full prep mode. The scent of something rich and savory filled the air, and as Rio wandered into the kitchen, she found Agatha at the stove, sleeves rolled up, moving with effortless precision.

“Morning—” Rio paused, then corrected herself with a smirk. “Afternoon.”

Agatha glanced over her shoulder, arching an amused brow. “Good nap?”

Rio stretched, feeling the lingering heaviness of sleep in her limbs. “Mm, needed it. You let me sleep.”

“You looked like you were about to drop,” Agatha said simply, returning her focus to the pan in front of her. “Besides, you won’t be much help if you’re half-conscious.”

Rio grinned, stepping closer and wrapping her arms loosely around Agatha’s waist from behind. “Bold of you to assume I’d be much help either way.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “Fair point.”

Rio pressed a kiss to the back of her shoulder before peeking over it. “What’s cooking?”

“Short ribs,” Agatha replied, tilting her head slightly so Rio could see. “Figured we needed something substantial before the champagne starts flowing.”

Rio let out an appreciative whistle. “You really are trying to impress me, huh?”

Agatha smirked, finally turning to face her. “It’s been nearly two months, Rio. I think I’ve already won you over.”

Rio hummed, brushing a teasing kiss against her jaw. “Debatable.”

Agatha gave her a look but didn’t pull away. “Mm-hmm. If you want to stay on my good side, you can help finish setting up.”

Rio saluted. “Yes, ma’am.” She glanced toward the living room, where a few bags of decorations were still untouched. “Where’s Nicky?”

“Upstairs,” Agatha said. “He wanted to pick out what to wear for tonight.”

Rio grinned. “Kid’s got priorities.”

Agatha shook her head fondly. “He’s excited.”

Rio felt a warmth settle in her chest at that. She liked that Nicky was part of this—part of them.

She grabbed a bag of decorations and slung it over her shoulder. “Alright, where do you want these?”

Agatha nudged her toward the living room. “Anywhere that doesn’t involve you climbing on furniture. I’d like to keep my paramedic in one piece.”

Rio smirked. “No promises.”

Agatha just sighed, shaking her head as she turned back to the stove.

As Rio started untangling a string of lights, she couldn’t help but think—yeah, this was exactly where she wanted to be as the year came to a close.

 

~*~

As Rio set to work on the decorations, she could hear Agatha moving around the kitchen, the occasional clatter of utensils and the rich aroma of the short ribs filling the house. The warmth of it all—the food, the soft hum of jazz playing from the speaker, the quiet comfort of knowing they were spending this night together—settled deep in her chest.

She unraveled a particularly tangled string of lights, muttering under her breath, when footsteps sounded on the stairs.

“Rio!”

Nicky came bounding down, a bundle of energy as always, his dark curls slightly damp from a recent shower. He was wearing a button-down shirt, still untucked, with socks that were clearly a mismatched pair—one with tiny sharks, the other a bold, glittery silver.

Rio grinned, setting the lights aside just in time to catch him as he launched himself at her. “Whoa, kiddo, you trying to knock me out before the party even starts?”

Nicky giggled but didn’t let go. “Mom said you were sleeping.”

Rio ruffled his curls. “Yeah, I crashed for a bit. Long shift.”

He pulled back just enough to peer up at her. “Did you have any emergencies?”

She hesitated, debating how much detail to give, then settled on a lighthearted approach. “A couple. Nothing too wild. No aliens, no zombies, no superheroes in distress.”

Nicky huffed. “ Boring .”

Rio chuckled. “Tell me about it.”

Agatha’s voice carried from the kitchen. “Nicky, did you pick out shoes?”

Nicky groaned, dramatically dragging his feet toward the stairs again. “They’re just gonna get stepped on anyway…”

As Nicky disappeared back upstairs, Rio returned to her decorating. The living room was already half set up—Agatha had gone for a mix of elegant and fun, with gold and silver accents, fairy lights strung along the fireplace, and a few festive touches on the bookshelves.

“So, who is coming tonight?” Rio asked, pulling a small step stool over to reach a high corner.

Agatha turned off the stove before answering. “Wanda and Viz and the kids, obviously. Alice and Jen. Will and his boyfriend—”

“First New Year’s with Will,” Rio noted with a grin. “I bet he’s excited. No third-wheeling tonight.”

Agatha let out a soft laugh, leaning against the counter. “And your family will be calling?”

Rio nodded. “Yeah, probably after midnight. You know how my mom gets—she’ll want to make sure I’m eating, staying warm, making good decisions.”

Agatha smirked. “Should I tell her you climbed onto the furniture against my orders?”

Rio gasped, pressing a hand to her chest. “You wouldn’t.”

Agatha tilted her head. “Wouldn’t I?”

They held each other’s gaze for a beat before Rio gave in, climbing off the stool with exaggerated care. “Fine. I’ll behave. For now.”

Agatha looked pleased with herself, but before she could say anything, Rio strode over and stole a quick kiss, just to keep her on her toes.

“Go finish your fancy cooking, Professor,” Rio teased.

Agatha sighed, shaking her head but unable to hide the small smile on her lips as she turned back to the stove.

Rio watched her for a moment before getting back to work, feeling something warm and steady settle deep in her bones.

~*~

The party was in full swing, the house filled with warmth, laughter, and the soft hum of music playing in the background. Rio had long since settled into the night, the exhaustion from her shift melting away as she enjoyed the company of her friends. She moved easily through the space, checking in on Alice and Jen, making sure Will and his boyfriend had drinks, and stealing glances at Agatha whenever she could.

At some point, she found herself next to Wanda near the fireplace, both of them watching the party unfold. Agatha was across the room, deep in conversation with Lilia, her expression animated as she gestured with her wine glass. It was a sight Rio had grown to love—Agatha in her element, comfortable and at ease.

Wanda nudged her lightly. “You’ve got it bad,” she teased, smirking.

Rio didn’t even bother denying it. “Yeah,” she admitted, a small smile tugging at her lips. “I do.”

Wanda exhaled, swirling the wine in her glass. “I’m happy for you both, Rio. Really. It’s just…” She hesitated, glancing around before lowering her voice. “You know how risky this is, right?”

Rio’s expression sobered slightly, and she met Wanda’s gaze head-on. “I know,” she said. “Believe me, we’ve talked about it.”

“And?”

“And we’re being careful,” Rio assured her. “It’s not like we’re reckless. I know she’s my professor. I know she’s my mentor. But this—” she gestured between herself and Agatha, “—it’s real, Wanda. We’re in love. She gave me a key to her house for Christmas.”

Wanda’s brows lifted slightly, but there was no surprise in her eyes—just understanding. “I figured you were serious. But love doesn’t stop the fact that if the wrong person finds out, Agatha could lose everything. You both could.”

Rio’s jaw tightened. She knew that. It was something they had both been hyper-aware of since the beginning. “You don’t think I worry about that?” she asked, her voice quiet but firm. “Every time I walk into Northwestern, I have to remind myself to keep my distance. Every time we’re in her class, I have to make sure I don’t look at her the way I want to.”

Wanda studied her for a long moment before sighing. “I get it. And I trust you—I do. I just don’t want to see either of you get hurt.”

Rio softened, nudging Wanda’s shoulder. “We’re in too deep to walk away from this now. And honestly? I don’t want to.”

Wanda gave her a long look before finally offering a small, approving nod. “Alright. Just promise me you’ll keep your guard up.”

Rio smirked. “Always.”

Before Wanda could respond, a warm hand slipped around Rio’s wrist, and she turned to see Agatha beside her, a knowing look in her eyes.

“Stealing my girlfriend, Wanda?” Agatha teased, her voice light but affectionate.

Wanda held up her hands in mock innocence. “Just making sure she doesn’t break your heart, professor.”

Agatha arched an amused brow, but before she could respond, Rio wrapped an arm around her waist and pressed a quick kiss to her temple. Then turned back to Wanda. “You worry too much.”

Wanda snorted. “Someone has to.”

Agatha just shook her head, but Rio felt the way her fingers brushed lightly against the small of her back—subtle, reassuring. And as the party continued around them, Rio knew, despite the risks, that they were exactly where they were meant to be.

~*~

As the night stretched toward midnight, the house buzzed with laughter, music, and the warmth of people who felt like home.

Rio stood in the kitchen with Agatha, their bodies close in the way they always seemed to be now. Agatha had one arm resting against the counter, the other hooked lightly around Rio’s waist, fingers idly playing with the hem of her shirt. It was effortless. Easy. The kind of closeness that no longer required permission.

From where they stood, Rio could see the rest of the party unfolding in the living room. Alice and Jen were curled up on the couch, Alice half in Jen’s lap as they watched Will and his boyfriend dance dramatically to whatever pop song was playing. Lilia and Wanda stood off to the side, drinks in hand, watching the scene with a mix of amusement and fondness.

Billy and Tommy were in the middle of an increasingly chaotic game that involved jumping over pillows and yelling about points, while Nicky—still full of energy despite the late hour—ran around them, egging them on. He’d barely stopped moving all night, bouncing between the twins, Rio, and Agatha like an excited pinball.

Agatha traced a slow circle against Rio’s back. “You’re holding up well for someone who just got off a shift.”

Rio exhaled a quiet chuckle, shifting closer. “You’re a good distraction.”

Agatha hummed, lips curving slightly. “I try.”

Before Rio could tease her, Alice’s voice rang through the house.

“Alright, everyone, grab your drinks! It’s almost midnight!”

There was a flurry of movement as people reached for their glasses. Rio grabbed a beer, while Agatha lifted her wine. The countdown started, voices rising together.

Ten.

Billy and Tommy abandoned their game, scrambling over to Wanda and Viz.

Nine.

Will draped an arm over his boyfriend’s shoulders, both of them grinning.

Eight.

Nicky skidded to a stop, wide-eyed with excitement. “It’s time!”

Seven.

Rio turned toward Agatha, heart already picking up its pace.

Six.

Agatha mirrored her, their bodies now fully pressed together.

Five.

Four.

Rio’s hand found Agatha’s waist.

Three.

Agatha’s fingers brushed against her jaw, featherlight but sure.

Two.

Agatha leaned in first.

One.

Their lips met at midnight.

It wasn’t rushed or hurried—it was steady, certain, grounding in a way that settled something deep between them. Rio’s hand slid up, fingers tangling in the hair at Agatha’s nape, and Agatha let herself sink into it too.

And then—

A blur of energy crashed into them.

Nicky, full-speed, barreled into their legs, wrapping his arms around both of them in a tight, breathless hug. “Happy New Year!” he shouted, practically vibrating with excitement.

Rio and Agatha broke apart, startled into laughter. Agatha ruffled Nicky’s curls, her face full of affection. “Happy New Year, sweetheart.”

Around them, the house erupted into cheers. Billy and Tommy were yelling their own excited Happy New Years, Alice and Jen kissed, and Will dramatically dipped his boyfriend, making everyone laugh.

Rio glanced at Agatha, her heart still racing from the kiss, from the way Agatha was looking at her—like she was everything.

Agatha leaned in again, softer this time, her lips brushing just below Rio’s ear. “I love you,” she murmured, quiet but sure.

Rio’s breath hitched, her fingers tightening against Agatha’s waist. But there was no hesitation, no doubt.

She turned, catching Agatha’s gaze, letting it sink in before she whispered back, “I love you too.”

Agatha smiled, and when Rio kissed her again—Nicky still latched onto them, still grinning wildly—she knew this was it.

This was home.

This was everything.

~*~

The morning light filtered softly through the curtains, casting a golden hue over the bedroom. Rio stirred, feeling the warmth of the bed and the faint scent of Agatha’s perfume lingering in the sheets. She blinked herself awake, momentarily disoriented before the realization settled in—Agatha’s house. Morning.

A slow, satisfied smile curled at her lips. She turned her head slightly, catching sight of Agatha still asleep beside her, hair tousled, face relaxed in a way Rio rarely got to see. For a moment, she considered staying in bed, lingering in the comfort of this stolen time, but then Agatha shifted, exhaling a sleepy sigh before blinking open her eyes.

“You’re staring,” Agatha murmured, voice rough with sleep.

Rio grinned. “Can you blame me?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but there was no real exasperation there. “What time is it?”

Rio glanced at the clock. “A little past six.”

Agatha groaned, pressing her face back into the pillow. “Why did I agree to an early meeting today?”

“Because you’re a dedicated professor,” Rio teased. “And because if you’re late, Lilia will personally come find you.”

Agatha let out a muffled noise of protest but forced herself upright. She stretched, running a hand through her hair, before turning to Rio. “You have class at nine, right?”

“Yeah, but I can take my time. I don’t have to be there too early.”

Agatha gave her a look, thoughtful. “I was going to take Nicky to school, but if you don’t mind, he’d probably love a ride from you.”

Rio perked up. “Oh, yeah? You’re trusting me with school drop-off duty again?”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “I trusted you with my life in an ambulance. I think you can handle a school run.”

“Fair enough.” Rio stretched before slipping out of bed. “Alright, I’ll take him. That means you can focus on your meeting, and I get to bribe your kid with snacks. Win-win.”

Agatha gave her a knowing look. “No bribing. And no letting him talk you into stopping for donuts.”

Rio feigned offense. “I would never.”

Agatha shot her a flat look, clearly unconvinced.

Rio just grinned and headed for the shower.

By the time they were both dressed and moving through the house, the morning had settled into an easy rhythm. Agatha sipped her coffee while packing the last of Nicky’s things, and Rio helped by stealing pieces of bacon from Nicky’s plate, much to his outrage.

“Hey!” Nicky frowned, clutching his plate protectively. “That’s mine.”

Rio grinned. “You snooze, you lose, kid.”

Nicky narrowed his eyes but quickly laughed and shifted gears when Agatha reminded him to grab his backpack. By the time they were ready, Agatha kissed Nicky’s forehead, gave Rio a quick peck on the cheek, and headed out first, leaving Rio and Nicky to take off in her car.

As they pulled out of the driveway, the radio hummed softly in the background. Nicky was quiet for a moment, but Rio could feel him looking at her.

She glanced at him briefly. “What?”

Nicky hesitated, then tilted his head. “So… what are your intentions?”

Rio blinked. “My what now?”

Nicky crossed his arms, his expression serious. “With my mom.”

Rio barely suppressed a laugh. “Damn, kid. That’s a loaded question for eight in the morning.”

“I’m serious,” Nicky insisted. “I just—I need to know if you really like her.”

Rio softened. She took a second before answering, her grip firm but relaxed on the steering wheel. “I really like her, Nicky.” Then, because it was the truth, she added, “I love her.”

Nicky studied her for a long moment. “Like… for real?”

“For real.”

He nodded, thoughtful. “So… does that mean you’re gonna be around for a long time?”

Rio considered that. “I hope so. That’s the plan.”

Nicky let out a little hmm, as if weighing her words. Then, after another beat of silence, he finally nodded. “Okay.”

Rio arched an eyebrow. “Okay?”

“Yeah,” Nicky said, a little more relaxed now. “I mean, I figured you were serious, but I had to ask, you know? I’m not just gonna let anyone date my mom.”

Rio chuckled. “Good to know you’re keeping an eye on things.”

“I am.” Nicky leaned back in his seat, finally seeming satisfied. Then, as if the serious moment had never happened, he perked up. “Sooo… can we stop for donuts?”

Rio burst out laughing. “Damn, you’re smooth.”

“I learned from the best,” Nicky said smugly.

Rio shook her head, already making the turn toward the donut shop. “Alright, kid. But if your mom asks, we ate fruit for breakfast.”

Nicky grinned. “Deal.”

~*~

Rio leaned against the wall outside the lecture hall, her fingers lazily scrolling through her phone as she waited for Agatha to arrive. She’d gotten there a little too early and the lecture hall was still closed. It was their first Neurology II class today, and they were in a different room than they used to be in the previous semester.

The sound of heels clicking against the tile pulled her attention up, and sure enough, Agatha was making her way down the hall, keys dangling from her fingers, looking effortlessly put together as always. The sight of her still made something in Rio’s chest tighten, even now, two months in.

Agatha spotted her and slowed, a small smile pulling at the corner of her lips. “Lurking outside my classroom, hm?”

Rio smirked. “Just making sure my favorite professor has a strong start to her day.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow, stopping in front of her. “Flattery this early? What do you want?”

“Maybe just a kiss,” Rio murmured, keeping her voice low as a few students walked past them.

Agatha huffed, shaking her head. “You are impossible.”

“And yet you love me,” Rio countered in a whisper, flashing her a grin, as Agatha unlocked the door to the lecture hall.

Agatha just rolled her eyes, but her expression softened. “Get to class, Vidal.”

“Yes, ma’am.”

Rio gave her a playful salute before slipping into the lecture hall, taking a seat toward the back. A few minutes later, Agatha started class, and Rio let herself fall into the familiar rhythm of taking notes, watching the way Agatha moved through the material with ease.

The day passed in a blur after that— a quick lunch with Alice, then another lecture. It wasn’t until she was on her break that she realized Agatha hadn’t responded to her last text.

Or the one before that.

Or the one before that.

Rio frowned, unlocking her phone again and tapping out a quick ‘ You good? ’ before setting it aside.

No response.

An hour later, she tried again.

Still nothing.

A flicker of unease settled in her stomach. Agatha wasn’t the type to ignore her messages for hours, especially without a heads-up.

Finally, she texted Wanda.

Rio 

Hey, have you talked to Agatha today? She’s not answering her phone.

Wanda 

Not since this morning. Why?

Rio 

She’s just been MIA for hours. It’s weird.

Wanda 

You want me to check in?

Rio 

No, I’ll go wait for her at her place. Let me know if you hear from her.

By the time Rio pulled up to Agatha’s house, the sun was already dipping below the horizon. She let herself in with the key Agatha had given her for Christmas, tossing her bag onto the couch before pacing the length of the living room.

She tried calling this time. It went to voicemail.

Another twenty minutes passed. Then thirty.

Just as she was starting to really worry, her phone buzzed.

Agatha 

Sorry, got caught up in something. On my way home now.

Rio exhaled, some of the tension in her chest easing. But not all of it.

Rio 

Everything okay?

Agatha 

Yeah. I’ll be home soon.

Rio stared at the screen for a second before shoving her phone in her pocket. Something didn’t sit right, but at least Agatha was finally responding.

Now she just had to wait.




Chapter 20

Chapter Notes

So I’m off today and I know you guys are anxious after that cliffhanger, so I figured I’d surprise you with another chapter. I’ve been so excited to get to this part and I truly hope you guys like it.

Also, just to make things clear, this picks up in the morning that Agatha went MIA on Rio, but in Agatha’s pov. And then…

Fasten your seatbelts, children. 👀

The morning light filtered through the curtains, soft and golden, coaxing Agatha awake. For a moment, she just lay there, savoring the quiet and warmth of the bed. It was still early, and Rio was beside her, her presence a steady, comforting weight. Agatha turned her head, watching as Rio shifted slightly, blinking herself awake. She caught her gaze, and the corners of Rio’s lips tugged into a sleepy smile.

Agatha couldn’t help but smile back. “You’re staring,” she muttered, her voice thick with sleep.

Rio’s grin widened. “Can you blame me?”

She rolled her eyes but didn’t push the teasing. Instead, she stretched, her muscles protesting from the long hours of work. “What time is it?” she asked, more out of habit than necessity.

Rio glanced at the clock. “A little past six.”

“Six? Why did I agree to an early meeting today?” Agatha groaned, burying her face back in the pillow.

Rio chuckled softly. “Because you’re a dedicated professor. And because Lilia will personally track you down if you’re late.”

Agatha let out a muffled sound of agreement but finally pushed herself up, running a hand through her tousled hair. She sighed as she straightened up, the pull of sleep still lingering. She glanced at Rio. “You have class at nine, right?”

Rio nodded, stretching lazily. “Yeah, but I don’t have to rush. I can take my time.”

Agatha hesitated for a moment, thinking about the school run. “I was going to take Nicky to school… but if you don’t mind, he’d probably love a ride from you.”

Rio’s eyes lit up at the suggestion. “Oh, yeah? You‘re trusting me with school drop-off duty again?” she teased, raising an eyebrow.

Agatha gave her a pointed look, the smallest smirk tugging at her lips. “I trusted you with my life in an ambulance. I think you can handle a school run.”

Rio feigned offense, dramatically placing a hand over her chest. “Fair enough. I’ll take him. Means you can focus on your meeting, and I get to bribe your kid with snacks. Win-win.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “No bribing. And definitely no donuts.” She shot Rio a playful glare, though she couldn’t keep the amusement out of her voice.

Rio chuckled, her grin never faltering. “I would never.”

Agatha gave her a skeptical look, but by the time she finished getting dressed, the house had settled into its usual morning rhythm. Rio poured herself a cup of coffee, and Nicky sat at the table, looking entirely too energetic for the hour. Agatha gathered Nicky’s things, slipping into the routine they’d established. Rio, of course, stole bites of Nicky’s bacon, earning a playful scowl from her son.

“Hey! That’s mine!” Nicky protested, clutching his plate.

Rio just smirked. “You snooze, you lose, kid.”

Nicky shot her a glare, but then, like most eight-year-olds, was distracted by Agatha reminding him to grab his backpack. Agatha kissed his forehead and gave Rio a quick, affectionate peck on the cheek before heading out the door. “You two have a good morning drive safe,” she called as she left.

The drive to her department meeting was a blur, and Agatha was grateful for the time alone. She needed a few moments to herself before the day kicked into full gear. By the time she arrived, the day’s grind was already well underway, filled with meetings, papers to review, and the small but necessary bustle of academia. She checked her watch again. Class was in just a couple of hours.

Her first Neuro II lecture was always a bit of a challenge—students were excited, nervous, and some were always insufferable know-it-alls, thinking they were seasoned neurologists just because they did a semester with her. 

But today, with Rio sitting somewhere in the lecture hall, after their amazing holiday season and everything they’d shared, things felt… different. 

Finding her waiting for her by the door had been enough to give her that warm feeling in her chest she’d learned to associate with Rio. The woman she loved so completely.

From Agatha’s viewpoint, the sight of Rio was both amusing and endearing. There, with her phone in hand and a mischievous glint in her eyes, Rio seemed to be biding her time, even though she’d arrived a bit early. Agatha couldn’t help but smile at the thought—of how, even after two months, Rio’s playful presence still managed to soften the sharp edges of her busy world.

Agatha unlocked the door and set her materials on the desk, her mind flicking back to the playful, easy conversation with Rio earlier. She’d asked her to take Nicky to school without thinking too much about it, and now, watching Rio walk into the room, a part of her still felt the rush of warmth that came from knowing how close they were. She caught Rio’s smirk as she entered, her gaze meeting Agatha’s before Rio casually slid into a seat at the back.

Agatha’s heart gave a little jolt, but she kept her professional face on as she turned to face the class, pushing away the flutter of nerves. “Good morning, everyone,” she began, voice steady. “Welcome to Neurology II. I hope you’re ready to dive even further into the complexities of the human brain.”

~*~

The door to Agatha’s office clicked open with a sharpness that made her look up from her papers. Jordan stood there, leaning casually against the doorframe, his expression knowing, like a cat who had just cornered its prey.

“Can I help you, Mr. Jordan?” Agatha asked, her voice smooth, though inside, her heart was already picking up speed. There was something off about this.

He stepped inside without waiting for an invitation, his shoes tapping against the floor as he made his way to the center of the room. “I think you already know why I’m here.”

Agatha’s stomach tightened, but she didn’t flinch. “I don’t think I do.”

Jordan smirked, his eyes glinting with malice. “Oh, you will. I know about you and Rio Vidal.”

Agatha’s pulse quickened at the mention of Rio’s name, but she masked her surprise quickly. “And what exactly do you know?” she asked, keeping her tone even, trying not to betray any reaction.

Jordan crossed his arms, a smug grin spreading across his face. “I know everything. I have photos. The texts. All of it. And I’ve got it all right here.” He reached into his jacket pocket, pulling out a phone with a flourish.

Agatha’s eyes flicked to the device, her mind racing. She fought to keep her expression neutral, refusing to show any sign of panic. “Is that so? Let me see it then.”

Jordan raised an eyebrow, clearly not expecting that response. “What?”

Agatha leaned back in her chair, meeting his gaze head-on. “You say you have proof. Let me see it. If you think you can intimidate me with pictures and messages, you’re wasting your time.”

Jordan’s smug smile faltered, but only for a moment before he recovered. “You think I’m bluffing?”

“I think you’re trying to manipulate me,” Agatha said coolly, “and I’m not the kind of person who folds under threats. If you’re serious, show me what you’ve got.”

For a long moment, Jordan didn’t move. Agatha could see the wheels turning behind his eyes, trying to figure out if she was bluffing, too. But in the end, he smirked again, this time with a little more hesitation. “Fine. You want to play it that way?”

He held out the phone, tapping a few buttons before turning it toward her. Agatha’s eyes scanned the screen, seeing exactly what he’d described: pictures of her and Rio, moments from their time together that she hadn’t even realized had been captured. The messages, too—texts they had exchanged, things that could easily be misconstrued.

She didn’t flinch, though. Her gaze remained steady on him as she processed the images. “These aren’t going to change anything, Jordan. You’re still wasting my time.”

Jordan’s grin returned, but it was sharper now. “Not if I take this to Dr. Calderu, Harkness. I’m sure she’d love to hear about this little ‘sordid affair’ you’ve been having with one of your students. And if you think she won’t make things difficult for you… well, you’re sadly mistaken.”

Agatha’s blood ran cold at the mention of Lilia. She knew exactly what he meant, and the thought of it made her stomach twist. Lilia was a good friend, but also the head of the department—she’d have to consider the politics and the optics of the situation.

Still, Agatha wasn’t ready to back down. “You think you can just walk in here and demand whatever you want?” Her voice dropped, low and dangerous. “You’re playing a dangerous game, Jordan.”

Jordan took a step closer, and for a moment, Agatha almost felt a flicker of doubt. But she steadied herself. She had to be careful. She couldn’t let him see how rattled she was. She couldn’t afford to make the situation worse. 

“What's your angle? What exactly do you want here?”

“Everything,” he said, his tone casual, but with an edge. “Mentorship. The OR spot for the neurosurgery. And if you don’t give them to me, I’ll make sure this ends up on Calderu’s desk. And trust me, she won’t be pleased to know what her star professor has been up to.”

Agatha stared him down, feeling the weight of the situation pressing down on her. She had two choices—comply, or fight back. The truth was, though, neither option felt good. She couldn’t risk this coming out. Not now. Not when things with Rio were so good.

But Agatha wasn’t going to back down. Not this easily.

“I’m not giving you what you want,” she said, her voice steady now, full of conviction. “You want to go to Dr. Calderu? Fine. But know this—if you try to drag my personal life into this, I’ll make sure everyone knows exactly what you’ve been doing behind the scenes.”

Jordan’s smile faltered for the briefest moment, and for the first time, Agatha could see the doubt in his eyes. But he didn’t back off. He just nodded, eyes cold.

“I’ll be back. And you’d better remember who has the power here, Harkness.”

Agatha stood as he turned to leave, her heart hammering in her chest. She couldn’t let him think he’d won. She’d figure out a way to handle this. But she wouldn’t tell Rio. Not yet. Rio had enough to deal with—Agatha would protect her from this. Somehow.

~*~

 

Agatha walked swiftly down the hallway toward Lilia’s office, her mind racing with the threat Jordan had made. She barely looked at Lilia’s assistant on her way in. Her hand hovered over the door handle before she opened it, walking in without the usual knock. 

Lilia was seated at her desk, papers spread out in front of her. When she saw Agatha’s tense posture, she put down her pen and leaned back in her chair.

“Agatha,” Lilia said, her voice neutral but laced with concern. “What’s going on?”

Agatha didn’t waste any time. She paced to the front of the desk and spoke quickly, the words tumbling out. “Thomas Jordan came to me today. He’s blackmailing me. He knows about Rio and me. He said he has photos of us—private moments, and screenshots of our texts.”

Lilia’s eyes narrowed. She’d been expecting something like this, but hearing it aloud made her pulse quicken. “Do you know what else he has?”

Agatha swallowed hard. “I don’t know. He didn’t say. But I… I saw the photos. He has proof. He’s been following us. There are photos of us together, kissing, hugging… God, Lilia, he has everything.”

Lilia’s gaze softened for a moment, but it was quickly replaced by a hard edge. “And what does he want?”

“He wants the mentorship I denied him. And he wants a spot in the OR. He’s threatened to come to you… and report everything if I don’t give him what he wants.”

Lilia didn’t flinch, but Agatha could tell that her words hit their mark. “And have you confronted him about the photos? The texts?”

Agatha clenched her fists, frustration and fear mixing. “I don’t want to give him the satisfaction. I’m not going to let him see me sweat. But… I have to do something.”

Lilia leaned forward, steepling her fingers in front of her. “This is a serious situation, Agatha. If he has proof and he’s threatening to go public, this could ruin both of you. Not to mention it’s illegal, what he’s doing.”

“I know,” Agatha replied, voice tight. “I thought about going to the police, but it’s not just the photos… He could use the texts. He’s got leverage. He’s going to spin this however he wants, and I can’t afford that. Not with Rio.”

Lilia exhaled, her expression hardening as she processed the gravity of the situation. “You’ve been with Rio long enough for me to know you care about her. This isn’t just about your job—it’s about protecting her, too. But the longer you keep this from her, the harder it will be for both of you when it comes to light.”

Agatha shifted uncomfortably but met Lilia’s gaze. “I’m trying to protect her. She doesn’t need to be dragged into this. I don’t want her to know. Not yet.”

Lilia’s eyes softened, but only briefly. “I understand wanting to protect her, but you’re already walking a thin line. If this gets out, you won’t be able to shield her from the fallout. And I’m not sure how much longer I can look the other way, Agatha, especially if this escalates.”

Agatha closed her eyes briefly, biting back the wave of anxiety that threatened to overwhelm her. “I’m not asking for special treatment. I’m just… asking for time. I’ll handle this on my own, but I need to keep this quiet for as long as possible.”

Lilia’s gaze didn’t waver. “You’ve been honest with me so far, and I appreciate that. But if anyone files a formal complaint… or if there’s any indication that you’ve been taking this lightly, I’ll have no choice but to act. I can’t protect you forever if you don’t take the necessary steps to protect yourself—and Rio.”

Agatha’s chest tightened, but she nodded. “I get it. I’ll talk to a lawyer. I’ll figure this out.”

Lilia exhaled, the weight of her role as Chair of Medicine settling into her tone. “Good. I’ll be here for you, Agatha. But don’t underestimate the gravity of this. You can’t avoid it forever.”

Agatha nodded again, her mind already reeling with the next steps. But before she left, she turned to Lilia one last time. “Thank you… for not making this harder.”

Lilia’s gaze softened just a touch, her voice quiet but resolute. “I’m doing what I can. Just don’t forget—time is not on your side.”

Agatha nodded once more and walked out of the office, her heart heavy with the knowledge that things were about to get much more complicated.

~*~

 

Not even an hour later, Agatha was on her way to her lawyer’s office. Her phone buzzed as she drove and she saw a text notification from Rio.

Rio

Hey beautiful! I was thinking maybe we could get some Thai food tonight? Does Nicky like it?

Agatha took a deep breath, telling herself that she would just sort this out and get back to Rio. Everything would be fine. It had to be.

A few minutes later, Agatha sat across from the lawyer, the sterile, quiet office doing little to calm the churn in her stomach. She’d called in a favor from an old colleague—someone who specialized in both personal and professional matters—and now she was sitting in front of her, explaining the situation.

The lawyer, a sharp-eyed woman in her mid-forties, adjusted her glasses, listening carefully. “So, to summarize, this Jordan character has photos of you and your partner—personal, intimate photos—and has threatened to release them unless you give him what he wants: a mentorship and a spot in the operating room?”

Agatha nodded, her jaw tight. “Yes. He also has screenshots of my texts with Rio. There’s nothing super incriminating there, but they are personal in nature. It definitely shows that our relationship is romantic.”

The lawyer raised an eyebrow, clearly disturbed. “That’s a serious violation of privacy, and it could be classified as harassment and even stalking, depending on how far he’s gone with this. I don’t know how much he’s actually done, but if he’s secretly taken photos and hacked into your phone, it’s already crossing into criminal territory.”

Agatha clenched her hands in her lap, the weight of it all sinking in. “I haven’t told anyone—especially not Rio. Actually, I only told Lilia Calderu, she’s the Chair of Medicine at Northwestern and a close friend. We talked and she’s known about my relationship with Rio for a while, but if Jordan does something, she won’t be able to help me. So I’m trying to handle this quietly. But I don’t know what my next step should be.”

“First off,” the lawyer said, “you need to document everything. Write down the exact words Jordan said to you, the threat he made, and how you know he has these photos and texts. If possible, gather whatever you can from your phone—screenshots of the texts, records of any conversations you’ve had with him about this mentorship and the OR thing. You say he’s been insisting that you reconsider for months, right?”

Agatha nodded, already going through the details in her mind. She’d seen the photos, and she knew the texts were likely a mixture of innocent exchanges and things they’d said that could be taken out of context. “I already have some evidence… the photos he showed me, but I do have the messages, but I’m afraid that’s not enough. He said he could make it look worse than it is.”

The lawyer leaned forward, her expression firm. “I understand the fear. But it’s important to know that no matter what he says, it’s not your fault. The fact that he’s using this against you is the crux of the matter here. What he’s doing is illegal, and if he follows through with these threats, he’s committing extortion.”

Agatha took a deep breath, trying to calm the tightening in her chest. “I can’t let this get out. I don’t want Rio to get dragged into this. She doesn’t deserve this. She’s fought so hard to get to where she is now. I have to protect her.”

The lawyer paused, eyes sharp with understanding. “I get why you want to protect her. But if it were me, I’d tell her as soon as possible. Keeping her in the dark only makes it harder later. She might be upset, but it’s better than her finding out from someone else. And… if this goes public, you need to be prepared for the consequences.”

Agatha stared at the desk for a moment, her fingers tapping on the edge. She knew the lawyer was right, but it wasn’t something she could face yet. “I’ll think about it. But I need to know… what should I do right now?”

The lawyer slid a business card across the desk, along with a legal pad. “The best course of action is to make sure you’re fully protected. File a police report about the harassment and the blackmail. If he has these photos, he's stalking you, so he’s already be breaking the law. Not t mention hacking into your phone. I’ll help you gather the evidence you need. But also—don’t engage with him directly. You don’t want him to have any leverage over you.”

“I’ll do that,” Agatha said, feeling the first flicker of relief in her chest. “I’ll file a report. And I’ll gather the evidence. Thank you.”

“Of course,” the lawyer said, giving her a tight smile. “Remember, this is about protecting yourself. And if you want to keep your job and your relationship intact, you need to take action quickly.”

Agatha stood up, her resolve slowly hardening. “I will. I’ll handle it.”

As she left the office, her mind raced. There were a lot of moving parts to this, but for the first time today, she felt like she was taking control.

~*~

Agatha stepped out of the police station, the weight of the report she had just filed settling heavily on her chest. The next steps weren’t clear yet, but at least she had done something. It didn’t erase the dread of what might come next, particularly where Rio was concerned.

Her phone buzzed in her pocket. Rio’s texts and missed calls filled the screen.

Rio

Where are you?

Rio

Agatha, I’m starting to get worried. Are you okay?

Rio

Call me. Please.

Agatha’s stomach clenched. She’d been so caught up in everything that she hadn’t realized how much time had passed. She quickly typed a response:

Agatha

 Sorry, got caught up in something. On my way home now.

First, she needed to grab Nicky. The evening had gotten away from her, and she hadn’t even been able to check in on him since leaving for the lawyer’s office.

After picking him up from his friend’s house, Agatha drove home, her mind swirling with everything she’d done that day. As she pulled into the driveway, a pang of concern struck her when she saw the lights on in her living room.

She parked the car, getting out with Nicky in tow. The house was silent, except for the quiet hum of the heater from inside. As they approached the door, it creaked open slightly, and Agatha found herself holding her breath. When she stepped into the foyer, she saw Rio standing there, waiting for them.

Rio’s expression softened when she saw them. Her concern was still evident, but there was a warmth to her eyes that made Agatha’s heart ache. She was clearly relieved to see them both.

“I was starting to worry,” Rio said softly, closing the door behind her. “I’ve been texting and calling. Where’ve you been?”

Agatha forced a smile, trying to keep the weight of the situation off her face. “Sorry, just had to take care of some things. I didn’t mean to make you worry.”

Nicky, looking up at Rio, seemed more concerned about the fact that his mom was acting a little off than anything else. “Are you okay, mama?” he asked, his small voice filled with innocence.

Agatha nodded quickly, kneeling down to ruffle his hair. “I’m fine, baby. Just got caught up with some work stuff, that’s all.” She gave Rio a quick glance, the unspoken tension between them not lost on her, but she hoped it wasn’t obvious to Nicky.

Rio eyed them both carefully, and for a moment, Agatha felt the weight of the unspoken words lingering in the air. But Rio just smiled and pulled Nicky into a gentle hug. “Good. I’m glad you’re both okay.”

She gave Agatha a lingering look, one that held a little too much curiosity, as if she could sense Agatha was keeping something from her. But Agatha could only offer a tight smile, hoping she wasn’t betraying herself too obviously.

“I’m gonna go start dinner,” Rio said, stepping away from Nicky and giving Agatha a soft smile. “What do you think, kiddo? You in the mood for something easy, like pasta?”

Nicky grinned, relieved by the return to normalcy. “Pasta sounds great!”

Agatha watched Rio walk to the kitchen, the weight of her silence heavier than ever. She had to keep the truth from her—for now. It was all too much to share. Agatha just wasn’t ready to let Rio carry that burden.

When Rio glanced back at her with that gentle, concerned expression, Agatha felt a wave of guilt wash over her, but she couldn’t bring herself to break.

She couldn’t risk it. Not yet.

 

~*~

A few hours later, the house was quiet once again. The sounds of Nicky’s bedtime routine had faded, and now only the soft hum of the refrigerator and the faint rustle of wind outside filled the space.

Agatha stood at the kitchen counter, her hands wrapped around a mug of tea, trying to steady herself. Rio was in the living room, flipping through a book but clearly not as absorbed in it as she wanted to be. Agatha could feel her presence in the room—the soft energy that Rio always brought, the way she made the air lighter, warmer, without even trying.

But tonight felt different. The weight of everything that had happened today—the police report, the threat from Jordan, the lies she’d had to keep up—hung heavily on her. She could almost feel Rio’s eyes on her, the unspoken questions in the air. The silence was thick, and Agatha was finding it harder and harder to pretend that everything was fine.

Rio’s voice broke through the quiet. “Agatha.”

She looked up, finding Rio’s eyes on her, full of concern. “Are you sure you’re okay?” she asked softly. “You’re… different tonight.”

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat, her heart pounding as she struggled to find the words. She couldn’t tell Rio the truth—not yet, at least. She couldn’t risk it. Not when everything was still so uncertain.

“I’m fine,” Agatha said quickly, offering a smile she didn’t feel. “Just tired, that’s all. Been a very long day.”

Rio didn’t seem entirely convinced, but she didn’t push. She gave a small nod and returned to her seat on the couch, though her gaze remained fixed on Agatha.

It was a few moments before Rio spoke again, her tone hesitant. “I know something’s off,” she said quietly. “And I don’t want to push you, but… if you ever want to talk, I’m here. You know that, right? You can tell me anything, love.”

Agatha felt a lump form in her throat. Rio’s offer, her genuine concern, only made the situation harder to bear. How could she keep this from Rio? How long could she pretend everything was fine?

“I appreciate it,” Agatha said softly, looking at Rio for a moment before turning her gaze to her mug, unable to hold her eye contact. “But this is something I have to figure out on my own.”

Rio’s lips pressed together, and for a moment, Agatha thought she might argue, but instead, she nodded and fell silent. The tension lingered between them like a storm waiting to break, and Agatha could feel the distance growing.

As the minutes stretched on, Agatha found herself standing in the doorway, the weight of everything pressing in on her. She wanted to reach out to Rio, to let her in, but the fear of everything unravelling kept her frozen.

Finally, Rio spoke again, quieter this time. “I don’t want you to feel like you have to hide things from me, Agatha. I can’t promise I’ll always understand, but I want to be there for you.”

Agatha’s heart squeezed painfully in her chest, and she swallowed hard. She was so close to breaking, so close to telling Rio everything, but she couldn’t. Not yet.

“I know,” Agatha whispered. “I just need a little more time. I promise I’ll tell you when I can.”

Rio didn’t push further, but the quiet weight of the room pressed down on Agatha. She could feel Rio’s gaze, steady and unwavering, but it wasn’t judgmental. It was just… there. A soft reminder that Rio would be there when Agatha was ready.

For now, though, Agatha had to keep the walls up.

With a shaky breath, she finally looked up at Rio. “I’m going to head to bed. I’m exhausted.”

Rio nodded, her expression softening. “Of course. I’ll be up soon. We can talk tomorrow if you feel like it.”

Agatha didn’t trust herself to speak, so she simply gave a small nod and walked toward the stairs, the silence once again settling in around them.

But even as she made her way up the stairs, Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that the truth was pulling her toward Rio, and it was only a matter of time before she couldn’t hide from it any longer.

 

Chapter 21

Chapter Notes

Once again, thank you so much for your lovely comments! I'm really glad you guys are enjoying this, even if I'm stressing you out for now.

As you all know, I'm always a few chapters ahead and I hit a block a few chapters from now. So in order to get my writing juices flowing again, I started writing another story because obviously I'm not busy enough, right? lol

Anyway, I will probably post the first chapter soon. Either later tonight or tomorrow. It's called The Space Between Notes, so keep an eye out for it, if you're interested in reading more stuff from yours truly.

I hope you guys enjoy the angst in this chapter. Fasten your seatbelts, children. We're in for a bumpy ride.

The sunrise filtered softly through the window, casting a pale glow across Agatha's room. Rio had been awake for a while, lying beside Agatha and watching her sleep. She couldn’t help but notice the way Agatha seemed so distant the night before, the subtle tension that hadn’t been there when they had last spoken yesterday morning. Even in her sleep, Agatha was different—her brow furrowed slightly, like there was something weighing on her that she couldn’t shake off.

Rio had learned to read Agatha’s moods in the time they’d been together. She knew when something was off, and yesterday was one of those days. The tightness in Agatha’s shoulders when she spoke, the way she kept her gaze a little too low, the forced smiles—Rio could feel it all. She hadn’t asked about it yet, not wanting to push, but it was clear that Agatha was hiding something.

Part of her ached at the thought. She wanted to help, to be there for her in the way that Agatha always was for her, but Agatha had been pulling away in little ways. Rio knew she had to be patient, but it was hard. There was a quiet fear creeping into her chest, the kind that whispered that maybe Agatha didn’t want her in the same way anymore.

Sighing quietly, Rio shifted carefully out of bed, trying not to disturb Agatha. She had an early shift at the firehouse today, and though she hated leaving with the tension still hanging in the air, she knew she had to go.

She stood beside the bed for a moment, watching Agatha’s peaceful expression, the way her hair fell across the pillow in soft waves. Rio smiled softly, a flicker of warmth spreading through her at the sight. Despite everything that was unsaid, there was something deeply comforting about being here, in this space with Agatha. She felt at home in a way she hadn’t known was possible.

Bending down, Rio placed a gentle kiss on the top of Agatha’s head, letting her lips linger for just a second longer than usual, before whispering softly, “I’m going to work, babe. I’ll see you later.”

Agatha stirred, mumbling something unintelligible at first before blinking her eyes open. Her gaze was blurry with sleep, but it softened when she met Rio’s eyes. “Mm, okay,” Agatha mumbled, her voice still thick with sleep.

Rio’s heart gave a small flutter at the softness in Agatha’s tone. It wasn’t much, but it was enough. She wanted to stay, to pull Agatha closer, to forget about the space between them, but her shift was calling.

“I love you,” Agatha murmured in her sleep, her voice small but sincere, almost like it slipped out without her realizing.

Rio froze, her chest tightening as the words hit her. She could feel the warmth spreading in her chest, the comfort of hearing those words even when Agatha wasn’t fully awake. It was a reassurance, a thread of connection, a lifeline that told Rio that Agatha still felt what she felt, even if the distance between them was starting to grow.

“I love you too,” Rio whispered back, her voice low and soft, a promise to herself as much as it was to Agatha.

She stayed a moment longer, watching Agatha’s chest rise and fall steadily, before she reluctantly turned and made her way toward the door, trying to shake off the uneasy feeling that lingered. She couldn’t ignore it anymore—there was something happening, and while Agatha was keeping her distance, Rio wasn’t going to give up.

Not yet.

~*~

A couple of days later, it was a typical Friday afternoon, and Rio was eager to get out of her pediatrics class. The new semester was in full swing, and while she was excited for the classes ahead, nothing compared to the thought of getting to Agatha’s place later, curling up with her, and putting the stresses of school and work behind her.

She had had Cardio II earlier that morning, and though the material had been tough, she was looking forward to Agatha’s company. She couldn’t shake the feeling that there was something off with Agatha for the past couple of days, but she’d decided to let it go for now. After all, maybe Agatha was just stressed with work. She had her own busy schedule, so Rio understood.

Walking down the hallway toward the exit of the medical building, her phone buzzing in her pocket, Rio was already mentally planning the rest of her day. She barely noticed the figure approaching her until she bumped into him.

“Hey there,” Thomas Jordan’s voice sounded behind her, and she turned, frowning when she saw him.

Jordan. Of course.

“Didn’t expect to see you here, Vidal,” he said with a smirk. “Still chasing that little neurology professor of yours around, huh?”

Rio narrowed her eyes. There was something about his tone that felt off. “What are you talking about?”

Jordan chuckled, his expression darkening with a bit of amusement. “Your little girlfriend—has she come to any conclusions yet? You know, about the whole… situation?”

Rio’s stomach dropped, confusion swirling inside her. “What situation?” she asked, her voice laced with suspicion.

His laugh was low and knowing, as if he’d been waiting for this moment. “Oh, come on. You can’t be that naive. I know you two have been… close.” He leaned in slightly, lowering his voice, “Maybe you should’ve talked to her more about things before getting all tangled up. Maybe this was just a fling after all, huh? If you two don’t even trust each other enough to share stuff like this, it doesn’t seem like it’s going anywhere.”

Rio froze, her heart thudding against her chest. She didn’t know what he meant, but she could tell from the way he was looking at her, from that smug expression on his face, that it wasn’t something innocent. The words were loaded, heavy with something she didn’t want to acknowledge.

“You’re really out of line, Jordan,” Rio said, her voice low but firm, her anger rising. “I don’t know what you think you know, but I’m not going to stand here and listen to you talk about my personal life like that.”

He shrugged, that same arrogant smirk still in place. “Oh, come on. You’re really going to pretend like you don’t know what I’m talking about?” His eyes glinted with something sinister. “I’ve got proof. You should ask her about it sometime. Maybe you’ll both feel better getting it out in the open.”

Rio felt a cold shiver run down her spine, her blood turning to ice. Proof? What the hell was he talking about?

Before she could respond, Jordan was already turning away, tossing a casual glance over his shoulder. “Maybe you should rethink things. No one’s a fool for long.”

Rio stood there for a moment, her mind racing. What had just happened? What did he mean by ‘proof’? Was there something between Agatha and Jordan she didn’t know about? She didn’t believe it for a second, but the unease gnawing at her stomach wouldn’t go away.

She could feel her pulse quickening as she gripped her phone, wanting to call Agatha, but she held off, unsure of what to say, unsure of what to even ask. The doubt that Jordan planted, that strange feeling of betrayal, lingered.

Rio’s heart was pounding as she walked away from Jordan, her mind a storm of confusion and suspicion. His words echoed in her ears, gnawing at her insides. She barely even remembered leaving the building, her feet carrying her on autopilot toward Agatha’s office.

She needed to see Agatha. To hear from her what this was about. Whatever it was, Jordan’s insinuations couldn’t be true. He had to be lying. He had to be.

But the more she thought about it, the more she realized she didn’t know what to think. She’d felt the distance between them lately, the way Agatha had been pulling back. But this—this was something else entirely. Jordan had said ‘proof,’ and the cold, knowing way he’d said it made something in her stomach twist uncomfortably.

By the time Rio reached the medical building, she was already fuming. Her fingers trembled slightly as she pushed open the door to Agatha’s office. She found herself standing there, momentarily frozen, before she took a deep breath and knocked sharply on the door.

“Agatha?” Her voice was tight, but she couldn’t stop it. The fear—dread—swirled in her chest. “We need to talk.”

She waited for a response, her heart hammering in her chest as she tried to steady her breathing. She needed answers, but part of her dreaded hearing them. Part of her feared what Agatha might say—or worse, what she might not say at all.

Rio stood there, her chest tight as she took in Agatha’s startled expression. Her heart was pounding, her mind racing with the aftermath of the encounter with Jordan. The words he had said echoed in her mind, sharp and accusatory: ‘ Your little girlfriend’

Agatha’s gaze flickered, almost like she was preparing for this, but Rio couldn’t shake the feeling that she was being kept at arm’s length. Again. She stepped into the room, her body tense, her fingers curled into fists by her sides as she forced herself to stay steady.

Jordan’s words kept playing on a loop in her head, and she couldn’t understand how Agatha could keep things from her. This wasn’t just about a fling. This was them, and it was clear now that something was wrong.

“What’s going on, Agatha?” Rio demanded, her voice low but sharp. “Jordan just talked to me. He said he has proof of us… of everything. Is that true?”

Agatha’s expression froze for just a second, and Rio caught it—caught the way her shoulders stiffened, how her eyes narrowed slightly, as though she was weighing her response. For a moment, Rio felt a sinking feeling in her stomach.

“Agatha?” she pressed again, her voice trembling now with the force of her frustration. She felt betrayed—like she’d been living in the dark while Agatha kept her secrets tucked away like something to be ashamed of.

Agatha let out a long, slow breath and finally nodded. Her gaze didn’t quite meet Rio’s as she spoke. “It’s true. Jordan… he has photos and screenshots of our conversations. He’s been… spying on me, Rio. On us. He hacked into my phone, took pictures when he thought I wasn’t looking.”

Rio’s heart skipped a beat at the words. “What? He… he’s been stalking you?” she asked, her voice barely above a whisper. Her mind reeled. “Why didn’t you tell me this? Why didn’t you say anything?”

Agatha’s eyes finally met hers, and Rio saw the weight of the truth in them—heavy, uncomfortable, but undeniable. “I didn’t want to get you involved. I thought I could handle it. I thought if I kept it from you, you’d be safe. He’s threatening to go to Lilia if I don’t give him the mentorship and the OR opportunity. I’m… trying to fix this, but I didn’t want you to worry.”

Rio’s breath caught, the shock hitting her like a punch to the gut. The realization of what Agatha had been trying to protect her from made her stomach twist in a way she couldn’t explain. But the hurt was there, deep and raw, because it wasn’t just about protecting her anymore. It was about the distance—about the fact that Agatha had kept all of this from her.

“Agatha,” Rio said, her voice trembling with a mix of anger and disbelief. “ I’m already involved. You didn’t trust me enough to tell me this? You kept me in the dark while he’s been stalking you? And you thought I wouldn’t care? Or that I wouldn’t want to help? That I didn’t deserve to know what’s going on with you?”

Agatha took a step forward, but Rio backed away, shaking her head. “I get that you’re trying to protect me, but you can’t keep doing this. I can’t be in a relationship where I don’t know what’s going on. Where you’re hiding things from me because you think it’s easier.”

Agatha’s expression softened, and Rio could see the hurt there too, but it wasn’t enough. “I’m sorry, Rio. I didn’t want to put you in danger. I wanted to keep you safe.”

“But I’m already here , Agatha! I’m already involved!” Rio’s voice cracked, and she couldn’t stop herself from taking a step closer. “I’m already in this with you. I don’t want to be kept in the dark anymore. I need you to trust me. I need you to tell me everything.”

Agatha looked at her, eyes filled with regret. “I will. I promise. But right now, I need to handle this. Please… I’ll explain everything when it’s safe.”

Rio’s chest tightened with the weight of the situation. “I don’t know if I can keep doing this if I don’t know what’s going on,” she whispered, her voice raw. “I can’t keep being kept out of the loop.”

Agatha’s expression faltered, and she reached for Rio’s hand, but Rio pulled back before she could make contact.

“I need to think,” Rio said softly, her throat tight as she turned toward the door.

Agatha didn’t say anything. She just stood there, watching Rio leave.

As Rio walked away, her heart felt heavier with every step. She didn’t know if she could keep doing this. Didn’t know if the distance between them, the lack of trust, could be fixed.

~*~

The weekend stretched on, each moment feeling like an eternity for Rio. She couldn’t shake the conversation with Agatha from her mind. The hurt was still raw, an aching reminder of how much she felt like she had been left in the dark. She couldn’t understand why Agatha hadn’t trusted her enough to share what was going on. It was a sharp, bitter feeling that refused to fade.

Alice had been relentless in trying to get Rio to talk, but every time she tried, Rio just shrugged it off, her responses curt and distant.

“I’m fine, Alice,” Rio had muttered for what felt like the hundredth time. “Just need some space.”

Alice, ever the observant friend, seemed to sense Rio’s mood. “You know you can talk to me, right? You’re not alone.”

But Rio wasn’t ready to talk. Not yet. Not about the thing that was gnawing at her from the inside, not about how betrayed she felt, and certainly not about Agatha. She didn’t know how to voice the anger, the confusion, or the disappointment. So she stayed quiet, hiding behind her silence and her stubbornness.

Agatha’s calls, texts, and even a few voicemails came pouring in, but Rio ignored them all. The phone buzzed in her pocket like a constant reminder of what was happening, but she couldn’t bring herself to answer. She needed space. Time to process. Time to figure out what this relationship meant, especially now that Agatha had kept something so important from her.

When Agatha showed up on her doorstep, knocking insistently, Rio just stared at the door for a moment before taking a deep breath and unlocking it. She opened it just enough to see Agatha standing there, looking both apologetic and desperate.

“I just want to talk, Rio,” Agatha said softly, her voice tinged with concern and something else, something that made Rio’s chest tighten.

Rio couldn’t deal with it. Not now. She shook her head, stepping back and leaning against the doorframe. “I need some time, Agatha. I can’t… I can’t do this right now.”

Agatha’s face fell, but she didn’t push, understanding the finality in Rio’s tone. “I’m sorry, I—”

“I know,” Rio interrupted quietly. “You’re sorry. But I need some space. I need time to think.”

With a heavy, silent sigh, Agatha stepped back, her hand lingering in the air as if wanting to reach out but knowing it wasn’t the right moment.

“Okay,” she said, her voice barely audible. “I’ll give you time.”

The door closed softly between them, and Rio felt the weight of it press against her chest. She knew she wasn’t ready to forgive Agatha yet, but somewhere deep down, she also knew she wanted to. She just didn’t know how.

~*~

By Sunday night, Rio was still wrapped up in the same bitter funk she’d been in all weekend. She barely noticed the world around her as she suited up for her shift, the usual chatter of the firehouse sounding muffled, like she was underwater. The weight of everything from the past few days felt heavy on her shoulders, making each movement feel sluggish, her thoughts disjointed.

She grabbed a few supplies to restock the ambulance and walked out to the rig with her mind a million miles away. She didn’t even realize Will was standing next to her until he spoke.

“Hey, you good?” Will’s voice was casual, but Rio could hear the concern in it. He was the only one brave enough to ask, everyone else content to let her be—until it was obvious she wasn’t going to snap out of it on her own.

Rio glanced at him, not even attempting a smile. “I’m fine.”

Will raised an eyebrow, crossing his arms as he leaned against the truck. “Yeah? You sure? You’ve been quiet all weekend. And you’ve been carrying some serious weight around with you tonight.”

Her jaw tightened. She wanted to brush him off, but something in his tone made her pause. He wasn’t asking out of judgment—he genuinely cared. And for whatever reason, the walls she’d been putting up all weekend cracked just a little.

“I’m… I don’t even know,” she muttered, glancing at the ground. She knew she should’ve kept it to herself, but Will had always been someone she trusted, someone who had seen her through tough times without pushing too hard. Maybe it wouldn’t hurt to say it out loud, even if she wasn’t ready to figure it all out.

“Talk to me,” Will urged, his voice softening. He was still leaning against the rig, watching her with an open, understanding gaze.

Rio exhaled sharply, running a hand through her hair. She couldn’t keep it in anymore. She needed to get it out, even if she didn’t fully understand it herself.

“Okay, here’s the thing,” she started, looking up at him. “It’s Agatha. I—” She hesitated, not sure how to explain it all. She’d been holding onto so much. “There’s stuff she’s been hiding from me. She got caught up in something with… someone. And now it’s this whole mess.
