I found out—” Rio paused, her hands clenching in frustration. “I found out someone’s been threatening her, and she didn’t even tell me. She kept it from me like I couldn’t handle it. Like she couldn’t trust me.”

Will listened carefully, his expression serious but soft. “That sounds like a lot to carry,” he said quietly.

Rio nodded, swallowing against the tightness in her throat. “It is. I mean, I get why she didn’t want to drag me into it. But she kept me in the dark, Will. And I—I don’t know what to do. I don’t know what to feel anymore.”

Will leaned in slightly, keeping his tone steady. “You’re upset because you feel betrayed. And maybe she wasn’t honest with you. But what she did, holding it all in? Sounds like she was trying to protect you from it. Doesn’t mean it was right, but it doesn’t mean it was about you, either.”

Rio crossed her arms, shaking her head. “I don’t know. It feels like she doesn’t trust me. And I can’t be with someone who doesn’t trust me.”

He gave her a sympathetic smile, his voice low. “I get that. But Rio, you’re not the only one in this. I’m not saying you shouldn’t be hurt, because you have every right to feel that way. But have you thought about why she might’ve kept things from you?”

Rio looked at him, her brow furrowing as she thought for a moment. “She says it was to protect me. But I don’t know if that’s enough to make it right.”

“I’m not gonna tell you how to feel,” Will said, his voice kind but firm. “But you’ve been carrying this for days now, and I think it’s time to stop pushing it down. Talk to her. Get the full picture before you make any decisions.”

Rio bit her lip, her mind a whirlwind. Will was right, though. She couldn’t keep ignoring this. She had to hear Agatha out, even if she was afraid of what that might mean for them.

“I guess I have to talk to her, don’t I?” Rio muttered, her voice low.

Will gave a small nod. “Yeah, I think you do.”

~*~

A few hours later, Rio stood there for a moment, phone in hand, hovering over Agatha’s contact. She wasn’t sure how to even begin the conversation, but Will’s words echoed in her mind. You have to talk to her.

She took a deep breath and quickly typed out the message:

Rio

We need to talk. Please call me when you can.

Before she could hit send, the shrill sound of the station bell pierced the air. The tone of urgency cut through her thoughts instantly. Her heart skipped, and her body went into autopilot as the crew scrambled into action. The dispatcher’s voice crackled over the speaker.

“ Large structure fire. 14th and Broadway. Multiple units needed. ”

Rio’s hand shot out, quickly clicking send before shoving the phone back into her pocket, not even realizing it was nearly midnight. She sprinted to the rig, her mind already racing with the urgency of the call. They had no time to think, no time for anything else.

The call came in fast—a five-alarm blaze in a commercial building downtown. Rio’s adrenaline kicked in as she slid into the driver’s seat of the ambulance, the sirens already blaring. Alice’s fire truck was already on the move, lights flashing as it roared down the street.

“Stay safe, Wu!” Rio called out to Alice through the open window, but the firetruck had already sped off, the sound of its engine drowned out by the chaos.

When they arrived on scene, the building was fully engulfed in flames, smoke pouring from every window. Rio joined her team, getting ready to help evacuees and assess injuries. She kept an eye on Alice, watching the firefighters gear up as they entered the building, while Rio and her crew began working with evacuees outside.

The fire raged faster than expected, and Rio’s gut tightened. Her radio crackled to life—firefighters were still inside, trying to contain the blaze, but they needed backup.

“Alice!” Rio called into the smoke-filled air, spotting her friend among the firefighters. But the noise and chaos of the scene drowned out her voice.

Then, a deafening crack sounded. The sound of wood splintering, followed by a thundering collapse of beams and debris falling from the ceiling. Rio’s heart lurched as she saw the direction the debris had fallen.

“Alice!” Rio yelled, her voice frantic now.

She sprinted toward the building just as the other firefighters managed to pull Alice from the wreckage. They laid her on the ground, her suit torn and bloodied. Rio was there in an instant, kneeling beside her, heart racing.

“Alice!” Rio breathed, trying to assess the situation.

Alice groaned, her eyes barely open. “Not… the plan…” she mumbled, her breath shallow.

“Hang on, I’ve got you,” Rio said, hands shaking as she worked to stabilize Alice’s airway. She quickly checked for any signs of severe injuries—broken ribs, possible internal bleeding. Her mind raced with protocol and triage, but the fear of seeing her best friend hurt clouded her thoughts.

The other firefighters stepped back to allow Rio to do her work. One of the medics from the ambulance team approached, but Rio shook her head.

“I’m not leaving her. I need to get her stabilized before she’s moved.”

“Rio, we’ve got it covered. Let us take over,” the medic urged gently, but Rio ignored him, focusing entirely on Alice. She couldn’t let anyone else take the lead with her best friend in this condition.

After a few tense minutes, she’d done everything she could to stop the bleeding and stabilize Alice’s vitals. The medic nodded in approval, signaling to the team to carefully lift Alice onto the stretcher. Rio’s hands hovered over her, reluctant to let go, even though the job wasn’t finished.

“I’ve got you, Wu,” Rio whispered as the team moved Alice toward the ambulance. Her heart ached with the weight of it all, but she didn’t let herself break down—not yet.

Once Alice was secured in the ambulance, Rio climbed in beside her, never leaving her side. The only sounds in the back of the ambulance were Alice’s uneven breathing and the rush of the sirens outside.

“It’s gonna be okay,” Rio murmured to Alice, though she didn’t fully believe it. Not yet.

 

~*~

The ambulance was rocking with every sharp turn, the flashing lights outside casting eerie shadows through the windows. Alice’s breathing was erratic, and Rio’s hands were trembling as she worked to stabilize her.

“Alice, come on, stay with me,” Rio muttered, checking for a pulse when the monitor beeped and then flatlined. There was nothing. Rio’s heart raced as panic threatened to take hold, but she pushed it down, refocusing.

“Alice, please.”

She started chest compressions, counting in her head, moving fast, methodical. Every push was a plea, but no matter how hard she tried, Alice didn’t respond.

“Come on, Wu, don’t do this to me!” Rio gritted out, switching to rescue breaths, desperation seeping into every motion. The pressure in her chest was suffocating.

Finally, after what felt like an eternity, Alice’s chest gave a weak rise. Rio didn’t stop. She continued CPR until she felt the faintest pulse, but it was still so weak.

“Come on, Alice. Just hold on, okay? I need you to hold on for me.”

By the time they reached the hospital, Rio’s arms were burning from the force of her efforts. She jumped out of the ambulance, pulling Alice’s stretcher toward the emergency room. Her voice was steady, but there was a tremor beneath her words.

“Alice Wu, 39 years old, blunt force trauma to the chest, possible internal bleeding. Lost pulse briefly en route. Respiration and heartbeat restored, pulse weak. Ongoing CPR. BP 80 over 40.”

She rattled off the details without missing a beat, but her voice was shaking—small cracks starting to show through the control she’d forced herself to maintain. The doctors and nurses took over, wheeling Alice inside as quickly as they could.

The hours in the hospital passed with excruciating slowness. Rio barely moved from her spot in the waiting area, her mind racing with a thousand thoughts, each one more frantic than the last. Alice’s surgery, the uncertainty, the aftermath of the fire—everything felt like a blur. The wait seemed endless.

Mick, John, Will, and Ben stayed by her side, their usual banter subdued, everyone too tense to speak. The only sound was the quiet hum of the hospital, but it felt like Rio’s whole world was holding its breath, waiting for the next update.

Finally, a doctor emerged from the ICU, his expression professional but tinged with a sense of calm. He scanned the group and then focused on Rio.

“Alice Wu’s family?”

She immediately jumped to her feet. “How is she?”

The doctor nodded. “She made it through surgery. She’s stable now, resting in the ICU. We’ll need to monitor her closely, but everything looks promising. She’s not awake yet, but we’ll keep you posted if anything changes.”

Rio exhaled a shaky breath, relief flooding her system, and she saw the same sense of relief ripple through her colleagues. Will clapped her on the back, a soft, “Good job, Rio,” slipping out, but she barely heard him, her mind already turning to the next thing.

Rio sagged against the wall, her body finally giving in to exhaustion. She let out a shaky breath, hands still trembling as she wiped at her face, feeling the full impact of the day.

She reached for her phone, her thumb swiping across the screen absently. It was a flurry of missed calls and texts. Her heart skipped when she saw Agatha’s name at the top of the list. Several calls. A handful of worried messages. The last one reading, Are you okay? I’ve been trying to reach you for hours. I’m worried.

Rio checked the time for the first time. It was 1:15pm. Rio’s stomach twisted, guilt and something else gnawing at her. She hadn’t been able to answer. Not with everything going on.

But now, everything that had been building—everything she had tried to suppress—rushed to the surface.

Without thinking, she booked an Uber, her body on autopilot as she rode to Northwestern. She couldn’t breathe, couldn’t think of anything except Agatha.

When the Uber pulled up to Northwestern, Rio was already halfway out the door. She didn’t even pause to fix her uniform, still smeared with Alice’s blood. She didn’t care. All she could focus on was getting to Agatha, getting answers, making things right, and for the first time, realizing how much she’d been hurting, too.

She practically ran into the building, ignoring the tightness in her chest, heading straight for Agatha’s office. She knocked on the door with shaking hands. When Agatha opened it, Rio didn’t have the strength to hold herself upright anymore.

She collapsed into Agatha’s arms, all the weight of the last few days crashing over her in one overwhelming wave.

Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio, pulling her inside and shutting the door behind them.

“Rio? What happened?” she asked, her voice filled with concern and confusion, but Rio couldn’t speak yet. Her body was still shaking with the adrenaline, and her throat was tight, fighting the wave of emotion.

Agatha held her, rubbing soothing circles on her back as Rio clung to her.

“I… I thought I was going to lose her,” Rio finally managed to choke out. “I thought I was going to lose Alice last night.”

Agatha said nothing for a long moment, just holding Rio, letting her lean into her warmth.

“I’m here,” Agatha whispered, voice gentle, but Rio could hear the edge of worry that had crept in.

And for the first time all weekend, Rio let herself lean into Agatha’s presence, letting the feeling of being held in her arms drown out the noise of everything else that had been happening.

Chapter Notes

So glad you guys enjoyed the last chapter. It was my favorite so far and I'm so happy it was well received! Thank you so much for your lovely comments.

I'd also like to take the time to thank everyone who checked out my new fic "The Space Between Notes", and took the time to comment and leave kudos. You guys are the absolute best.

I hope you guys enjoy this one. Let me know what you think!

Agatha held Rio in her arms, her heart pounding as she felt the weight of everything. Rio had pulled away from her earlier, keeping her distance, but now she was here, in her arms again. Agatha could feel the tension in Rio’s body, the way her breathing was shallow, the weight of whatever she’d been carrying pressing down on her. The familiar rhythm of Rio’s heartbeat thudded against her chest, grounding Agatha in a way she hadn’t realized she needed.

Her mind raced, overwhelmed with the need to comfort her, to be there for her—especially after everything that had happened. There was something more in the air now, an unspoken shift between them. But Agatha kept her grip tight, not wanting to let go. She needed to hold on, to keep her close for just a little while longer.

“Rio,” she murmured, her voice soft but firm, “just breathe. Just… stay with me for a while.”

Rio nodded, her head resting against Agatha’s shoulder, and for a moment, everything felt like it was right where it should be. But Agatha knew better than to think it was that simple. The unease in Rio’s posture was still there, lingering beneath her quiet breaths. There was a storm inside of her, one that Agatha could feel but didn’t yet understand.

As Agatha gently pulled back, wanting to look into Rio’s eyes, she finally spoke. “What happened, Rio? You said something happened to Alice?”

Rio hesitated, her fingers tightening on the fabric of Agatha’s shirt, her knuckles white as she drew a breath. Agatha could see the unease in her eyes, the conflict in the way Rio’s gaze kept darting away.

Rio exhaled, trying to steady herself before she spoke, but the words came out in a rush, barely coherent. “She was… caught in the fire. She was trapped. We pulled her out, and then—then her heart stopped. Her heart stopped, Agatha. She crashed on the way to the hospital.”

The way Rio’s voice cracked made Agatha’s chest tighten, and instinctively, she pulled Rio back in. She needed to feel her in her arms again, to offer whatever comfort she could, even though she could see that nothing would be enough to take the pain away.

Rio continued, her voice softer now but still trembling. “I—I had to do it, Agatha. I had to give her CPR. I thought I was going to lose her right there. She wasn’t responding. I was… I don’t know what I was thinking. I just kept doing it until we got to the hospital and she—” Her voice caught, and Agatha could hear the rawness of it, the weight of the fear and the adrenaline that had kept Rio going all this time.

Agatha held her tighter, feeling the way Rio’s body trembled, the pain in her voice sinking deep into her heart. She knew Rio was strong, knew how much she cared for the people in her life. But this… this was different. This wasn’t just the adrenaline of a rescue. It was the gut-wrenching fear of almost losing someone she loved, and Agatha felt the depth of that fear like it was her own.

“Shh,” Agatha whispered, pressing her cheek to the top of Rio’s head. “You did everything you could. Alice is going to be okay, right?”

Rio’s breath hitched as she nodded, and Agatha could feel the sudden shake in her shoulders as the tears started to fall. She felt the warmth of them against her neck, and her heart broke for the woman in her arms.

Rio pulled back just slightly, enough to look Agatha in the eyes, her face streaked with tears and her expression a mix of exhaustion and vulnerability. “I—I was so scared, Agatha,” she whispered, her voice trembling with the weight of everything. “I didn’t think I could do it. I thought I was going to lose her. I thought I wouldn’t be able to save her.”

Agatha cupped Rio’s face gently, wiping away a tear with the pad of her thumb, the moment raw and tender. “You did save her, Rio. You’re a hero, you know that?”

Rio shook her head, her eyes filled with disbelief. “I don’t feel like a hero. I just feel… lost. Like everything’s spinning out of control.”

Agatha could see it then—the way the fear, the weight of the responsibility Rio carried, had been building for days. It wasn’t just Alice or the fire. It was everything. It was the fear of losing someone close, the pressure of keeping it together, and, maybe, the strain of everything she and Agatha hadn’t been able to say to each other.

“Rio,” Agatha said, her voice steady but full of warmth. “I’m here. You don’t have to go through this alone.”

But Rio didn’t seem to hear her. She was too lost in her own thoughts, her head dropping to Agatha’s shoulder again. Agatha held her, the silence between them comfortable for once, both of them knowing that words weren’t needed at the moment.

As Rio’s body shuddered with the weight of her emotions, Agatha wrapped her arms around her once more, not letting go this time. She could feel Rio’s breath hitching in her chest, could feel the tremors of fear and exhaustion that still lingered, and she knew this was the moment to let her feel safe, to give her the comfort she needed.

“Come on,” Agatha whispered, gently guiding Rio by the shoulders. “Let’s sit down. You need to rest for a moment.”

She led Rio toward the small couch in her office, the one Agatha had used countless times for meetings with students, but it felt different now—more personal, more intimate, as she guided Rio to sit down. The couch was soft, and as Rio sank into it, Agatha settled beside her, sitting close but allowing Rio the space to breathe.

Rio exhaled deeply, her head dropping to rest on Agatha’s shoulder as she sat down. Agatha reached for a nearby blanket, draping it gently over Rio’s shoulders. It was simple, but in the moment, it felt like exactly what Rio needed—a safe space to process everything, to let go for just a little while.

Agatha’s hand found its way to Rio’s, intertwining their fingers as she rested her head against Rio’s, her heart beating steadily, reassuringly.

“I’m here, Rio,” Agatha murmured again, her voice soft but full of meaning. “I’m right here with you.”

And for the first time in days, Rio let herself sink into the comfort of Agatha’s embrace. As they sat there in silence, Agatha knew that no matter what came next, they would find a way to face it together.

~*~

Agatha held Rio close as the tears continued to pour, allowing her to cry without interruption, without judgment. She just let her lean into her, softly whispering reassurances, knowing Rio needed this—needed the space to let it all out. It wasn’t just the fear or the trauma of what had happened to Alice; it was everything—her confusion, her guilt, her exhaustion.

As the minutes passed, Rio’s sobs started to quiet, her body slowing its shaking. Agatha kissed her temple gently, the warmth of the gesture grounding both of them.

“Are you feeling a little better?” Agatha asked softly, her voice tender.

Rio nodded against her shoulder, her breath still uneven but more stable now. She hadn’t said a word for a while, but Agatha could feel the slight relief that was starting to seep through her tense frame.

“Good,” Agatha murmured. She brushed a strand of hair from Rio’s face, her thumb lightly grazing her cheek. “Listen, I know you probably want to get out of those clothes. They’re soaked in—” she paused, swallowing a knot in her throat, “blood. I’ve got some sweatpants and a hoodie in my car. You can change into those if you want.”

Rio hesitated, her eyes glistening with exhaustion, but her grip on Agatha’s hand tightened in response. “Yeah… I’d really appreciate that.”

Agatha smiled softly, brushing another kiss to Rio’s temple before standing up. “Okay, I’ll be right back.”

As she left the office to grab the clothes from her car, Agatha’s heart was still heavy with worry, but she knew that Rio needed some comfort, some way to shed the weight of the night. And Agatha would be right there with her, helping to carry it as much as she could.

~*~

Agatha returned a few minutes later with the clothes, the soft fabric of the hoodie and sweatpants a welcome contrast to the tension that had lingered in the air. She stepped into her office, where Rio was sitting on the small couch, her eyes closed, her expression a mixture of exhaustion and emotional overload.

“Here,” Agatha said gently, offering the clothes. “I’ll wait outside. You can change in here, take your time.”

Rio looked up, her eyes still red, but a faint, tired smile tugged at the corner of her lips. “Thanks, Agatha. You’ve done enough already.” Her voice was rough from all the crying, but there was warmth in it, even if it was tinged with uncertainty.

Agatha nodded, her chest tightening as she watched Rio struggle to get her bearings. “I’m not going anywhere, sweetheart. Just let me know if you need anything.”

She stepped out into the hallway, giving Rio the space to change. The minutes stretched on, each second seeming to hang heavier in the air. Agatha couldn’t shake the worry gnawing at her insides. She could only imagine what Rio had gone through, how her heart must have been pounding in her chest when Alice crashed in the ambulance. The weight of it all was unbearable, and Agatha knew she had to be there for Rio—she had to be strong, especially when Rio felt like she might break.

When Rio finally opened the door to the office, dressed in the clothes Agatha had given her, she looked softer somehow, though still fragile. Her eyes met Agatha’s, and there was a flicker of something unspoken between them—gratitude, vulnerability, something deeper that neither of them could yet name.

“Feel a little better?” Agatha asked, her voice low but caring.

Rio nodded, though she seemed too tired to form a response. She sat back down on the couch, her shoulders slumping with relief, but there was still a haunted look in her eyes. Agatha could tell that, even though the worst was over for Alice, the emotional toll on Rio hadn’t even begun to fade.

Agatha sat beside her, her presence a quiet comfort. She didn’t try to force a conversation, letting the silence stretch between them, but it wasn’t an uncomfortable silence. It was one of understanding, a space where they didn’t need to fill the gaps with words. Agatha’s hand gently brushed against Rio’s, a subtle offering of support.

“I’m here,” Agatha whispered, her voice almost a promise.

Rio didn’t respond immediately. She just leaned into Agatha’s side, her head resting on her shoulder. Agatha could feel the tension in Rio’s body slowly ease, bit by bit, as they sat there together, two souls navigating the aftermath of a nightmare that had somehow pulled them closer.

“Thank you for staying with me,” Rio said quietly after a long pause, her voice soft but full of sincerity. “For everything.”

Agatha kissed her forehead lightly, her heart swelling with a tenderness that only Rio could inspire in her. “I’ll always stay with you.”

Rio’s breath evened out, her head still resting on Agatha’s shoulder, the soft rise and fall of her chest giving away how exhausted she truly was. Agatha stayed as still as she could, not wanting to disturb the fragile peace that had settled over Rio. She could feel the weight of Rio’s body, the exhaustion that had claimed her, and she knew that the last thing Rio needed was to be rushed.

For a moment, Agatha allowed herself to simply be present—just holding Rio, keeping her close, as time seemed to stretch and bend around them. It wasn’t until Rio’s breathing deepened, her face relaxing into sleep, that Agatha knew she had drifted off.

After a few minutes, Agatha carefully shifted, adjusting so she could look down at Rio without disturbing her too much. The exhaustion on Rio’s face was undeniable, but so was the trust Rio had placed in her today. Agatha’s heart ached, but there was something else there too—a warmth that she couldn’t quite explain, a sense of belonging that settled in her chest.

She gently brushed a few strands of hair from Rio’s face, feeling the softness of her skin beneath her fingers. It felt almost intimate, this quiet moment between them, and Agatha held on to it as long as she could before she knew she had to do something.

“Rio,” Agatha whispered softly, brushing a kiss to the top of her head, “You should get some real rest. Come on, baby, I’ll drive you home.”

Rio stirred slightly, mumbling incoherently for a moment before blinking her eyes open. She looked up at Agatha, still a little dazed.

“You’re falling asleep on me, Rio,” Agatha said with a soft smile, her hand gently brushing Rio’s cheek. “I think you could use a few more hours of sleep at home. I can take you there.”

Rio’s lips parted as if to protest, but the words never came. She seemed to think about it for a beat, then nodded slowly, too tired to argue.

“Okay,” Rio murmured, her voice still rough. “Thank you.”

Agatha offered her a reassuring smile, helping Rio stand up from the couch. “Let me get you home.. We can talk tomorrow, when you’re ready.”

Rio gave a small, weary smile in return as Agatha helped her gather her things and they walked together out of the office. Agatha’s heart remained heavy with the events of the day, but there was comfort in knowing she was there for Rio in this moment—right when she needed it most.

~*~

As Agatha and Rio entered the apartment, the tension between them was palpable. The silence in the air seemed heavy, like it was waiting for something to break it. Rio moved toward her bedroom without saying much, and Agatha followed quietly, understanding that this wasn’t the time for pressing conversations. It was just the two of them, and Agatha wanted to respect that.

Rio stopped at the edge of the bed, standing still for a moment, as though uncertain of what to do next. She glanced at Agatha, her expression unreadable. Agatha didn’t push her. Instead, she stood nearby, allowing Rio the space to decide what she needed.

“Do you want me to stay?” Agatha asked gently, breaking the silence but keeping her voice calm and low. She wasn’t about to make any moves without Rio’s direction.

Rio didn’t answer immediately. She simply moved to the side of the bed, slowly sitting down. After a beat, she patted the spot next to her, an unspoken invitation. Agatha hesitated for a moment but then sat down beside her.

They sat like that, a small distance between them, neither of them quite sure how to bridge it. The weight of the night still lingered in the air, both of them worn out from the chaos of the fire, the fear, and the events that had followed. But Agatha could see it—the way Rio’s shoulders were slumped, the way her hands fidgeted with the hem of her sleeve. She could tell that Rio wasn’t okay, that there was something more underneath the surface, something that Rio was holding back.

The quiet stretched on, but then Rio shifted. She turned slightly, looking at Agatha, her eyes vulnerable. “I don’t want to be alone right now,” Rio admitted quietly, her voice rough.

Agatha felt a pang in her chest, a sharp ache of empathy. She reached for Rio’s hand gently, offering comfort without words, and to her surprise, Rio took it. The contact seemed to break the invisible wall between them, and Rio leaned a little closer, her face still tight with the exhaustion of the day.

Agatha’s heart softened, and she could feel Rio slowly letting herself rely on her.

Rio let out a shaky breath. “I feel like everything’s falling apart, Agatha. I don’t even know where to start… or how to deal with all of it.”

“You don’t have to figure it out right now,” Agatha said softly, moving a little closer herself. “It’s okay to just… be. We can figure it out when you’re ready.”

There was a long moment of stillness, before Rio finally sought comfort, just like she had earlier on the couch. She inched closer, leaning her head gently on Agatha’s shoulder. The action was simple, yet it felt monumental—like a shift, a sign of trust, of allowing herself to need someone.

Agatha’s arm naturally wrapped around her, pulling her a little closer. For a while, they just sat like that, Rio’s breath steadying as she rested against Agatha’s shoulder. Agatha didn’t try to rush her, didn’t push for more. She just held her, offering what little comfort she could.

When Rio spoke again, her voice was quiet but sincere. “Thank you… for being here. For not letting go.”

“I’ll never let go, Rio,” Agatha whispered. “I’m here, no matter what.”

The silence that followed wasn’t uncomfortable. It was filled with understanding, with the quiet connection they were building, step by step.

Rio’s body eventually relaxed into her arms, and Agatha slowly made the woman she loved lie down, as her breathing started to even out. Before long, Rio’s head tilted against Agatha’s, her eyelids fluttering closed as she dozed off in the safety of Agatha’s embrace.

Agatha let her sleep, watching over her, knowing that there would be time to talk, time to sort through the mess of everything that had happened. But for now, all that mattered was this—being here, together, letting Rio rest.

As Rio drifted off to sleep, Agatha kissed her hair softly, whispering to herself more than to Rio, “I’ll protect you, baby. Always.”
