A few hours passed in a quiet, peaceful stillness. Agatha hadn’t moved from the couch, her eyes flicking between the quiet apartment and Rio’s room, her thoughts occupied by everything that had happened and everything that was yet to be addressed. She knew Rio needed space to breathe, to let the weight of the day sink in before anything else could be discussed. Agatha made the decision to text Wanda and ask her to pick up Nicky and keep him for a bit, giving Rio the time to sleep uninterrupted.

When Rio finally emerged from her room, it felt like the calm after a storm. Her hair was mussed, and she rubbed her eyes sleepily as she stepped into the living room, looking every bit the vulnerable, tired woman Agatha knew she was at that moment.

“Hey,” Agatha said gently, her voice a soft whisper in the quiet apartment. She looked up from her phone, where she’d been texting Wanda updates on Nicky.

Rio gave her a small, tired smile, but there was still a hesitancy in her movements. She shuffled over to the couch and sat down next to Agatha, her eyes still heavy from sleep.

“How do you feel?” Agatha asked softly, her gaze studying Rio’s expression, looking for any hint of what she might be feeling.

Rio let out a small, shaky breath before answering. “Better, I think. Just… tired.” She glanced at Agatha, her eyes lingering a bit longer than usual, but she didn’t say anything else.

Agatha nodded, offering her a small smile. “You needed the rest. Don’t worry about anything right now.”

Rio leaned back into the couch, her body sinking into the cushions, and for a moment, neither of them spoke. The silence was comfortable, a brief respite from the chaos of the past few days.

“Thank you,” Rio murmured after a while, her voice quiet but sincere. “For everything. For being here, even when I was… well, distant.”

Agatha gave her a soft smile, reaching out to gently touch Rio’s arm. “You don’t have to thank me. I’m here, Rio. I’m not going anywhere.”

Rio’s gaze softened, her exhaustion mixing with a quiet sense of relief. She let her head fall back against the couch, closing her eyes for a moment, just enjoying the calm presence of Agatha beside her.

“I just needed a little time,” Rio murmured, her voice still thick with sleep.

Agatha nodded, understanding. “Of course. Take all the time you need. I’m not going anywhere.”

Rio didn’t say anything else for a while, and Agatha gave her the space to think. She could tell Rio wasn’t ready to dive back into the heavy emotions of the night, but Agatha was here, ready to offer her support whenever Rio was ready.

A few moments later, Rio shifted slightly, looking at Agatha with a small but appreciative smile. “I know I’ve been hard to deal with these past few days,” she said, her voice quiet but sincere. “But I’m glad you’re here. I don’t know what I’d do without you.”

Agatha’s heart swelled at the words. She wanted to tell Rio that she didn’t have to do anything alone, but she just nodded, offering her a soft smile in return.

“No place I’d rather be,” Agatha promised quietly.

Rio’s gaze softened, and for the first time that day, a small, genuine smile tugged at the corner of her lips. “I’m lucky to have you.”

Agatha returned the smile, squeezing Rio’s hand gently. “We’re in this together.”

Rio nodded at Agatha’s words, letting them settle into the quiet of the apartment. She squeezed Agatha’s hand back, just for a moment, before leaning forward and rubbing her face with both hands.

“I should eat something,” she murmured, though she didn’t move just yet.

Agatha watched her carefully. “I can make you something,” she offered.

Rio glanced at her with a small smile. “Yeah?”

Agatha brushed a strand of Rio’s hair behind her ear. “Of course.”

Rio’s smile was faint, but it was real, and Agatha counted that as a win. “Alright, professor. Show me what you’ve got.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but stood, extending a hand to Rio, who took it and let herself be pulled up. She was still moving slower than usual, exhaustion clinging to her bones, but she was up. That was enough for now.

~*~

As Agatha moved around the kitchen, Rio sat at the counter, watching her with an unreadable expression. The quiet between them wasn’t heavy, but it wasn’t exactly light either. It was the kind of silence that came after a long, exhausting night—the kind that didn’t need to be filled.

Agatha worked efficiently, scrambling eggs and toasting some bread, something quick and warm that wouldn’t take too much effort to eat. She was aware of Rio’s eyes on her the entire time, though the younger woman hadn’t said much since they got up.

When she finally set the plate in front of her, Rio muttered a quiet “Thanks” before picking up her fork.

Agatha leaned against the counter, arms crossed, watching as Rio took her first bite.

Rio chewed slowly, then swallowed, letting out a soft sigh. “I think this is the first thing I’ve eaten in… I don’t even know.”

Agatha frowned. “Since before your shift?”

Rio just nodded, not meeting her eyes.

Agatha exhaled, rubbing her forehead. “You need to take care of yourself.”

“I know,” Rio muttered, picking at her toast. She hesitated, then sighed, shaking her head. “It’s just—” She paused, gripping the fork a little tighter. “I can still feel it, you know? The way her ribs felt under my hands when I was doing compressions. The way she just—” She stopped, pressing her lips together like she was trying to push back the memory. “It’s like it’s stuck to me.”

Agatha’s expression softened. She stepped closer, resting a hand on the counter beside Rio. “I know it doesn’t feel like it now, but that weight won’t always be this heavy.”

Rio let out a breath that sounded almost like a laugh, though there was no humor in it. “You say that like it’s something I can just put down.”

“Not put down,” Agatha corrected gently. “But carry differently.”

Rio finally looked at her, eyes tired but open. “You ever carried something like this?”

Agatha held her gaze, thinking of all the patients she’d lost, the ones she hadn’t been able to save. Of the times she had to step into a waiting room and tell a family there was nothing more they could do. Of how—no matter how much time passed—some names never faded.

“Yes,” she said simply.

Rio searched her face for a long moment, then nodded. She turned back to her plate, picking at the food but eating a little more. It wasn’t much, but it was something.

And for now, something was enough.

~*~

The silence between them stretched, thick with things left unsaid. Agatha watched as Rio absently pushed her toast around the plate, eyes unfocused, her mind clearly elsewhere. She wanted to reach for her, to pull her back, but she knew now wasn’t the time.

Not when Rio was still raw from everything that had happened.

Not when she was still carrying Alice’s near-death like it was etched into her skin.

Agatha swallowed, shifting her weight. She thought about the past weekend, about the way her stomach had twisted when she spotted Jordan sitting in his car outside her house, watching. She’d felt her heart hammer in her chest, a cold dread creeping up her spine. He hadn’t done anything—hadn’t approached, hadn’t spoken—but he hadn’t needed to. His presence alone had been a reminder. A warning.

She should tell Rio.

She wanted to.

But as she looked at her now, still shaken, still struggling to push down the weight of what had happened to Alice, Agatha knew she couldn’t. Not yet.

She wouldn’t make the same mistake as before, though. She wouldn’t shut Rio out completely.

Taking a slow breath, Agatha reached out, resting a hand lightly on Rio’s arm. “Hey.”

Rio blinked, finally looking up.

Agatha met her gaze, steady and open. “We can talk. If or when you’re ready.”

Rio studied her for a long moment, something flickering behind her tired eyes. Then, finally, she gave a small nod. “Okay.”

Agatha hesitated, fingers curling slightly on the edge of the table. The distance between them—so unfamiliar, so heavy—made her chest ache. They were walking on eggshells, careful and uncertain in a way that neither of them had ever been before. And it just about killed her.

She cleared her throat, voice quieter than she intended. “Do you want me to go?”

Rio’s head snapped up, startled. Her brows pulled together as if the question hadn’t even crossed her mind.

Agatha held her breath, bracing herself for whatever came next.

Rio blinked, her expression shifting—hesitation, something close to disbelief, then something softer. She exhaled, rubbing a hand over her face before shaking her head. “No,” she said, voice rough with exhaustion. “I don’t.”

Agatha felt something in her chest unclench. She nodded, slow and careful. “Okay.”

Rio’s fingers drummed idly against the table, a restless energy still lingering in her. “I know I’ve been—” She sighed, shaking her head like she didn’t know how to put it into words. “I just—”

“You don’t have to explain,” Agatha said gently. 

Rio’s jaw tensed. She looked away for a moment, then back at Agatha. “No, no. I just… don’t want you to think I don’t want you here.”

Agatha’s throat tightened. She reached across the table, hesitating for only a second before covering Rio’s hand with her own. “I don’t,” she murmured. “I just don’t know how to help.”

Rio looked down at their hands, then flipped hers over so their fingers curled together. “Just stay.”

It was barely more than a whisper, but it was enough.

Agatha squeezed her hand. “Okay.”

~*~

The quiet stretched between them, the soft flicker of the screen casting shadows across the room. Rio’s gaze wandered, but her mind seemed far away, her thoughts weighing heavier than the light atmosphere the comedy was trying to provide.

She shifted slightly, a quiet sigh escaping her lips. After a moment, she spoke, her voice soft but tinged with something deeper. “I miss Nicky,” she admitted, her eyes briefly meeting Agatha’s before drifting away again. “I’ve been so caught up in everything… and I miss him. I miss how things used to be.”

Agatha’s chest tightened, her heart warming as she listened to Rio’s words. There was something about hearing Rio talk about Nicky with such longing that made Agatha feel closer to her, like she was opening up in a way that only came when someone truly cared. She reached out instinctively, her hand resting lightly on Rio’s, a quiet gesture of reassurance.

“I know,” Agatha murmured, her voice soft. “I see how much you care for him, Rio. He’s lucky to have you.”

Rio swallowed, her throat tight. “I just want to make sure he’s okay. I’ve been away for a few days now, and I… I don’t know. I guess I’m not sure if I’m doing this whole ‘family’ thing right. If I even should.”

Agatha’s entire demeanor softened and she squeezed her hand gently. “You’re doing just fine, sweetheart. He loves you, and he’s growing up with a role model like you. He’s lucky to have you in his life, just like you’re lucky to have him.”

A silence fell again, but this time it felt lighter, like a weight had been lifted just a little. Rio shifted again, her eyes lowering to her lap as her fingers played with the edge of the blanket. After a moment, she let out a quiet breath, as if letting something out that she had been holding in for far too long. “And… I miss you, Agatha,” she confessed, her voice barely above a whisper, but it hit Agatha like a wave. “I don’t know what I’m doing anymore, but I know I miss you.”

Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, warmth flooding her chest as she looked at Rio, the vulnerability in her eyes more than enough to silence any other thoughts. She leaned closer, brushing a lock of hair from Rio’s face.

“I miss you too,” Agatha said, her voice soft, almost tender. She gave a small, wry smile, a hint of self-consciousness creeping in as she added, “I’m just following your lead here.”

Rio’s eyes softened as she looked at Agatha, and for a moment, everything else seemed to fade away—the worries, the confusion, the pain. It was just the two of them, finding solace in the quiet, in the shared understanding that things weren’t perfect, but they were still trying.

“I don’t know what’s going to happen next,” Rio murmured, “but I want to figure it out… with you.”

Agatha smiled, her thumb brushing against Rio’s hand in a gentle, reassuring motion. “We’ll figure it out. Together.”





Twenty Three

Chapter Notes

Thank you so much for your thoughtful comments. They really do make my day.

Rio blinked slowly as the morning light filtered through the curtains, the warmth of Agatha’s presence next to her pulling her from the depths of sleep. Her gaze shifted to Agatha, who was still sleeping soundly beside her, her features soft and peaceful in the early light.

Rio hadn’t expected this — hadn’t expected to wake up with Agatha beside her, to find herself tangled in the quiet comfort of her presence after everything that had happened. She never thought the first time Agatha would sleep in her bed would be under such fragile circumstances. It wasn’t the start she’d imagined for them, but somehow, it was the beginning they had found.

Her heart ached, the remnants of the conversation they’d had the night before still lingering in the air, as raw and tender as the moments between them. They were still walking on eggshells, still trying to find their footing in the aftermath of everything, and it hurt more than Rio had expected. But despite the fragility, there was a quiet understanding between them now. They didn’t need to rush into fixing everything; they just needed to be together.

She stared at Agatha for a moment longer, her heart swelling with emotions she wasn’t sure how to put into words. The hurt and betrayal she’d felt when Agatha hadn’t told her about Jordan’s threat was still there, still heavy, but it was tempered by something deeper, something more potent: the undeniable ache of being without her.

It had only been three days. Four, now. But every second without Agatha had felt like an eternity. She couldn’t imagine living without her again.

Rio’s hand moved slowly to where Agatha’s rested beside her, her fingers brushing against the older woman’s. The simple contact sent a spark of warmth through her, a reminder of the tenderness between them that she still held onto. Despite everything, the connection was still there, fragile but real.

She loved Agatha. So much that it hurt sometimes. But this was worth fighting for. They were worth fighting for.

“I want this,” Rio whispered to herself, her voice barely a breath, but it felt like a declaration. She didn’t know exactly how they were going to navigate the mess they were in, didn’t know how long it would take to get through everything, but she knew she wanted to try.

She wanted to fight for them, for their love, for their future, whatever that might look like. Because with Agatha beside her, the world felt a little less heavy, and she felt like she could take on whatever came next.

For a moment, she just stayed there, watching Agatha’s peaceful expression. Her heart ached a little at how still and tender Agatha looked, how vulnerable in that quiet, unspoken way. Rio couldn’t believe how much she had missed this—her, Agatha, just being close to her like this.

After everything that had happened, everything they’d been through, it was hard to believe they were still here, still connected. But Rio wasn’t ready to let go, not yet, not after everything that had passed between them.

She reached out, her hand trembling slightly, but she didn’t pull back. Her fingers traced the curve of Agatha’s face, brushing against her cheek as she caressed her, almost like it was instinct. She could feel Agatha’s warmth beneath her touch, the gentle rise and fall of her breath. Rio closed her eyes for a second, savoring the moment, feeling the soft weight of Agatha’s presence like a lifeline.

When Agatha stirred, blinking her eyes open, Rio met her gaze immediately. There was so much unspoken in that look, so much that neither of them knew how to say just yet. But Rio felt the warmth in Agatha’s gaze, the understanding, and it made her heart skip.

Rio couldn’t stop herself from smiling faintly, her thumb continuing to glide over Agatha’s cheek. She hadn’t meant to say it, but the words just slipped out.

“I missed you,” she whispered, her voice low, almost hesitant. It felt strange to admit, to say it aloud, but it was true. She missed her so damn much.

Agatha’s expression softened, her eyes flickering with emotion. Rio felt something shift in her chest at the sight—something that felt like hope, like maybe everything wasn’t as broken as it had seemed.

“You’re here,” Agatha whispered, the words heavy with something Rio couldn’t quite place but felt deep in her bones. “You’re here with me.”

Rio nodded slowly, her heart pounding in her chest. “Always,” she murmured, her voice barely above a whisper. The words felt natural, as though that was exactly what she had always known she wanted to say, even before she had the courage to.

She moved then, closing the gap between them, her lips hovering just a breath away from Agatha’s. For a moment, everything was suspended—her heartbeat, her breath, her thoughts—until Agatha’s hand reached up to gently cup her face, urging her closer. And Rio couldn’t help herself. She leaned in, pressing a soft, lingering kiss to Agatha’s lips, a kiss full of all the things she hadn’t known how to say. It wasn’t perfect. It was messy, just like them, but it was real.

When they finally pulled away, Rio let her forehead rest against Agatha’s, her breath shaky. She closed her eyes and sighed, feeling the weight of everything they had been through, everything they hadn’t yet said, but also feeling a fragile, growing peace settle in her chest.

“Thank you,” Rio whispered, her voice small but filled with gratitude. “For being here. For not giving up on me.”

Agatha’s arms moved to hold her, pulling her closer, and Rio let herself melt into her embrace. “I’m not going anywhere,” Agatha murmured softly. “We’re not giving up on us.”

And for the first time in what felt like forever, Rio allowed herself to believe that—really believe it.

Rio’s heart was racing, her thoughts a whirlwind. The closeness between her and Agatha was everything she wanted, but it was also the thing that scared her most now. There were still so many things left unsaid, and the weight of them felt too heavy to ignore any longer. They couldn’t keep going like this, not when there was so much between them, unresolved.

She took a deep breath, pulling back slightly to look Agatha in the eye. The vulnerability was thick in the air, but there was something else, too—determination. If they were going to move forward, they needed to talk, really talk. They had to lay everything out on the table. It was the only way.

“Agatha,” Rio started softly, but her voice was steady. “I need to know everything. About Jordan’s threat. All of it.”

Agatha froze, her body tensing slightly, like she was about to pull away. Rio could see the flicker of hesitation in her eyes, and for a moment, it felt like all the air was sucked out of the room. But she kept her gaze on Agatha, waiting, giving her the space to speak, knowing this wasn’t going to be easy.

“I should’ve told you sooner,” Agatha said quietly, her voice filled with regret. “I thought… I thought I could handle it myself, and I didn’t want you to worry, especially after everything else we’ve been through. But that was wrong.”

Rio reached out, her fingers brushing over Agatha’s hand. She wasn’t angry. She understood the impulse to protect, but they were in this together now. That was the point. They couldn’t build anything if they didn’t have complete honesty.

“I can handle it,” Rio replied, her voice firm, though it softened at the end. “But I can’t handle not knowing. If we’re going to fight for this, for us, then I need to know. Everything, Agatha. I don’t care how ugly it is.”

Agatha sighed, looking away for a moment before finally meeting Rio’s gaze again. There was a heaviness in her eyes, and Rio’s chest tightened in response. She could see the weight Agatha had been carrying, the burden of this secret. But it wasn’t just her burden anymore.

“Okay,” Agatha said, taking a breath. “Okay, here’s the truth. Jordan… he’s been blackmailing me. He found out about us. He threatened to report me to Lilia, saying he had proof of our relationship, and he demanded my mentorship and access to the OR, or he’d go to Lilia immediately. He has screenshots of our texts, pictures, everything. He’s been following us.”

Rio’s breath hitched as the realization hit her. Jordan had been stalking Agatha. Watching them. Taking pictures.

“He… he had pictures of us? He showed them to you? Like, you actually saw them?” Rio asked, her mind spinning. She could feel the anger rising, the sickening weight of what had been done to them, to Agatha. Her heart squeezed for Agatha—how she must have felt, how alone she must have been trying to deal with this by herself.

“Yeah,” Agatha admitted, her voice barely audible. “He’s been watching. I’m so sorry, Rio. I should’ve told you. I was just trying to keep you safe from all of this.”

Rio squeezed her eyes shut for a moment, trying to take it all in. She wanted to rage, to lash out at Jordan, but it wasn’t going to help anyone. She had to stay grounded, stay calm—for Agatha, and for them.

“I’m so sorry you’ve had to deal with this alone,” Rio said quietly, her voice cracking as the words left her mouth. “But we’re in this together now, okay? We’re going to fix this.”

Agatha nodded, the relief in her eyes so clear it almost broke Rio’s heart. It was like Agatha had been holding her breath, waiting for Rio to understand.

“Thank you,” Agatha whispered, her voice soft. “I don’t know what I’d do without you.”

Rio leaned in again, pressing her forehead to Agatha’s. “You’re not going to have to find out,” she said with certainty. “We’re going to handle this. Together.”

The weight of the moment settled between them, the air thick with everything they had just laid bare. But Rio felt something shift inside her—something solid, something unshakable. They weren’t hiding anymore. No more secrets. No more fear.

They were going to fight for this. For their love. For their future.

And no one—especially not Jordan—was going to take that from them.

Agatha took a deep breath, clearly struggling with the weight of what she was about to share, but Rio’s unwavering gaze gave her the strength to keep going.

“There’s something else,” Agatha said quietly, her eyes dropping to their joined hands. “Something that really rattled me. This weekend… Jordan was outside my house. I saw him. Sitting in his car.”

Rio felt a shiver run down her spine at the thought. “What?” she asked, her voice barely above a whisper. “He was… just sitting there?”

Agatha nodded, her jaw tightening. “Yeah. He wasn’t doing anything but watching my house. I was so scared. I had to act, so I took pictures. I hid behind the curtain, tried to stay out of sight. I wanted to show the police, to have evidence in case I needed it. But the whole thing was just… terrifying.”

Rio felt her stomach churn, the image of Jordan lurking outside Agatha’s house, stalking her, sending a wave of protectiveness over her. “You were alone,” she murmured, her heart aching for Agatha. “You didn’t tell me.”

Agatha met her eyes, a vulnerability she rarely showed surfacing in her expression. “I couldn’t. You were already dealing with so much. You asked for space. I couldn’t just throw this at you. And when you showed up in my office yesterday… I’d just spoken to the lawyer about everything. I was still trying to figure out what the next step was, and then… you were there, and I just wanted to focus on you.”

Rio took a moment to process this. Agatha had been dealing with so much—Jordan’s threats, the pressure of legal action, and then Rio had just shown up, demanding to know everything. She should’ve been more patient, more understanding.

“But you shouldn’t have been alone with all of this,” Rio said softly, squeezing Agatha’s hand. “I should’ve been there. I should’ve known.”

Agatha smiled faintly, her fingers brushing over Rio’s. “I didn’t want to drag you into it. I thought I could handle it on my own. But I know now that I don’t have to. You’re here.”

Rio looked down for a moment, letting the weight of what Agatha had gone through settle in. The image of Jordan sitting outside Agatha’s house, the threat hanging over her head, was enough to make her blood boil. He had been trying to control her, intimidate her. And yet, here was Agatha, still standing strong, fighting back.

“You did the right thing,” Rio said, her voice firm. “Going to the lawyer, filing the report. We’re gonna handle this together, Agatha. No more secrets, no more pretending everything’s fine. We’re in this together. All of it.”

Agatha’s gaze softened, a flicker of something deep and unspoken passing between them. She nodded, her voice low. “I’m glad you’re with me, Rio. I really am.”

Rio squeezed her hand, her heart swelling with affection and determination. “Always.”

~*~

Rio couldn’t help herself. As she watched Agatha move around the kitchen, flipping pancakes with such effortless grace, an overwhelming sense of affection surged through her. Without thinking, she stepped forward and wrapped her arms around Agatha’s waist from behind, pulling her close. Agatha tensed at first, clearly startled, but she quickly relaxed into Rio’s embrace.

Rio rested her cheek against the back of Agatha’s shoulder, her voice barely above a whisper. “I love you so much,” she murmured, feeling the weight of those words settle in her chest. She closed her eyes, trying to focus on the moment, on the warmth of Agatha’s body against hers. “Please, let’s not fight ever again.”

Agatha stilled for a heartbeat, and Rio could feel the way her breath caught. When Agatha turned in her arms, their eyes met, and Rio felt the pull of her gaze deep in her chest. She had never been so vulnerable, and yet, in this moment, she felt an undeniable closeness that made everything else seem distant.

Agatha’s hands gently cupped her face, and Rio’s heart skipped a beat as she saw the hesitation in her eyes. Then Agatha pulled her in, their lips meeting in a soft, almost tentative kiss. Rio melted into it, feeling the weight of all the tension, the uncertainty, the fear, and the love that had been building between them. This kiss was everything. It was an apology, an understanding, a promise.

When they finally broke apart, Rio rested her forehead against Agatha’s, her heart still racing. Agatha’s voice was gentle as she spoke, and Rio could hear the sincerity in every word. “I’m sorry. I— I never wanted to hurt you. You’re everything to me.”

Rio tightened her grip around Agatha, the words sinking deep into her. She closed her eyes for a moment, feeling the emotional rawness of it all. She didn’t want to dwell on what happened, not now. She just wanted to hold on to this moment, to the connection they shared.

“I know you didn’t mean to,” Rio whispered, her voice thick with emotion. She pulled Agatha in for another kiss, this one slower, deeper, like she was trying to tell Agatha everything she couldn’t put into words. “But I’m glad we’re here, now. I don’t want to go through anything like that again either.”

For a long moment, the world outside disappeared. It was just the two of them, their hearts beating in sync. All the misunderstandings and hurt seemed to melt away, and in that quiet, peaceful space, they both found comfort in each other’s arms.

The pancakes could wait.

 

~*~

Rio reluctantly pulled herself away from Agatha’s embrace, the warmth of their closeness still lingering. As much as she wanted to stay in her arms, to show Agatha how much she loved her, to lose themselves in each other’s touch and forget the world outside, there was still reality waiting for her. Her heart sank just a little at the thought of leaving Agatha’s side, but she knew she couldn’t put off what she had to do.

She gently cupped Agatha’s face, leaning in for a soft kiss before pulling back. “I need to get to class,” Rio said, her voice quieter than usual, a mixture of regret and necessity. “And I want to check in on Alice, see how she’s doing. I can’t keep avoiding that.”

Agatha nodded, her hand lingering on the small of Rio’s back as she met her gaze. “I understand,” she replied, her voice soft but steady. “I have a consult with a patient later today, but I’ll check in with the lawyer again about Jordan. I’ll keep you posted on what the next steps are.”

Rio gave a slight nod, appreciating Agatha’s dedication to everything that was happening. “I’ll be waiting for your updates,” she said, her eyes lingering on Agatha, reluctant to leave her presence.

Agatha smiled, a slight sadness in her expression. “I’ll keep you in the loop,” she promised. “And hey—” She paused, her eyes softening as she looked at Rio. “Let me know if you need anything. Okay?”

Rio smiled, her heart lightening a little. “I will. And, uh…” she hesitated, but the words came naturally after a second. “You can wear some of my clothes if you want. I know you didn’t bring anything extra.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow playfully. “Are you sure?”

Rio laughed softly, brushing a hand through her hair. “Yeah, I’m sure. I’d rather you be comfortable. And look better on you, anyway.”

Agatha chuckled, shaking her head. “You’re something else,” she said fondly. She leaned in for one last kiss, her lips brushing lightly against Rio’s before she pulled back. “Alright, I’ll take you up on that offer. Thanks.”

Rio watched as Agatha headed to the bathroom, a feeling of tenderness spreading through her chest. Even with everything going on, this felt right. They would handle everything—together.

Rio watched Agatha move to the bathroom, but before she could fully step through the door, Rio called out softly, “Hey, you can take a shower if you want. Towels are in the cabinet, and you can help yourself to anything in my closet.”

Agatha turned back to her with a soft smile. “Thanks,” she said, her voice warm. “I’ll be quick.”

But Rio wasn’t ready to let her go just yet. There was still a bit of uncertainty in the air, but beneath it, Rio felt the pull between them, that undeniable connection. Agatha was already under so much pressure, dealing with the aftermath of Jordan’s actions, and Rio couldn’t help but feel like they needed this—something just for them, to reaffirm that, despite everything, they were still together. Not just physically, but emotionally. They had been through so much already, and Rio needed to prove to herself that nothing had changed between them.

She stood up from the bed, slipping over to the bathroom door. For a moment, she hesitated, but then, gathering her courage, she pushed it open, stepping inside just as Agatha was adjusting the water temperature in the shower.

Agatha blinked in surprise but didn’t pull away. “Rio?” she said, her voice a little uncertain.

“I… I just want to be with you,” Rio said, her voice low and earnest. “It’s not about… anything else. I just need to feel close to you. We’ve been through so much, and I don’t want any of this to get in the way of what we have. We’re still us, right?”

Agatha’s expression softened, the vulnerability in Rio’s eyes catching her off guard. She let out a breath, a soft smile tugging at her lips. “Of course we are. We’re still us. And I need that too.”

Rio stepped closer, and this time, Agatha didn’t pull away. They stood there for a moment, just looking at each other, each one searching the other’s eyes for reassurance, for the same unspoken truth—that despite the chaos, despite the fear and the uncertainty, they were still here. Together.

Without a word, Rio gently placed her hand on Agatha’s shoulder, her thumb grazing the soft fabric of her shirt before it trailed up to her neck. Agatha closed her eyes briefly, and Rio’s heart swelled at the quiet moment of trust.

Agatha stepped closer, her hand gently resting on Rio’s hip, pulling her just a little nearer. Their faces were only inches apart, and Rio could feel the warmth of Agatha’s breath on her lips.

“I love you,” Rio whispered, her voice steady but filled with longing. “I just… need you to know that. I don’t want anything to come between us.”

Agatha’s lips curved into a small, reassuring smile. She leaned in, brushing a soft kiss across Rio’s forehead before pulling her into an embrace. “I love you too,” she murmured, her voice full of tenderness. “And nothing is going to change that.”

Rio closed her eyes, allowing herself to lean into Agatha’s embrace, savoring the quiet intimacy between them. No words were necessary; the connection between them spoke louder than anything else ever could.

~*~

Rio stood in the parking garage, the cool concrete beneath her feet matching the weight in her chest. She watched Agatha as she approached her car, both of them knowing that saying goodbye was inevitable, but neither of them wanting to let go. The last few days had been nothing short of a whirlwind, and even now, standing here, Rio still felt like she was trying to make sense of everything that had happened.

“We should probably avoid riding together for a bit,” Rio said, her voice thick with everything left unsaid between them. She didn’t want to be here in the parking garage, didn’t want to be apart, but they both knew it was for the best.

Agatha nodded, her eyes full of understanding. “Yeah. It’s safer this way.”

Rio hated the distance between them, the cold separation that had become necessary for their own protection. But there was nothing else to be done.

As Agatha started to open her car door, Rio reached out, touching her arm gently. She could feel the tension between them, the reluctance to part. Her voice came out softer than she intended. “I don’t want to do this. I don’t want to be apart.”

Agatha paused, turning to look at her with a quiet intensity. “I know. I don’t either.” She moved closer, her fingers brushing Rio’s cheek in a way that made Rio’s heart beat faster. “But we’ll make it through this, okay?”

Rio nodded, her throat tight. She wanted to tell Agatha so many things — how much she loved her, how much she hated the thought of being apart, how she feared what might happen if they couldn’t find a way to make this work. But all that came out was a soft, almost desperate whisper. “Just… stay safe.”

Agatha stepped closer, her hand finding Rio’s and holding it like she might never let go. “I will. You too.”

Rio leaned in, her lips finding Agatha’s in a kiss that was tender, almost hesitant. It wasn’t a kiss of urgency or passion. It was the kind of kiss that told them both they weren’t ready to say goodbye, not yet. It lingered, slow and soft, as if time had stopped for a moment, just for them.

When they finally pulled away, their foreheads touched, both of them breathing a little heavier, eyes closed for just a moment. Rio didn’t want to open her eyes, didn’t want to step away. But they had to.

“Call me,” Rio said, her voice still thick with emotion.

“I will. I promise.”

With one last look, Rio turned toward the elevator, her heart aching with every step away from Agatha. But she knew this wasn’t the end. It couldn’t be. They were in this together. They just needed time. And for the first time in a while, Rio felt like maybe that was enough.

~*~

As Rio entered the classroom, the tension in the air was immediate. She felt the weight of Jordan’s gaze before she even saw him. It was like a physical pressure, his eyes boring into her as she walked down the aisle between the rows of desks. Her heart pounded, anger coiling in her chest, but she kept her head high, not letting him see how much he rattled her.

She wanted to scream at him, to call him out right there in front of everyone. To ask him what the hell his problem was, why he thought he could threaten her and her life with impunity. Her fingers itched to grab him by the collar and shake him, to demand answers. But she wouldn’t give him the satisfaction. She wouldn’t let him see how deeply he had gotten under her skin.

Instead, Rio held her composure, walking straight to her seat as if nothing were wrong, as if the knot in her stomach wasn’t threatening to undo her. She could feel his eyes following her, like a shadow, even as she sat down. He was watching her, trying to make her uncomfortable, trying to push her buttons.

She clenched her jaw, doing everything she could to focus on the lecture as the professor began speaking. But she couldn’t shake the feeling of Jordan’s presence lingering behind her. He was like a dark cloud in her peripheral vision, and she had no idea how much longer she could stand it.

It wasn’t just the threat to Agatha, the looming danger hanging over them both. It was the sheer audacity of Jordan. The smug satisfaction he seemed to take in making her feel small, in trying to control her. He was trying to intimidate her, to make her doubt herself, and she refused to let him win. Not today.

But as she sat there, trying to breathe and focus on the lecture, the anger still simmered beneath her skin. One thing was for sure: she wasn’t going to let him get away with this. She wouldn’t let him tear her and Agatha apart. Not if she could help it. And maybe, just maybe, she was going to make sure he regretted ever trying to play this game with her.

~*~

Rio’s phone buzzed in her pocket, snapping her out of her angry haze as she tried to focus on the lecture. She glanced down at the screen, her heart skipping a beat when she saw Jen’s name. The text was simple: Alice is awake and alert.

A rush of relief flooded through her, so overwhelming that she nearly collapsed in her seat. She quickly shoved her phone back in her pocket, trying not to let her emotions spill over, but she felt lighter, as if the weight that had been crushing her chest had finally eased.

The rest of the class passed in a blur. She barely heard what the professor was saying, her mind only focused on getting to the hospital, on seeing Alice alive and awake. When the professor finally dismissed the class, Rio was already halfway out the door before anyone could stop her.

She didn’t even care about getting there just in time for visiting hours—she had to see Alice now . The drive to the hospital felt like an eternity, and when she finally arrived, she rushed through the corridors, barely pausing to acknowledge the nurses at the front desk.

Rio’s hand shook as she pushed the door to Alice’s hospital room open, the weight of the moment almost too much to bear. She had been running on adrenaline all day, but now that she was finally here, with Alice awake and alive, it was hard to stop the tears from welling up.

When Alice’s eyes met hers, Rio’s breath caught in her throat. The woman in front of her was battered and bruised, but she was alive. That was all that mattered.

“ Alice ,” Rio whispered, her voice thick with emotion. She could hardly bring herself to speak, afraid if she did, the floodgates would open. “Oh my god, Alice.”

Alice blinked a few times, as if trying to process what was happening. Her lips curled into a small, tired smile, but her eyes were soft, a little confused but mostly reassuring. “Hey, girl,” she rasped, her voice hoarse. “You okay?”

That was when it hit Rio, like a freight train, the real emotion of it all. She had almost lost Alice. She had been this close to having her best friend slip away, and the weight of that nearly crushed her. She felt tears sting her eyes, but she didn’t fight them, didn’t try to hold them back.

Without thinking, she moved closer to Alice’s bed, sinking down into the chair beside her. She just needed to be near her. Needed to touch her.

“Don’t scare me like that ever again, do you hear me?” Rio finally managed, her voice breaking. She gripped Alice’s hand tightly, as if she could anchor herself in this moment and make sure nothing would change. “I thought I lost you. I—I had to perform CPR on you, Alice. You stopped breathing, and I…”

Her words trailed off, choked by the rush of emotions that threatened to overwhelm her. She didn’t know how to explain it, how to put into words how terrifying it had been to work on her best friend, to feel that weight in her chest as she desperately tried to bring her back.

Alice’s hand squeezed hers back, the only real sign that she was truly there. “I’m sorry,” Alice whispered, her voice shaky now, more from the strain of her own emotions than anything physical. “I didn’t mean to worry you.”

Rio shook her head, more tears slipping down her face. “You didn’t mean to, but you did,” she said, her voice barely above a whisper. “I—I don’t even know how I kept it together. I just… I couldn’t think, Alice. I was so scared. But you’re here. You’re here.”

Alice’s face softened, her exhaustion finally taking over as she closed her eyes for a moment. “I’m here,” she confirmed, her voice quieter now. “I’m sorry for putting you through that.”

Rio leaned forward, resting her forehead against Alice’s hand, feeling the cool touch of her skin, grounding herself. “I’m just glad you’re okay. I don’t know what I would’ve done without you.” She paused, realizing how close she was to breaking down again. “I couldn’t have lost you. Not like that. Not on my watch.”

Alice opened her eyes again, her expression full of affection and understanding. “You wouldn’t have,” she promised softly. “Hey, I’m tougher than I look.”

Rio let out a shaky laugh, but it didn’t last long. She wiped her eyes quickly, trying to regain some composure. “I’ll be right here. I’m not going anywhere.”

Alice’s smile was faint, but it was there. “You’ve got your own stuff going on, Rio. You don’t need to sit here with me all day.”

Rio shook her head vehemently. “Oh yeah? Watch me, I’m staying with you whether you like it or not. At least for a little while.”

And so, they sat there for a while, the silence between them comfortable in its own way, both of them processing what had just happened. Rio needed to stay in the moment, needed to hold onto the fact that Alice was breathing, that she was alive.

As she left Alice’s room, a sudden burst of relief came over her, and it wasn’t just for Alice—it was for herself, for her own heart that had been holding its breath all weekend. She texted Agatha, her fingers a little unsteady, and then hurried to her car.

Rio

Alice is awake. She’s gonna be okay. I need to see you.

Her phone buzzed almost immediately. 

Agatha

I’m so relieved to hear that. Want to come by for a late lunch? Swing by my practice? 

Rio didn’t even have to think about it. She was already on her way to Agatha. She texted back that she would love to, a genuine smile starting to tug at the corners of her lips for the first time in what felt like days.

Finally, things were starting to feel like they might be okay again.

~*~

Rio’s hands gripped the steering wheel as she navigated the streets toward Agatha’s private practice. The text from Agatha was still fresh in her phone, the address clearly laid out, but Rio couldn’t quite focus on the directions. Her mind felt like a whirlwind, a storm of tangled thoughts and emotions she couldn’t quite untangle.

Alice.

The relief she felt when she saw her friend awake, alive, was still making her heart beat a little faster. She had almost lost her, and the terror of that moment still clung to her. But Alice was going to be okay. It had to be enough.

Then there was Agatha.

As much as Rio tried to keep things clear in her head, it was hard to ignore how she felt about Agatha. After everything that had happened between them—the kiss, the tension, the misunderstandings, and the emotional baggage they both carried—it all felt like it had been leading to this moment. Being with Agatha again, holding her, talking to her, even just sitting together and letting the silence do the work—it felt right. But still, there was so much to navigate. Rio knew that, deep down. They were starting from a place of raw honesty, but there was a lot left unsaid.

And then there was Jordan.

The looming threat that made Rio feel uneasy every time her mind wandered to him. She hated that someone like him could manipulate, control, and intimidate Agatha like that. She hated that he was still in their lives, that his dark shadow lingered over everything they tried to build. But Agatha was strong, and Rio knew that. They would deal with him. Together.

But as she turned onto the street where Agatha’s practice was, Rio’s chest tightened again, and it wasn’t from any of the threats, or fears, or doubts—it was the way her love for Agatha had intensified since they’d gotten back together. It was like a dam had broken, flooding her chest with a love so fierce, so strong, she didn’t even know how to keep up with it.

The last few days, when Agatha wasn’t around, had been unbearable. She hadn’t realized just how much she needed her. But now that they were back in each other’s lives, it felt like everything was falling into place—like everything they had been through only made this moment, right here, more precious.

Agatha was no longer just a teacher, no longer a mentor. She was someone Rio couldn’t imagine her life without. And that realization, powerful and overwhelming, left Rio breathless every time she thought about it.

She parked in front of the building, her heart racing with anticipation. She needed to see Agatha again, needed to feel that warmth, that grounding presence. She needed to feel like things were real, like this—them—was real.

She texted Agatha that she’d arrived and then took a deep breath, bracing herself for whatever came next. There were so many things she wanted to say to her, but she didn’t know where to start. There was still so much to figure out. Yet, somehow, just knowing that Agatha was here, that they were both willing to try again, felt like the most important thing in the world.

Stepping out of the car, she straightened her shoulders, pushing aside the confusion and the weight of all that had happened. She had her love for Agatha. And that was enough for now.

As Rio walked into the building, the sleek, modern decor made her feel like she was stepping into another world. It was a sharp contrast to the cozy, intimate spaces they’d shared in her apartment, but it was still Agatha’s—professional, polished, yet undeniably hers.

When she stepped up to the front desk, she was greeted by an older woman with kind eyes and a professional demeanor. “Hello, you must be Rio,” the woman said with a smile, her tone warm but efficient. “I’m Sharon Davis. Dr. Harkness is expecting you, dear. You can go right in.”

Rio offered a quick, appreciative smile, still feeling a little out of place in the pristine office. She thanked Sharon before heading down the corridor to Agatha’s door. When she reached it, her pulse quickened. She could feel the weight of the day lifting as she was finally, finally about to be with Agatha again.

She knocked softly before opening the door, her heart already racing in anticipation. The moment it clicked shut behind her, she didn’t think—she just moved. Her feet carried her across the room, and before Agatha could even react, Rio was on her, cupping her face and pulling her into a kiss so deep, so fierce, that it felt like a floodgate had opened inside her chest.

The kiss was unrestrained, raw with all the emotion that had built up in the hours and days they’d been apart. Rio needed Agatha, needed to feel her close, to pour every ounce of love, longing, and frustration she’d been holding back into this one moment. The world outside, the worries, the tension—it all faded as she lost herself in Agatha’s embrace.

Agatha responded with equal intensity, her hands finding Rio’s waist, pulling her even closer. Rio could feel her breath coming in sharp bursts as they kissed, a mixture of urgency and tenderness.

When they finally pulled away, Rio rested her forehead against Agatha’s, her fingers still tracing the curve of her jaw. Her voice was shaky, almost hoarse, as she spoke. “I love you so much, Agatha. I couldn’t stand being apart from you anymore. It’s like—it’s like everything inside me’s been waiting for this moment.”

Agatha’s eyes softened, her hand lifting to gently touch Rio’s cheek. “I feel the same way,” she murmured, her voice laced with emotion. “I’ve been… so afraid, but this—us—this is what matters.” She took a deep breath, her thumb brushing across Rio’s skin, her gaze steady and warm. “I’ll never let you go again. I promise.”

Rio smiled, her heart swelling with emotion. The weight of everything that had been left unsaid seemed to melt away in that moment. No more doubts, no more hesitation. They were here, together, and that was enough.

Agatha leaned in and kissed her again, slower this time, more deliberate, as if to savor the moment. Rio melted into the kiss, letting the love and relief wash over her.

As they finally pulled away from the kiss, Agatha nodded toward the containers of Thai food neatly set out on the table. “I figured you’d like a warm meal,” she said softly, her voice a comforting mix of practicality and tenderness. 

Rio couldn’t help but smile, her heart swelling with affection. Agatha had thought of everything—just like she always did. She reached up and kissed Agatha’s cheek in gratitude. “Thank you,” she murmured, before walking over to the plush, modern couch across from a massive floor-to-ceiling window.

The view from the 30th floor was nothing short of breathtaking. Rio paused for a moment to take it all in, her breath catching slightly as she gazed out at the shimmering expanse of the lake, stretching out in the distance. The buildings around her were a mix of modern steel and glass, their sharp angles and intricate lines reflecting the sky. It was beautiful, but there was something about the view that felt almost surreal—a reminder of how far they had come and how much more was still ahead.

Agatha joined her shortly, taking a seat beside her on the couch, still wearing the remnants of her professional demeanor, but Rio could see the softness in her eyes. There was comfort here. A sense of home.

As they unwrapped the containers, Rio couldn’t help but smile at the spread—sushi, pad Thai, a selection of spring rolls—and the thoughtfulness behind it all. She took a bite, savoring the familiar flavors as Agatha did the same, but her eyes kept flicking back to Agatha, that steady pulse of affection rising in her chest once more.

After a quiet moment, Agatha’s voice broke the comfortable silence. “You’re really okay, aren’t you?” She asked it so gently, as if the question had been lingering on her mind for a while. “After everything that’s happened with Alice, and… with Jordan.”

Rio glanced out the window again, trying to gather her thoughts. Her life had felt like it was spinning out of control for so long—between Alice’s accident, the threat from Jordan, and everything in between. But sitting here with Agatha, in this moment of peace, she felt a sense of clarity she hadn’t known in days.

“I am,” Rio said softly, her voice full of quiet resolve. “It’s been a lot to process, but… I’m okay. And I’m grateful that you’re here. That we’re here.”

Agatha nodded, her hand resting gently on Rio’s. “I’m here,” she echoed, squeezing her hand reassuringly. “For as long as you’ll have me.”

Agatha took a deep breath, her fingers wrapping around her cup of tea before she began speaking again. “So, I talked to the lawyer yesterday,” she said, her voice calm but serious. “She recommended that we file for a restraining order against Jordan. With the way he’s been behaving, and the fact that he was sitting outside my house and threatening me, it’s the safest thing to do. He also advised that we go ahead and officially disclose our relationship to Lilia and the university. It’s the only way to get ahead of this.”

Rio’s brow furrowed, processing what Agatha was saying. “What do you mean, disclose it to the university? Like, make it official?”

Agatha nodded, her gaze steady on Rio. “Yes, exactly. It means going to Lilia together and officially telling her about us. I know it’s a big step, and I know it’s not something we planned for, but if we do this now, if we tell the university officially, then if and when Jordan files a complaint, it’ll be dismissed because they’re already aware of our relationship.”

Rio felt her chest tighten at the idea. The prospect of making their relationship public like this felt like a leap she wasn’t sure she was ready to take. “And what if Lilia doesn’t approve? What if she—” Rio stopped herself, uncertain how to voice the concern, her mind racing with worst-case scenarios.

Agatha interrupted gently, her voice warm but firm. “Lilia already knows. She’s been more than aware of us for a while. This is just the formal step to make it official, so it’s on record. It’s about protecting us both and making sure there’s no ambiguity if Jordan tries to use this against me.”

Rio let out a slow exhale, still digesting everything. The idea of putting themselves on the university’s radar like that was intimidating, but Agatha was right. If they didn’t act now, the situation could only get worse. “So, we do this together. Tell Lilia, get the restraining order, and deal with whatever happens next.”

Agatha gave a small nod, her eyes softening as she gazed at Rio. “Yes. It’s the only way to stay ahead of him.”

Rio met Agatha’s gaze, her heart steadying at the strength and certainty she saw in her eyes. “Okay. Let’s do it. We’ll face this together, no matter what.”

 

Twenty-four

Chapter Notes

Hope you enjoy this one!

Agatha watched as Rio sat beside her, her face tense with focus as they went through the online forms for the restraining order. Agatha took the lead, carefully filling in every detail about Jordan’s threats, the blackmail, and how he had been stalking her outside her home. She uploaded the photos she had taken from her window, her fingers tightening on the mouse as the memory of that night crept back in.

Rio remained silent but seething. Agatha felt it in the way her jaw tensed, the way her knee bounced slightly against the leg of Agatha’s desk. When they finally submitted the request, a heavy silence settled between them.

“It’s done,” Agatha murmured, leaning back in her chair. She let out a slow breath, but the tension in her shoulders didn’t ease.

Rio exhaled sharply through her nose, then ran a hand over her face. “Now we wait?”

Agatha nodded. “Yes. If the judge grants the emergency hearing, we’ll have something in place soon. If not…” she trailed off, not wanting to voice the alternative just yet.

Rio clenched her jaw. “Then we fight for a regular hearing as soon as possible.”

Agatha reached out, her fingers finding Rio’s. She squeezed gently. “Yeah.”

For a moment, they just sat there, holding onto each other. Then, Agatha glanced at the time. “We should head to Northwestern. We still need to talk to Lilia.”

Rio let out a deep breath, nodding. “Yeah. Let’s get this over with.”

They gathered their things and left Agatha’s practice, both knowing that the next few hours could change everything.

~*~

 

Agatha pulled into the faculty parking lot at Northwestern, her fingers tight around the steering wheel. The drive from her private practice had been mostly quiet, both of them lost in thought. Filing for the restraining order had been one thing—an official step forward, a tangible action. But now came the next hurdle: disclosing their relationship to the university before Jordan could weaponize it against them.

She glanced over at Rio as she shut off the car. She looked exhausted, tension still pulling at the corners of her mouth, but she was here. She was standing beside Agatha, ready to face this.

They made their way through the halls, heading toward Lilia’s office. It wasn’t their first time here, but today felt different. The weight of what they were about to do hung between them like a storm cloud.

The wait outside Lilia’s office stretched on, the weight of what they were about to do settling heavily in Agatha’s chest. She could feel Rio’s tension beside her—the way her knee bounced restlessly, the way she kept exhaling sharply, like she was trying to release some of the nerves coiling inside her.

Agatha understood. This wasn’t just about them anymore. It was about safeguarding their careers, about controlling the narrative before someone else twisted it. About making sure that, whatever happened next, they stood on solid ground.

Miriam, Lilia’s assistant, barely spared them a glance as she typed away at her computer. “She’s finishing up a meeting. Shouldn’t be long.”

Agatha nodded and sat down. Rio followed, shifting in her seat, fingers tapping an absent rhythm against the fabric of her jeans.

Then a familiar chime broke the silence.

Agatha pulled out her phone, expecting something mundane—an update from Wanda, maybe, or a message from Nicky’s school. But when she glanced at her screen, her breath caught.

1 New Email – Subject: Neuro OR Selections – Finalized

It was from Dr. Patel, the only one of her colleagues who hadn’t yet sent in his final picks. She hadn’t expected his selections so soon—he’d said he would take his time deciding—but now, here it was.

A small coil of anticipation formed in her stomach as she opened the email. Her eyes scanned the message, heart hammering against her ribs.

Selected Students for the OR Observation based on presentation delivered on December 18th and student history:

  • Rio Vidal
  • Daniel Cho

For a split second, she couldn’t breathe.

Then relief hit her like a wave.

She turned to Rio, unable to keep the small smile off her lips. “You got it.”

Rio blinked. “What?”

“The OR spot for the surgery.” Agatha tilted her phone toward her. “You got it.”

Rio’s breath stilled. She stared at the screen as if the words weren’t quite registering. Then she exhaled, shaky and disbelieving.

“ Holy shit .”

Agatha’s smile softened. “Congratulations.”

Rio let out a half-laugh, half-sigh, running a hand through her hair. “I—I can’t believe it.”

Agatha’s chest tightened in the best way. She had seen firsthand how much Rio had wanted this, how hard she had worked. This moment—seeing the stunned joy on her face—made everything worth it.

Before she could say anything else, Miriam’s voice cut through the moment.

“Dr. Harkness, Lilia will see you now.”

Agatha felt Rio’s hand brush against hers as they stood. It was subtle, almost instinctive, like she had reached for her before remembering where they were.

Agatha didn’t take her hand, but as they walked into Lilia’s office, she wished she could.

~*~

Lilia leaned back in her chair after Agatha and Rio finished explaining, her fingers steepled together as she let out a sharp breath.

“This is absolutely unacceptable,” she said, her voice clipped. “Thomas Jordan is a menace, and if he wasn’t already skating on thin ice with his performance in the program, I’d—” She cut herself off, shaking her head. “But we have to be careful about how we handle this. You’re right to want to get ahead of him.”

Agatha shifted in her chair, already tense. “We need to disclose our relationship officially.”

Lilia nodded. “Yes, that’s the cleanest way forward. And that means changes.” She turned to Rio. “You’ll need to switch mentors.”

Rio had braced herself for this, but the words still landed like a punch to the gut. “I—” She exhaled slowly. “Right. That makes sense.”

Agatha sat straighter. “Lilia—”

“No, Agatha,” Lilia interrupted, firm but not unkind. “You know this is the best option. If you two are serious about this—and I have no doubt that you are—then we have to eliminate any conflicts of interest. Jordan won’t have a leg to stand on if Rio is no longer your mentee.”

Rio ran a hand down her face, grounding herself. She had worked so damn hard on her research with Agatha. The thought of starting over with someone else made her stomach churn. But this wasn’t just about her project anymore.

“I’ll do it,” she said, voice steadier than she felt. “But I still get to keep my OR spot, right? The list just came out.”

“Absolutely,” Lilia assured her. “Your selection was merit-based and chosen by a committee.. That stands. As for Neuro II, I’ll assign you to another class.” She paused, thoughtful. “Dr. Meyer. She’s excellent, and I know she’ll take you on. The semester is only starting, so it won’t make that big of a difference.”

Rio nodded, jaw tight, but she didn’t protest.

Lilia’s gaze softened slightly. “I know this isn’t ideal, but it protects both of you. The university can’t be blindsided by Jordan filing a complaint. By disclosing first, we take that power away from him.”

Agatha exhaled, tension lining her shoulders. “And what about him? We’ve filed for a restraining order.”

“Let me know as soon as you hear back about the hearing,” Lilia said. “In the meantime, I’ll speak with Dr. Olsen. If Jordan so much as breathes in either of your directions, we’ll be prepared.”

Rio exchanged a glance with Agatha, and despite the ache of giving up their mentorship, she knew this was the right choice.

Agatha reached for her hand under the desk, squeezing lightly. Rio squeezed back.

“I’ll make it clear that this disclosure is coming from you, not from a complaint. That puts us in control of the narrative. And given that Jordan is already trying to blackmail you, we need to eliminate any leverage he thinks he has,” Lilia continued and Agatha nodded, feeling Rio’s thumb gently caressing her hand in an attempt to calm them both down.

“Okay, that sounds good,” Rio said, her voice quiet and resigned.

“It’s the best way to protect both of you. It doesn’t mean you stop working on your project, just that Agatha won’t be your official advisor anymore.”

Agatha glanced at Rio, whose jaw was tight, but she gave a small nod.

Lilia clasped her hands together. “I’ll call Dr. Olsen now. You two sit tight.”

 

~*~

Dr. Olivia Olsen’s office exuded the same composed authority as the woman herself—dark wood, shelves lined with medical journals and framed accolades, and a floor-to-ceiling window that overlooked the city skyline. She sat behind her desk, impeccably dressed in a deep blue blazer, her expression unreadable as she regarded them.

Agatha had met her several times over the years, as she was the Dean of Medicine, but never like this. Never with stakes this high.

Beside Dr. Olsen, Lilia sat with her hands folded neatly in her lap, her usual sharp eyes softened just a fraction. But there was no mistaking the tension in the room.

“So,” Dr. Olsen said, her voice smooth but firm, “you’re both here to formally disclose your relationship.”

Agatha gave a small nod. Rio, sitting stiffly beside her, barely moved.

“I appreciate the honesty,” Dr. Olsen continued. “It makes handling this situation significantly easier.”

Rio exhaled sharply through her nose and muttered, “Easier for who?” 

Dr. Olsen’s dark eyes settled on her, unwavering. “For all of us. The cleanest way forward is for you to be reassigned to a different mentor and a different professor for Neurology II.”

Rio’s jaw tightened. “So I lose everything I’ve worked for.”

Lilia sighed. “No one is taking your research away from you, Rio. We’ll ensure that your new mentor is someone who supports your goals. As for Neuro II, I’ll personally oversee your transition to another professor.”

“That doesn’t change the fact that this isn’t fair,” Rio shot back.

Dr. Olsen sat forward slightly, hands clasped on the desk. “I understand why this feels like a punishment. But let me be clear—this is about protecting you. If we do this now, on our terms, Thomas Jordan has no case against Dr. Harkness or you. We remove his leverage completely.”

Rio’s throat bobbed as she swallowed. “And if I refuse?”

Dr. Olsen didn’t hesitate. “Then if Jordan files a complaint, the university will be forced to investigate, and you both risk far greater consequences. This way, we control the narrative.”

Agatha finally found her voice, quiet but certain. “She’s right.”

Rio turned to her, eyes stormy.

Agatha wished she could tell her otherwise.

Rio stared at Agatha, the betrayal flickering across her face like a slow burn. Agatha felt it in her chest, sharp and deep, but she held her gaze steady. She wasn’t choosing the university over Rio. She was choosing to protect them both.

Dr. Olsen leaned back in her chair, giving them space. “This isn’t easy,” she said, her voice measured. “And I won’t pretend that it is. But Dr. Harkness is right. If you fight this, you’re giving Thomas Jordan exactly what he wants—an opening.”

Rio exhaled harshly, rubbing a hand over her jaw. She looked to Lilia, then back at Dr. Olsen. “Who would my new mentor be?”

Lilia exchanged a glance with the dean before answering. “Dr. Simon Patel. He’s in neuro-oncology, but his background in neurodegenerative diseases makes him a strong fit for your research.”

Rio’s shoulders tensed. Agatha knew why. Patel was a brilliant researcher, but he wasn’t Agatha. He wasn’t the mentor Rio had chosen.

“And Neuro II?” Rio asked, voice tight.

“I’ll assign you to Dr. Lena Meyer,” Lilia said. “She’s tough, but fair. You’ll still be set for your rotations and clinicals as scheduled.”

Rio let out a slow, heavy breath. “And the OR spot?”

Silence stretched between them.

Dr. Olsen’s eyes softened just a fraction. “You were selected by a panel, not just Dr. Harkness. And I hear it was a unanimous choice. So that stands.”

Rio closed her eyes, letting a heavy breath in relief. When she opened them again, she looked at Dr. Olsen. “And if Jordan still reports Agatha after all this?”

“Then he loses all credibility,” the dean said simply. “The university will see it for what it is—retaliation. And he will face the consequences for that.”

Rio didn’t respond right away. She drummed her fingers against her knee, exhaling through her nose before finally nodding. “Fine. Let’s do it.

Agatha felt a pang in her chest at those words, but she swallowed it down. This wasn’t about her.

“Good,” Dr. Olsen said, brisk and efficient now. “Lilia will start the paperwork immediately. Dr. Patel will be notified today. You’ll meet with him soon. And as of next week, you’ll be in Dr. Meyer’s class for Neuro II.”

Rio didn’t move. Didn’t even blink.

“Is there anything else?” Dr. Olsen asked.

Rio shook her head, frustration coming off of her in waves.

Dr. Olsen smiled sympathetically. “We’ll give you two a minute alone.”

Lilia glanced at Dr. Olsen, who gave a curt nod before rising from her chair. “Of course.”

Agatha stood as well, but Rio didn’t move, her fingers laced tightly together in her lap.

“We’ll be right outside,” Lilia said before stepping out with Dr. Olsen, the door clicking shut behind them.

The moment they were alone, Agatha sat back down, her heart heavy. “Rio—”

“Do you know what this feels like?” Rio’s voice was quiet, but there was a sharp edge to it, one that Agatha knew was barely holding back something deeper.

Agatha swallowed. “Tell me.”

Rio let out a humorless breath, shaking her head as she ran a hand over her face. “It feels like I’m losing everything I worked for.” She looked up then, her dark eyes raw with emotion. “I fought so hard for this, Agatha. For you as my mentor. For your guidance. And now I have to give that up because some asshole decided he wanted to ruin us.”

Agatha exhaled, reaching out instinctively, but Rio flinched. Not away from her, but just enough that Agatha froze.

“I know this isn’t fair,” Agatha said, keeping her voice steady. “I know this is cruel. And if I could take this from you, if I could carry the weight of it instead, I would.”

Rio clenched her jaw, looking away.

“But this is the best way to protect us both,” Agatha continued. “To make sure Jordan doesn’t have any leverage over us.”

Rio let out a slow breath. “And if he still comes after you?”

Agatha’s chest ached. “Then the university will handle it.”

Silence stretched between them, heavy and unresolved. Then, finally, Rio’s shoulders slumped.

“Can you just—” Her voice wavered, and she shut her eyes for a second before looking back at Agatha. “Can you just hold me for a second?”

Agatha didn’t hesitate. She moved closer, wrapping her arms around Rio, pulling her in as Rio buried her face against her shoulder.

“I’m so tired,” Rio whispered.

Agatha pressed a kiss to her hair. “I know, baby.”

They stayed like that, wrapped in each other, as the weight of it all settled between them.

They stayed in the embrace for several moments, the quiet of the office wrapping around them like a cocoon. Agatha could feel Rio’s breath slow, the tension in her body softening under the comfort of her touch. Agatha wanted to say more, to make Rio feel better, but words seemed inadequate in the face of all that was unfolding.

Rio pulled back slightly, just enough to look at Agatha, her eyes glistening with unspoken emotions. “I hate that it has to be this way,” she murmured, her voice thick with frustration.

“I hate it too,” Agatha admitted, her heart heavy. “But we’re doing this together. And whatever happens, we’ll face it together, Rio.”

Rio nodded slowly, her fingers finding Agatha’s once more. “I’m just scared. I’m scared of losing you, of losing this… of everything I’ve worked for.” She looked at Agatha with a vulnerability that tugged at her chest. “But I can’t lose you. I won’t.”

Agatha gently cupped Rio’s cheek, her thumb brushing across her skin. “You won’t. I promise you, I’m not going anywhere.”

The door to Lilia’s office creaked open, and they both looked up as Dr. Olsen and Lilia reentered. Dr. Olsen’s expression was unreadable, but Lilia’s gaze softened when she saw them together, her concern palpable.

“I’ll make sure you stay on track,” Dr. Olsen added. “You’re still a top student in our program, Rio. Nothing about your ability or your passion for the work changes or is being questioned here. This… this situation doesn’t define you.”

Rio’s eyes softened, but there was still a flicker of doubt. “I just don’t know if I can keep doing this—pretending like nothing’s wrong. It feels like I’m giving up part of myself.”

Lilia leaned forward, her voice firm but understanding. “I won’t sugarcoat it, Rio. This isn’t easy. But the more proactive you are in handling it, the stronger you’ll be. I’ve seen the way you fight for what you care about. I have no doubt you’ll get through this.” She paused, letting her words sink in. “But if you want to make it out of this with your career intact, you need to be strategic. And that means we need to be honest with the university, right now, before Jordan has a chance to escalate anything.”

Agatha’s stomach churned at the thought, but she nodded. “I agree. We’ll do it together.”

Lilia looked at them both, her expression softening just a bit. “Good. We’ll take it one step at a time.”

Dr. Olsen stepped back, her voice quiet but reassuring. “And we’ll support you every step of the way. We’ll make sure that everything is handled with care and professionalism.”

With that, the conversation shifted into more logistical details, but the weight of their discussion hung in the air. It wasn’t over. It wasn’t going to be easy. But for the first time in a while, Rio felt like maybe—just maybe—there was a way forward. A way to hold on to what mattered.

As the meeting came to a close, Agatha and Rio stood, and Agatha gently touched Rio’s arm. “Let’s go home,” she said quietly.

Rio met her eyes, a small but genuine smile forming. “Yeah. Let’s go home.”

~*~

As Agatha and Rio walked through the door of Agatha’s house, the familiar scent of lavender and clean linen filled the air, but it couldn’t wash away the tension that still lingered. Rio kicked off her shoes and settled on the couch, leaning back with a sigh, her eyes tired but still full of so much emotion—frustration, love, and fear. Agatha stood in the kitchen for a moment, her hands on the counter as she took a deep breath, trying to steady herself.

Then, her phone buzzed on the kitchen counter.

Her stomach dropped when she saw the notification, the text from her lawyer’s office confirming the bad news: “Emergency hearing denied. Formal hearing scheduled for January 25th at 10am.”

She stared at the message for a moment, her chest tightening. Rio had already taken a seat on the couch, but the room felt heavier now, the quiet between them more oppressive. Agatha’s hands trembled as she set the phone down, running her fingers through her hair. The feeling of helplessness gnawed at her. Two weeks. Two weeks. She couldn’t believe it.

Rio must have seen her reaction, because she got up and crossed the room, her eyes searching Agatha’s face. “What’s wrong?” she asked, her voice full of concern.

Agatha didn’t even have to say it. She didn’t need to explain. Rio read her expression, her face falling as she put the pieces together.

“Denied,” Agatha whispered, her voice heavy. “The emergency hearing was denied. We have to wait two weeks for the formal one.”

Rio exhaled, sinking onto the couch, her face darkening with frustration. “That’s bullshit . How can they just… leave you hanging like that? With that asshole out there?”

Agatha shook her head, feeling her own frustration rising. “I don’t know. It’s just the way the system works. And now we have to wait, while he’s out there, doing God knows what.”

Rio reached for her hand, squeezing it tightly. “I’m sorry, Agatha. I know this is tough. But we’ll get through it. We have to.”

Agatha looked down at their joined hands, then back up at Rio’s face. “I want to believe that. I do.” She ran her other hand over her face, wiping away a tear that had silently fallen. She hadn’t even realized it was there. “But waiting… it’s just hard. It’s like everything’s out of my control.”

Rio pulled Agatha close, wrapping her arms around her. “I know. But this? It’s not forever. We’ll make it through these next two weeks, and when that hearing happens, we’ll be ready. I promise you, I’m here for you. All the way.”

Agatha buried her face in Rio’s shoulder, finding comfort in the warmth of her embrace. In this moment, the outside world seemed to fade, and all that mattered was the strength of the woman holding her. The weight of everything they’d been through, of everything that still loomed over them, was still there, but for now, in the quiet of Rio’s arms, Agatha allowed herself to feel a flicker of peace.

“We’ll be okay,” Rio said, almost like a vow.

Agatha nodded, her arms tightening around Rio. “Yeah. We will.”

As they pulled away from the embrace, Rio’s concern didn’t fade. She looked at Agatha, her brow furrowing. “Do you need me to go pick up Nicky fro you? He’s still at Wanda’s, right?”

Agatha paused, taking a deep breath before shaking her head. “Wanda said she can keep him for now, while we figure this out. But I’ll definitely get him tomorrow. He’s probably confused, too, with everything that’s been happening.”

Rio nodded in understanding. She’d seen how much Nicky meant to Agatha—how deeply she loved him. She couldn’t imagine the stress Agatha was feeling, balancing all of this with the worry about her son.

Agatha’s eyes softened as she spoke about Wanda keeping Nicky for dinner, but before she could say anything else, Rio murmured, “Then let me take care of you.”

The words lingered in the air between them, charged with a quiet intensity that made Agatha’s chest tighten. Her gaze met Rio’s, a mix of gratitude and longing flickering across her face. She hadn’t realized how much she needed this—this simple gesture, this reminder that despite everything, they were still each other’s anchor.

Rio stepped a little closer, brushing her thumb gently over Agatha’s knuckles. “Let me take care of everything tonight,” Rio said softly, her voice a quiet promise. “You’ve been carrying so much, love. Let me help.”

Agatha’s heart ached with the weight of the day’s events, but the tenderness in Rio’s voice was enough to ease some of the tension. She nodded, her breath shaky, and for the first time in what felt like forever, she let herself lean into the warmth of Rio’s presence, trusting her to guide them through this difficult moment.

“Okay,” Agatha whispered. “Just… be here with me.”

Rio’s answer was a simple kiss, a slow, comforting press of lips against Agatha’s, as if to say that they were in this together. When they pulled apart, Agatha’s eyes searched Rio’s, seeing both strength and vulnerability in her gaze.

“I’m here,” Rio whispered. “Always.”
