Rio barely had time to set her fork down before she heard the quick shuffle of little feet on the tile.

“Rio!”

Nicky’s voice was high with excitement as he ran straight into her side, throwing his arms around her waist. She barely managed to catch the glass Wanda had been handing her before she spilled it.

“Whoa, bud!” Rio laughed, quickly setting the wine down so she could hug him properly. “Didn’t see you there.”

“I missed you so much!” Nicky mumbled into her sweater, clinging tightly.

Rio’s chest ached at the sheer sincerity in his voice. She ran a hand through his curls, squeezing him close. “Missed you too, kid. What’s been going on? You holding down the fort for me?”

Nicky nodded against her. “Yeah, but it’s been boring.” He tilted his head up to look at her. “You weren’t here.”

Agatha let out a quiet sigh, but Rio didn’t look away from Nicky’s expectant face. She cupped his cheek lightly. “Well, I’m here now. And I wanna hear all about what you’ve been up to.”

Nicky’s face brightened instantly. “I got a new book at the library! It’s about space.”

“Oh, cool,” Rio said, grinning. “Think you could tell me all the facts before I leave?”

“I can try!” Nicky said eagerly. “Wait here!” He pulled away and dashed out of the kitchen.

Rio watched Nicky dart out of the kitchen, the soft patter of his footsteps fading as he disappeared down the hall. She shook her head fondly, but when she turned back, she found Agatha watching her with an expression she couldn’t quite decipher.

Wanda, on the other hand, just smirked knowingly over the rim of her wine glass.

“What?” Rio asked, raising an eyebrow.

Agatha didn’t answer right away. She blinked, as if realizing she’d been staring, and shook her head slightly. “Nothing,” she said, but her voice was quieter than before.

Rio tilted her head, unconvinced. “You sure about that?”

Agatha exhaled, glancing down at her own glass before meeting Rio’s eyes again. This time, there was something unmistakably tender in her gaze.

“He really missed you,” she murmured.

Rio felt something deep in her chest pull tight. She swallowed, glancing toward the hallway where Nicky had vanished before turning back to Agatha. “Yeah,” she said softly. “I missed him too.”

Something flickered in Agatha’s expression—something vulnerable, something open. For a second, it looked like she wanted to say more, but then Wanda let out a quiet chuckle, breaking the moment.

“Well,” Wanda said, leaning back in her chair. “You’re in it now, kid. No backing out.”

Rio huffed a laugh, but she didn’t look away from Agatha. “I’m not going anywhere.”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, her fingers tightening around her glass. Then, just as she started to speak, the sound of Nicky’s hurried footsteps filled the kitchen again.

“I found it!” he announced, holding up a thick book nearly as big as his torso. “Okay, Rio, I have so many things to tell you.”

Rio grinned, stretching her arms out. “Lay it on me, little man.”

As Nicky climbed into the chair beside her, eagerly flipping through pages, Rio caught Agatha’s gaze once more. And this time, Agatha wasn’t looking away.

Nicky dove straight into an enthusiastic explanation about the book he was holding—something about space, black holes, and whether or not wormholes could actually exist. Rio listened with a grin, nodding along as he spoke, occasionally glancing at Agatha, who was still watching them with that same unreadable expression.

She didn’t say much, just sipped her wine, but there was something about the way she was looking at Rio and Nicky that made Rio’s chest feel strangely warm. Like she was witnessing something she hadn’t expected to see but also couldn’t look away from.

“You’re really into space, huh?” Rio said, nudging Nicky’s shoulder.

“Duh,” he said, as if the answer was obvious. “I told Mom we should go to the planetarium again. But she’s been busy.” His little nose scrunched. “And also weird.”

Rio’s eyes flickered to Agatha, whose expression shifted in an instant. “Weird how?” she asked lightly, though Rio could hear the underlying tension in her voice.

Nicky shrugged, flipping another page. “I dunno. Just… distracted. And kind of quiet.” He frowned, looking up at Agatha with a rare seriousness for his age. “Is everything okay?”

Agatha’s breath hitched just slightly, but she recovered quickly. She reached over, smoothing a hand over Nicky’s hair. “Of course, darling,” she said, her voice softer than before. “Things have just been… a little complicated lately.”

Rio watched as Nicky seemed to think about that for a second before nodding, accepting the answer for now. But then his gaze flicked back to Rio, and he grinned. “But at least Rio’s here now!”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, her fingers tightening around her wine glass again. Wanda, still leaning back in her chair, shot her a knowing look over the rim of her own glass.

Rio smirked, deciding to ease the tension. “Yeah, well, someone’s gotta make sure you’re still the smartest kid in the room.”

Nicky beamed, satisfied, and went back to flipping through his book.

Agatha, however, didn’t look away from Rio this time. There was something different in her gaze now—not just surprise, but something deeper. Something Rio felt settle in her bones.

And for the first time since everything with Jordan had started, since the threats and the stress and the uncertainty of what came next, Rio saw a piece of Agatha finally relax.

~*~

The transition to the living room was an easy one. Nicky, Billy, and Tommy disappeared into the other room, their excited voices echoing as they set up their game. Rio stretched out on the couch next to Agatha, her legs loosely crossed, while Wanda poured them all more wine.

Viz arrived not long after, dropping onto an armchair with a sigh. “Those kids are gonna wear themselves out before bedtime,” he said, taking a sip from Wanda’s glass before Wanda huffed and went to grab his own.

Rio glanced at Agatha, who had been quiet since they sat down. She could see the tension creeping back into her shoulders, the way she was rolling the stem of her glass between her fingers. Wanda must have noticed too, because she didn’t waste time getting to the point.

“So,” Wanda said, stretching her legs out onto the coffee table, “what’s the latest with our favorite scumbag?”

Agatha let out a slow breath. “Jordan knows about the restraining order,” she said, voice steady but tight. “He confronted me this morning.”

Wanda and Viz both sat up straighter at that.

“What?” Viz’s expression darkened instantly. “Where?”

“My office. He—” Agatha exhaled sharply, fingers tightening around her glass. “He called me a bitch for filing it. Threatened me again. Said I was ruining his career.”

Rio’s jaw clenched at the memory, her hands curling into fists on her lap. “I swear to God, if I ever get five minutes alone with that bastard—”

“I don’t need you getting yourself in trouble, love,” Agatha murmured, her hand brushing lightly against Rio’s knee.

Rio huffed, leaning into the touch but not relaxing entirely. “So what now?”

Agatha looked at Wanda. “Lilia’s getting the dean involved. We disclosed our relationship officially, so Jordan’s complaint, if he makes one, won’t have as much weight. We wanted to get ahead of him.”

Wanda nodded approvingly. “Smart move.”

Viz, however, tilted her head. “But there’ll still be consequences, right?”

Agatha sighed, rubbing at her temple. “Rio has to change mentors. Take Neuro II with someone else. Dr. Patel reached out to her about a potential mentorship, but nothing’s set in stone yet.”

Viz looked at Rio. “Damn, that’s rough.”

Rio shrugged, trying for nonchalance. “Yeah, well. Could be worse.”

Wanda studied her for a long moment, then softened. “I know how much you wanted to work with Agatha,” she said gently.

Rio swallowed, forcing a smirk. “At least I still got the OR spot. And Agatha said I can still bounce research ideas off her. You know, in our personal time.” She shot Agatha a playful glance.

That earned her a small smirk in return, but Agatha’s eyes still held something heavier. A weight Rio recognized.

Wanda exhaled. “Well, I hate that this is happening, but at least you two are facing it together. And if that asshole tries anything else, you know I have no problem breaking a kneecap.”

Viz raised her glass. “To legally dubious solutions.”

Rio clinked her glass against Viz’s, smirking. “I’ll drink to that.”

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh at that, but her fingers were still toying with the stem of her glass, her thoughts clearly elsewhere. Rio noticed—of course she did—but she let it be for now.

Instead, Wanda leaned back with a satisfied sigh. “Alright, enough of the serious talk. We’ll handle it as it comes. Right now, I’d rather enjoy my wine and hear about something not infuriating.” She looked at Rio with a sly grin. “So, you and Agatha, officially official now, huh?”

Rio grinned. “Guess so.”

Viz raised an eyebrow. “So what’s that like? Dating a distinguished professor and highly regarded neurosurgeon?”

Rio made a show of looking thoughtful, then turned to Agatha. “Babe, how is it dating a second-year med student?”

Agatha scoffed, finally rolling her eyes. “Infuriating.”

Wanda burst out laughing, and Rio clutched her chest in mock offense. “I am a delight, thank you very much,” she said, nudging Agatha’s thigh with her knee.

“You’re a menace,” Agatha corrected, but there was warmth in her voice now, a lightness that hadn’t been there before.

Rio smirked. “And yet, here you are, in love with me.”

Agatha arched a brow but didn’t argue.

Viz snorted. “God, you two are disgusting.”

“Disgustingly in love,” Wanda said, grinning.

Rio just shot Agatha a knowing look, her smirk softening as Agatha reached over, squeezing her knee lightly.

For the first time in what felt like days, the weight pressing on her chest loosened just a little.

~*~

Before Rio could fire back with another cocky remark, the sound of feet padding across the floor interrupted them. A second later, Nicky came running into the living room, his face lighting up the moment he spotted Rio.

“Come play Mario Kart with us!”

Rio chuckled. “Oh, buddy, I don’t know if you’re ready for that.”

“Rio,” Agatha warned, though her lips twitched.

“What?” Rio said, feigning innocence. “I just think it’s important to teach him humility.”

“You’re just mad because I beat you last time,” Nicky shot back, eyes gleaming with challenge.

Wanda let out a bark of laughter. “Oh, I love this kid.”

Rio narrowed her eyes playfully, then cracked her knuckles. “Alright, let’s go, squirt. Time for a rematch.”

As Nicky whooped and ran back toward the other room, Rio turned back to Agatha, leaning down just enough to murmur, “You okay?”

Agatha’s fingers curled lightly around her wrist. “Yeah,” she said softly. “More than okay.”

Rio squeezed her hand once before standing. “Alright, time to go break a kid’s spirit,” she announced, cracking her neck like she was preparing for battle.

Viz groaned. “I’m putting my money on Nicky.”

As Rio headed off, she caught the way Agatha watched her, something warm and unguarded in her gaze. And for the first time in a while, Rio let herself sink into it, let herself believe that despite everything, this—they—were going to be okay.

~*~

 

The problem was, things were not okay.

At first, it was easy to dismiss. Jordan was in her ortho class, and their schedules overlapped enough that running into him was inevitable. She felt his eyes on her when she walked in, the weight of his gaze pressing against her back as she took her seat. But she never looked at him. Never acknowledged him. That was the only power she had over him right now.

Then, it started happening outside of class. The first time was at the café near the firehouse. It was a popular spot, and plenty of med students hung around there, so she didn’t think much of it. But then it happened again. And again. Every time she stopped by for coffee, he was there. Never sitting too close, never doing anything outright threatening—but watching. Always watching.

The first real spike of unease hit when she spotted him near her apartment building. She had just come off a brutal shift and was half-asleep when she stepped out of her car, only to catch sight of a figure leaning against a parked sedan across the street. At first, she thought she was imagining it—her mind playing tricks on her from exhaustion—but then he shifted, stepping forward just enough for the streetlamp to catch his face.

Her stomach turned to lead.

She forced herself to keep moving, refusing to acknowledge him. He wasn’t breaking any laws. He wasn’t doing anything. But he was making damn sure she saw him.

And then, the worst of it—he showed up when she was with Agatha and Nicky.

They had taken Nicky out for ice cream after school, a rare moment of peace in the chaos of their lives. She had been laughing at something Agatha said, the sound warm in her chest, when a familiar shape in the distance made her blood run cold.

Jordan. Standing across the street, pretending to be on his phone. But his eyes weren’t on his screen. They were on them.

Rio tensed. Agatha, picking up on it immediately, followed her gaze.

“Rio?” she asked, voice quiet but alert.

She swallowed hard, shifting so she was partially in front of Nicky. “It’s fine,” she murmured. “Let’s just go.”

Agatha didn’t argue, but the look she gave Rio said this is not fine.

And she was right. It wasn’t fine at all.

~*~

Rio exhaled as she crossed the hospital parking lot, phone pressed to her ear.

“Damn, Al, finally,” she said, relieved. “I was starting to think you were milking this whole near-death experience just for the VIP treatment.”

Alice snorted. “You’re just mad I got a week off while you’re still running on fumes.”

“Please, if I had your chart, I’d be out in two days.”

Alice laughed, and Rio was about to fire back when movement near the entrance caught her eye.

Jordan.

He was leaning against a parked car, arms crossed, like he had been waiting for her.

Her stomach twisted. Not here. Not now.

Alice was still talking. “So what’s the plan? You sweeping me off my feet and carrying me out of here, or—”

“Hold on a sec,” Rio murmured.

She switched her phone to speaker and, with a few quick swipes, started recording her screen. Then she angled the camera down just enough that Jordan would be visible without making it obvious what she was doing.

Alice’s voice crackled through the line. “Uh, what’s up?”

Jordan pushed off the car and stepped toward her.

“You gonna keep pretending you don’t see me?” he asked, voice cold and low.

Rio clenched her jaw, not letting him intimidate her. “I don’t see you,” she shot back. “You’re nothing to me.”

Alice went silent on the other end.

Jordan hummed, looking her over like he was unimpressed. “Funny. I figured we’d at least be cordial, considering you’re the reason my life just went up in flames.”

Rio scoffed. “Your own damn actions did that.”

“You don’t think filing for that bullshit restraining order had anything to do with it?”

Her pulse ticked faster, but she refused to flinch.

“You are stalking Agatha,” she said coolly. “And now me, too, apparently.”

Jordan let out a short, humorless laugh. “Oh, get over yourself.” Then he stepped closer, dropping his voice. “Tell me, Vidal, do you like being her little pet? Is that what gets you off? Jumping whenever she calls?”

Alice swore under her breath, but Rio barely heard her over the rush of blood in her ears.

“Or maybe,” Jordan went on, lips curling, “you like pretending she actually cares about you. That you’re not just a fun little game for her.”

Rio saw red.

But she didn’t react—not in the way he wanted. Instead, she let the corner of her mouth lift, slow and sharp.

“You really wanna test me right now?” she asked, voice calm.

Jordan’s smirk faltered.

Rio tilted her head, just slightly. “You’re already circling the drain. Keep pushing, and I’ll make sure you drown.”

Jordan’s eyes narrowed, and his voice dropped, now full of venom. “I’m just getting started. You think you’re safe, but you’re not. I’ll make sure both of you regret this. Agatha Harkness and her little project. I’ll destroy her, and you’ll be right there with her.”

Her heart rate spiked. He was threatening them both, openly.

“You really think I’m scared of you?” Rio spat, her voice steady despite the storm raging inside her. “Keep talking, Jordan. Keep threatening me. I’ll make sure the next time you try anything, you won’t walk away so easily.”

Jordan’s smirk faltered for a split second, but his eyes darkened with rage. “You think you can do something about it? Keep your nose clean, Vidal. You won’t know what hit you if you get in my way again.”

“Try me,” Rio said, her voice ice-cold.

For a moment, they just stared at each other—intense, charged, like a slow-motion collision waiting to happen.

Finally, Jordan sneered, “You’ll be sorry. You’ll both be sorry.” He turned on his heel and stormed off, leaving Rio standing there, her chest tight with the threat still hanging in the air.

Alice’s voice came through the speaker, frantic. “What the fuck was that?”

Rio exhaled sharply, her pulse still racing. “Nothing I can’t handle. I’ll deal with it.”

“Deal with it?” Alice scoffed. “You better tell me what the hell that was, because that wasn’t just some angry ex. That was a threat.”

“I know, Al,” Rio muttered, her hand clenched into a fist. “I know. And he’s only just getting started.” Her mind raced, but she didn’t let it show. “Let’s just focus on getting you out of here, okay? I’m on my way up.”

“I’m not letting this go, Rio,” Alice said, her voice tight with concern.

“I know you’re not,” Rio said with a forced laugh, pushing back the fear trying to creep in. “And neither am I. Let’s get you out of here, then I’ll figure out how to deal with this.”

She glanced back in the direction Jordan had disappeared to, her jaw tightening. He wants to play? Fine. She’d make sure he knew just how badly he’d miscalculated.



Twenty-six

Chapter Notes

I'm still not super happy with this chapter, but I don't know how to improve it any more, so here it is. Hope you guys like it!

Agatha sat at her desk, reviewing her latest research, but her mind wasn’t on the papers in front of her. She kept glancing at her phone, waiting for Rio’s update. She felt on edge today, as if she was just waiting for the other shoe to drop. She and Rio had instituted a rule to let each other know where they were at every given time, at least until the restraining order came through.

She knew that Rio was supposed to pick up Alice from the hospital today, and she was definitely overdue in checking in with her. Every moment felt drawn out, and the seconds seemed to stretch into hours.

Finally, her phone buzzed with a text notification.

Rio

Just home with Alice, but I had to text you right away. We have proof. Jordan threatened me. Has been stalking me actually. Been showing up at places I usually go to. Today he approached me in the parking lot and said some really fucked up shit. I recorded it. It’s all on my phone.

Agatha’s breath caught in her chest, and her eyes flicked to the door. Her first instinct was to run straight to Rio. But she couldn’t—not yet. She needed to process this, to make sure she wasn’t overreacting. But every nerve in her body was already on fire.

Agatha

Are you okay??? Did he touch you???

There was a pause before Rio replied.

Rio  

I’m fine, babe. He didn’t get close enough. But the threats… damn, Agatha. He’s more dangerous than I thought .

Agatha let out a shaky breath, pushing herself to stand. Her hands were shaking, and she instinctively checked her watch. Rio had been avoiding telling her about Jordan showing up at her usual spots. The realization hit her hard.

Agatha

You’ve been seeing him? Where?? At the firehouse?? You should’ve told me!

The reply came back quickly, an apology in Rio’s tone even through the screen.

Rio

I know. I should’ve told you sooner. But I didn’t want to freak you out. And I didn’t want to get you more involved.

More involved.

It was exactly what Agatha had been afraid of. The deeper Rio got tangled with Jordan, the more dangerous it would become. She had hoped that Rio would’ve told her sooner, that she wouldn’t have had to find out like this. But she wasn’t going to let herself spiral. Not now. Not when Rio was dealing with this.

Agatha

It’s not about that, Rio. It’s about safety. We should’ve been handling this together from the start. You’re not alone in this.

She paused, rubbing the bridge of her nose, trying to keep calm. She needed to be the rock for both of them right now.

Rio  

You’re right. I’m sorry. I’ll stop by your place later tonight. Let’s talk when I get there?

Agatha

I can swing by your place. I have something for Alice.

Rio

Sounds good, love. The door is unlocked. Just let yourself in.

With that, Agatha grabbed her things, walked out of her office, and drove toward Rio’s apartment, her mind racing with thoughts of Jordan, of how to protect Rio, and how this would affect everything—both professionally and personally. Agatha wasn’t sure what this would all mean in the long run, but she wasn’t about to let anything happen to Rio. Not while she had breath in her lungs.

Twenty minutes later, Agatha stepped into Rio’s apartment with a soft smile, the bag with Alice’s welcome home gift hanging from her hand. She felt an overwhelming need to take care of both of them after the chaos that had unfolded. As the door clicked shut behind her, she was immediately hit with the scent of something delicious cooking.

Rio was in the kitchen, moving around with practiced ease, clearly in the middle of making them something to eat. Alice was curled up on the couch, a blanket wrapped around her, her face soft with the relief of being home.

“Hey,” Agatha said quietly, her gaze flicking between Alice and Rio. Rio glanced over at her and smiled, but there was a tension in her shoulders that Agatha knew well.

“Hey, I wasn’t expecting you so soon,” Rio said, though her voice held a note of relief.

“I wanted to see you,” Agatha replied, walking over to the kitchen counter where Rio was chopping vegetables. She placed the gift bag down. “I brought Alice a little something.”

Rio looked over at the bag, then back at Agatha, her brow furrowed with concern. “You didn’t have to… but I know Alice will love it.”

Agatha leaned against the counter, eyes never leaving Rio. “How’s she doing?” she asked softly, genuinely wanting to know.

“She’s doing a lot better. She’s just glad to be out of the hospital, you know? But… I think we both know there’s more to this than just her recovery.” Rio’s tone shifted, and Agatha could hear the worry in her voice.

“What happened?” Agatha asked, her voice growing serious. “With Jordan?”

“I haven’t had the chance to talk to you about it yet. I’m sorry,” Rio admitted, her eyes flicking to Alice briefly before she exhaled sharply. “It’s… it’s been a lot. I don’t know why I didn’t tell you sooner, but I’ve been seeing him around more. It’s like he’s everywhere. And then today… I recorded everything when he confronted me.” Rio’s gaze darkened as she reached for her phone, showing Agatha the video of Jordan’s encounter.

Agatha’s heart sank as she watched it. The anger inside her swelled, but she quickly forced it down, the protective instinct flaring to life once again.

“I’m sorry you’ve had to go through this,” Agatha murmured, reaching out to touch Rio’s arm. “I should’ve been there for you. I should’ve known.”

Rio shook her head. “No, it’s not your fault. But… I get it now, Agatha. I know why you didn’t tell me about Jordan before. About what he did to you… I know how it feels now.”

Agatha’s heart clenched, and she swallowed hard, guilt gnawing at her. “I should’ve trusted you,” she whispered, “but I didn’t want to drag you into it. I didn’t want to put you at risk.”

“I get it,” Rio said softly. “And I’m sorry, too. But we’re in this together, right? ”

Agatha nodded, fighting back the lump in her throat. She gently cupped Rio’s face, brushing her thumb over her cheek. “Yeah. We are.”

~*~

As the evening settled in, the scent of simmering pasta filled the apartment, and Rio carefully set the table, placing a bottle of wine in the center. The kitchen was warm with the gentle hum of the stove, the clink of plates, and the low murmur of conversation as Alice slowly got comfortable back in the apartment. It was a rare moment of normalcy, the quiet hum of life after Alice’s discharge, but both Rio and Agatha knew it wouldn’t last long—there was still too much to address.

Once they were seated at the table, Alice dug into her meal first, as if she hadn’t eaten in days. Agatha could see the tension in Rio’s shoulders, the weight of everything that had happened still hanging between them, but the warmth in the air from the comfort of dinner made it easier to start unpacking everything.

Alice looked from one to the other as she chewed, her gaze shifting between them. “Okay, spill. What the hell is going on? You two are being so quiet about it, but I can tell something’s off.” Her words weren’t sharp, but there was an underlying edge to them. She wasn’t a fool, and she knew when something was being left unsaid.

Rio glanced at Agatha before answering, her voice quieter than usual. “It’s that lunatic I told you about a few weeks ago, remember? Thomas Jordan,” she began. “He’s been stalking me. Following me to places I hang out, showing up around my neighborhood. Today, he—” She paused, visibly bracing herself for what she was about to say. “He threatened me. You saw the whole thing.”

Agatha squeezed Rio’s hand across the table, her heart aching at the words. She could still see the hurt in Rio’s eyes, the lingering fear, and the uncertainty that clung to her. Agatha had always hated the thought of someone hurting Rio. It was a weight she hadn’t been able to lift for her.

Alice stopped chewing, her fork still suspended mid-air, and her eyes narrowed. Her voice had a sharpness now, a protective edge to it. “How long has this been going on? Why the hell didn’t you tell me earlier?”

Rio sighed, rubbing her temples before meeting Alice’s gaze. “I didn’t want to worry you, Al. You were in the hospital! I thought I could handle it, but today—today, I just couldn’t pretend it wasn’t happening anymore. He’s threatened both me and Agatha. He said he was going to ruin everything. I thought he was just full of shit, that he was too much of a chicken shit to actually do anything to us. But today he actually scared me. You heard what he said. I didn’t realize until now how much of a risk this actually is.”

Agatha swallowed hard at the mention of herself. The thought of Jordan trying to involve her in this mess made her blood boil, but it was the reality they were facing. The severity of the situation wasn’t something Agatha could ignore anymore.

“Listen,” Rio said, noticing the change in her demeanor. “We’ve got proof now. I recorded him today. And I—I didn’t want you to know sooner because I didn’t want you to worry, but Agatha is filing for a restraining order. It’s just… everything’s happening so fast, and I don’t know how to keep him away from us. He keeps showing up everywhere.”

Alice set down her fork with a heavy sigh, her frustration clear now. “I’m going to make sure we get him. This isn’t happening. We’ll deal with this the right way—he’s not going to get away with this. I know people in the police. We both do, Rio! If I have to go down there and find him myself—”

Agatha held up a hand, stopping Alice before things escalated any further. “No, Alice. We’re not taking matters into our own hands. We’re going through the legal process. We’re gathering everything we need to ensure he’s kept away from both Rio and me.”

Alice glared at her but nodded slowly. “Fine. But don’t think for a second that if I find him out there, I won’t kick his sorry ass. No one messes with my family.”

Rio smiled softly at Alice’s protectiveness. “I know, Al. And I’m not going to let him mess with me anymore either.”

Agatha leaned forward, her eyes meeting Rio’s. “We’ll get through this. Together. We’ll make sure he’s stopped.”

The warmth of the words didn’t fully take away the weight of the situation, but Rio found some comfort in Agatha’s reassurance. Her presence was a grounding force, and Rio knew she wasn’t alone anymore.

Alice sighed deeply, shaking her head. “I swear, if that fucker comes anywhere near you again—” She cut herself off, shaking her head. “I just can’t believe this is happening. I thought we left high school drama behind. But nope. Here we are.”

The conversation slowed as they finished their meal, each of them lost in their own thoughts, but the weight of their conversation still hung in the air. They had a plan, they had proof, and they had each other.

When the plates were cleared away, Agatha rose from the table and walked over to the counter, pulling out a bottle of wine. She uncorked it, poured a glass for each of them, and turned back to face Rio and Alice. “To the truth,” Agatha said, her voice steady.

“To the truth,” Rio echoed, raising her glass.

Alice clinked her glass with theirs and gave them both a wry grin. “And to kicking Jordan’s ass out of your lives for good.”

They all laughed, the sound genuine despite the tension that still lingered. But it was a moment of relief. A small victory against the darkness that had been trying to consume their lives.

Agatha sat back down at the table, looking at both of them, her heart full. “We’ve got this,” she said quietly. 

~*~

Agatha woke up to the feeling of warmth pressed against her. Rio’s arm was draped over her waist, her face buried in Agatha’s neck, breathing deep and steady. 

They had made it back to her place late the night before, making a quick detour to pick up Nicky at Wanda’s.

She shifted slightly, just enough to turn onto her side and take in the sight of Rio still sleeping. There was a peacefulness to her features that Agatha wished she could preserve, untouched by the stress of classes, work, and now the looming threat of Jordan. She reached up, brushing a few stray curls from Rio’s face. At the touch, Rio stirred, humming softly before cracking one eye open. A slow, lazy smile spread across her lips.

“Mmm… morning, beautiful,” Rio murmured, voice thick with sleep.

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh. “Morning.”

Rio stretched, her arm tightening around Agatha before she leaned in to press a soft kiss against her lips. It was unhurried, gentle, like the world hadn’t started moving yet. But eventually, Rio sighed and flopped onto her back. “What time is it?”

Agatha turned her head toward the clock on the nightstand. “Almost seven.”

Rio groaned. “I hate early mornings.”

“You’re a paramedic. That’s half your job.”

“Doesn’t mean I like it,” Rio said, but she sat up, rubbing a hand over her face. “I should get moving. My schedule’s different now with the new Neuro II professor.”

Agatha tensed slightly at that. Another reminder of what Rio had lost because of Jordan’s threats. She reached out, resting a hand on Rio’s back. “Are you ready for it?”

Rio tilted her head back, looking at Agatha over her shoulder. “Ready as I’ll ever be. Can’t say I’m thrilled, but I’ll survive. Hopefully, Dr. Meyer won’t make me regret everything.”

Agatha offered a small smile. “She’s competent. You’ll get a fair shot with her.”

Rio sighed, then turned to fully face Agatha again, her expression softening. “What about you? What’s on your schedule today?”

Agatha hesitated for a moment before sitting up. “I have a conference in New York next week. I’m giving a talk on my latest research.”

Rio’s brow quirked. “That’s big . Why didn’t you mention it before?”

“I’ve been a little preoccupied,” Agatha admitted wryly. “It just feels like another thing on top of everything else. But it’s important, so I need to focus and prepare for it.”

Rio studied her for a long moment, then reached out to tuck a strand of Agatha’s hair behind her ear. “Hey. You’ll kill it. You always do.”

Agatha exhaled, leaning into Rio’s touch just slightly. “I appreciate the confidence.”

“Always.” Rio leaned in, stealing another kiss before reluctantly pulling away. “Alright, I really do need to get ready. New professor, new routine.”

Agatha nodded, watching as Rio moved toward the bathroom. She stayed in bed a moment longer, considering everything ahead—Jordan, the conference, the weight of all of it. But then she took a breath and pushed the thoughts aside. For now, she had the morning, and she had Rio. That was enough.

~*~

The morning at Agatha’s started in a slow, sleepy haze, but quickly gave way to the familiar rhythm of getting ready for the day. The scent of coffee filled the kitchen as Agatha stood by the counter, sipping from her mug, watching Rio and Nicky work on breakfast together. It had become an unspoken routine—Rio handling the eggs while Nicky took charge of buttering toast, his little hands moving with exaggerated precision.

“Mom, did you know that Venus spins the opposite way from all the other planets?” Nicky asked, eyes bright as he looked up at Agatha.

Agatha smirked over the rim of her cup. “I did, actually.”

Nicky huffed, turning to Rio. “Did you?”

Rio ruffled his curls. “Nope. But that’s why I’ve got my favorite expert here to teach me.”

Nicky beamed, completely won over. “We’re doing the solar system for my class project, and Rio said she’s gonna help me.”

Agatha’s gaze softened as she watched the two of them. Something in her chest tightened—something warm and so dangerously full. She loved them. She loved this. More than she’d ever let herself admit before.

“You don’t have to do that,” she told Rio, even though part of her was thrilled at the idea of Rio being even more entrenched in their little world.

Rio just shrugged, scooping scrambled eggs onto their plates. “I want to.”

They sat down to eat, the conversation flowing easily between them. Nicky, as always, had an endless supply of facts to share, and Rio egged him on, gasping at every new piece of information. Agatha, content, let herself bask in the simple joy of the moment.

Soon enough, the morning rush resumed. Agatha helped Nicky pack his school bag while Rio finished the dishes. They fell into sync so naturally that it was hard to believe Rio hadn’t always been a part of this routine.

As they headed out, Agatha drove, with Nicky chattering excitedly in the backseat about his day ahead. When they pulled up to the school, Rio twisted in her seat to high-five him.

“Knock ‘em dead, champ,” she said.

“I will! Love you, Mom!” Nicky said, already climbing out of the car.

Agatha smiled. “Love you too, sweetheart.”

He waved before disappearing into the school, and Agatha lingered a moment, watching until he was out of sight. When she turned back, Rio was studying her with something soft in her gaze.

“What?” Agatha asked, feigning ignorance.

Rio just shook her head with a small smile. “Nothing.”

The moment lingered between them as Agatha pulled back onto the road, heading toward Northwestern. But as they neared campus, that quiet warmth slowly gave way to tension.

Because Jordan was there.

Standing near the entrance to the parking lot, just far enough not to seem overly suspicious, but close enough that it was obvious he was waiting for someone. Or watching someone.

Agatha’s grip on the wheel tightened. Rio went rigid beside her.

He was always around. Always watching.

And they were done pretending not to notice.

~*~

Agatha was absorbed in her notes when she heard the soft knock at the door, followed by the familiar creak of it opening. Her heart gave a little flutter when she looked up to find Rio standing there, her usual bright smile gracing her face. It was a Monday, and they hadn’t seen each other in a couple of days because Rio was working a double shift, and Agatha missed her like crazy.

“Hey,” Rio said, voice tinged with warmth after the long shift, her eyes meeting Agatha’s with a certain ease that made Agatha’s chest tighten in a way she was still learning to navigate.

“Hey yourself,” Agatha replied, standing up from her desk. A brief silence passed between them, the kind that felt comfortable in its own way, before Rio crossed the room, her hand reaching up as she closed the distance.

They greeted each other with a soft kiss—quick, but full of quiet affection, a silent acknowledgment of how much they had missed each other. Agatha’s lips lingered for a moment before she pulled back, meeting Rio’s gaze.

“I was hoping you’d come by,” Agatha said, her voice softer than she intended, but it felt right. “How was your shift?”

Rio shrugged lightly, her exhaustion still visible in the slight slump of her shoulders but masked by the warmth in her expression. “Long, but nothing I couldn’t handle. Glad to be off.” She stepped back a little, leaning against the doorframe casually, but her gaze remained on Agatha, almost too focused. “You doing okay? You’ve got that meeting with Dr. Olsen today, right?”

Agatha nodded, a faint smile tugging at her lips. “Yeah, I’m meeting with her to update her on everything with Jordan. We’re still working out how best to handle your transition to Dr. Patel for the mentorship.” She tilted her head, watching Rio. “I’ve been thinking about you… making this change, and I just want to make sure you’re feeling okay with everything.”

Rio’s eyes softened, and she pushed off the desk she’d leaned against, taking a step closer. “It’s not easy, but I’ve already been in touch with Dr. Patel. He seems great. I think we’ll figure it out. Plus, I’ll still be around.” She paused, her voice lowering as she added, “And I’ll still stop by to say hi whenever I can.”

Agatha chuckled, a light blush coloring her cheeks. “I think I’d be disappointed if you didn’t.”

Rio grinned, her hand gently brushing the side of Agatha’s arm as she stood close enough that Agatha could feel the warmth of her presence. There was something effortless about the way they stood there, no longer trying to hide the connection between them. “You don’t have to worry about that,” Rio replied with a teasing glint in her eyes. “I don’t let go of people that easily.”

“Good,” Agatha said, her voice softer now, full of a deeper kind of sincerity. “I don’t want you to.”

Agatha stood just a little closer to Rio, still feeling the warmth of their earlier kiss. The silence stretched between them, comfortable but filled with unspoken thoughts. Agatha finally let out a quiet breath and met Rio’s gaze, feeling a flutter in her chest.

“You know,” Agatha began, her voice slightly hesitant but warm, “I’ve been meaning to ask you something.”

Rio tilted her head, a knowing look crossing her face. “Yeah? What’s up?”

Agatha took a moment, gathering her thoughts. She’d been thinking about this for a while, but the timing had never felt quite right—until now. “I’m heading to New York tomorrow for that Neurology conference I told you about,” she said, her words coming a little faster now. “I was wondering if you’d want to come with me?”

Rio’s eyes widened slightly in surprise, but the warmth never left her expression. “You want me to come to New York with you?”

Agatha gave a soft nod, feeling the weight of the question hanging in the air. “Yeah. I mean, I could use the company. I’ll be tied up with the panels and lectures most of the time, but I’ll have some free time in the afternoons, and… it would be nice to have someone with me. You’re interested in the research, and I thought, well… maybe you’d want to come along.”

Rio stood there for a moment, looking thoughtful, her gaze flicking to Agatha’s face as if weighing the invitation. Then, a grin broke across her face, playful and genuine. “You’ve been working up the courage to ask me, haven’t you?”

Agatha chuckled softly, a bit embarrassed but relieved to have finally said it. “Maybe a little,” she admitted, her voice light.

Rio stepped closer, her hand brushing Agatha’s arm as she looked up at her with that teasing glint in her eyes. “Well, I’d be lying if I said I wasn’t interested. New York with you sounds… pretty damn good right about now.”

Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, the warmth in Rio’s eyes making everything else fade away for a second. “So, you’re saying yes?”

Rio grinned, her voice softening. “I’m saying yes… but,” she added, her tone shifting to something more practical, “I need to check with my captain at the firehouse first to make sure I can get the time off. We’ve got a lot going on right now.”

Agatha nodded, understanding. “Of course, I get it. I just wanted to ask, and if you can swing it, we’ll make it work. I’ll book your flight as soon as you’re sure.”

Rio gave her a reassuring smile. “I’ll check in with him and get back to you. But I really want to make this happen, Agatha.”

“Let me know as soon as you can,” Agatha said, trying to keep her tone light, though she couldn’t help the little spark of anticipation that ran through her. 

Rio stepped closer once again, her hand brushing Agatha’s arm as she looked at her with that familiar warmth. “I’ll see what I can do,” she promised, then leaned in to place another soft kiss on Agatha’s cheek, lingering for a moment before pulling back to meet her gaze. “Looking forward to it. I’ll keep you posted.”

Agatha felt a quiet warmth spread through her at the gesture, and for a second, the room felt a little smaller, a little more intimate. “I’m looking forward to it too,” Agatha replied, her voice softer than before.

Rio gave her one last smile, her eyes lighting up as she turned to head toward the door. “I’ll text you as soon as I get the okay from my captain.”

“Take care of that, and I’ll be ready when you are,” Agatha said with a smile, watching her leave.

As the door closed behind Rio, Agatha stood there for a moment, a quiet thrill rushing through her. It was happening. Slowly, but it was happening.

~*~

That afternoon, after finishing up a few last-minute tasks, Agatha sat in her office, trying to focus on the paperwork scattered before her. Her phone buzzed again, breaking her concentration. It was Rio.

Rio

Got the time off. I’m all in for New York!

Agatha’s heart lifted at the message. She quickly responded: 

Agatha

Perfect! I’ll book your flight right now. Looking forward to it.

She grinned to herself, her mind racing with thoughts of the trip. It would be a nice break from the stress, a chance to reconnect with Rio away from the mess at the university. Checking the time on her phone, Agatha realized she was borderline late for her meeting with Dr. Olsen. So she picked up her purse and quickly made the trek to the fifth floor where the Dean’s office was.

When she got there, Dr. Olsen’s assistant told her to right in.

Agath entered, finding the Dean behind the desk, her expression all business. “Agatha,” she said with a nod, and Agatha closed the door behind her. 

Agatha straightened in her chair, instinctively bracing herself. She knew this meeting was coming, but it didn’t make it any easier.  

Dr. Olsen waited for her to take a seat across from her, her gaze sharp but understanding. “I wanted to check in on everything, especially with Jordan’s situation. How are you holding up?”

“I’m managing,” Agatha said, but the weight of the situation lingered in her tone. “I’ve got the lawyer involved, and we’re waiting for the hearing for the restraining order. That’s this Friday, finally. But I’m trying to stay focused on work until then.”

Olsen nodded, her eyes narrowing slightly. “Good. You’ve done what you can there. But let’s talk about Rio. I know she’s in transition now, moving over to Dr. Patel for her mentorship, right? Have you spoken with her about how that’s going?”

“I have,” Agatha replied, her voice steady. “She’s been great about it. She understands the situation, even if I know it’s disappointing for her.” She hesitated, the familiar pang of guilt washing over her. “She was a great fit for my mentorship. This is just… a difficult situation all around.”

Olsen leaned back in her chair, studying Agatha for a moment. “I’m sure this is hard, but you’re doing the right thing. Having her switch to another mentor is the smart call. You’ve got to protect yourself, Agatha, and you’ve got to protect her too.”

“I know,” Agatha said quietly, swallowing the lump in her throat. “I just… wish things were different. It just feels like everything’s falling apart.”

Olsen’s expression softened, her tone more supportive. “It’s not falling apart, but I understand why it feels that way. You’re trying to juggle too much, and it’s a lot. You’re only human.”

Agatha took a deep breath, nodding. She appreciated Olsen’s reassurance, though it didn’t quite ease the weight she was carrying. “I just want to make sure Rio’s okay. This is tough for her, and I… don’t want to make it harder.”

Olsen gave a short nod. “You’re doing the best you can. That’s all you can do. And if you feel like you need more time away from all this, there’s no shame in that. I know you’ve got that conference in New York this week, right? Take a breather. It might help you clear your head.”

Agatha straightened slightly, the thought of the conference making her feel a bit lighter. “Actually, I was just about to book the flights. Rio’s coming with me. I think a few days away could be good for both of us.”

Olsen raised an eyebrow. “So, you’re not going solo?”

Agatha smiled faintly, a small but genuine smile. “No, I’m not. I invited her. I could use the company, and she’s been working hard on her research. She’s earned the break.”

“That sounds like a good plan. A change of scenery might do you both some good,” Olsen said, her tone approving. 

“Yeah,” Agatha said, nodding. “I’ll have a lot to go over, but I think it’ll be a nice escape from the pressure here.”

Olsen gave her a small smile. “I’m glad to hear it. You deserve that.”

“Thanks,” Agatha replied, the relief of having this conversation behind her settling in. “I’ll be sure to take it easy. It’ll be good for us to get out of here for a bit, too. Jordan is starting to bother Rio, so if we’re both out of town, he won’t be able to do anything against us.

Olsen nodded, standing up. “Let me know if this thing with Mr. Jordan escalates further. You’re doing well, Agatha. Keep your head above water. And if Jordan keeps bothering you even after the restraining order, we will see what we can do about disciplinary actions here. He might lose his spot.”

Agatha followed her lead, standing up as well. “Thanks, Dr. Olsen. I appreciate it.”

As Olsen left, Agatha sat back down in her chair, her thoughts briefly drifting to Rio. She’d booked the flights, and everything was set. The idea of getting away for a few days, with Rio by her side, felt like a lifeline.

She took a deep breath, feeling a little lighter, and sent a quick message to Rio: 

Agatha

Flights are booked. I’ll pick you up tomorrow around 10-ish after I drop Nicky off at school.

A few moments later, Rio’s reply came: 

Rio

Can’t wait, love. I’ll be ready.

Agatha smiled to herself, a quiet excitement settling in her chest. Tomorrow couldn’t come soon enough.







Twenty-seven

Chapter Notes

I know it’s been a while. Life has been extremely hectic and stressful. I hope you guys are still interested. I’m still not 100% satisfied with this chapter, but I can’t look at it anymore either, haha.

Let me know what you think.

Rio zipped up her duffel bag, moving quickly between the pile of clothes on the bed and the bathroom counter where her toiletries were scattered. It felt like she was running on autopilot. A long shift at the firehouse, barely any sleep, and now packing for a trip to New York with Agatha. Not that she was complaining. In fact, the idea of spending a few days with Agatha, away from the chaos, was exactly what she needed. The whole Jordan situation had been weighing on them both, and a break was long overdue.

Alice, sitting on the couch with her foot propped up on a pillow, gave Rio an amused glance. “So, let me get this straight,” she said, the corner of her mouth curving into a grin. “Your first romantic trip together is to… a neurology conference?”

Rio froze for a second, looking over at her with a raised eyebrow. “What’s wrong with that?”

Alice let out a dramatic sigh, shaking her head. “You two are literal neuro nerds. I thought your first getaway together would be some romantic weekend at the beach or a cute little cabin in the mountains, not… a conference about brain science.”

Rio laughed, her heart lightening at Alice’s teasing. “It’s not like we planned it that way. Agatha’s speaking at the conference, and I’m going along to support her—and, okay, yeah, to check out the research. I mean, it’s New York, and we do both kind of geek out about neurology.”

“Yeah, sure,” Alice replied, her grin widening. “But I bet the only thing on your minds will be neurons and synapses, huh? Don’t you dare come back and tell me you spent the whole time talking about Alzheimer’s research and neurodegenerative diseases. That’ll be a mood killer for sure.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t help the smile tugging at her lips. “Okay, we’re not only going to talk about neuro stuff. We’ll have some fun too. It’ll be nice to get away for a bit. No work, no school, no psycho Jordan. Just us.”

Alice arched an eyebrow, her playful tone turning a bit more teasing. “Yeah, sure. Just make sure you take some time for, I don’t know, romance too, yeah? You two deserve it.”

Rio’s cheeks flushed, and she glanced away, busying herself with stuffing a pair of socks into the bag. “Yeah, I guess we do.”

“You’re both in love, and it’s pretty obvious to anyone who’s seen you two together. But hey, take your time. Just make sure you don’t spend the whole trip locked in your hotel room talking about the hippocampus or whatever.”

Rio couldn’t suppress a laugh. “Okay, okay. I get it. But I really am excited for this. We both need a little break from everything, and the last couple of months have been… a lot. I’ll bring you back a souvenir or something.”

“Better make it a big one,” Alice said, grinning. “Have fun in New York, you two lovebirds. I’ll be here, holding down the fort and still recovering from this stupid injury.”

Rio gave Alice a thumbs-up as she finished packing the last of her things. “Thanks. I’ll check in with you after we get settled.”

She was zipping up her suitcase when her phone buzzed on the counter. She glanced at the screen and saw Agatha’s name.

“Hey,” Rio answered, hurrying to toss the last pair of shoes into the bag. “Everything okay?”

“I’m on my way to pick you up,” Agatha’s voice came through the phone, warm and steady. “The Uber will be there in ten minutes, so get your things together and meet me outside.”

Rio quickly glanced around her apartment, making sure she hadn’t missed anything. Her bag was packed, and she had everything she needed. “Okay, I’m almost done. I’ll be out in a few minutes.”

“Great. See you soon.”

After hanging up, Rio rushed around the apartment, stuffing a few last items into her bag before slinging it over her shoulder. She darted over to Alice, who was still lounging on the couch, looking way too comfortable.

“I’m heading out,” Rio said, hurriedly gathering her things. “You behave while I’m gone. Don’t do anything to make your injury worse, okay?”

Alice just grinned at her, “No promises, but I’ll try. Have fun, and don’t forget to tell me all the actual details when you get back.”

Rio rolled her eyes, her heart light with excitement. “I will. I swear. But don’t make me regret leaving you alone with your Netflix marathon.”

“You’re the one leaving me with the remote,” Alice teased back, laughing.

Rio shook her head as she rushed out the door, the thrill of the trip ahead of her making everything else fade into the background. She’d finally have a few days to focus on herself—and Agatha—without the weight of everything else. She was ready.

~*~

 

Rio barely had time to catch her breath before she reached the curb and saw Agatha’s Uber pull up. She smiled, feeling a flutter of excitement, and moved quickly to the trunk to stow her suitcase. As she slammed it shut, Agatha stepped out of the car, looking effortlessly chic in a simple but elegant coat and scarf, her dark hair flowing loosely around her shoulders.

Without thinking, Rio moved toward her and pulled her into a warm kiss, their lips meeting in a soft, quick embrace. Agatha’s familiar, comforting scent washed over her, and for a moment, everything else disappeared.

Agatha pulled back slightly, her eyes sparkling. “Hi there. You ready for this?”

Rio nodded, her heart racing. “Definitely. Let’s get out of here.”

They slid into the backseat of the Uber, and Rio settled into the plush seat next to Agatha, feeling the warmth of her presence settle around her. As the car started moving, she glanced at Agatha, watching the way the light played on her face.

“How’s Nicky doing?” Rio asked, her voice soft. “Has he been looking forward to the trip?”

“Yeah,” Agatha said with a small smile. “He’s really excited to spend a couple of days with Wanda and the twins. I think he’s already planned a list of movies to watch with them and the things they’re going to do.” She laughed lightly, shaking her head. 

“That’s great,” Rio said, shaking her head. “He won’t even have time to miss us.”

“We’ll be back before you know it,” Agatha reassured her, her fingers brushing against Rio’s as she settled into the seat. “It’ll be nice to just focus on each other for a bit. We’ve both needed this, I think.”

Rio smiled, her stomach fluttering. “I agree. No work, no school, no… psycho. Just us.”

“Exactly.” Agatha’s smile widened, and she shifted slightly, turning to Rio. “So, what do you want to do once we get there? I know you’re all about checking out the research, but we’ll have time to explore a bit, right?”

Rio leaned back in the seat, eyes closing briefly. “I’m honestly just excited to be away from everything for a while. But yeah, we can check out the city a little. Maybe go to a museum or something. I’m pretty sure you’ll love all the art in New York.”

Agatha nodded, a hint of mischief in her eyes. “I’m in, as long as there’s some time to relax. No neuro talk 24/7, promise?”

“Deal,” Rio said with a chuckle. “We’ll save that for the conference only.”

They chatted more as the Uber made its way to the airport, Rio’s mind buzzing with the idea of the trip ahead. There was something peaceful about the way Agatha made everything feel easy. It was just the two of them, a little getaway, and—hopefully—a much-needed break from all the tension.

As they arrived at the airport and went through the usual motions of checking in and getting their tickets, Rio found herself becoming a bit more fidgety. It wasn’t that she didn’t want to go—she was looking forward to the time away—but there was always this gnawing feeling in the pit of her stomach whenever she had to fly.

She kept it to herself, as she usually did, focusing on the task at hand. But as they made their way through security, Rio found her nerves starting to build. She felt the familiar tension in her chest, her palms sweating slightly. It was hard to ignore, but she wasn’t about to let it show.

Agatha, always perceptive, noticed the subtle changes in Rio’s posture. “Everything okay?” she asked quietly as they moved through the terminal.

Rio nodded quickly, trying to brush it off. “Yeah, just… a little tired. Nothing to worry about.”

But Agatha, not fooled, raised an eyebrow. “Are you sure?”

Rio hesitated for a moment, her gaze flickering to Agatha’s. She really didn’t want to admit it—not now, not with all the excitement of the trip ahead. But Agatha was already watching her with that knowing look.

“I… I’m just not great with flying,” Rio admitted softly, her voice barely above a whisper.

Agatha’s eyes softened with understanding, and she reached out to gently take Rio’s hand. “Hey,” she said, squeezing it lightly. “It’s okay. We’ll be fine. I’ll be here with you the whole time.”

Rio took a deep breath, her anxiety still there but lessening with Agatha’s calming presence. “I’m fine. I just… I don’t like the feeling of being up there. It’s like I have no control, you know?”

Agatha nodded, her fingers still wrapped around Rio’s. “I get it. But you’re not alone in this. We’ll make it through together. And if you need anything, just let me know.”

Rio felt a wave of relief wash over her at Agatha’s words. She wasn’t alone in this, and that made all the difference. She gave Agatha a small smile, grateful for her support.

“Thanks,” Rio whispered, leaning into her for a brief moment before straightening up again. “I’ll be okay.”

They made their way to the gate, Rio’s nerves slowly settling as they passed through the final steps of getting on the plane. The discomfort still lingered in the back of her mind, but with Agatha beside her, she felt like maybe—just maybe—she could handle it.

As they boarded the plane and settled into their seats, Agatha took her hand once more, a soft smile on her face. Rio couldn’t help but feel a little lighter, knowing that with Agatha by her side, she wasn’t facing this fear alone.

~*~

 

The Uber pulled up in front of the Four Seasons Hotel, and Rio’s breath caught in her throat as she looked up at the towering building. She could already tell from the sleek, modern exterior that this was going to be something special.

As they got out of the car, Rio hesitated for a moment, looking at the opulent entrance. The doorman greeted them with a warm smile, but Rio couldn’t help feeling a little out of place. She had grown up in a very different world—one where luxury like this wasn’t even on the horizon. A place like this felt… way beyond her reach. She glanced over at Agatha, trying to ignore the feeling creeping in.

Agatha noticed the shift in Rio’s demeanor but didn’t say anything. She simply smiled, reaching out to take Rio’s hand as they walked toward the entrance. “You okay?” she asked, her voice gentle.

Rio gave a small, unsure smile. “Yeah, just—” She paused, then took a breath. “This place is amazing. But it feels like I’m out of my depth, you know?”

Agatha’s smile didn’t waver as she squeezed Rio’s hand. “I get it,” she said, her voice calm and reassuring. “But this is just a little something I wanted to do for us. A way to celebrate what we’ve built together. Our relationship. Our love.” She leaned in close, dropping her voice to a soft whisper. “It’s a gift for both of us, Rio. Don’t think for a second it’s out of your range. You deserve this and more.”

Rio’s eyes softened as she met Agatha’s gaze. There was a warmth and sincerity in Agatha’s expression that made the knot in Rio’s stomach loosen, just a little. Still, the reality of the difference in their financial worlds lingered in the back of her mind, but Agatha’s words made her feel a little better about it.

“You really mean that?” Rio asked quietly, her voice tinged with uncertainty.

Agatha nodded, her hand never leaving Rio’s. “Of course I do,” she replied, her thumb brushing gently against Rio’s skin. “You mean the world to me. And I want you to feel comfortable. This is just about us. Nothing more.”

Rio smiled, though she still felt a little uneasy. She allowed herself to relax into Agatha’s touch, her heart warming at the thought of Agatha’s thoughtfulness.

When they entered the lobby, the grandeur of the space took Rio’s breath away once again. The marble floors, crystal chandeliers, and modern artwork scattered throughout—it all felt surreal.

They made their way to the elevator, and Rio couldn’t help but glance around, feeling as if she was in a dream. She still wasn’t completely sure how she felt about it, but Agatha’s assurance helped ease the tension in her chest.

Once inside the suite, Rio’s breath hitched. The view of Central Park through the floor-to-ceiling windows was absolutely breathtaking, and the room itself—luxury at its finest. Her mind raced with thoughts of how this was way beyond what she could ever afford, but Agatha had given her that reassurance, and for now, she allowed herself to feel the joy of it all.

“Wow, this place is… incredible,” Rio murmured, stepping closer to the window, her fingers lightly brushing against the glass.

Agatha moved up beside her, her hand slipping into Rio’s as they both took in the view. “It’s ours for the next few days,” Agatha said softly. “Just us. No stress, no worries. Just time together.”

Rio looked at Agatha, her heart swelling with affection. “Thank you,” she whispered, her voice thick with emotion. “I know I don’t always feel like I belong in places like this, but… I’ll try to let myself enjoy it.”

Agatha’s fingers tightened around hers, a gentle, grounding gesture. “You belong with me. That’s all that matters.”

The suite was nothing short of breathtaking, and Rio couldn’t help but let out a soft, awed laugh as she turned around, taking in every luxurious detail. The crisp white sheets on the king-sized bed, the modern furnishings, and the soft glow of ambient lighting—it was the kind of place she had only ever seen in movies. The grand view of Central Park was like a painting, framed perfectly by the floor-to-ceiling windows.

“Seriously, Agatha… this is insane,” Rio murmured, running her fingers over the smooth surface of the polished wood furniture. “I feel like I’m in a dream.”

Agatha smiled warmly, watching Rio’s reaction. “I’m glad you like it. I wanted it to be special,” she said, her voice full of affection. She moved closer, her hand brushing against Rio’s arm, sending a spark of warmth through her.

“I don’t even know where to start,” Rio said, still taking it all in. She looked at Agatha, eyes soft. “You really didn’t have to do all this. But I’m glad you did. It feels like… we’re really doing this. Together.”

Agatha’s heart swelled as she stepped forward, closing the gap between them. “I wanted us to have something to remember. Something perfect.”

Agatha’s eyes shimmered with something between gratitude and exhaustion, but Rio could see the weight lifting, just a little, from her shoulders.

Together, they stood in the wake of Evanora’s cruelty, knowing that the bond they shared was stronger than anything that could be thrown their way.
